## Agent 4 response — global trace / positive functional route

I worked against the stated Agent 4 target: find a global or semi-local positive functional for

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)
=
\int w(m-m_0)\,|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\]

that could prove Gate 1,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

The coordinator background correctly flags the main danger: naive positivity gives only \(\mathcal E_w\ge0\), while Gate 1 needs a **coercive lower bound** at the specific off-line packet center. 

My conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No unconditional trace/Weil-positive coercive route is visible yet.}
}
\]

There are, however, two plausible conditional theorem candidates and one fairly strong no-go diagnosis.

---

# 1. Prime-side expansion of the trace energy

Write, schematically,

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=R(m)+P(m),
\]

where

\[
R(m)=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

and

\[
P(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For the complexified polynomial

\[
P_c(m)=\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n},
\]

the packet energy is

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)
=
\int w(t)\,|R(m_0+t)+P_c(m_0+t)|^2\,dt.
\]

Expanding,

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)
=
\sum_{n,k\le X}
a_n\overline{a_k}
e^{-im_0(\log n-\log k)}
\widehat w(\log n-\log k)
\]

\[
+
2\Re
\sum_{n\le X}
a_n e^{-im_0\log n}
\int w(t)\overline{R(m_0+t)}e^{-it\log n}\,dt
+
\int w(t)|R(m_0+t)|^2\,dt.
\]

So the core matrix is

\[
G_w(n,k)
=
e^{-im_0(\log n-\log k)}
\widehat w(\log n-\log k).
\]

If \(w\ge0\), then \(G_w\) is positive semidefinite. But this only gives

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)\ge0
\]

for the pure prime piece. It does **not** give

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

To get coercivity, one would need a lower frame bound:

\[
\sum_{n,k\le X}
a_n\overline{a_k}
e^{-im_0(\log n-\log k)}
\widehat w(\log n-\log k)
\ge
Q^{-B}\sum_{n\le X}|a_n|^2
\]

or at least

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

This is not available from large sieve technology at the relevant packet scale.

The obstruction is frequency density. For a window of length \(T\sim |I_\rho|\), Ingham-type lower bounds need approximate separation

\[
|\log n-\log k|\gtrsim T^{-1}.
\]

But

\[
\log(n+1)-\log n\sim \frac1n,
\]

and the AFE length \(X\) is large. Thus the frequency set \(\{\log n:n\le X\}\) is far denser than the reciprocal packet length. The Gram matrix has very small eigenvalues in generic coefficient space.

So a large-sieve or positive-kernel lower bound cannot prove Gate 1 unless it uses the **fixed actual zeta coefficients** \(a_n\), not merely separation or positivity.

---

# 2. Zero-side expansion of the trace energy

On the zero side, write schematically

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\mathrm{reg}} K_2(m;\rho).
\]

Then

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)
=
\sum_{\rho,\rho'}
\int w(t)
K_2(m_0+t;\rho)
\overline{K_2(m_0+t;\rho')}
\,dt
\]

\[
+
2\Re\sum_\rho
\int w(t)B_2(m_0+t)\overline{K_2(m_0+t;\rho)}\,dt
+
\int w(t)|B_2(m_0+t)|^2\,dt.
\]

The zero-zero term is again a positive Gram form if \(w\ge0\):

\[
G_w(\rho,\rho')
=
\int w(t)
K_2(m_0+t;\rho)
\overline{K_2(m_0+t;\rho')}
\,dt.
\]

But positive semidefinite is not enough. The known same-scale quadrature adversary constructs positive local packets whose low source-curvature jets vanish:

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Equivalently, the local source term has a high-order Taylor zero at the packet center. Therefore, for any \(w\) supported inside a sufficiently small normalized packet \(X\), the local energy can be forced to satisfy an estimate of the form

\[
\int_X w(x)|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ll C_w\,\eta_R,
\]

with \(\eta_R\) decaying rapidly as the number of canceled moments grows.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-side positive Gram structure is compatible with source flattening.}
}
\]

It gives nonnegativity, not coercivity.

---

# 3. No-go diagnosis for naive positive functionals

The following route appears blocked:

\[
w\ge0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathcal E_w(m_0)\ge0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathcal E_w(m_0)\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

The final implication is false without an extra arithmetic input.

More precisely:

## No-go statement

Let \(X\subset\mathbb R\) be a fixed normalized packet interval and let \(w\ge0\) be any smooth weight supported in \(X\). The existence of positive same-scale quadrature packets implies that there are positive local zero-source configurations for which

\[
\int_X w(x)|F(x)|^2\,dx
\]

is arbitrarily small compared to the natural packet scale, after canceling finitely many source-curvature moments.

Therefore, no packet-local positive functional depending only on the zero-kernel geometry can prove Gate 1.

It must use one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual prime coefficients,}
\qquad
\text{zero-prime compatibility,}
\qquad
\text{or a genuinely global Weil/trace contradiction.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Candidate theorem A — constrained prime-frame coercivity

This is the cleanest possible large-sieve-flavored route, but it is a **new arithmetic theorem**, not standard large sieve.

## Candidate theorem A

Let

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m)+P_2(m),
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n}
\]

using the fixed actual-zeta coefficients. Suppose \(m_0\) is an admissible off-line packet center satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Then there exists a packet-adapted nonnegative weight \(w_{m_0,\lambda}\), supported on \(I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X\), such that

\[
\int w_{m_0,\lambda}(m-m_0)
|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Equivalently, in normalized variables,

\[
\int_X w(x)|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

## Required proof mechanism

This theorem would need to prove that the actual coefficient vector

\[
(a_n e^{-im_0\log n})_{n\le X}
\]

does not lie close to the small-eigenvalue subspace of the packet Gram matrix

\[
\widehat w(\log n-\log k).
\]

In formula form, one needs

\[
a(m_0)^*G_w a(m_0)
\ge Q^{-B}\|a_{\mathrm{eff}}\|^2
\]

after adding \(B_2,D_2,E_2\) and controlling cross terms.

## Status

This is plausible only if the fixed zeta coefficients impose a nonrecurrence constraint. Generic Dirichlet-polynomial arguments will not prove it, because generic dense frequency systems have near-null packet modes.

So this route collapses into Agent 2’s fixed-coefficient prime/AFE nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 5. Candidate theorem B — packet Weil minorant / explicit-formula contradiction

A second possible route is to construct a Weil-positive or explicit-formula test that sees source flattening as an impossible prime-side imbalance.

## Candidate theorem B

Assume an off-line packet centered at \(m_0\). Suppose Gate 1 fails:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I_\rho|
\]

for arbitrarily large \(A\). Then there exists a packet-adapted test function \(h=h_{m_0,\lambda}\) such that the explicit formula gives incompatible bounds:

\[
\mathcal Z(h)
=
\mathcal G(h)+\mathcal P(h),
\]

where:

\[
|\mathcal Z(h)|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

from source flattening, but

\[
|\mathcal G(h)+\mathcal P(h)|\ge Q^{-B}
\]

from gamma plus prime structure.

Here \(\mathcal Z(h)\) is the zero-side packet statistic, \(\mathcal G(h)\) the gamma/background contribution, and \(\mathcal P(h)\) the prime contribution.

## Proof skeleton

1. Gate 1 failure implies smallness of the local source distribution:

   \[
   q''_{\can}\approx0
   \quad\text{on }I_\rho.
   \]

2. By duality, for every normalized packet test \(\psi\),

   \[
   \left|
   \int_{I_\rho}\psi(m-m_0)q''_{\can}(m)\,dm
   \right|
   \le
   \|\psi\|_2
   \left(
   \int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2
   \right)^{1/2}.
   \]

3. Choose \(\psi\) as a differential or localized transform of an explicit-formula test \(h\), so that this integral equals a zero-side statistic.

4. Use the explicit formula to rewrite the same statistic as gamma plus prime terms.

5. Prove a lower bound for the gamma-plus-prime side.

The hard point is step 5. Without it, this is just a restatement of Gate 1 in dual form.

## Status

This route is attractive because it connects directly to the zero-prime anti-design obstruction. But it again requires a genuinely arithmetic lower bound. It is not supplied by Weil positivity alone.

---

# 6. Why ordinary Weil positivity does not by itself close Gate 1

A tempting argument is:

\[
\text{choose } h=g*\widetilde g
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\widehat h\ge0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{positive explicit-formula functional}.
\]

This is insufficient.

The problem is that Weil positivity is not a free coercive inequality for packet source curvature. In its strongest form, positivity for all suitable tests is essentially RH-equivalent. Using it directly to rule out an off-line packet would risk proving RH by assuming an RH-equivalent positivity input.

For Gate 1, we need something narrower:

\[
\text{off-line packet}
+
\text{source flatness}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{explicit-formula contradiction}.
\]

That contradiction must be proved from the actual prime/gamma terms, not from a general assumed zero-side positivity principle.

So the viable Weil route is not “Weil positivity implies energy positive.” It must be a **packet-specific Weil minorant** whose prime side has a certified sign or magnitude.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No such packet-specific Weil minorant is presently identified.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Candidate theorem C — global average trace

One can average \(\mathcal E_w(m_0)\) over a long interval of centers:

\[
\int_M^{2M}\mathcal E_w(m_0)\,dm_0.
\]

Prime-side orthogonality gives approximately

\[
\int_M^{2M}\mathcal E_w(m_0)\,dm_0
\sim
M\,\widehat w(0)\sum_{n\le X}|a_n|^2
\]

plus off-diagonal and background terms.

This proves that the source curvature has average \(L^2\)-mass over many packet centers.

But Gate 1 needs mass at the **specific** off-line center \(m_0\). A global average cannot exclude rare packet centers where

\[
q''_{\can}\approx0.
\]

Thus the average trace gives only:

\[
\text{many centers are non-flat},
\]

not:

\[
\text{off-line packet centers are non-flat}.
\]

To use this route, one would need an additional theorem:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
m_0
\text{ belongs to a thick set of high trace mass}.
\]

That again reduces to an arithmetic coupling between \(Z_\alpha\) and \(q''_{\can}\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global average trace is not enough.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Best current Agent 4 recommendation

The global trace route should not be abandoned, but it should be narrowed to a precise conditional target.

The best target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet explicit-formula coercivity under }Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
}
\]

Concrete theorem to try next:

## Packet explicit-formula coercivity theorem

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible off-line packet center and let

\[
I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X.
\]

There exists a packet-adapted test \(\psi_{m_0,\lambda}\), with

\[
\operatorname{supp}\psi_{m_0,\lambda}\subset I_\rho
\]

or rapidly decaying outside \(I_\rho\), such that

\[
\left|
\int \psi_{m_0,\lambda}(m)q''_{\can}(m)\,dm
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^3|X|^{1/2}.
\]

Then Gate 1 follows immediately by Cauchy-Schwarz:

\[
Q^{-B}\lambda^3|X|^{1/2}
\le
\|\psi_{m_0,\lambda}\|_2
\left(
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\right)^{1/2}.
\]

If

\[
\|\psi_{m_0,\lambda}\|_2\ll |I_\rho|^{-1/2},
\]

then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B'}|I_\rho|.
\]

So Agent 4’s route reduces to finding a **single explicit-formula-visible linear statistic** of \(q''_{\can}\) that cannot vanish at an off-line packet center.

This is weaker than proving full \(L^2\) coercivity directly and more plausible than a positive quadratic trace.

---

# 9. Final diagnosis

\[
\boxed{
\text{Naive positive trace: no-go.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Large-sieve lower bound: no-go without fixed-coefficient arithmetic.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Weil positivity: dangerous/circular unless converted into a packet-specific prime-side contradiction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Best viable Agent 4 route: construct a packet explicit-formula linear statistic whose prime/gamma side has a }Q^{-B}\text{ lower bound under }Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
}
\]

So the trace/positive-functional route does not currently provide an independent proof of Gate 1. It collapses into a sharper dual formulation of the same missing arithmetic fact: actual zeta cannot realize same-scale source-flattening at an admissible off-line packet center.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 18:56:09)

_Thought for 1m 6s_

## Agent 4 / D — Packet spectral leakage theorem

I am executing the **Agent 4 / D** instruction: construct or diagnose a packet spectral leakage theorem using packet probes \(h_{k,\lambda,m_0}\), with the target that high packet modes \(k\ge 3\) cannot all be small at an admissible off-line center. The supplied instruction explicitly assigns Agent 4 to this packet-wavelet/spectral-leakage route. 

## 1. Probe family

Use the normalized packet coordinate

\[
x=\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda}.
\]

For a same-scale zero packet, the local normalized Cauchy/Poisson kernel is

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

The key identity is

\[
\frac{1}{(k-1)!}K_\theta^{(k-1)}(0)
=
\sin(k\theta).
\]

So the cleanest packet probe for the \(k\)-th sine moment is a smoothed derivative-of-delta probe.

Let \(\eta\in C_c^\infty((-1,1))\), \(\int\eta=1\), and choose a small fixed smoothing parameter \(0<\varepsilon\ll1\). Define

\[
h_{k,\varepsilon}(x)
=
\frac{(-1)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
\varepsilon^{-k}
\eta^{(k-1)}(x/\varepsilon).
\]

Then, for analytic packet kernels away from the singular endpoints \(\theta=0,\pi\),

\[
\int h_{k,\varepsilon}(x)K_\theta(x)\,dx
=
\sin(k\theta)+O_k(\varepsilon).
\]

In physical variables,

\[
h_{k,\lambda,m_0}(m)
=
\lambda^{-1}
h_{k,\varepsilon}\!\left(\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda}\right).
\]

Thus the zero-side statistic recovers

\[
\mathcal Z_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
=
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)
+
O_k(\varepsilon)
+
\text{off-packet leakage}.
\]

The off-packet leakage is controllable if the packet window is separated from external zeros by the ordinary/singular packet assumptions. If separation fails, the probe becomes contaminated and must be treated as Yellow, not Green.

---

## 2. Fourier transform and prime-side coefficient

The normalized Fourier transform is

\[
\widehat h_{k,\varepsilon}(s)
=
\frac{(-is)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
\widehat\eta(\varepsilon s),
\]

up to the harmless convention-dependent sign.

Therefore the explicit-formula prime contribution has the form

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-im_0}
\frac{(-i\lambda\log n)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
\widehat\eta(\varepsilon\lambda\log n).
\]

So the packet modes are precisely smoothed finite-jet prime/AFE moments.

The gamma/background and tail/dual terms give

\[
\mathcal Z_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
=
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
+
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
+
\mathcal D_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
+
\mathcal E_{k,\lambda}(m_0).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
\]

is just the explicit-formula expression for the same local sine moment, with \(\mathcal T\) bundling dual, tail, and regularization conventions.

---

## 3. Can all \(k\ge3\) modes be small while the low mass mode remains nonzero?

Yes, in the local packet model.

The deterministic sine quadrature adversary gives positive weights such that

\[
\sum_{j=1}^{N}w_j\sin(k\theta_j)
=
\delta_{k1},
\qquad
1\le k\le N.
\]

Hence, for \(N\ge R+3\),

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

while

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j=1.
\]

Therefore the high packet modes may vanish exactly while the low packet mass mode remains nonzero.

This kills any proof based only on:

\[
\text{local packet positivity},
\quad
\text{orthogonality of sine modes},
\quad
\text{finite zero-counting},
\quad
\text{quartet symmetry},
\quad
\text{or generic uncertainty}.
\]

The packet spectral leakage theorem cannot be a purely zero-side theorem. It must use actual zeta arithmetic, consistent with the prior conclusion that local zero geometry alone is insufficient and that the canonical proof must use the actual \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) object. 

---

## 4. Large-sieve / orthogonality attempt

Consider the prime mode vector

\[
\mathbf P_R(m_0)
=
\left(
\mathcal P_{3,\lambda}(m_0),
\dots,
\mathcal P_{R+3,\lambda}(m_0)
\right).
\]

Using the Fourier expression above,

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
=
2\Re
\sum_n b_n(m_0)
\frac{(-i\lambda\log n)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
\widehat\eta(\varepsilon\lambda\log n),
\]

where

\[
b_n(m_0)=\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}n^{-im_0}.
\]

A large-sieve estimate can plausibly give an average upper/lower relation over long \(m_0\)-ranges, for example

\[
\int_M^{2M}
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
|\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m)|^2\,dm
\asymp
M
\sum_n
\frac{\Lambda(n)^2}{n}
W_R(\lambda\log n),
\]

with

\[
W_R(s)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\frac{|s|^{2k-2}}{((k-1)!)^2}
|\widehat\eta(\varepsilon s)|^2.
\]

But this only says the modes have average mass in \(m\). It does not rule out special centers \(m_0\) where

\[
\mathbf P_R(m_0)
\approx
\mathbf G_R(m_0)+\mathbf T_R(m_0).
\]

The frequency set \(\{\log n\}\) is dense at packet scale, and the vector

\[
(n^{-im_0})_n
\]

can recur near finite-codimension targets unless one proves a fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence theorem.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{large sieve gives average mass, not pointwise spectral leakage at an off-line center.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Candidate spectral leakage theorem

The clean theorem would be:

### Packet spectral leakage theorem

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible off-line packet center satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
R=R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively \(R=O(\log Q)\). For the packet probes \(h_{k,\lambda,m_0}\) above, suppose the canonical explicit formula is valid with

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

and with packet errors satisfying

\[
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
|\mathcal E_{k,\lambda}(m_0)|^2
\le
Q^{-C}.
\]

Then there exists \(B>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
|\mathcal Z_{k,\lambda}(m_0)|^2
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

By the derivative-probe identity, this implies finite-jet anti-design:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-B'}\lambda^3,
\]

after applying the already-established finite-jet-to-Gate-1 reduction.

So this theorem would close Gate 1, modulo canonical transfer.

---

## 6. Why this theorem is not currently proved

The theorem is essentially equivalent to Agent 2’s fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence theorem.

Indeed, the packet vector

\[
\left(
\mathcal P_{3,\lambda},
\dots,
\mathcal P_{R+3,\lambda}
\right)
\]

is a wavelet/derivative-coordinate version of the jet vector

\[
\left(
\Delta^r\partial_m^rP_2(m_0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}.
\]

The target lower bound

\[
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}
-
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}
-
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

is therefore the same as saying

\[
\mathcal J_R[P_2](m_0)
\]

cannot lie \(Q^{-B}\)-close to the affine target

\[
-\mathcal J_R[B_2+D_2](m_0)
\]

under the additional condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

That is precisely the fixed actual-zeta coefficient nonrecurrence problem.

So the packet-wavelet language is useful because it aligns zero-side quadrature moments with prime-side spectral coefficients, but it does not create an independent lower bound.

---

## 7. No-go result

### No-go: local packet spectral leakage is false

For any fixed \(R\), there exist positive same-scale local packet configurations with

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

while

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j=1.
\]

Therefore no theorem of the form

\[
\text{positive packet mass}
\Rightarrow
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

can hold in local zero geometry.

### No-go: generic prime spectral leakage is also false

If the coefficients \(b_n\) are allowed to vary, or if the phases \(n^{-im_0}\) are treated as free torus variables, then the finite system

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
\approx
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}(m_0)+\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}(m_0),
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

is merely a finite-codimension target. With enough active prime phases, it is underdetermined.

Thus no generic Dirichlet-polynomial spectral leakage theorem can prove Gate 1.

The only viable theorem must use the fixed arithmetic orbit

\[
m_0\mapsto \left(n^{-im_0}\right)_n
\]

with the actual zeta coefficients.

---

## 8. Final Agent 4 verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet probes can cleanly translate zero-side anti-design into prime-side spectral coefficients.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{But the desired spectral leakage lower bound is not a consequence of local packet geometry, orthogonality, uncertainty, or large sieve alone.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The route reduces to fixed-coefficient prime/AFE nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

The cleanest surviving theorem is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-B},
\]

but this is not presently proved. It is best viewed as the packet-wavelet coordinate form of the finite-jet anti-design theorem, not an independent proof of it.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 18:59:39)

_Thought for 11s_

## Agent 4 / D — Packet spectral leakage with \(Z_\alpha\)-conditioning

I am executing the Agent 4 instruction from the latest coordinator prompt: test whether adding the off-line condition \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) improves the packet spectral leakage theorem, or whether the route still collapses to fixed-coefficient prime nonrecurrence. 

## 1. Put \(Z_\alpha\) into the same packet-mode coordinates

The packet prime modes are

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-im_0}
\widehat h_k(\lambda\log n),
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

For the derivative-probe family from the previous Agent 4 round,

\[
\widehat h_k(s)
\simeq
\frac{(-is)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}\widehat\eta(\varepsilon s).
\]

So the packet modes test the prime phase vector

\[
u_n(m_0)=n^{-im_0}
\]

against the symbol vectors

\[
v_k(n)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
\frac{(-i\lambda\log n)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
\widehat\eta(\varepsilon\lambda\log n).
\]

Now write the AFE-side off-line equation as

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\sum_{n} z_n(\alpha)n^{-im_0}
+
\sum_n z_n^\ast(\alpha)n^{+im_0}
+
Z_{\mathrm{bg}}(m_0,\alpha)
+
Z_E(m_0,\alpha).
\]

On the same active packet-frequency block, this is another linear statistic of the same phase vector:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\langle z_\alpha,u(m_0)\rangle
+
\langle z_\alpha^\ast,\overline{u(m_0)}\rangle
+
Z_{\mathrm{bg}}+Z_E.
\]

Thus \(Z_\alpha=0\) adds one complex linear constraint, or two real constraints, on the same prime-phase orbit.

The relevant finite-dimensional question is therefore:

\[
z_\alpha
\stackrel{?}{\in}
\operatorname{span}\{v_1,v_2,\dots,v_{R+3}\}
\]

on an active block, and more specifically whether its projection onto the high-mode subspace

\[
V_{\ge3}:=\operatorname{span}\{v_3,\dots,v_{R+3}\}
\]

has a polynomially large component.

---

## 2. Does \(Z_\alpha=0\) constrain low packet modes \(k=1,2\)?

At the level of packet coordinates, the answer is: possibly \(k=1\), possibly \(k=2\), but not generically \(k\ge3\).

The low modes are

\[
v_1(n)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}\widehat\eta(\varepsilon\lambda\log n),
\]

\[
v_2(n)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
(-i\lambda\log n)
\widehat\eta(\varepsilon\lambda\log n).
\]

These correspond to local packet mass and first packet slope/centering.

If \(z_n(\alpha)\) is locally smooth as a function of \(\log n\), then on a short active frequency block one has a Taylor expansion

\[
z_n(\alpha)
=
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
\widehat\eta(\varepsilon\lambda\log n)
\left[
a_0(\alpha)
+
a_1(\alpha)\lambda\log n
+
a_2(\alpha)(\lambda\log n)^2
+\cdots
\right].
\]

Then \(Z_\alpha=0\) mostly constrains a low-order combination of packet modes. The first two terms are exactly \(k=1,2\)-type information. The higher coefficients \(a_j\), \(j\ge2\), are what could force leakage into \(k\ge3\).

So the key object is the high-mode residual

\[
z_\alpha^{\perp}
=
z_\alpha
-
\Pi_{\le2} z_\alpha,
\]

or more generally

\[
z_{\alpha,R}^{\perp}
=
z_\alpha
-
\Pi_{\le R+3} z_\alpha.
\]

But if \(z_\alpha\) is well-approximated by a low-degree polynomial in \(\lambda\log n\), then the high-mode component may be small.

Thus the condition \(Z_\alpha=0\) gives useful packet leakage only if one proves a quantitative non-polynomiality statement:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
z_\alpha,
\operatorname{span}\{v_1,v_2\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}\|z_\alpha\|
\]

with nontrivial projection into \(V_{\ge3}\), or more strongly,

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
z_\alpha,
V_{\le2}+V_{\mathrm{flat}}
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}\|z_\alpha\|,
\]

where \(V_{\mathrm{flat}}\) denotes the phase directions that kill all high source modes.

No such bound is presently available from packet geometry alone.

---

## 3. Does \(Z_\alpha=0\) force leakage from low modes into \(k\ge3\)?

Only under an extra symbol-transversality condition.

Let

\[
M_{\mathrm{hi}}(u)
=
\left(
\langle v_3,u\rangle,
\dots,
\langle v_{R+3},u\rangle
\right),
\]

and

\[
Z(u)=\langle z_\alpha,u\rangle + \text{dual/bg}.
\]

The desired implication is

\[
Z(u)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|M_{\mathrm{hi}}(u)-\mathrm{target}_{\mathrm{hi}}\|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

This is false unless \(Z\) is transverse to the high-mode-flat subspace.

Define the high-flat affine space

\[
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{hi}}
=
\left\{
u:
\langle v_k,u\rangle
=
\tau_k,
\quad
3\le k\le R+3
\right\},
\]

where

\[
\tau_k
=
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}
+
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}.
\]

Then \(Z_\alpha=0\) improves leakage only if

\[
Z|_{\mathcal F_{\mathrm{hi}}}
\]

is bounded away from zero on the admissible phase orbit.

In a relaxed linear model, \(\mathcal F_{\mathrm{hi}}\) has codimension \(R+1\), while \(Z=0\) adds codimension \(1\). With many active primes, the intersection is still high-dimensional. Therefore \(Z_\alpha=0\) does not force leakage by dimension count alone.

A leakage theorem would require arithmetic nonrecurrence of the actual orbit

\[
m_0\mapsto (n^{-im_0})_n,
\]

not merely linear algebra.

---

## 4. Phase-relaxed countermodel

Here is the clean countermodel showing why \(Z_\alpha\)-conditioning does not by itself solve the packet leakage problem.

Take an active block \(\mathcal B\) with

\[
N:=|\mathcal B|\gg R+3.
\]

Treat the phases

\[
u_n=n^{-im_0}
\]

as independent variables on the unit torus, or first in the larger polydisc \(|u_n|\le1\).

Impose the high-mode flatness equations

\[
\langle v_k,u\rangle=\tau_k,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

This is \(R+1\) complex linear equations.

Also impose

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0.
\]

This is one additional complex linear equation.

Total complex codimension is \(R+2\). If

\[
N>R+2,
\]

then the relaxed solution space is nonempty generically. With the unit-disc relaxation it is easy to solve; with the unit-torus restriction, one expects solutions by phase-balancing whenever the target vector lies in the zonotope generated by the coefficient vectors

\[
\left(
v_3(n),\dots,v_{R+3}(n),z_n(\alpha)
\right).
\]

Thus there are phase-relaxed configurations satisfying simultaneously

\[
Z_\alpha=0
\]

and

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}
-
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}
-
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}
\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

The same construction can preserve low packet mass by also requiring

\[
\langle v_1,u\rangle=\mu_1\neq0,
\]

provided \(N>R+3\). It can also set or tune \(v_2\) if \(N>R+4\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha=0
\text{ does not force high-mode leakage in the phase-relaxed model.}
}
\]

Any successful theorem must use the actual one-parameter arithmetic orbit, not free phases.

---

## 5. Possible conditioned leakage theorem

The best plausible theorem is the following.

### Candidate theorem: \(Z_\alpha\)-conditioned packet leakage

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible off-line packet center, and let \(R=R(Q)\). Suppose the canonical AFE expansion is valid in packet coordinates with controlled background, dual, tail, and error terms. Suppose further that the actual prime-phase orbit satisfies the conditioned nonrecurrence estimate

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
u(m_0),
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{hi}}\cap\{Z_\alpha=0\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}
\]

in the active block metric induced by the packet symbols \(v_3,\dots,v_{R+3}\). Then

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\mathcal P_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal G_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
-
\mathcal T_{k,\lambda}(m_0)
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

By the packet-probe/finite-jet equivalence, this implies

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-B'}\lambda^3,
\]

and hence Gate 1 via the finite-jet reduction.

But the hypothesis

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
u(m_0),
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{hi}}\cap\{Z_\alpha=0\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is essentially the fixed actual-zeta nonrecurrence theorem in packet coordinates.

So this is a valid conditional theorem, but not an independent proof.

---

## 6. Stronger theorem requiring symbol transversality

A more algebraic version is:

Assume that on some active block \(\mathcal B\),

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
z_\alpha,
\operatorname{span}\{v_1,v_2\}+V_{\mathrm{flat}}
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}\|z_\alpha\|,
\]

where \(V_{\mathrm{flat}}\) is the annihilator of high packet modes. Then \(Z_\alpha=0\) prevents complete high-mode flattening unless the phase vector lies in a codimension-\((R+2)\) exceptional set.

This gives a two-step proof path:

\[
\text{symbol transversality}
+
\text{arithmetic nonrecurrence of }m\mapsto u(m)
\Rightarrow
\text{conditioned spectral leakage}.
\]

But symbol transversality alone is insufficient. It rules out algebraic degeneracy of \(Z_\alpha\), not recurrence to the bad affine set.

---

## 7. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha=0
\text{ adds a real constraint, but by itself it does not force packet leakage into }k\ge3.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{In phase-relaxed models, one can satisfy }Z_\alpha=0
\text{ and kill all high packet modes simultaneously.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Therefore, }Z_\alpha\text{-conditioned packet leakage still collapses to fixed actual-prime nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

The useful output of this lane is a sharper formulation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove that the actual orbit }m_0\mapsto(n^{-im_0})_n
\text{ cannot hit }
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{hi}}\cap\{Z_\alpha=0\}
\text{ within }Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is the packet-mode version of the Wronskian/transversality bottleneck.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:03:00)

I’ll treat this as the Agent 4/D lane: whether a normalized filter can isolate a Wronskian minor without destroying packet locality. The key tradeoff is frequency resolution versus the packet-scale support needed for Gate 1.

_Thought for 49s_

## Agent 4 / D — Filtered Wronskian / block isolation

I am executing the **Agent 4 / D** instruction: try to rescue the normalized Wronskian determinant by isolating one active block or minor, and determine whether such filtering remains local enough to imply Gate 1. The coordinator prompt assigns Agent 4 specifically to the “filtered Wronskian / block isolation” lane. 

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
L:=R+2.
\]

The normalized Wronskian has main-term expansion

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{|S|=L}
\widetilde C_S(\alpha)
e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
\Omega_S=\sum_{n\in S}\log n
=\log N_S.
\]

The desired lower bound is

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

at admissible centers. The problem is cancellation among the many subset-product phases

\[
e^{-im_0\Omega_S}.
\]

A filtered-minor strategy would try to isolate either:

\[
S_0
\]

or a small structured family

\[
\mathfrak S_0
\]

so that the filtered Wronskian has a non-cancelling main contribution.

---

# 2. Candidate filter 1 — local convolution in \(m\)

Let

\[
K_T(t)=T^{-1}K(t/T)
\]

be a filter of physical support length \(T\), centered at \(m_0\). Define

\[
\mathcal F_T\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)
=
\int K_T(t)\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0+t,\alpha)\,dt.
\]

Then

\[
\mathcal F_T\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)
=
\sum_{|S|=L}
\widetilde C_S(\alpha)
e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
\widehat K(T\Omega_S)
+
\cdots.
\]

To isolate \(S_0\), one needs

\[
\widehat K(T\Omega_{S_0})\approx1
\]

and

\[
\widehat K(T\Omega_S)\approx0
\qquad
S\neq S_0.
\]

This requires frequency resolution

\[
T^{-1}
\lesssim
\min_{S\neq S_0}
|\Omega_S-\Omega_{S_0}|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
T
\gtrsim
\frac1{\operatorname{sep}(\Omega)}.
\]

For subset products,

\[
\Omega_S-\Omega_{S'}
=
\log\frac{N_S}{N_{S'}}.
\]

If the underlying active integers or primes are \(\le P\), then distinct subset products satisfy only the weak Diophantine lower bound

\[
\left|
\log\frac{N_S}{N_{S'}}
\right|
\gtrsim
P^{-L}
\]

in the worst case. Hence single-minor isolation may require

\[
T\gtrsim P^L.
\]

This is much larger than the packet scale

\[
I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X
\]

unless the active set is artificially sparse.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{single subset-product isolation by an }m\text{-local filter is nonlocal.}
}
\]

It cannot directly imply Gate 1, because Gate 1 needs control on the packet interval \(I_\rho\), not on a huge averaging interval.

---

# 3. Candidate filter 2 — coarse frequency-band projection

Instead of isolating one subset \(S_0\), choose a band \(J\) in subset-frequency space and define a filter with

\[
\widehat K(T\Omega)\approx 1_J(\Omega).
\]

This gives

\[
\mathcal F_{T,J}\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)
\approx
\sum_{\Omega_S\in J}
\widetilde C_S
e^{-im_0\Omega_S}.
\]

This avoids the microscopic spacing problem if \(J\) has width

\[
|J|\gg \operatorname{sep}(\Omega).
\]

But then many subset terms remain. The phase sum

\[
\sum_{\Omega_S\in J}
\widetilde C_S
e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
\]

can still cancel.

A band projection helps only if the selected family \(\mathfrak S_J\) has one of the following properties:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coefficient dominance, sign/phase rigidity, or a separate nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

None follows from the Wronskian algebra alone.

So coarse filtering reduces the number of terms but does not solve the pointwise lower-bound problem.

---

# 4. Candidate filter 3 — polynomial filter in \(\mathcal D\)

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m.
\]

Apply a polynomial filter

\[
p(\mathcal D)
\]

to the Wronskian. Since

\[
\mathcal D e^{-im\Omega_S}
=
-i\sigma\Omega_S e^{-im\Omega_S},
\]

where \(\sigma=\lambda\) or \(\Delta\), we get

\[
p(\mathcal D)\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\sum_S
p(-i\sigma\Omega_S)
\widetilde C_S e^{-im\Omega_S}.
\]

To isolate a single \(S_0\), one would need

\[
p(-i\sigma\Omega_{S_0})=1,
\]

and

\[
p(-i\sigma\Omega_S)\approx0
\qquad S\neq S_0.
\]

If there are \(M\) active subset products, exact interpolation requires

\[
\deg p\ge M-1.
\]

But

\[
M=\binom{B}{L}
\]

if \(B\) active base frequencies are available. Since \(L=R+2\), this is enormous even for moderately large \(B\).

The available derivative budget is only

\[
O(R),
\]

or at most \(O(2R+1)\) in the normalized Wronskian audit. Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a polynomial } \mathcal D\text{-filter of admissible degree cannot isolate a subset product.}
}
\]

It can only create coarse weights across the subset-frequency range.

High-degree \(p\) would require derivatives well beyond the canonical AFE/error budget and would introduce non-polynomial constants.

---

# 5. Candidate filter 4 — prefilter the base \(n\)-block

One could attempt to filter the AFE representation first, selecting a base block

\[
\mathcal B_0\subset\mathcal B
\]

before forming the Wronskian. This would reduce the determinant sum to

\[
\sum_{S\subset \mathcal B_0,\ |S|=L}
\widetilde C_S e^{-im\Omega_S}.
\]

This is better than filtering subset products directly, because selecting \(n\)-blocks only requires resolving frequencies \(\log n\), not sums of \(L\) logs.

However, it does not isolate a determinant minor unless

\[
|\mathcal B_0|=L.
\]

If \(|\mathcal B_0|=L\), the Wronskian uses exactly one subset, but the projection onto \(\mathcal B_0\) is extremely narrow in prime-frequency space. To isolate individual \(n\)’s or a tiny cluster of \(n\)’s, an \(m\)-space filter needs length at least

\[
T\gtrsim
\frac1{\min_{n\neq n'}|\log n-\log n'|}
\sim n,
\]

for consecutive integers near \(n\).

That is again nonlocal relative to the packet interval unless the chosen base frequencies are deliberately sparse and separated.

If \(\mathcal B_0\) is thick enough to be selected locally, then it contains many \(L\)-subsets, and subset-product cancellation returns.

Thus base-block filtering gives the dilemma:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\text{thin block} &\Rightarrow \text{nonlocal projection},\\
\text{thick block} &\Rightarrow \text{subset-product cancellation remains}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

---

# 6. Coefficient lower bound for an isolated minor

Suppose, hypothetically, that one could isolate a single minor

\[
S_0=\{n_0,\dots,n_{L-1}\}.
\]

The normalized coefficient has schematic form

\[
\widetilde C_{S_0}(\alpha)
\sim
\left(\prod_{n\in S_0} c_n\right)
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n(\alpha)\\
1\\
\xi_n\\
\vdots\\
\xi_n^R
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S_0},
\]

where

\[
r_n(\alpha)=\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n},
\]

and

\[
\xi_n=\lambda\log n
\quad\text{or}\quad
\xi_n=\Delta\log n.
\]

If the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality theorem holds, then

\[
\inf_{P\in \mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{n\in S_0}|r_n(\alpha)-P(\xi_n)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

By the usual interpolation determinant identity, this gives

\[
\left|
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n(\alpha)\\
1\\
\xi_n\\
\vdots\\
\xi_n^R
\end{pmatrix}
\right|
\gtrsim
Q^{-C}
\cdot
\left|
\prod_{i<j}(\xi_j-\xi_i)
\right|
\]

up to conditioning constants.

Thus, if the normalized nodes satisfy a well-conditioned spacing condition such as

\[
|\xi_i-\xi_j|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and the coefficients \(c_n\) are not too small, then

\[
|\widetilde C_{S_0}(\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-C'}
\prod_{n\in S_0}|c_n|.
\]

This is the best possible isolated-minor theorem.

But it does not solve the real problem, because isolating \(S_0\) locally appears impossible.

---

# 7. Viable conditional theorem

The strongest viable statement is conditional:

## Conditional filtered-minor theorem

Assume there exists a family \(\mathfrak S_0\) of \(L\)-subsets satisfying:

1. **Frequency separation**

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \bigl(
   \{\Omega_S:S\in\mathfrak S_0\},
   \{\Omega_S:S\notin\mathfrak S_0\}
   \bigr)
   \ge \gamma,
   \]

   with

   \[
   \gamma^{-1}\lesssim \lambda Q^C.
   \]

2. **Coefficient lower bound**

   \[
   \left|
   \sum_{S\in\mathfrak S_0}
   \widetilde C_S(\alpha)e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
   \right|
   \ge Q^{-C}.
   \]

3. **Filter locality**

   There exists \(K\) supported on \(O(\lambda Q^C)\), or on an admissible packet thickening, with

   \[
   \widehat K(\Omega_S)\approx1
   \quad(S\in\mathfrak S_0),
   \]

   and

   \[
   \widehat K(\Omega_S)\approx0
   \quad(S\notin\mathfrak S_0).
   \]

Then the filtered Wronskian obeys

\[
|\mathcal F_K\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

up to canonical errors.

If the filtering support remains within the admissible thickened packet scale, this can be transferred back to finite-jet anti-design and then to Gate 1.

## Status

The theorem is formally valid, but its hypotheses are essentially as hard as the original determinant nonrecurrence problem.

In actual subset-product spectra, condition 1 is the implausible one. The subset-product frequencies are too dense for packet-local separation.

---

# 8. No-go result for local block isolation

The following no-go diagnosis is the main result of this lane.

## No-go: packet-local filters cannot isolate Wronskian minors

Let

\[
\Omega=\{\Omega_S:|S|=R+2\}
\]

be the subset-product frequency set from a thick active block. Let \(K\) be an \(m\)-space filter supported on a packet-scale interval

\[
|t|\lesssim \lambda Q^C.
\]

Then \(\widehat K\) cannot resolve frequency differences smaller than

\[
(\lambda Q^C)^{-1}.
\]

But for a thick active block, the subset-product set \(\Omega\) contains many distinct frequencies inside intervals of length

\[
(\lambda Q^C)^{-1}.
\]

Therefore any packet-local filter leaves many subset-product terms active:

\[
\mathcal F_K\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)
=
\sum_{S\in\mathfrak S_{\mathrm{many}}}
\widetilde C_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+
\cdots.
\]

No coefficient-dominance or sign rigidity follows from normalization alone. Hence packet-local filtering cannot convert the Wronskian expansion into a single-minor lower bound.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local filtered-minor isolation is not a viable independent proof of Gate 1.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Single-minor isolation is possible only with nonlocal filters of length }
T\gtrsim \operatorname{sep}(\Omega)^{-1}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{At subset-product scale, this length is far larger than the packet interval.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Polynomial } \mathcal D\text{-filters cannot isolate minors within the allowed derivative budget.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Base-block filtering either becomes nonlocal or leaves subset cancellation intact.}
}
\]

Therefore the filtered-Wronskian route does **not** presently rescue the determinant method. It reduces again to the same missing arithmetic theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual normalized subset-product Wronskian exponential sum does not become }Q^{-A}\text{-small at admissible centers.}
}
\]

Filtered block isolation may still be useful diagnostically, but it does not provide an independent path to Gate 1 unless one proves a new sparse/separated active-block theorem or a genuine coefficient-dominance mechanism.
## User (2026-04-26 19:06:08)

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:06:17)

_Thought for 7s_

## Agent 4 / D — Filtered Wronskian / block isolation

Executing the **Agent 4 / D** assignment: try to isolate a Wronskian block/minor by filtering, while preserving packet locality and polynomial constants. The instruction asks for theorem statements, determinant estimates, or no-go diagnoses only. 

# 1. Object to filter

The normalized Wronskian has schematic expansion

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+2}
\widetilde C_S(\alpha)e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S.
\]

The cancellation problem is

\[
\sum_S \widetilde C_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}\approx0.
\]

A filtered-minor strategy wants to isolate either one subset \(S_0\), or a structured family \(\mathfrak S_0\), so that

\[
\sum_{S\in\mathfrak S_0}\widetilde C_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
\]

has a certified lower bound.

---

# 2. \(m\)-space convolution filter

Let \(K_T\) be supported at physical scale \(T\). Define

\[
(\mathcal F_T\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R)(m_0)
=
\int K_T(t)\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0+t,\alpha)\,dt.
\]

Then

\[
(\mathcal F_T\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R)(m_0)
=
\sum_S
\widetilde C_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
\widehat K_T(\Omega_S)
+
\cdots.
\]

To isolate \(S_0\), one needs

\[
\widehat K_T(\Omega_{S_0})\approx1,
\qquad
\widehat K_T(\Omega_S)\approx0
\quad(S\neq S_0).
\]

This requires

\[
T
\gtrsim
\frac{1}{\min_{S\neq S_0}|\Omega_S-\Omega_{S_0}|}.
\]

But

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_{S'}|
=
\left|\log\frac{N_S}{N_{S'}}\right|.
\]

If the active base integers are \(\le P\), then the crude worst-case separation is only

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_{S'}|
\gtrsim P^{-(R+2)}.
\]

Thus single-minor isolation may require

\[
T\gtrsim P^{R+2}.
\]

This is far larger than the packet scale \(\lambda\), or even \(\lambda Q^C\), unless the active frequency set is artificially sparse.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Convolution filtering can isolate a Wronskian minor only by becoming nonlocal.}
}
\]

This does not feed back into Gate 1, because Gate 1 is a packet-local estimate on \(I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X\).

---

# 3. Polynomial filter in \(\mathcal D\)

Let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m.
\]

For

\[
p(\mathcal D)=\sum_{\ell=0}^{d}a_\ell \mathcal D^\ell,
\]

we have

\[
p(\mathcal D)e^{-im\Omega_S}
=
p(-i\sigma\Omega_S)e^{-im\Omega_S},
\]

where \(\sigma=\lambda\) or \(\Delta\).

To isolate a single subset \(S_0\), \(p\) must satisfy approximately

\[
p(-i\sigma\Omega_{S_0})=1,
\]

\[
p(-i\sigma\Omega_S)=0
\qquad(S\neq S_0).
\]

If there are \(M\) active subset frequencies, exact interpolation requires

\[
d\ge M-1.
\]

For a base block of size \(B\),

\[
M=\binom{B}{R+2}.
\]

This is far beyond the allowed derivative budget. The normalized Wronskian already needs derivatives through roughly \(2R+1\); adding a high-degree polynomial filter would require derivatives through

\[
2R+1+d.
\]

Unless \(d=O(R)\), the AFE derivative/error budget becomes non-polynomial.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Admissible polynomial }\mathcal D\text{-filters can only coarse-weight subset frequencies.}
}
\]

They cannot isolate a minor.

---

# 4. Frequency-space projection

Suppose one defines a smooth cutoff \(\chi(\Omega)\) and tries to keep only

\[
\Omega_S\in J.
\]

A physical filter realizing this has length

\[
T\gtrsim |J|^{-1}.
\]

To stay packet-local, one needs

\[
T\lesssim \lambda Q^C.
\]

Therefore the frequency window width must satisfy

\[
|J|\gtrsim (\lambda Q^C)^{-1}.
\]

But the subset-product spectrum in a thick block has many \(\Omega_S\) inside such a window. So packet-local frequency projection selects not one minor but many:

\[
\sum_{\Omega_S\in J}
\widetilde C_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}.
\]

Without sign rigidity or coefficient dominance, this selected sum can still cancel.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coarse frequency projection reduces term count but does not produce a lower bound.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Base-block prefiltering

A more promising idea is to filter the original AFE frequencies \(\log n\) before forming the determinant.

Choose a base block \(\mathcal B_0\), then form the Wronskian only from \(n\in\mathcal B_0\). If

\[
|\mathcal B_0|=R+2,
\]

there is only one determinant minor.

However, isolating such a thin base block requires resolving individual \(\log n\)’s. Near height \(n\sim P\),

\[
\log(n+1)-\log n\sim \frac1P.
\]

Thus an \(m\)-space filter selecting \(R+2\) individual frequencies needs length

\[
T\gtrsim P.
\]

That is already nonlocal at ordinary packet scale. If we instead choose a thick block so that the filter is local, then the Wronskian again contains many subset minors.

So base-block prefiltering has the dichotomy

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
|\mathcal B_0|=R+2
&\Rightarrow
\text{single minor, but nonlocal selection},\\
|\mathcal B_0|\gg R
&\Rightarrow
\text{local selection, but subset cancellation remains}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

---

# 6. Coefficient bound for a hypothetically isolated minor

Suppose a minor

\[
S_0=\{n_0,\dots,n_{R+1}\}
\]

is isolated. Its coefficient has the normalized form

\[
\widetilde C_{S_0}(\alpha)
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S_0}c_n\right)
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n(\alpha)\\
1\\
\xi_n\\
\vdots\\
\xi_n^R
\end{pmatrix}_{n\in S_0},
\]

where

\[
r_n(\alpha)=\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n},
\]

and

\[
\xi_n=\lambda\log n
\quad\text{or}\quad
\xi_n=\Delta\log n.
\]

If the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol transversality theorem holds, namely

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{n\in S_0}|r_n(\alpha)-P(\xi_n)|
\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and the normalized nodes are well-conditioned,

\[
\prod_{i<j}|\xi_i-\xi_j|\ge Q^{-C_R},
\]

then

\[
|\widetilde C_{S_0}(\alpha)|
\ge
Q^{-C'}
\prod_{n\in S_0}|c_n|.
\]

So isolated minors are algebraically useful. The obstruction is not the coefficient formula. The obstruction is local isolation.

---

# 7. Conditional filtered-minor theorem

A filtered-minor proof would be valid under the following strong hypotheses.

Assume there exists a subset family \(\mathfrak S_0\) such that:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
\{\Omega_S:S\in\mathfrak S_0\},
\{\Omega_S:S\notin\mathfrak S_0\}
\bigr)
\ge \gamma,
\]

with

\[
\gamma^{-1}\le \lambda Q^C.
\]

Assume also

\[
\left|
\sum_{S\in\mathfrak S_0}
\widetilde C_S(\alpha)e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
\right|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then a packet-local filter \(K\) with support

\[
\operatorname{supp}K\subset[-\lambda Q^C,\lambda Q^C]
\]

can isolate \(\mathfrak S_0\), yielding

\[
|(\mathcal F_K\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R)(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

after canonical error control.

This would imply a filtered Wronskian lower bound.

But the hypotheses are essentially the missing arithmetic theorem in disguised form. In thick subset-product spectra, the required separation condition is not expected.

---

# 8. No-go theorem: packet-local minor isolation

## Statement

Let the active base block contain \(B\gg R\) frequencies \(\log n\), and let

\[
\Omega=\{\Omega_S=\sum_{n\in S}\log n:|S|=R+2\}.
\]

Let \(K\) be an \(m\)-space filter supported on a packet-thickened interval of length

\[
T\le \lambda Q^C.
\]

Then \(K\) cannot isolate a single \(S_0\) unless

\[
\min_{S\neq S_0}|\Omega_S-\Omega_{S_0}|
\gtrsim (\lambda Q^C)^{-1}.
\]

For a thick block, this separation fails for many \(S_0\). Therefore any packet-local filter leaves a cluster

\[
\mathfrak S(S_0)
=
\left\{
S:
|\Omega_S-\Omega_{S_0}|
\lesssim
(\lambda Q^C)^{-1}
\right\}
\]

of active terms. The filtered expression remains

\[
\sum_{S\in\mathfrak S(S_0)}
\widetilde C_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S},
\]

which has no certified sign or lower bound.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-local filtering cannot turn the Wronskian sum into a single-minor lower bound.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Filtered Wronskian/block isolation is not an independent path to Gate 1.}
}
\]

The reason is an uncertainty tradeoff:

\[
\boxed{
\text{resolving subset-product frequencies requires nonlocal filters.}
}
\]

Admissible packet-local filters leave many subset-product terms, so cancellation remains. Polynomial \(\mathcal D\)-filters face the same barrier through derivative degree.

The only surviving route is still the arithmetic determinant/nonrecurrence theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual normalized canonical Wronskian, without relying on local minor isolation.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:11:38)

I’ll focus this round on the direct incidence theorem itself: whether \(Z_\alpha=0\) repels the normalized Wronskian from zero, rather than trying to isolate Wronskian minors.

_Thought for 23s_

## Agent 4 / D — Direct incidence theorem attempt

I am executing the **Agent 4 / D** prompt: attack the direct incidence theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

or diagnose why such a theorem is unavailable. The current coordinator framing identifies this as the core remaining arithmetic incidence problem. 

# 1. Objects

Treat

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\]

as two fixed actual-zeta exponential sums. Schematically,

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
\sum_n z_n(\alpha)e^{-im\log n}
+
\sum_n z_n^\ast(\alpha)e^{+im\log n}
+
Z_{\mathrm{bg}}(m,\alpha)
+
Z_E(m,\alpha),
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_S \widetilde C_S(\alpha)e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error}.
\]

Here

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
|S|=R+2.
\]

The desired incidence theorem is a small-value repulsion statement:

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

At points where \(Z_\alpha(m)=0\), this becomes the required Wronskian lower bound.

---

# 2. Expansion at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero

The normalized Wronskian is

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\det
\bigl(
\mathcal D^\ell G_j
\bigr)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1},
\]

with

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the first entry of the first row vanishes, but the rest of the \(Z_\alpha\)-row remains:

\[
\bigl(
0,\mathcal D Z_\alpha,\mathcal D^2 Z_\alpha,\ldots,\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha
\bigr)(m_0).
\]

Expanding the determinant along the first row gives

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
(-1)^\ell
\mathcal D^\ell Z_\alpha(m_0)
M_\ell(m_0),
\]

where \(M_\ell\) is the corresponding \(q''_{\can}\)-jet minor.

Therefore the direct incidence theorem is equivalent to:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(\mathcal D Z_\alpha,\ldots,\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha),
\operatorname{RowSpan}
(\mathcal D^\ell \mathcal D^j q''_{\can})
\right)
\not\ll Q^{-A}.
}
\]

So \(Z_\alpha=0\) alone is not enough. One also needs derivative-row transversality at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

---

# 3. Expected codimension

There are two cases.

## Case A: fixed \(\alpha\)

If \(\alpha\) is fixed, then \(m\) is the only variable. The equation

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\]

is two real equations in one real variable, so exact zeros are exceptional unless \(Z_\alpha\) has the actual zero-structure built in.

But in the RH setting, admissible off-line centers are precisely selected from such zeros, so one should condition on their existence rather than count codimension naively.

At those zeros, the additional event

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\le\varepsilon
\]

is two further real small-value constraints.

A random model would predict probability roughly

\[
\asymp \varepsilon^2
\]

per admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.

If the number of admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros up to height \(H\) is \(\asymp H\log H\), then the expected number with

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\le Q^{-A}
\]

is roughly

\[
H\log H\cdot Q^{-2A}.
\]

If \(Q\sim \log H\), this is enormous for any fixed \(A\). Thus a random transverse model predicts that polynomially small Wronskian values at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros should occur often.

So a universal polynomial lower bound

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is not supported by generic incidence heuristics.

## Case B: \((m,\alpha)\) both variable

If \((m,\alpha)\) are two real variables, then

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\]

is two real equations in two real variables, giving isolated points generically.

Adding

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\approx0
\]

adds two more real constraints.

The joint event has expected codimension \(4\) in a two-dimensional parameter space. Locally that is unlikely, but globally over very large height it can still recur because the underlying exponential phases explore a high-dimensional torus.

A volume heuristic gives tube-hit probability

\[
\asymp \varepsilon^4
\]

in the two-complex-value space

\[
(Z_\alpha,\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R).
\]

Over parameter area \(\asymp H\cdot A_\alpha\), the expected count is

\[
\asymp H A_\alpha \varepsilon^4.
\]

For

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\qquad Q\sim\log H,
\]

this is again large unless one proves a non-generic arithmetic exclusion.

Thus adding \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) raises codimension, but not enough to yield a polynomial lower bound over the full admissible height range.

---

# 4. Does \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) become forced small near \(Z_\alpha=0\)?

Not structurally.

At \(Z_\alpha=0\),

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
\]

depends on the derivative jet

\[
(\mathcal D Z_\alpha,\ldots,\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha)
\]

and the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet minors. There is no formal determinant identity forcing it to vanish merely because \(Z_\alpha=0\).

However, \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) can become small if the derivative jet of \(Z_\alpha\) lies nearly in the span generated by the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows.

Equivalently, the failure mode is:

\[
\mathcal J_{R+1}[Z_\alpha](m_0)
\approx
\sum_{j=0}^R a_j
\mathcal J_{R+1}[\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}](m_0),
\]

with \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\).

This is precisely the finite-dimensional symbol-dependence/nonrecurrence obstruction already identified by the Wronskian route.

So:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha=0
\text{ does not force }
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=0,
\text{ but it also does not repel it from zero.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Phase-relaxed countermodel

A direct no-go appears in the phase-relaxed model.

Let \(\mathcal P\) be an active prime set and treat

\[
z_p=e^{-im\log p}
\]

as independent phases.

Then

\[
Z_\alpha(z)=
\sum_p a_p(\alpha)z_p+\cdots
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(z,\alpha)
=
\sum_S b_S(\alpha)\prod_{p\in S}z_p+\cdots
\]

are two Laurent polynomials on a high-dimensional torus.

If the number of active phases is \(d\gg R\), then the system

\[
Z_\alpha(z)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(z,\alpha)=0
\]

has real codimension at most \(4\) in a \(d\)-dimensional torus. For \(d\ge5\), solutions are generically expected.

This remains true even if \(Z_\alpha\) contributes genuine symbol rank to the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet system. Symbol rank prevents algebraic redundancy; it does not prevent simultaneous zeros of two independent functions.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The direct incidence theorem is false in the phase-relaxed model.}
}
\]

Any proof must use the actual one-parameter orbit

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\in\mathcal P},
\]

not only finite-dimensional algebra.

---

# 6. One-parameter recurrence model

Now restrict to the actual orbit

\[
z_p(m)=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

The pair

\[
\bigl(Z_\alpha(m),\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\bigr)
\]

is an almost-periodic curve in \(\mathbb C^2\).

If one models its values as equidistributed at scale \(\varepsilon\), then the expected recurrence time to

\[
|Z_\alpha|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\le\varepsilon
\]

is roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-4}.
\]

For

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

this recurrence time is

\[
Q^{4A}.
\]

That is polynomial in \(Q\), far below the typical admissible height range when \(Q\sim\log m\).

This is only a heuristic, but it cuts against the desired implication. It suggests that simultaneous polynomial smallness of two independent exponential sums should not be rare enough to exclude by recurrence alone.

If instead one conditions on exact zeros of \(Z_\alpha\), then the expected spacing of zeros is about \((\log m)^{-1}\), and the values of \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) sampled at those zeros should still occasionally be \(Q^{-A}\)-small unless there is arithmetic repulsion.

Thus the direct incidence theorem requires a special mechanism beyond codimension.

---

# 7. Possible positive theorem: derivative repulsion at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros

The strongest plausible positive theorem is not the raw incidence theorem. It is a derivative transversality theorem.

## Candidate theorem

Let \(m_0,\alpha\) be admissible and satisfy

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Assume:

1. **Simple zero / derivative lower bound**

   \[
   \max_{1\le \ell\le R+1}
   |\mathcal D^\ell Z_\alpha(m_0)|
   \ge Q^{-A_1}.
   \]

2. **Jet-row distance**

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   \mathcal J_{1:R+1}[Z_\alpha](m_0),
   \operatorname{Span}
   \{
   \mathcal J_{1:R+1}[\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}](m_0)
   :0\le j\le R
   \}
   \right)
   \ge Q^{-A_2}.
   \]

3. **Minor conditioning**

   Some \(q''_{\can}\)-jet minor obeys

   \[
   |M_\ell(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A_3}.
   \]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This theorem is basically linear algebra and is plausible.

But the hard hypotheses are exactly the missing arithmetic content. In particular, hypothesis 2 is a normalized Wronskian nonrecurrence statement in derivative coordinates.

---

# 8. Small-value repulsion theorem: obstruction

A direct theorem

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

cannot be expected for generic exponential sums because almost-periodicity produces simultaneous small values at polynomial scales over long intervals.

The only ways it could hold are:

1. **Shared arithmetic obstruction**

   The actual coefficients impose a rigid relation excluding the joint small-value locus.

2. **Hidden positivity**

   \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) has a sign or monotonicity structure on \(Z_\alpha=0\).

3. **Resultant lower bound**

   \(Z_\alpha\) and \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) have a nonzero exponential-polynomial resultant with an effective lower bound.

4. **Zero-repulsion identity**

   At zeros of \(Z_\alpha\), the Wronskian reduces to an explicitly nonzero curvature/torsion quantity.

Currently none of these mechanisms is established. In particular, the subset-product determinant expansion has no visible sign, dominance, or positivity.

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The direct incidence theorem is not supported by generic codimension or recurrence heuristics.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It is false in the phase-relaxed model.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{On the actual one-parameter orbit, polynomial-scale simultaneous smallness appears too cheap unless actual zeta arithmetic supplies a special exclusion.}
}
\]

The best replacement theorem is conditional derivative transversality:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
+
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathcal J[Z_\alpha],
\operatorname{Span}\mathcal J[q''_{\can}]
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

But that is essentially a restatement of the normalized Wronskian bottleneck.

## Final Agent 4 conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{Direct incidence does not currently provide an independent route to Gate 1.}
}
\]

The route remains Yellow and reduces to a hard actual-zeta arithmetic repulsion theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros must repel the normalized canonical Wronskian from }0.
}
\]

No local algebra, codimension count, or generic exponential-sum argument proves that repulsion.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:16:57)

_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 4 / D — Incidence via derivative transversality at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros

Executing the assigned **Agent 4 / D** task: expand the normalized/basis-normalized Wronskian at \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\), test whether derivative transversality can prove the incidence theorem, and diagnose countermodels. 

# 1. Normalized Wronskian at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero

Let

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=B_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R,
\]

where \(B_j(\mathcal D)\) are the basis-normalized jet operators, for example discrete-orthonormal, Chebyshev, or another stable polynomial basis in \(\mathcal D\). Let the column operators be

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D),
\qquad
0\le \ell\le R+1.
\]

Then the basis-normalized Wronskian is

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det
\left(
C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)
\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1}.
\]

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

if \(C_0=1\), then the first entry of the first row vanishes:

\[
C_0G_0(m_0)=Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Expanding along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row gives

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
\,M_\ell(m_0),
\]

where

\[
M_\ell(m_0)
=
\det
\left(
C_{\ell'}(\mathcal D)G_j(m_0)
\right)_{
1\le j\le R+1,\ 
0\le \ell'\le R+1,\ \ell'\ne \ell
}.
\]

In vector form,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\left\langle
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),
\mathbf M(m_0)
\right\rangle,
\]

with

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left(
-C_1Z_\alpha,
C_2Z_\alpha,
\ldots,
(-1)^{R+1}C_{R+1}Z_\alpha
\right)(m_0,\alpha),
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M
=
(M_1,\ldots,M_{R+1})(m_0).
\]

Thus the incidence theorem reduces to proving that this pairing cannot be too small:

\[
\left|
\left\langle
\mathbf z',
\mathbf M
\right\rangle
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

---

# 2. Conditional derivative-transversality theorem

A clean conditional theorem is available.

## Theorem candidate

Assume \(m_0,\alpha\) are admissible and

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Assume the following three bounds.

### A. \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative nondegeneracy

\[
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|
\ge Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\max_{1\le \ell\le R+1}
|C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-A_1}.
\]

### B. Minor nondegeneracy

\[
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

### C. Angle / transversality lower bound

\[
\frac{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
}{
\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|
}
\ge Q^{-A_3}.
\]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-(A_1+A_2+A_3)}.
\]

This gives the desired incidence theorem with

\[
A=A_1+A_2+A_3.
\]

The theorem is algebraically valid. The hard part is proving A–C for the actual canonical object.

---

# 3. Does zero simplicity imply the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative lower bound?

Only partially.

If \(m_0\) is a simple zero of \(Z_\alpha\), then

\[
\partial_m Z_\alpha(m_0)\ne0.
\]

Therefore, for \(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\),

\[
\mathcal D Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\lambda Z_\alpha'(m_0)
\ne0.
\]

But simplicity gives nonvanishing, not a polynomial lower bound.

The needed estimate is

\[
|\mathcal D Z_\alpha(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This requires an effective lower bound on the derivative at zeros. Such a bound is not automatic. In the presence of nearby zeros or high local flatness, one can have

\[
|Z_\alpha'(m_0)|
\]

very small. A standard analytic argument using Cauchy estimates gives upper bounds, but lower bounds require zero-spacing or simplicity with quantitative separation.

A plausible sufficient condition is:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(m_0,\mathcal Z_\alpha\setminus\{m_0\})
\ge Q^{-C}\lambda
\]

plus a local upper/lower normalization of \(Z_\alpha\). Then Jensen/Cauchy-type arguments can yield

\[
\max_{1\le \ell\le R+1}
|\mathcal D^\ell Z_\alpha(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But without quantitative zero separation, simplicity alone is too weak.

So:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha\text{ simple}
\not\Rightarrow
\max_{\ell}|\mathcal D^\ell Z_\alpha|\ge Q^{-A}
\text{ by itself.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Do the minors \(M_\ell\) have sign, dominance, or conditioning?

No sign or dominance is visible.

Each minor \(M_\ell\) is itself a basis-normalized Wronskian minor built from the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows. Its Cauchy–Binet expansion has the form

\[
M_\ell(m)
=
\sum_{S}
C_{S,\ell}e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error}.
\]

The coefficients \(C_{S,\ell}\) may be basis-conditioned and individually nontrivial, but the subset-product phases still oscillate.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{basis conditioning gives good coefficients, not pointwise non-cancellation.}
}
\]

A lower bound

\[
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is itself a smaller Wronskian/nonrecurrence theorem for the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet system. It is easier than the full determinant only if one can prove that at least one \(q''_{\can}\)-minor is protected by a source/curvature identity. No such identity is currently identified.

The angle condition

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|
\]

is even harder. It is a genuine incidence/nonalignment statement between the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative row and the \(q''_{\can}\)-minor vector.

---

# 5. Phase-relaxed countermodel at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero

The derivative-transversality route fails in the phase-relaxed model.

Let the active prime phases be independent variables

\[
u_p=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Then

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=\sum_p z_p(\alpha)u_p+\cdots
\]

and the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows are

\[
J_j(u)=\sum_p c_p \phi_j(x_p)u_p+\cdots.
\]

The conditions

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0
\]

are two complex equations on a high-dimensional torus. For sufficiently many active primes, the solution set is expected to be nonempty.

More concretely, impose:

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\]

and require the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative vector to lie in the bad hyperplane:

\[
\langle \mathbf z'(u),\mathbf M(u)\rangle=0.
\]

These are four real scalar constraints. With \(d\gg R\) active phases, the relaxed phase space has dimension \(d\), so the constraint set is generically positive-dimensional.

Even if the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol has genuine rank relative to the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols, this only prevents row redundancy. It does not prevent the derivative row from aligning accidentally with the minor vector at some phase point.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative transversality is false in the phase-relaxed model.}
}
\]

The actual one-parameter orbit must be used.

---

# 6. One-parameter recurrence diagnosis

Restrict now to the true orbit

\[
u_p(m)=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

At \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, the value

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m,\alpha),\mathbf M(m)\rangle
\]

is a scalar observable sampled along the zero set of another exponential sum.

A generic transverse model predicts no deterministic polynomial lower bound. If \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros have density roughly polynomial in \(Q\) over the relevant height range, and if the normalized Wronskian values are distributed with a smooth density near zero, then values

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\le Q^{-A}
\]

should occur for arbitrarily large heights.

Thus a theorem of the form

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

requires special arithmetic repulsion, not generic transversality.

Possible special mechanisms would be:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&\text{a resultant identity between }Z_\alpha\text{ and }\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R,\\
&\text{a zero-repulsion law for the actual zeta AFE coefficients},\\
&\text{a sign/positivity identity for }\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle,\\
&\text{or a source-curvature conservation law at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

None is currently established.

---

# 7. Refined incidence theorem candidate

The most honest theorem candidate is conditional.

## Conditional incidence theorem

Let \(m_0,\alpha\) be admissible, with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Suppose:

1. **Quantitative simple zero**

   \[
   \max_{1\le\ell\le R+1}
   |C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|
   \ge Q^{-A_1}.
   \]

2. **Basis-normalized \(q''_{\can}\)-minor lower bound**

   \[
   \|\mathbf M(m_0)\|
   \ge Q^{-A_2}.
   \]

3. **Actual arithmetic angle bound**

   \[
   \operatorname{angle}
   \bigl(
   \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),
   \mathbf M(m_0)
   \bigr)
   \ge Q^{-A_3}.
   \]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is a valid bridge from derivative transversality to the Wronskian lower bound.

But hypothesis 3 is the core unsolved incidence theorem in another form.

---

# 8. No-go diagnosis

The derivative-row expansion is useful because it identifies exactly what must be proved:

\[
\boxed{
\text{At }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros, the }Z_\alpha\text{ derivative jet must not align with the }q''_{\can}\text{ minor vector.}
}
\]

However:

\[
\boxed{
\text{simplicity of }Z_\alpha\text{ gives only nonzero derivative, not polynomial size;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{basis-normalized minors have no visible sign/dominance;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{phase-relaxed models allow derivative-row alignment;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{generic one-parameter recurrence does not rule out polynomial smallness.}
}
\]

Therefore the derivative-transversality route does **not** yet prove the incidence theorem. It converts the problem into a sharper arithmetic nonalignment theorem.

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative expansion at }Z_\alpha=0\text{ is structurally correct and useful.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It gives a clean conditional theorem: derivative size + minor size + angle bound }\Rightarrow\text{ Wronskian lower bound.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{But the required angle bound is precisely the missing actual-zeta arithmetic incidence theorem.}
}
\]

So this lane remains **Yellow**. It clarifies the target but does not independently close Gate 1.
