## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:38:10)

_Thought for 11s_

## Agent 4 / D — Incidence theorem at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros on packet-frequency blocks

Executing the **Agent 4 / D** instruction from the latest prompt: test the actual incidence theorem using packet-frequency active blocks satisfying \(\lambda\log n\asymp 1\), not low-prime plateau blocks. The correction from the prior round is that low-prime blocks are useful for symbol-rank sanity checks but likely fail as determinant blocks because \(x_p=\lambda\log p\ll1\) at ordinary scale.  The operative Agent 4 task is to expand the packet-frequency basis-normalized Wronskian at \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\), then test derivative size, minor size, and angle/nonalignment. 

# 1. Packet-frequency basis-normalized Wronskian

Use an active block \(\mathcal B_{\mathrm{pf}}\) satisfying

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp 1.
\]

For ordinary packet scale,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp 1,
\]

this means

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

Let

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

or, for the dual/folded branch,

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n},
\]

up to the convention used in the exact AFE.

Choose stable basis-normalized column operators

\[
C_0(\mathcal D),C_1(\mathcal D),\ldots,C_{R+1}(\mathcal D),
\]

with

\[
C_0(\mathcal D)=1,
\]

and with \(C_\ell\) corresponding to a stable polynomial basis on the packet-frequency node set. Define rows

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\Phi_j(\mathcal D)q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R,
\]

where \(\Phi_j\) is another stable basis choice, or simply \(\Phi_j(\mathcal D)=\mathcal D^j\) if only the column basis is normalized.

Then

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det
\left(
C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)
\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1}.
\]

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the first entry of the first row vanishes:

\[
C_0(\mathcal D)G_0(m_0)=Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Expanding along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row gives

\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
M_\ell(m_0)
}
\]

where

\[
M_\ell(m_0)
=
\det
\left(
C_{\ell'}(\mathcal D)G_j(m_0)
\right)_{
1\le j\le R+1,\ 
0\le \ell'\le R+1,\ \ell'\ne\ell
}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle,
\]

with

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left(
(-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
\right)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M=(M_1,\ldots,M_{R+1}).
\]

Thus the incidence theorem is exactly a derivative-row/minor-vector nonalignment theorem.

---

# 2. What packet-frequency blocks improve

Packet-frequency blocks fix one real defect of low-prime blocks.

For low primes,

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\ll1,
\]

so the normalized nodes are compressed and rank-\(R\) determinants become ill-conditioned or effectively low-rank.

For packet-frequency blocks,

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

and the block can have diameter

\[
\operatorname{diam}\{x_n:n\in\mathcal B_{\mathrm{pf}}\}
\gtrsim R^{-C}
\]

if the AFE support supplies a sufficiently thick \(n\)-range.

Therefore packet-frequency blocks improve:

\[
\boxed{
\text{node spread, basis conditioning, and determinant coefficient size.}
}
\]

They also make the operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) genuinely order-\(\ell\) probes rather than nearly degenerate low-frequency probes.

So packet-frequency blocks are the correct place to build the Wronskian determinant.

But they do **not** by themselves solve the incidence problem. They improve the algebraic conditioning of \(\mathbf z'\) and \(\mathbf M\), not the arithmetic angle

\[
\frac{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
}{
\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|
}.
\]

---

# 3. Derivative size of \(Z_\alpha\) at its zero

The desired estimate is

\[
\max_{1\le\ell\le R+1}
|C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Simplicity alone gives only

\[
Z_\alpha'(m_0)\ne0.
\]

It does **not** give

\[
|\mathcal D Z_\alpha(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A quantitative statement needs local zero separation or local amplitude normalization.

A plausible lemma is:

## Quantitative zero-derivative lemma

Let

\[
H(x)=Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda x).
\]

Assume:

1. \(H(0)=0\);
2. \(H\) is analytic in \(|x|\le r\), with

   \[
   \sup_{|x|\le r}|H(x)|\le Q^{A_0};
   \]

3. there is a point \(|x_1|\le r/2\) such that

   \[
   |H(x_1)|\ge Q^{-A_1};
   \]

4. \(H\) has no other zero in \(|x|\le \delta\), with

   \[
   \delta\ge Q^{-A_2}.
   \]

Then for some \(1\le\ell\le R+1\),

\[
|C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-A_3}.
\]

This is essentially Jensen/Cauchy plus stable-basis norm equivalence.

But the assumptions are nontrivial. In particular, the needed local non-tiny amplitude and quantitative zero separation are not consequences of \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) alone.

So the best current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency blocks make derivative lower bounds plausible, but still require quantitative simplicity/separation.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Minor-vector lower bound

The needed estimate is

\[
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Packet-frequency blocks help at the **coefficient** level.

For a packet-frequency minor \(S\), the basis-normalized Cauchy–Binet coefficient has schematic form

\[
\widetilde C_S
=
\left(\prod_{n\in S}c_n\right)
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
r_n(\alpha)\\
\phi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\phi_R(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\phi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\phi_{R+1}(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

On packet-frequency nodes, a stable basis can make

\[
\left|
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\phi_0(x_n)\\
\vdots\\
\phi_{R+1}(x_n)
\end{pmatrix}
\right|
\]

lose at most

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

If the two-branch symbol residual satisfies

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then at least one minor coefficient should be

\[
|\widetilde C_S|\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

after amplitude normalization.

However, \(\mathbf M(m_0)\) is a pointwise exponential sum over subset-products:

\[
M_\ell(m_0)
=
\sum_S C_{S,\ell}e^{-im_0\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error}.
\]

The coefficient lower bound does not prevent cancellation. Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency blocks can give good minor coefficients, but not pointwise minor lower bounds.}
}
\]

A pointwise estimate

\[
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is already a nonrecurrence theorem for the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet minors.

---

# 5. Angle/nonalignment bound

Even if we had

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

we still need

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A_3}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|.
\]

This is the real incidence theorem.

Packet-frequency blocks improve this only insofar as they make the symbol map nondegenerate. They do not prevent accidental alignment:

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)\perp \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha).
\]

At the exact bad event,

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0,
\]

i.e.

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)=0.
\]

There is no visible sign, positivity, dominance, or monotonicity in this pairing.

So a successful proof would need an actual-zeta arithmetic theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{angle}
\left(
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

That theorem is not supplied by packet-frequency localization alone.

---

# 6. Phase-relaxed countermodel with packet-frequency nodes

The incidence theorem still fails in the phase-relaxed model, even with packet-frequency nodes.

Let \(\mathcal B_{\mathrm{pf}}\) be a packet-frequency block with

\[
|\mathcal B_{\mathrm{pf}}|=B\gg R.
\]

Treat

\[
u_n=e^{-im\log n}
\]

as independent torus variables.

Then

\[
Z_\alpha(u)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_{\mathrm{pf}}}z_n(\alpha)u_n
+
\text{dual/background},
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)
=
\sum_S \widetilde C_S(\alpha)\prod_{n\in S}u_n
+
\text{dual/background}.
\]

The equations

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0
\]

are two complex equations, i.e. four real constraints, on a high-dimensional torus.

For \(B\ge5\), a phase-relaxed solution is generically expected. With \(B\gg R\), there is ample freedom.

This remains true even if:

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

the basis conditioning is healthy, and the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol has genuine rank.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency blocks do not remove the phase-relaxed countermodel.}
}
\]

The actual one-parameter orbit

\[
m\mapsto(e^{-im\log n})_{n\in\mathcal B_{\mathrm{pf}}}
\]

must be used.

---

# 7. One-parameter recurrence diagnosis

On the true orbit, the simultaneous event is

\[
Z_\alpha(m)\approx0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\approx0.
\]

A generic recurrence heuristic says this event is not rare enough to be excluded at polynomial scale over large height ranges.

If both are complex-valued observables with smooth local distributions, then

\[
|Z_\alpha|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\le\varepsilon
\]

has probability roughly

\[
\varepsilon^4.
\]

For

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

the recurrence time is roughly

\[
Q^{4A},
\]

which is far below the height range if \(Q\sim\log m\).

Conditioning on exact zeros of \(Z_\alpha\), the sampled values

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
\]

should still hit \(Q^{-A}\)-small scales unless there is special arithmetic repulsion.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{generic one-parameter recurrence does not prove the incidence theorem.}
}
\]

It actually suggests that the raw statement may be too strong unless admissibility imposes an additional structure not yet encoded.

---

# 8. Conditional incidence theorem

The viable theorem is conditional.

## Packet-frequency derivative-transversality theorem

Let \(m_0,\alpha\) be admissible with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Assume the Wronskian is built on packet-frequency blocks satisfying

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp1
\]

and has stable basis conditioning. Suppose:

1. **Quantitative \(Z_\alpha\)-zero nonflatness**

   \[
   \|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|
   =
   \left(
   \sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
   |C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|^2
   \right)^{1/2}
   \ge Q^{-A_1}.
   \]

2. **Minor-vector nonflatness**

   \[
   \|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A_2}.
   \]

3. **Arithmetic angle bound**

   \[
   |\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
   \ge
   Q^{-A_3}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|.
   \]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-(A_1+A_2+A_3)}.
\]

This proves the incidence theorem and hence supports the Wronskian route to finite-jet anti-design.

But conditions 2 and 3 remain hard actual-zeta nonrecurrence/repulsion statements.

---

# 9. Strong no-go diagnosis

Packet-frequency blocks repair the **rank geometry** but not the **incidence arithmetic**.

They fix:

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\ll1
\]

by enforcing

\[
x_n\asymp1.
\]

They plausibly give:

\[
\text{healthy basis conditioning}
\]

and

\[
\text{nontrivial symbol residuals}.
\]

But they do not provide:

\[
\text{minor pointwise non-cancellation}
\]

or

\[
\text{angle repulsion at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency localization is necessary for the Wronskian route, but not sufficient.}
}
\]

The remaining theorem is still:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual one-parameter zeta phase orbit and full canonical object.

# 10. Final Agent 4 verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Incidence on packet-frequency blocks remains Yellow.}
}
\]

The improved block choice removes the low-prime determinant-rank defect, but the same obstruction remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no known arithmetic angle/nonalignment theorem at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros.}
}
\]

A proof must now target one of the following exact subtheorems:

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{angle}(\mathbf z',\mathbf M)\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

at admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, using actual zeta arithmetic rather than phase-relaxed or generic recurrence heuristics.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:41:51)

_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 4 / D — Direct packet-frequency incidence theorem

Executing the assigned **Agent 4 / D** attack: test the direct incidence theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

for **ordinary-scale packet-frequency blocks**

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<1/2,
\]

with

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\asymp R^{-1}.
\]

This follows the latest coordinator instruction for Agent 4. 

---

# 1. Two exponential sums on the actual one-parameter orbit

On the packet-frequency block, write the main schematic forms as

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}
z_n(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}
+
\text{dual}+
\text{background}+
\text{error},
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{S}
\widetilde C_S(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\text{dual}+
\text{background}+
\text{error},
\]

where

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
|S|=R+2.
\]

The packet-frequency correction improves the determinant geometry because

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1
\]

rather than \(x_n\ll1\). Thus the basis-normalized coefficients \(\widetilde C_S\) can plausibly have polynomially visible size, assuming the two-branch \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol residual holds.

But the incidence theorem is not a coefficient theorem. It is a **pointwise non-cancellation theorem** along

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log n})_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}.
\]

---

# 2. Recurrence / codimension cost of the joint small-value event

The joint bad event is

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

Treating these as two complex-valued observables, the naive codimension is four real constraints. A generic small-ball heuristic gives probability

\[
\asymp Q^{-4A}
\]

at polynomial scale.

Therefore the expected recurrence time is

\[
T_{\rm rec}\asymp Q^{4A}.
\]

If \(Q\sim \log m\), this is far smaller than the global height budget available to the one-parameter orbit. Thus codimension alone does **not** support a universal lower bound

\[
|Z_\alpha|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Conditioning on exact zeros of \(Z_\alpha\) does not fix this. At \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, one samples the scalar sequence

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_j,\alpha),
\qquad
Z_\alpha(m_j)=0.
\]

Unless those sampled values have arithmetic repulsion from zero, one expects polynomially small values to occur.

So the recurrence/codimension verdict is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency block structure does not by itself raise recurrence cost enough.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Phase-relaxed model remains a countermodel

Even with healthy packet-frequency nodes, the phase-relaxed model still permits simultaneous vanishing.

Let

\[
u_n=e^{-im\log n}
\]

be independent phases. Then

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=\sum_n z_n u_n+\cdots
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u)
=
\sum_S \widetilde C_S \prod_{n\in S}u_n+\cdots
\]

are two Laurent polynomials on a high-dimensional torus.

The system

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u)=0
\]

has four real equations. Since

\[
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}|\gg R,
\]

there are many more phase variables than constraints. Thus the phase-relaxed solution set is generically nonempty, even if:

\[
\rho_{\rm rank}\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\kappa_{\rm basis}\le Q^{C},
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x)\gtrsim R^{-C}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{packet-frequency localization repairs rank, but not incidence.}
}
\]

Any proof must use the actual one-parameter prime-log orbit, not just finite-dimensional phase geometry.

---

# 4. Algebraic dependence / resultant route

A possible direct proof would be an effective exponential-polynomial resultant:

\[
\operatorname{Res}
\left(
Z_\alpha,
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
\right)
\ne0
\]

with a polynomial lower bound on common small values along the actual orbit.

The desired form would be:

## Candidate resultant theorem

For admissible \(m,\alpha\), ordinary packet scale, and packet-frequency blocks,

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently, \(Z_\alpha\) and \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) have no common \(Q^{-A}\)-approximate zero along the actual orbit.

To prove this, one would need at least one of:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&\text{effective lower bound for a finite exponential-polynomial resultant},\\
&\text{zero-repulsion identity for }Z_\alpha\text{ and the Wronskian},\\
&\text{sign/phase rigidity in }\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\text{ at }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros},\\
&\text{or an explicit formula forcing prime/dual imbalance at joint small values.}
\end{aligned}
}
\]

No such mechanism is currently visible.

The subset-product frequencies

\[
\log N_S
\]

are numerous and have no apparent sign structure. Basis normalization controls coefficient conditioning but does not create positivity.

Thus the resultant route remains only a formal possibility.

---

# 5. Main+dual plus \(B_2\): does it create sign or phase obstruction?

The full canonical object is

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Adding \(B_2\) and the dual block changes the target affine offset and the coefficients in the Wronskian. It may improve rank and reduce fake main-only degeneracies.

But for the direct incidence theorem, the obstruction is stronger: we need to prevent

\[
Z_\alpha(m)\approx0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\approx0.
\]

The gamma/background term \(B_2\) is smooth and deterministic. On packet-frequency blocks, it contributes lower-frequency/background rows, not a sign-definite Wronskian determinant.

The dual block creates additional folded frequencies and may increase symbolic rank, but it also increases the number of oscillatory terms. No sign or dominance follows automatically.

So:

\[
\boxed{
B_2+D_2\text{ help canonical fidelity and may help rank, but do not currently give incidence repulsion.}
}
\]

A possible theorem would be:

\[
Z_\alpha=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\overline{P_2}D_2
\right)
\text{ or another main-dual commutator is } \ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But no such commutator identity has been derived.

---

# 6. Expansion at \(Z_\alpha=0\)

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the Wronskian has the expansion

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\,M_\ell(m_0).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

Packet-frequency blocks improve the conditioning of \(\mathbf M\), because \(x_n\asymp1\). They may also improve the size of \(\mathbf z'\), because \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) probes genuinely separated packet frequencies.

But the direct theorem still requires three lower bounds:

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A_3}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|.
\]

The first may follow from quantitative simplicity or local zero separation.

The second is a minor-vector nonrecurrence theorem.

The third is the actual arithmetic angle/incidence theorem.

Thus direct incidence decomposes as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero derivative size}
+
\text{minor-vector size}
+
\text{angle nonalignment}.
}
\]

At present, the last two are still open.

---

# 7. Direct theorem candidate

The strongest defensible theorem candidate is conditional.

## Conditional packet-frequency incidence theorem

Assume ordinary scale:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) be the basis-normalized canonical Wronskian built from packet-frequency blocks

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le\log n\le cQ+Q/R\}.
\]

Suppose:

1. **Two-branch symbol rank**

   \[
   \inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
   \max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
   |r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
   \ge Q^{-C_1}.
   \]

2. **Quantitative zero derivative**

   \[
   \max_{1\le \ell\le R+1}
   |C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)|
   \ge Q^{-C_2}
   \]

   whenever \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\).

3. **Minor-vector lower bound**

   \[
   \|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-C_3}.
   \]

4. **Arithmetic angle bound**

   \[
   |\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
   \ge Q^{-C_4}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|.
   \]

Then

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This would imply finite-jet anti-design and hence Gate 1.

But assumptions 3 and 4 are essentially the remaining arithmetic incidence theorem.

---

# 8. No-go diagnosis

The direct incidence theorem does **not** follow from:

\[
\text{packet-frequency node spread},
\]

\[
\text{basis-normalized conditioning},
\]

\[
\text{two-branch symbol rank},
\]

\[
\text{generic codimension},
\]

or

\[
\text{large-sieve/average lower bounds}.
\]

These ingredients make the Wronskian algebra well-posed, but they do not rule out pointwise simultaneous smallness.

The key obstruction remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{simultaneous small values of two actual exponential sums along the prime-log orbit.}
}
\]

Generic recurrence suggests polynomial smallness should occur unless actual zeta arithmetic imposes special repulsion.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No direct incidence proof yet.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet-frequency blocks are necessary and correct, but not sufficient.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The theorem remains plausible only if actual zeta arithmetic supplies a nonalignment/repulsion law.}
}
\]

The next useful mathematical targets are therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|
}
\]

at admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, for the full canonical \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) system.

## Agent 4 / D — Arithmetic angle/nonalignment at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros

Executing the assigned Agent 4 task: attack the angle/nonalignment subclaim

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|
\]

at admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, using ordinary packet-frequency blocks and the full canonical main+dual AFE structure. The current prompt identifies this as the hardest remaining subclaim and asks for either an arithmetic angle theorem candidate or a no-go showing equivalence to the full incidence theorem. 

---

# 1. Setup at a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero

At

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the basis-normalized Wronskian expands as

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle,
\]

where

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\bigl((-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\bigr)_{\ell=1}^{R+1},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M=(M_1,\ldots,M_{R+1})
\]

is the cofactor/minor vector built from the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows.

The desired angle bound is

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|\,\|\mathbf M\|.
}
\]

Together with

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\qquad
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

this gives

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and hence the incidence theorem.

---

# 2. AFE-symbol expressions

On an ordinary packet-frequency block,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\]

we have

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\asymp1.
\]

For the dual branch,

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n},
\]

up to the exact convention of the smoothed AFE.

The \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative vector has schematic main+dual form

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)
\mathbf c(x_n^+)
e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)
\mathbf c(x_n^-)
e^{+im_0\log n}
+
\mathbf z_{\rm bg}
+
\mathbf z_E,
\]

where

\[
\mathbf c(x)
=
(C_1(-ix),\ldots,C_{R+1}(-ix)).
\]

The minor vector has exterior-product structure:

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S(m_0,\alpha)
e^{-im_0\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/mixed/background/error},
\]

with

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

Thus the angle pairing is itself a higher-degree exponential sum:

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\sum_{n,S}
B_{n,S}(\alpha,m_0)
e^{-im_0\log(nN_S)}
+
\text{dual/mixed/background/error}.
\]

This is exactly the basis-normalized Wronskian expansion.

Therefore the angle theorem is not a separate local-geometric statement. It is the subset-product Wronskian nonrecurrence theorem in cofactor coordinates.

---

# 3. Search for structural mechanisms

## 3.1 Resultant mechanism

A possible route would be an effective resultant-type theorem:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\langle\mathbf z'(m_0),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle\ne0
\]

with polynomial separation.

But in the exponential-polynomial setting, non-identical vanishing does not imply a pointwise lower bound. The functions

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\]

can be algebraically independent yet still have approximate common zeros at polynomial scale along long orbits.

A usable resultant theorem would need an **effective actual-orbit exclusion**:

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

That is the original incidence theorem.

So the resultant route currently reformulates the target; it does not reduce it.

---

## 3.2 Zero-repulsion mechanism

A stronger route would prove that zeros of \(Z_\alpha\) repel zeros of the Wronskian:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)\ne0
\]

with quantitative separation.

At the cofactor level this would mean:

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0)
\not\perp
\mathbf M(m_0).
\]

Simplicity of \(Z_\alpha\) only gives

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0)\ne0
\]

or at best, under quantitative zero separation,

\[
\|\mathbf z'(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It says nothing about the angle with \(\mathbf M\).

Thus zero simplicity/separation can contribute to the **size** of \(\mathbf z'\), but not to the **angle** unless one proves an additional arithmetic relation between \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros and \(q''_{\can}\)-minors.

---

## 3.3 Main/dual commutator

One possible nonalignment source is a main/dual commutator. Schematically, if

\[
\mathbf z'=\mathbf z'_+ + \mathbf z'_-,
\qquad
\mathbf M=\mathbf M_+ + \mathbf M_- + \mathbf M_{\rm mix},
\]

then one might hope that

\[
\operatorname{Im}
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\operatorname{Im}
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\]

has a definite sign or polynomial lower bound.

I do not see such a sign. The dual branch improves symbol rank by adding a second folded frequency branch, but it also adds cancellation channels. After gamma-phase folding, the main and dual blocks are oscillatory and of comparable analytic status; they are not positive conjugate pairs in a way that makes the Wronskian pairing sign-definite.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{main/dual coupling may improve rank, but no commutator positivity is currently visible.}
}
\]

---

## 3.4 Euler-product rigidity

A successful Euler-product rigidity theorem would say that the actual coefficients prevent the phase vector

\[
(e^{-im\log n})_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}
\]

from entering the bad incidence set

\[
\{Z_\alpha=0,\ \mathbf z'\perp\mathbf M\}.
\]

This is the correct conceptual route, but it requires a new arithmetic nonrecurrence theorem for the actual prime-log orbit. Generic independence of \(\log p\) does not suffice, because recurrence to finite-codimension tubes is too cheap at polynomial \(Q\)-scale.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Euler-product rigidity is the right type of input, but no concrete theorem is yet available.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Phase-relaxed countermodel

The angle theorem is false in a phase-relaxed model.

Let

\[
u_n=e^{-im\log n}
\]

be independent phases for \(n\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}\). Because

\[
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}|\gg R,
\]

the phase space has many degrees of freedom.

Impose the constraints:

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\]

\[
\|\mathbf z'(u)\|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\|\mathbf M(u)\|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and

\[
\langle\mathbf z'(u),\mathbf M(u)\rangle=0.
\]

The first and last equations are two complex constraints, i.e. four real constraints. The size inequalities are open conditions. In a high-dimensional torus, this system is generically soluble.

Moreover, packet-frequency blocks ensure healthy node spread:

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

so this countermodel is not exploiting the old low-prime compression defect.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank + basis conditioning + size lower bounds do not imply angle nonalignment.}
}
\]

The missing ingredient must be the actual one-parameter arithmetic orbit, not finite-dimensional linear algebra.

---

# 5. One-parameter orbit diagnosis

On the actual orbit,

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n},
\]

the bad angle event at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros is

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0,
\qquad
\langle\mathbf z'(m),\mathbf M(m)\rangle\approx0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\approx0.
\]

This is the original incidence theorem.

A generic recurrence model predicts that simultaneous polynomial smallness of two complex exponential sums should occur unless there is special arithmetic repulsion. Codimension gives probability roughly

\[
Q^{-4A}
\]

for thresholds \(Q^{-A}\), hence recurrence time roughly

\[
Q^{4A},
\]

which is too cheap relative to the height range when \(Q\sim\log m\).

Therefore, an angle theorem cannot be justified by generic recurrence or transversality.

---

# 6. Conditional arithmetic angle theorem

The strongest usable statement is conditional.

## Conditional angle theorem

Assume ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

packet-frequency blocks

\[
cQ\le\log n\le cQ+Q/R,
\]

and safe depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) be the basis-normalized canonical Wronskian for

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Suppose:

1. **Two-branch symbol residual**

   \[
   \inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
   \max_{\pm,n}
   |r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
   \ge Q^{-C_1}.
   \]

2. **Quantitative zero derivative**

   \[
   \|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-C_2}.
   \]

3. **Minor-vector lower bound**

   \[
   \|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-C_3}.
   \]

4. **Actual-orbit angle repulsion**

   \[
   \operatorname{dist}
   \left(
   u(m_0),
   \{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \mathbf z'(u)\perp\mathbf M(u)\}
   \right)
   \ge Q^{-C_4}
   \]

   in the packet-frequency torus metric.

Then

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|,
\]

and hence

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

This is correct, but condition 4 is exactly the arithmetic incidence/nonrecurrence theorem in geometric form.

---

# 7. No-go diagnosis

The angle subclaim cannot be derived from the currently available components.

Known components:

\[
\text{packet-frequency node spread},
\]

\[
\text{basis-normalized conditioning},
\]

\[
\text{two-branch symbol rank},
\]

\[
\text{potential }|\mathbf z'|\text{ lower bound},
\]

\[
\text{potential }|\mathbf M|\text{ lower bound}
\]

do not imply

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|.
\]

The phase-relaxed countermodel survives all of them.

So the conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{angle nonalignment is equivalent, up to size lower bounds, to the full incidence theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Exact arithmetic needed to forbid the countermodel

To make the Wronskian route Green, one needs one of the following genuinely arithmetic inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&\text{1. Effective resultant/zero-repulsion: }
|Z_\alpha|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A};\\
&\text{2. Actual-orbit nonrecurrence: the prime-log orbit avoids }
\{Z_\alpha=0,\mathbf z'\perp\mathbf M\};\\
&\text{3. Main/dual commutator positivity: a sign-definite component of }
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle;\\
&\text{4. Euler-product rigidity: actual coefficients exclude the bad torus incidence.}
\end{aligned}
}
\]

At present, none has been proved.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No independent angle theorem yet.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The angle bound is essentially the incidence theorem in cofactor form.}
}
\]

The Wronskian route remains viable but Yellow. The remaining Green-blocking theorem is still:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the full canonical \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) object on the actual prime-log orbit.

## Agent 4 / D — Main/dual arithmetic obstruction to incidence

Executing the assigned Agent 4 task: test whether **exact main/dual AFE structure** can forbid the bad incidence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)\approx0.
\]

The current prompt explicitly identifies generic recurrence and phase-relaxed models as insufficient, leaving exact main/dual arithmetic as the plausible remaining soft spot. 

---

# 1. Main/dual packet-frequency structure

Work in the ordinary regime:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use packet-frequency main blocks

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<1/2,
\]

so

\[
x_n^+ = \lambda\log n \asymp 1.
\]

The folded dual branch has nodes

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n},
\]

up to the exact normalization convention.

For an AFE near height \(m\), the schematic canonical decomposition is

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)
\sim
\sum_n c_n^+(m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and

\[
D_2(m)
\sim
\sum_n c_n^-(m)e^{+im\log n}
\]

after gamma-phase folding.

Likewise,

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
\sim
\sum_n z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}
+
\sum_n z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n}
+
Z_{\rm bg}
+
Z_E.
\]

The basis-normalized Wronskian is built from

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

Its packet-frequency determinant expansion contains pure-main, pure-dual, and mixed main/dual subset-product terms:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\sum_{S_+} C_{S_+}^{++\cdots +} e^{-im\log N_{S_+}}
+
\sum_{S_-} C_{S_-}^{--\cdots -} e^{+im\log N_{S_-}}
+
\sum_{S_+,S_-} C_{S_+,S_-}^{\rm mix}
e^{-im\log N_{S_+}}
e^{+im\log N_{S_-}}
+
\cdots.
\]

Equivalently, mixed terms have phase

\[
e^{-im\log(N_+/N_-)}.
\]

So the exact main/dual system is not a scalar correction. It is a larger folded frequency system.

---

# 2. Avoiding saddle overlap

The condition

\[
0<c<c_1<1/2
\]

keeps the main packet-frequency block away from the AFE saddle.

If

\[
\log n\sim cQ,
\]

then the folded dual node is roughly

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
\sim Q-cQ
=
(1-c)Q
\]

at conductor scale.

Thus

\[
x_n^+\sim c,
\qquad
x_n^-\sim 1-c,
\]

after \(\lambda Q\asymp1\).

For \(c<1/2\), the two branches are separated:

\[
|x_n^+-x_n^-|
\asymp 1-2c.
\]

This separation is useful for **symbol rank** and **basis conditioning**. It reduces branch degeneracy and makes the two-branch rank condition plausible:

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

But separation alone does not create a sign or phase obstruction.

---

# 3. Does \(Z_\alpha=0\) force main/dual imbalance?

Write

\[
Z_\alpha=Z_+ + Z_- + Z_{\rm bg}+Z_E.
\]

At a zero,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

we have

\[
Z_+(m_0)+Z_-(m_0)
\approx
-Z_{\rm bg}(m_0)-Z_E(m_0).
\]

This is one complex equation coupling the two branches.

A hopeful route would be:

\[
Z_+ + Z_-\approx0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{some main/dual commutator is large}.
\]

For example, define a skew quantity

\[
\mathcal C_{ZD}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\overline{Z_+}Z_-
\right),
\]

or, for the Wronskian pairing,

\[
\mathcal C_{qZ}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\left(
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
\right).
\]

But \(Z_++Z_-\approx0\) does **not** force

\[
\operatorname{Im}(\overline{Z_+}Z_-)
\]

to be large. In fact, if

\[
Z_-\approx -Z_+,
\]

then

\[
\overline{Z_+}Z_-
\approx
-|Z_+|^2
\]

is essentially real, so the imaginary commutator can vanish.

Thus the simplest main/dual skew invariant fails.

---

# 4. Main/dual commutator at derivative level

The next attempt is to use the gamma-phase derivative mismatch.

The main derivative symbols have form

\[
\mathcal D^k e^{-im\log n}
=
(-i\lambda\log n)^k e^{-im\log n}
=
(-ix_n^+)^k e^{-im\log n}.
\]

The folded dual derivative symbols have form

\[
\mathcal D^k e^{+im\log n}
\approx
(+i x_n^-)^k e^{+im\log n}
+
\text{amplitude/gamma derivative terms}.
\]

Since

\[
x_n^+\neq x_n^-,
\]

one can construct branch-separating operators

\[
L_+(\mathcal D),
\qquad
L_-(\mathcal D),
\]

with

\[
L_+ \text{ large on main branch, small on dual branch},
\]

and vice versa.

This may prove that \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank survives and that the jet rows are not formally redundant.

But it still does not imply incidence. The bad event can satisfy both:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)\approx0
\]

because the Wronskian determinant is an oscillatory mixed-branch subset-product sum. Branch separation improves the basis representation; it does not stop phase cancellation.

So derivative mismatch is a **rank tool**, not yet an **angle tool**.

---

# 5. Mixed branch determinant terms

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

Decompose

\[
\mathbf z'=\mathbf z'_+ + \mathbf z'_- + \mathbf z'_{\rm bg}+\mathbf z'_E,
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M
=
\mathbf M_+ + \mathbf M_- + \mathbf M_{\rm mix}
+\mathbf M_{\rm bg}
+\mathbf M_E.
\]

Then

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_{\rm mix}\rangle
\]

\[
+
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_{\rm mix}\rangle
+
\cdots.
\]

The mixed branch terms have phases such as

\[
e^{-im\log(N_+/N_-)}
\]

and therefore introduce additional cancellation channels.

A positive main/dual obstruction would require one of these groups to dominate or have fixed sign. But the coefficient phases include:

1. AFE weight phases;
2. gamma-phase terms;
3. subset-product phases;
4. basis-determinant signs;
5. background/differentiation corrections.

No sign-definite group is visible.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mixed main/dual terms enlarge rank but also enlarge cancellation space.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Candidate obstruction theorem

A plausible theorem would be:

## Main/dual incompatibility theorem

Assume ordinary scale, packet-frequency blocks with \(0<c<c_1<1/2\), safe depth \(R\), and full canonical AFE symbols. Then no admissible \(m_0,\alpha\) can satisfy simultaneously

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)=O(Q^{-A}),
\]

and the healthy-rank/conditioning bounds

\[
\rho_{\rm rank}\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\kappa_{\rm basis}\le Q^C,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x)\gtrsim R^{-C}.
\]

A proof would need to show that folded main/dual coupling forces an imbalance:

\[
\max\{
|\mathcal I_{\rm skew}|,
|\mathcal I_{\rm asym}|,
|\mathcal I_{\rm comm}|
\}
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where possible invariants are:

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm skew}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\operatorname{Im}
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle,
\]

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm asym}
=
\langle \mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
-
\omega(m,\alpha)
\langle \mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle,
\]

or

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm comm}
=
\langle L_+\mathbf z',L_-\mathbf M\rangle
-
\langle L_-\mathbf z',L_+\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

Currently, none of these has a demonstrated sign or lower bound.

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed countermodel with exact branch separation

Even after enforcing packet-frequency branch separation, the obstruction persists in a phase-relaxed model.

Let

\[
u_n^+=e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
u_n^-=e^{+im\log n}
\]

be independent phase variables, or constrained only by conjugacy in a weaker real model.

Impose:

\[
Z_+(u^+)+Z_-(u^-)+Z_{\rm bg}=0,
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u^+,u^-)=0.
\]

These are two complex equations. The number of packet-frequency phase variables is much larger than four real dimensions. Healthy rank and branch separation are open conditions and can be maintained.

Thus the bad incidence survives the branch-separated phase-relaxed model.

The exact one-parameter relation

\[
u_n^-=\overline{u_n^+}
\]

or the more precise gamma-folded relation is the only remaining possible obstruction.

But generic one-parameter recurrence still suggests polynomial smallness is too cheap unless there is special arithmetic.

---

# 8. One-parameter main/dual relation

On the actual orbit, the main and dual phases are not independent. They are tied by

\[
e^{+im\log n}
=
\overline{e^{-im\log n}},
\]

plus gamma-phase/amplitude dependence.

This reduces phase freedom. But does it force nonincidence?

A generic real one-parameter curve

\[
m\mapsto
\left(
Z_\alpha(m),
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\right)
\in\mathbb C^2
\]

can still pass within \(Q^{-A}\) of the origin with recurrence time roughly

\[
Q^{4A}.
\]

That is not large enough to give a universal polynomial lower bound over the available height range.

Therefore the main/dual conjugacy relation alone is probably insufficient. One needs arithmetic rigidity stronger than conjugacy.

---

# 9. No-go diagnosis

The exact main/dual AFE structure currently provides:

\[
\boxed{
\text{better symbol rank and better canonical fidelity.}
}
\]

It does not yet provide:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a sign, dominance, positivity, or phase obstruction to incidence.}
}
\]

Avoiding saddle overlap gives separated branch nodes:

\[
x^+\not\approx x^-,
\]

which helps prevent symbolic degeneracy. But the incidence event is pointwise and oscillatory:

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0.
\]

Branch separation does not rule out that joint event.

So the current conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact dual coupling still shifts the nonrecurrence problem rather than solving it.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Final verdict

No main/dual arithmetic obstruction is presently proved.

The best candidate route is to search for a new invariant of the form

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm comm}
\]

or

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm asym}
\]

with a sign or lower bound forced by gamma-folded branch asymmetry. But absent such an invariant, the main/dual structure only reinforces the already-known requirements:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Thus this lane remains **Yellow** and reduces again to actual arithmetic incidence/nonrecurrence on the one-parameter zeta orbit.
## User (2026-04-26 19:51:43)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:51:53)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 4 / D — Resultant / zero-repulsion formulation of incidence

Executing the assigned Agent 4 task: formulate the incidence theorem as a resultant / zero-repulsion problem and test whether that formulation is genuinely easier than the original actual-orbit nonrecurrence problem. The prompt identifies the current blockers as local \(Z_\alpha\)-zero non-flatness, vector minor nonrecurrence, and especially arithmetic angle/incidence. 

---

# 1. Incidence target

The desired theorem is

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

On ordinary packet-frequency blocks,

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{p:cQ\le \log p\le cQ+Q/R\},
\]

write schematically

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
\sum_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}
a_p(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log p}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_S b_S(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
N_S=\prod_{p\in S}p.
\]

The core question is whether these two actual exponential sums can have a common or near-common zero along the one-parameter orbit

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\in\mathcal B_{\rm pf}}.
\]

---

# 2. Laurent-polynomial resultant formulation

Introduce torus variables

\[
u_p=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

Then the main-branch pieces become Laurent polynomials:

\[
Z_\alpha(u)
=
\sum_p a_p u_p
+
\cdots,
\]

\[
W(u)
:=
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u)
=
\sum_S b_S \prod_{p\in S}u_p
+
\cdots.
\]

A naive resultant would try to eliminate the variables \(u_p\) from

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\qquad
W(u)=0.
\]

But there are many variables:

\[
d=|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}|\gg R,
\]

and only two equations. In the full torus \((\mathbb C^\ast)^d\), two Laurent polynomials generically have a common zero set of dimension \(d-2\).

Thus the multivariable Laurent resultant is not the right object. It will not be nonzero in the sense needed to exclude common zeros.

\[
\boxed{
\text{As Laurent polynomials in independent phase variables, }Z_\alpha\text{ and }W\text{ generically do have common zeros.}
}
\]

So a torus-resultant formulation fails unless it incorporates the actual one-parameter constraint

\[
u_p=e^{-im\log p}.
\]

---

# 3. One-parameter exponential-polynomial resultant

Restricting to the actual orbit gives two exponential polynomials in \(m\):

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=\sum_i a_i e^{-i\omega_i m},
\]

\[
W(m)=\sum_j b_j e^{-i\Omega_j m}.
\]

A one-variable exponential-polynomial resultant would seek a certificate of the form

\[
A(m)Z_\alpha(m)+B(m)W(m)=\mathcal R(m),
\]

where \(\mathcal R\) is bounded below, or ideally constant:

\[
A(m)Z_\alpha(m)+B(m)W(m)=1.
\]

Then

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|W(m)|
\ge
\frac{1}{|A(m)|+|B(m)|}.
\]

If one could construct \(A,B\) with

\[
|A(m)|+|B(m)|\le Q^C,
\]

this would give

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|W(m)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

That would prove the incidence theorem.

But constructing such a Bezout certificate is essentially the same as proving that the actual orbit avoids the joint small-value set. For dense incommensurable frequency systems, the coefficients of such a certificate are expected to be enormous or nonexistent at polynomial scale.

So the useful conditional theorem is:

## Conditional Bezout-resultant theorem

If there exist exponential polynomials \(A,B\), with frequencies drawn from controlled packet-frequency combinations, such that

\[
A Z_\alpha+B\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=1
\]

on the relevant ordinary-scale window, and

\[
\|A\|_\infty+\|B\|_\infty\le Q^C,
\]

then

\[
|Z_\alpha|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is correct but currently empty: producing the controlled Bezout certificate is as hard as the incidence theorem itself.

---

# 4. Differential resultant attempt

Another possible certificate uses derivatives. Let

\[
D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

For ordinary differential polynomials, a common zero with high multiplicity can sometimes be ruled out using a Wronskian. Here one could define a differential resultant from

\[
Z_\alpha,\ DZ_\alpha,\ldots,D^KZ_\alpha
\]

and

\[
W,\ DW,\ldots,D^KW.
\]

But the desired theorem is not merely that \(Z_\alpha\) and \(W\) cannot share a high-multiplicity zero. It is that \(W\) cannot be polynomially small at a simple zero of \(Z_\alpha\).

A differential resultant could prove something like

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=W(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{some higher Wronskian nonzero}.
\]

It does not automatically imply

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|W(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

To get a polynomial lower bound, the differential resultant would need an effective lower bound and a local analytic lower-bound transfer. That again requires actual-orbit nonrecurrence.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a differential resultant may rule out exact algebraic dependence, but not polynomial-scale approximate incidence.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Approximate common zeros

The real obstruction is approximate incidence:

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
|W(m)|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

For two generic complex observables, the small-ball probability is

\[
\asymp Q^{-4A}.
\]

The expected recurrence time is therefore

\[
T_{\rm rec}\asymp Q^{4A}.
\]

Since in the global height problem one usually has

\[
Q\sim \log m,
\]

this recurrence cost is far too cheap to exclude approximate common zeros over large height ranges.

Thus codimension/recurrence heuristics cut against a bare resultant lower bound.

A resultant theorem would need to exploit special arithmetic of the actual coefficients, not just the fact that two exponential polynomials are not symbolically dependent.

---

# 6. Zero-repulsion formulation

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the Wronskian expansion gives

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

Thus a zero-repulsion theorem can be stated as:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\left|
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A more decomposed version is:

\[
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
\|\mathbf M(m_0)\|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

\[
\operatorname{angle}(\mathbf z',\mathbf M)\ge Q^{-A_3}.
\]

This is a clean zero-repulsion formulation. But the third line is the incidence theorem in angle form.

Simplicity or quantitative separation of \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros might prove the first line, but it gives no control on the angle with \(\mathbf M\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero-repulsion is a good formulation, but it does not reduce the arithmetic burden.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed no-go

In the phase-relaxed torus model, choose independent variables \(u_p\). Then the system

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\qquad
W(u)=0
\]

has many degrees of freedom and only two complex equations.

Even imposing healthy diagnostics,

\[
\rho_{\rm rank}\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\kappa_{\rm basis}\le Q^C,
\qquad
\operatorname{diam}(x)\gtrsim R^{-C},
\]

does not prevent common zeros.

So any successful resultant must not be a multivariable phase-space resultant. It must be a one-parameter arithmetic-resultant theorem for the specific orbit

\[
m\mapsto(e^{-im\log p})_p.
\]

That is precisely the missing actual prime-log nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 8. Candidate theorem worth keeping

The strongest useful formulation is:

## Actual-orbit resultant / zero-repulsion theorem

Let

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
\]

and

\[
W(m)=\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
\]

be the full canonical packet-frequency exponential sums, including

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

with healthy two-branch symbol rank and basis conditioning. Then

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|W(m)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for admissible \(m,\alpha\).

Equivalently,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|W(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This theorem would close the Wronskian incidence step.

But it is not presently supported by a known resultant mechanism. It must be proved using actual-zeta arithmetic.

---

# 9. What would make the resultant route genuinely easier?

The resultant route would become useful if one could prove one of the following:

### A. Controlled Bezout certificate

\[
A Z_\alpha+B W=1,
\qquad
\|A\|_\infty+\|B\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]

### B. Effective common-zero exclusion

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,\ W(m_0)=0
\]

is impossible, plus a quantitative Łojasiewicz-type inequality with polynomial constants.

### C. Arithmetic sampling repulsion

For the zero set

\[
\mathcal Z_\alpha=\{m:Z_\alpha(m)=0\},
\]

prove

\[
\min_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_\alpha}|W(m_j)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

### D. Explicit formula obstruction

Show that

\[
Z_\alpha\approx0,
\qquad
W\approx0
\]

forces a prime/dual imbalance contradicting the canonical AFE or explicit formula.

At present, none of A–D is available. C and D are essentially the original incidence theorem.

---

# 10. Final no-go diagnosis

\[
\boxed{
\text{A formal resultant formulation does not currently make the problem easier.}
}
\]

Reasons:

1. In the multivariable torus model, two Laurent polynomials in many variables generically have common zeros.

2. In the one-parameter model, approximate common zeros at polynomial scale are expected by recurrence unless actual arithmetic forbids them.

3. A nonzero resultant only excludes identical/common algebraic factors; it does not yield a polynomial lower bound for approximate common zeros.

4. A controlled Bezout certificate would prove the theorem, but constructing one is equivalent to the missing actual-orbit nonrecurrence.

Therefore the resultant/zero-repulsion route is best treated as a **reformulation** of the incidence theorem, not an independent proof.

Final status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Resultant/zero-repulsion formulation: Yellow, no independent close.}
}
\]

The exact remaining target remains:

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the full canonical actual-zeta packet-frequency system.
## User (2026-04-26 19:54:32)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:54:37)

_Thought for 4s_

## Agent 4 / D — Folded main/dual subset-product arithmetic

Executing the assigned Agent 4 task: search for a genuine folded main/dual arithmetic obstruction in the pairing

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
\]

at \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\). The current prompt asks specifically whether main/dual structure gives a sign, commutator, asymmetry, or phase obstruction, rather than merely improving rank. 

---

# 1. Folded main/dual decomposition

Use the ordinary packet-frequency regime:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

with packet-frequency blocks

\[
\mathcal B_+
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad 0<c<c_1<1/2.
\]

The main branch has normalized nodes

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\asymp c.
\]

The folded dual branch has nodes

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}\asymp 1-c,
\]

up to the exact AFE normalization.

For \(c<c_1<1/2\),

\[
|x_n^- - x_n^+|\asymp 1-2c>0.
\]

So the branches are separated in normalized packet frequency.

Write

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\mathbf z'_+
+
\mathbf z'_-
+
\mathbf z'_{\Gamma}
+
\mathbf z'_E,
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M
=
\mathbf M_+
+
\mathbf M_-
+
\mathbf M_{\rm mix}
+
\mathbf M_{\Gamma}
+
\mathbf M_E.
\]

Then

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_{\rm mix}\rangle
+
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_{\rm mix}\rangle
+
\cdots.
\]

The pure and mixed terms have distinct phase types.

---

# 2. Phase families

The pure-main contribution has phases

\[
e^{-im\log N_+},
\qquad
N_+=\prod_{n\in S_+}n.
\]

The pure-dual contribution has phases

\[
e^{+im\log N_-},
\qquad
N_-=\prod_{n\in S_-}n,
\]

together with gamma/folding phases depending on the exact AFE convention.

The mixed terms have phases

\[
e^{-im\log N_+}e^{+im\log N_-}
=
e^{-im\log(N_+/N_-)}.
\]

With gamma folding included, the mixed phases have schematic form

\[
e^{i\Theta(m)}
e^{-im\log(N_+/N_-)}
\]

or, for terms with several dual factors,

\[
e^{i k\Theta(m)}
e^{-im\log N_+}
e^{+im\log N_-}.
\]

Here \(\Theta(m)\) is the relevant completed gamma phase / saddle phase.

Thus the folded main/dual Wronskian is not a single Dirichlet polynomial but a finite mixture of exponential sums over:

\[
\log N_+,
\qquad
-\log N_-,
\qquad
\log(N_+/N_-),
\qquad
\log(N_+/N_-)-k\Theta'(m)\text{ locally}.
\]

This is structurally richer, but not sign-definite.

---

# 3. Candidate commutator invariants

A natural skew invariant is

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm skew}
=
\operatorname{Im}
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_-\rangle
-
\operatorname{Im}
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_+\rangle.
\]

Another is the asymmetric branch-energy difference

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm asym}
=
\langle\mathbf z'_+,\mathbf M_+\rangle
-
\omega(m,\alpha)
\langle\mathbf z'_-,\mathbf M_-\rangle,
\]

with \(\omega\) chosen from the approximate gamma/AFE branch ratio.

A third is a filtered commutator:

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm comm}
=
\langle L_+\mathbf z',L_-\mathbf M\rangle
-
\langle L_-\mathbf z',L_+\mathbf M\rangle,
\]

where \(L_+\) is large on \(x^+\asymp c\) and small on \(x^-\asymp 1-c\), and \(L_-\) does the reverse.

Because

\[
|x^+-x^-|\asymp1,
\]

a low-degree polynomial filter in \(\mathcal D\) can separate the two branches with cost

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

at the safe depth \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\).

So branch-filtered commutators are analytically feasible.

The problem is not construction. The problem is lower bounding them.

---

# 4. Branch separation gives rank, not sign

Branch separation means the two branches cannot be collapsed into a single degree-\(R\) polynomial model without visible residual:

\[
x^+\asymp c,
\qquad
x^-\asymp 1-c,
\qquad
|x^+-x^-|\asymp1.
\]

This helps prove two-branch symbol rank:

\[
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_{\pm}\max_n
|r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

But the angle/incidence problem is different. It asks for a pointwise lower bound on

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

Even if \(L_+\) and \(L_-\) separate the branches, the filtered pairings

\[
\langle L_+\mathbf z',L_-\mathbf M\rangle,
\qquad
\langle L_-\mathbf z',L_+\mathbf M\rangle
\]

remain oscillatory subset-product sums.

No positivity follows from

\[
x^+\neq x^-.
\]

At best, branch separation says the symbolic rows are independent. It does not say their actual phase sums cannot cancel.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
0<c<c_1<1/2
\text{ gives symbolic transversality, not incidence repulsion.}
}
\]

---

# 5. The \(\alpha\)-asymmetry

The main branch has a factor of the form

\[
e^{-\alpha u},
\qquad u=\log n,
\]

while the folded dual has the conjugate/opposite-side factor schematically

\[
e^{+\alpha u^-},
\qquad u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

In normalized packet-frequency coordinates,

\[
u\sim cQ,
\qquad
u^-\sim (1-c)Q.
\]

So if \(\alpha Q\) is not small, then the branch weights differ strongly:

\[
e^{-\alpha cQ}
\quad\text{versus}\quad
e^{+\alpha(1-c)Q}.
\]

This can create branch imbalance. In that regime, one might prove that either the main branch or the dual branch dominates a specific filtered statistic.

However, the hard regime is

\[
\alpha Q\ll1
\]

or simply

\[
\alpha\to0.
\]

Then

\[
e^{-\alpha u}=1+O(\alpha Q),
\qquad
e^{+\alpha u^-}=1+O(\alpha Q),
\]

so \(\alpha\)-asymmetry disappears at polynomially relevant scale.

In that regime, the only visible non-polynomiality comes from fixed algebraic/logarithmic factors like

\[
x^{-3},
\]

which is enough for symbol rank but not for pointwise angle control.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\alpha\text{-asymmetry may help away from }\alpha Q\ll1,\text{ but it cannot close the uniform theorem.}
}
\]

A possible conditional theorem is:

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge Q^{-\delta}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{branch-imbalance commutator lower bound}.
\]

But the complementary regime

\[
|\alpha|Q<Q^{-\delta}
\]

would still require the original arithmetic incidence theorem.

---

# 6. Search for sign or Hermitian positivity

A sign theorem would need a representation like

\[
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
=
\sum_\nu w_\nu |\mathcal A_\nu|^2
+
\text{small error},
\qquad
w_\nu\ge Q^{-C}>0.
\]

No such representation is visible.

The determinant/cofactor vector \(\mathbf M\) is alternating/exterior in the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows. Its coefficients inherit Vandermonde signs and AFE phases. Mixed main/dual terms introduce ratios \(N_+/N_-\), producing sign-changing or phase-rotating terms.

The pairing is not Hermitian in a natural positive space; it is a determinant expansion.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No sign-definite or positive-energy representation of }
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle
\text{ is currently visible.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Folded subset-product nonrecurrence formulation

The exact main/dual incidence theorem becomes:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\left|
\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal F}
B_\nu(m_0,\alpha)
e^{-im_0\Omega_\nu}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where \(\mathcal F\) contains pure and mixed folded subset frequencies:

\[
\Omega_\nu
\in
\left\{
\log N_+,\,
-\log N_-,\,
\log(N_+/N_-),\,
\log(N_+/N_-)-k\Theta'(m_0),
\ldots
\right\}.
\]

The branch-separated packet-frequency block ensures that the coefficient system is nondegenerate and well-conditioned.

But the lower bound is a pointwise nonrecurrence theorem for a large folded subset-product exponential sum, conditioned on

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

This is strictly more canonical than the main-only version, but not obviously easier.

---

# 8. Phase-relaxed countermodel with folded branches

Even enforcing branch separation and two-branch symbol rank, a phase-relaxed model still breaks the theorem.

Let

\[
u_n^+=e^{-im\log n},
\qquad
u_n^-=e^{+im\log n}
\]

be independent phase variables, initially ignoring conjugacy. Then impose:

\[
Z_+(u^+)+Z_-(u^-)+Z_{\Gamma}=0,
\]

and

\[
\langle\mathbf z'(u^+,u^-),\mathbf M(u^+,u^-)\rangle=0.
\]

These are two complex equations in many phase variables. The healthy rank and conditioning conditions are open conditions, so the solution set should persist.

If one imposes conjugacy

\[
u_n^-=\overline{u_n^+},
\]

the model becomes a real torus problem. But the codimension is still finite, and generic recurrence along a one-parameter prime-log orbit remains too cheap at polynomial scale unless actual arithmetic imposes additional rigidity.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{folded main/dual structure does not defeat the relaxed countermodel.}
}
\]

It only specifies more accurately what the actual-orbit nonrecurrence must forbid.

---

# 9. Candidate theorem if a commutator is found

The best possible theorem in this lane would have the following shape.

## Conditional folded commutator theorem

Assume ordinary packet scale, packet-frequency blocks with \(0<c<c_1<1/2\), safe depth \(R\), and full canonical \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\). Suppose there exists a branch-filtered invariant

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm comm}(m,\alpha)
\]

such that:

1. It is a component or controlled linear projection of the Wronskian pairing:

   \[
   |\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
   \ge Q^{-C}|\mathcal I_{\rm comm}|
   -
   \text{controlled error}.
   \]

2. At \(Z_\alpha(m)=0\),

   \[
   |\mathcal I_{\rm comm}(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-C}.
   \]

Then

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No such invariant has been identified.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Final verdict

The folded main/dual arithmetic analysis gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{better canonical structure, branch separation, and symbol-rank control.}
}
\]

But it does **not** currently give:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a sign, positivity, dominance, or commutator lower bound.}
}
\]

The \(\alpha\)-asymmetry can help only away from the hard regime \(\alpha Q\ll1\). Branch separation helps only with rank, not pointwise incidence.

Therefore the exact folded main/dual problem still reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual folded subset-product nonrecurrence conditioned on }Z_\alpha(m)=0.
}
\]

So the answer for this lane is a no-go in the requested sense:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact main/dual coupling still reduces to actual subset-product nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

The Wronskian route remains structurally viable but arithmetically open.

## Agent 4 / D — Explicit-formula / prime-side obstruction to simultaneous \(Z_\alpha\)-zero and Wronskian smallness

Executing the assigned Agent 4 task: attack the bad event

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)\approx0
\]

from the prime / explicit-formula side. The current instruction is to seek an explicit-formula obstruction rather than another Wronskian-structure refinement. 

---

# 1. Prime-side translation of \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\)

On packet-frequency blocks,

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\{n:cQ\le \log n\le cQ+Q/R\},
\qquad
0<c<1/2,
\]

write the canonical AFE form schematically as

\[
Z_\alpha(m)
=
Z_+(m,\alpha)
+
Z_-(m,\alpha)
+
Z_{\Gamma}(m,\alpha)
+
Z_E(m,\alpha),
\]

with

\[
Z_+(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and folded dual contribution

\[
Z_-(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n}.
\]

Thus

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

is the prime-side constraint

\[
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}
z_n^+e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_-}
z_n^-e^{+im_0\log n}
=
-
Z_{\Gamma}(m_0,\alpha)
-
Z_E(m_0,\alpha)
-
Z_{\rm outside}(m_0,\alpha).
\]

In normalized notation, with

\[
u_n=e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

this is one complex linear constraint:

\[
\langle z^+,u^+\rangle
+
\langle z^-,u^-\rangle
=
\text{known background}.
\]

So \(Z_\alpha=0\) is a **first-order prime-phase balance condition**.

---

# 2. Prime-side translation of \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0\)

The basis-normalized Wronskian expands into subset-product frequencies:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal F}
B_\nu(m,\alpha)e^{-im\Omega_\nu}
+
\text{background/error},
\]

where \(\mathcal F\) includes pure and mixed main/dual subset-product phases:

\[
\Omega_\nu
\in
\left\{
\log N_+,\,
-\log N_-,\,
\log(N_+/N_-),\,
\log(N_+/N_-)-k\Theta'(m),
\ldots
\right\}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\sum_{S_+}B_{S_+}^{+}
\prod_{n\in S_+}u_n
+
\sum_{S_-}B_{S_-}^{-}
\prod_{n\in S_-}\overline{u_n}
+
\sum_{S_+,S_-}B_{S_+,S_-}^{\rm mix}
\prod_{n\in S_+}u_n
\prod_{n\in S_-}\overline{u_n}
+
\cdots .
\]

Thus

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)\approx0
\]

is a **higher-degree subset-product phase cancellation condition**.

The bad event is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one linear AFE balance}
+
\text{one high-degree folded subset-product cancellation}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Can these constraints force incompatible prime moments?

The desired obstruction would be something like:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\left|
\sum_{\nu}B_\nu e^{-im_0\Omega_\nu}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently, the linear balance imposed by \(Z_\alpha=0\) would have to prevent the determinant-scale subset-product balance.

But in a relaxed prime-phase model, this is false.

Let \(u_n\) be independent phases. Then

\[
Z_\alpha=0
\]

is one complex equation, and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=0
\]

is another complex equation. Since the active packet-frequency block contains many more than two phase variables, the joint system is generically soluble.

Therefore the prime-side obstruction cannot be a purely algebraic incompatibility between the two constraints. It must use the actual one-parameter orbit

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

So the obstruction must be an **actual prime-log nonrecurrence theorem**, not a formal AFE identity.

---

# 4. Candidate lower-bound statistic

One natural attempt is to form

\[
\mathcal P
=
|Z_\alpha|^2
+
\beta |\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|^2
\]

or a mixed statistic

\[
\mathcal C
=
\operatorname{Re}
\left(
\overline{Z_\alpha}
\,L\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
\right)
\]

for some differential or branch-filter operator \(L\).

At \(Z_\alpha=0\), however,

\[
\overline{Z_\alpha}L\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=0,
\]

so a bilinear statistic using \(Z_\alpha\) itself gives no lower bound at the zero.

A better candidate would use derivatives:

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm der}
=
\operatorname{Re}
\left(
\overline{\mathcal D Z_\alpha}
\,
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
\right)
\]

or the cofactor form

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm cof}
=
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

But

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm cof}
=
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
\]

is exactly the target. Its prime-side expansion is the same folded subset-product exponential sum. No new positive diagonal appears.

So the natural statistics either vanish at \(Z_\alpha=0\) or are equivalent to the Wronskian itself.

---

# 5. Squared explicit-formula statistic

Consider the nonnegative expression

\[
\int_J
\left(
|Z_\alpha(m)|^2
+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|^2
\right)\,dm.
\]

On a long interval, the prime-side expansion has diagonal mass:

\[
\int_J |Z_\alpha|^2\,dm
\sim
|J|\sum_n |z_n|^2,
\]

and

\[
\int_J |\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|^2\,dm
\sim
|J|\sum_\nu |B_\nu|^2,
\]

provided \(J\) resolves the relevant frequencies.

This gives average mass. It does **not** prove the pointwise implication

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

For that, one would need a zero-set sampling theorem:

\[
\sum_{m_j:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_j,\alpha)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

This is not supplied by the explicit formula alone. It is a zero-set large-sieve / incidence theorem.

Thus the positive diagonal from \(|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|^2\) helps only after a separate sampling theorem.

---

# 6. Explicit-formula obstruction from zero-side cancellation?

A more ambitious route is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\quad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)\approx0
\]

forces a zero-side packet cancellation, which by explicit formula forces an abnormal prime response.

But \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0\) is already a prime-side folded subset-product cancellation, not a simple zero-side packet moment cancellation. The explicit formula maps linear zero statistics to linear prime statistics. Here the Wronskian is nonlinear/exterior:

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\det(C_\ell G_j).
\]

So the explicit formula does not linearize the determinant into a single prime moment with a positive diagonal. It produces a high-degree combination of prime moments.

Therefore the explicit-formula route again lands at:

\[
\boxed{
\text{folded subset-product nonrecurrence conditioned on }Z_\alpha=0.
}
\]

---

# 7. Possible theorem candidate

The strongest viable prime-side obstruction theorem would be:

## Prime-side incidence obstruction theorem

Let \(Z_\alpha\) and \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) be built from the full canonical AFE

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

on ordinary packet-frequency blocks. Suppose:

1. two-branch symbol rank holds;
2. high-derivative \(E_2\) is controlled;
3. \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\).

Then the folded subset-product polynomial

\[
\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal F}
B_\nu(m_0,\alpha)e^{-im_0\Omega_\nu}
\]

obeys

\[
\left|
\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal F}
B_\nu(m_0,\alpha)e^{-im_0\Omega_\nu}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is exactly the desired incidence theorem, but stated in prime-side subset-product language.

A proof would need to show that the linear AFE balance \(Z_\alpha=0\) cannot coexist with the high-degree folded subset-product balance. No known diagonal/positivity mechanism currently gives that.

---

# 8. No-go diagnosis

The explicit-formula / prime-side route does **not** currently close the incidence theorem.

Reasons:

1. \(Z_\alpha=0\) is a linear prime-phase balance.

2. \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0\) is a high-degree folded subset-product balance.

3. In a relaxed phase model, both balances can hold simultaneously with healthy symbol rank and conditioning.

4. Squared \(L^2\) statistics give average diagonal mass but do not give lower bounds at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

5. Mixed statistics involving \(Z_\alpha\) vanish at \(Z_\alpha=0\), while derivative/cofactor statistics reduce to the Wronskian itself.

6. The explicit formula is linear; the Wronskian condition is exterior/nonlinear. Linear explicit-formula positivity does not automatically control the determinant.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The explicit-formula route collapses back to actual folded subset-product nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

---

# 9. What would be needed to make this route work?

One of the following new inputs would be sufficient:

### A. Zero-set large sieve

\[
\sum_{m_j:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_j,\alpha)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}.
\]

### B. Folded subset-product nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\left|
\sum_{\nu}B_\nu e^{-im_0\Omega_\nu}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

### C. Positive determinant statistic

A representation

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|^2
=
\sum_\nu w_\nu |\mathcal A_\nu|^2
+
\text{controlled error},
\qquad
w_\nu\ge Q^{-C},
\]

valid at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

No such identity is currently available.

### D. Main/dual imbalance theorem

\[
Z_\alpha=0
+
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0
\Rightarrow
\text{contradiction with folded main/dual AFE coupling}.
\]

Prior analysis found no sign or commutator invariant yet.

---

# 10. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No prime-side explicit-formula obstruction is currently proved.}
}
\]

The best exact reformulation is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\text{folded subset-product determinant sum is }Q^{-A}\text{-nonzero}.
}
\]

This is not easier than the incidence theorem; it is the incidence theorem in prime-side coordinates.

So this lane remains **Yellow**, with the same core unresolved arithmetic input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual folded subset-product nonrecurrence conditioned on }Z_\alpha=0.
}
\]
