## Agent 4 / D — Main/dual cellwise cancellation

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: analyze whether the full canonical cell vector

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E
\]

can collapse cellwise through main/dual cancellation, even when the main and dual cell vectors are separately non-small. The prompt asks for either a main/dual cell nonalignment theorem candidate or a reduction to folded main/dual actual-orbit nonrecurrence. 

---

# 1. Main and folded-dual cell vectors

Use fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12,
\]

with

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\in[c_-,c_+]\subset(0,1/2).
\]

The folded dual coordinate is

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

Since \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), and \(\log(m/2\pi)\asymp Q\), the dual coordinate ranges over approximately

\[
x_n^-\in[1-c_+,1-c_-]\subset(1/2,1).
\]

Thus the two branches are separated:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
[c_-,c_+],
[1-c_+,1-c_-]
\bigr)
\ge
1-2c_+
>0.
\]

Define main cells \(I_r^+\subset[c_-,c_+]\) and dual cells \(I_r^-\subset[1-c_+,1-c_-]\), both of width \(\asymp R^{-1}\). To compare branches in a common cell index \(r\), use the folded coordinate map

\[
x^- \leftrightarrow 1-x^+
\]

or the exact AFE convention-dependent map. Then

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r^+}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r^-}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}.
\]

The full cell vector is

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

The main-dual obstruction is the possible cellwise cancellation

\[
B_r^+
\approx
-
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
\qquad
\forall r.
\]

---

# 2. Branch separation helps indexing, not cancellation

The separation

\[
x^+\in(c_-,c_+),
\qquad
x^-\in(1-c_+,1-c_-)
\]

is very useful for symbol rank and branch filtering. It implies that polynomial filters in \(\mathcal D\) can distinguish the two branches with cost

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}
\]

at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

However, the cell-sum theorem asks for a **pointwise vector lower bound**

\[
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^- + B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Branch separation alone does not prevent

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

It only says the two vectors came from separated packet-frequency regions. Since their phases are evaluated at the same \(m_0\), cancellation is still a folded main/dual actual-orbit question.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{branch separation is a rank/filtering input, not a cellwise nonalignment proof.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Hard regime: \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\)

The main and dual coefficients contain opposite \(\alpha\)-biases, schematically

\[
z_n^+ \sim e^{-\alpha u}A_+(u),
\qquad
z_n^- \sim e^{+\alpha u^-}A_-(u^-),
\]

where

\[
u=\log n\sim cQ,
\qquad
u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}\sim(1-c)Q.
\]

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

then

\[
e^{-\alpha u}=1+O(|\alpha|Q),
\]

\[
e^{+\alpha u^-}=1+O(|\alpha|Q).
\]

Thus \(\alpha\)-asymmetry gives no polynomially strong separation between branches.

In this regime, the only branch differences are:

\[
A_+(u)\ \text{versus}\ A_-(u^-),
\]

gamma/folding phases,

logarithmic factors,

and the coordinate separation \(x^+\neq x^-\).

These are enough for symbol-rank nondegeneracy but do not visibly imply

\[
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A phase-relaxed construction can still solve, cell by cell,

\[
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
=
0
\]

because each cell has many phases. With reflected dual phases, the freedom is lower but still not eliminated at the formal level.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll1
\text{ remains the hard uniform branch.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Easier regime: \(|\alpha|Q\gtrsim1\) or \(|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q\)

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim1,
\]

the branch amplitudes separate by

\[
\frac{|z^-|}{|z^+|}
\sim
\exp(\alpha u^-+\alpha u)
=
\exp(\alpha Q)
\]

up to fixed \(c\)-dependent constants and AFE weights.

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_0\log Q,
\]

then one branch dominates by a polynomial factor:

\[
\frac{\|B^-\|_{\rm expected}}{\|B^+\|_{\rm expected}}
\ge Q^{C}
\]

or the reverse, depending on the sign of \(\alpha\).

This gives a plausible conditional theorem.

## Conditional branch-dominance theorem

Assume

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_0\log Q,
\]

and assume the dominant branch cell vector satisfies

\[
\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Assume also the non-dominant branch and background/error satisfy

\[
\|B^{\rm sub}\|_2+\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\le
\frac12 Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\|B\|_2
=
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^- + B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge
\frac12 Q^{-A}.
\]

This proves cell mass in the separated-\(\alpha\) regime.

But this theorem still requires a single-branch cell noncancellation lower bound for \(B^{\rm dom}\). It removes cross-branch cancellation, not internal same-branch cancellation.

So in the easier regime, main/dual cellwise cancellation is not the main issue; the problem reduces to dominant-branch actual prime-log cell nonrecurrence.

---

# 5. Can branch separation force nonalignment of cell vectors?

One might hope that the cell vectors \(B^+\) and \(B^-\) live in different bases and therefore cannot align. But after folding into a common cell index, both are just vectors in

\[
\mathbb C^{M_{\rm cell}}.
\]

The map

\[
x^+\mapsto x^-=1-x^+
\]

pairs separated branches into corresponding cells. Once this pairing is made, there is no abstract linear-algebra obstruction to

\[
B^-=-e^{-i\Theta_Z}B^+.
\]

The obstruction, if true, must come from the actual phases

\[
e^{-im\log n}
\quad\text{and}\quad
e^{+im\log n},
\]

and the exact AFE weights, not from cell geometry.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is no pure cell-coordinate nonalignment theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Main/dual cell nonalignment candidate

The best possible theorem in this lane is:

## Main/dual cell nonalignment theorem

Let

\[
B^+(m),B^-(m)\in\mathbb C^M
\]

be the fixed-width main and folded-dual cell vectors. Assume

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0,
\]

i.e.

\[
\langle B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^- + B^{\rm bg}+B^E,\mathbf 1\rangle
\approx0.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^- + B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

A sufficient stronger condition is

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(B^+(m),B^-(m)),
\left\{
(U,V):U+e^{i\Theta_Z}V+B^{\rm bg}+B^E=0
\right\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently, the actual orbit avoids the cellwise folded cancellation variety.

This is a clean theorem statement, but it is still an actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In relaxed phases, the theorem is false.

Let each cell contain many terms. In each paired cell \(r\), choose main and dual phases so that

\[
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
=0.
\]

This is one complex equation per cell. With many phases inside each cell, the system is generically solvable, including with fixed magnitudes, provided polygon inequalities hold.

Even with the reflected condition

\[
u_n^-=\overline{u_n^+},
\]

one still has many real variables per cell and two real constraints per cell. There is no formal obstruction.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{main/dual cell nonalignment is false in relaxed models.}
}
\]

The first serious obstruction is again the one-parameter orbit

\[
u_n(m)=e^{-im\log n}.
\]

---

# 8. Final verdict

There is a partial positive result:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q
\text{ can plausibly reduce main/dual cell cancellation to dominant-branch cell nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

But the uniform theorem, especially in the hard branch

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

still requires:

\[
\boxed{
\text{folded main/dual actual-orbit cell nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

Branch separation

\[
0<c_-<c_+<1/2
\]

prevents symbolic degeneracy, but it does not prevent cellwise vector cancellation.

So the correct final statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{main/dual cellwise cancellation remains a real arithmetic issue.}
}
\]

The full cell-sum theorem reduces to proving that the actual one-parameter prime-log orbit avoids the variety

\[
B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^- + B^{\rm bg}+B^E=0
\]

at polynomial scale, under

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0.
\]

This is narrower and higher-codimension than full Wronskian incidence, but it is not solved by branch separation alone.

## Agent 4 / D — Actual-orbit avoidance theorem for the cell-flat variety

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: formulate the strongest actual-orbit avoidance theorem for

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}=\{v:P_{\rm cell}v=0\},
\]

and determine whether it can be proved from available structure or must be imported as a new nonrecurrence input. The current round is focused on same-branch cell mass, main/dual cell nonalignment, and actual-orbit avoidance for fixed-width multiblock cells. 

---

# 1. Cell-flat variety

Let the fixed-width packet-frequency support be

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Set

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n\in[x_-,x_+]\subset(0,1/2),
\]

and partition \([x_-,x_+]\) into cells

\[
I_r,\qquad |I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

Define the main-branch phase vector

\[
v^+(m)
=
\left(
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}
\right)_{n\in\mathcal B_+}.
\]

The main cell projection is

\[
(P_{\rm cell}^+v^+)_r
=
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

For the dual branch, using folded coordinates

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n},
\]

define

\[
v^-(m)
=
\left(
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n}
\right)_{n\in\mathcal B_-},
\]

and

\[
(P_{\rm cell}^-v^-)_r
=
B_r^-.
\]

The full canonical cell projection is

\[
P_{\rm cell}v
=
B
=
B^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m,\alpha)}B^-
+
B^{\rm bg}
+
B^E.
\]

The cell-flat variety is

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
=
\{v:P_{\rm cell}v=0\}.
\]

The desired theorem is

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
v(m_0,\alpha),
\ker P_{\rm cell}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha)\|_2
=
\|B(m_0)\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the fixed-width multiblock cell-sum theorem.

---

# 2. Relation to the scalar zero condition

The scalar zero condition is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

In cell variables this is approximately

\[
\sum_r B_r
=
\langle B,\mathbf 1\rangle
\approx0,
\]

up to contributions outside the selected support and background/error terms.

Thus \(Z_\alpha=0\) imposes one complex scalar constraint on the cell vector \(B\). The cell-flat event imposes

\[
B_r=0
\qquad
1\le r\le M_{\rm cell}.
\]

Therefore the desired theorem says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual orbit can satisfy the total cancellation }
\sum_rB_r\approx0,
\text{ but cannot satisfy cellwise cancellation }B_r\approx0\ \forall r.
}
\]

This is the right finite-dimensional separation. It is much stronger than saying \(Z_\alpha\) is nonzero, but much narrower than the full Wronskian incidence theorem.

---

# 3. Codimension and recurrence cost

The event

\[
B_r(m)\approx0
\qquad
1\le r\le M
\]

is \(M\) complex constraints, i.e. \(2M\) real constraints. Since

\[
M\asymp R,
\]

this is roughly

\[
2R
\]

real constraints.

The scalar condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m)\approx0
\]

is one complex constraint, i.e. two real constraints.

Conditioning on \(Z_\alpha=0\), cell-flatness adds approximately

\[
2(M-1)\asymp 2R
\]

additional real constraints.

For tolerance

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

a generic recurrence estimate gives

\[
T_{\rm cell}
\sim
\varepsilon^{-2(M-1)}
=
Q^{2A(M-1)}.
\]

With

\[
M\asymp R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this becomes

\[
T_{\rm cell}
=
\exp\left(
O_A\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is much more expensive than the full Wronskian scalar incidence event

\[
Z_\alpha\approx0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0,
\]

which is only two complex constraints and has heuristic recurrence cost

\[
Q^{O(A)}.
\]

So recurrence heuristics support the idea that the cell-flat event is a much smaller target.

However, recurrence cost alone is not a proof. The global height range may still be too large for this heuristic to exclude all approximate hits without a genuine arithmetic nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 4. Candidate actual-orbit avoidance theorem

The strongest useful theorem is:

## Fixed-width cell-flat avoidance theorem

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and let

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<1/2.
\]

Partition the normalized support into

\[
M\asymp R
\]

cells of width \(\asymp R^{-1}\). Let \(B(m,\alpha)\) be the full canonical cell vector

\[
B
=
B^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-
+
B^{\rm bg}
+
B^E.
\]

Then for admissible \(m_0,\alpha\),

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\|B(m_0,\alpha)\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
v(m_0,\alpha),
\ker P_{\rm cell}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem would imply

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and then

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

---

# 5. Possible proof mechanisms

## 5.1 Diophantine lower bounds for prime-log phases

The actual orbit is

\[
m\mapsto
(e^{-im\log n})_{n\in\mathcal B_{\rm wide}}.
\]

A Diophantine route would prove that \(m\log n\) cannot simultaneously arrange the phases inside every cell to polygon-cancel.

But standard linear independence of \(\log p\) over \(\mathbb Q\) gives density, not avoidance. It says the orbit eventually comes close to many phase targets, not that it avoids them.

To prove avoidance, one needs quantitative restrictions from admissibility, height budget, or actual zeta coupling. Pure Diophantine independence is insufficient.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prime-log Diophantine independence alone does not prove the theorem.}
}
\]

## 5.2 Exponential-sum nonrecurrence

One can state the desired theorem as a simultaneous small-value exclusion:

\[
\max_{1\le r\le M}|B_r(m)|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{cannot occur when}\quad
Z_\alpha(m)=0.
\]

This is a vector-valued exponential-sum nonrecurrence theorem. It is plausible because \(M\asymp R\), but it is not standard.

A sufficient theorem would be:

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{m:\,Z_\alpha(m)=0}
\sum_{r=1}^{M}
\left|
\sum_{x_n\in I_r}
z_n(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}
\right|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is essentially the target itself, but now correctly isolated.

## 5.3 Transversality of the cell map

Define

\[
\mathcal B(m)
=
(B_1(m),\ldots,B_M(m)).
\]

If

\[
\mathcal B'(m)
\]

has large norm whenever \(\mathcal B(m)\) is small, then the orbit crosses the cell-flat neighborhood quickly. This may help measure the small set, but it does not exclude intersection with it.

It could prove a bound like:

\[
\operatorname{meas}
\{m:\|\mathcal B(m)\|\le Q^{-A}\}
\ll Q^{-cA},
\]

but not pointwise avoidance at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

To use it, one would still need a sampling theorem saying zeros of \(Z_\alpha\) do not concentrate in that small set.

So transversality alone is not enough.

## 5.4 Explicit-formula obstruction

The cell vector is degree-one in the AFE coefficients. That is better than the Wronskian determinant, which is exterior/high-degree.

One might hope the explicit formula controls degree-one cell projections more directly.

But the cell projections are already prime-side packet sums. The explicit formula would map them to zero-side localized statistics. A proof would need to show that cellwise prime cancellation forces abnormal zero statistics incompatible with \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\). No such contradiction is currently identified.

Still, this is more promising than the Wronskian determinant because the statistic is linear/positive after squaring:

\[
\|B\|_2^2
=
\sum_r |B_r|^2.
\]

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit-formula methods are more plausible here than for the Wronskian, but no concrete obstruction is yet proved.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Phase-relaxed countermodel

The theorem is false in relaxed phase space.

For each cell \(I_r\), if there are sufficiently many terms and the polygon inequality holds,

\[
\max_{n\in I_r}|z_n|
\le
\sum_{n'\in I_r,n'\ne n}|z_{n'}|,
\]

then phases can be chosen so that

\[
B_r=0.
\]

This can be done independently for all cells.

Thus

\[
P_{\rm cell}v=0
\]

is nonempty and high-dimensional in the relaxed model.

Therefore, any proof must use the actual one-parameter orbit. The cell theorem is not a consequence of coefficient magnitudes, cell geometry, or AFE weights alone.

---

# 7. Main/dual issue

The full canonical vector is

\[
B=B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^- +B^{\rm bg}+B^E.
\]

The cell-flat variety is therefore not just

\[
B^+=0.
\]

It includes possible folded cancellation

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

In the regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q,
\]

one branch may dominate, reducing the theorem to one-branch cell nonrecurrence.

But in the hard regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

branch magnitudes are comparable, and main/dual cellwise cancellation remains possible in relaxed models.

Thus the uniform avoidance theorem must include folded main/dual actual-orbit nonrecurrence.

---

# 8. Final theorem statement to import

The exact black-box theorem needed is:

## Actual prime-log multiblock cell nonrecurrence

For fixed

\[
0<c_-<c_+<1/2,
\]

ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

and

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

let \(B(m,\alpha)\in\mathbb C^M\), \(M\asymp R\), be the full canonical cell vector on

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q.
\]

Then for admissible \(m,\alpha\),

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
\|B(m,\alpha)\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
u(m)\notin
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}^{(Q^{-A})}
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}^{(\varepsilon)}
=
\{u:\|P_{\rm cell}v(u)\|_2\le\varepsilon\}.
\]

This is the theorem to prove or import.

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No proof from standard recurrence/transversality/Diophantine facts alone.}
}
\]

But the cell theorem is still a substantially better target than the full Wronskian incidence theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell-flatness imposes }M\asymp R\text{ complex constraints, not just one extra scalar constraint.}
}
\]

The first serious obstruction to the adversary occurs precisely at the actual one-parameter phase law

\[
e^{-im\log n}.
\]

So the correct final conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the multiblock cell theorem is a new actual prime-log nonrecurrence theorem, but a narrower and more plausible one than full Wronskian incidence.}
}
\]
## User (2026-04-27 06:57:49)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 06:57:56)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 4 / D — Degree-one zero-set large sieve for cell vectors

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: formulate and attack the averaged zero-set cell theorem

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J),
\]

as a degree-one precursor to the later \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve. The prompt asks for the zero-sampling kernel, expansion, dual/main-dual terms, the required operator inequality, and whether the argument principle helps. 

---

# 1. Zero-sampling kernel

Let

\[
\mathcal Z_J
=
\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\},
\]

and let \(w_J\) be a smooth nonnegative cutoff supported on \(J\). Define

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

The desired zero-set cell large sieve is

\[
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}w_J(m_j).
\]

Here

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

Ignore \(B^{\rm bg},B^E\) first; they are lower-order/canonical-error perturbations.

---

# 2. Main-branch expansion

For the main branch,

\[
B_r^+(m)
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n}.
\]

First freeze the slowly varying amplitude \(z_n^+(\alpha,m)\) at \(m=m_0\), or assume its variation over \(J\) is absorbed into controlled derivative errors. Then

\[
|B_r^+(m_j)|^2
=
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\ x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
e^{-im_j(\log n-\log n')}.
\]

Summing over zeros gives

\[
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}w_J(m_j)|B^+(m_j)|_2^2
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
K_J(\log n-\log n').
\]

The diagonal contribution is

\[
K_J(0)\sum_r\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}|z_n^+|^2
=
K_J(0)\sum_{n\in\mathcal B_+}|z_n^+|^2.
\]

The off-diagonal contribution is

\[
\mathcal O_+
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{n\ne n'\\ x_n^+,x_{n'}^+\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^+}
K_J(\log n-\log n').
\]

Thus the main branch lower bound follows if

\[
|\mathcal O_+|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})
K_J(0)\sum_n |z_n^+|^2.
\]

---

# 3. Dual and main-dual terms

For the folded dual branch,

\[
B_r^-(m)
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)|B^-(m_j)|_2^2
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^-,x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^-\overline{z_{n'}^-}
K_J(-\log n+\log n').
\]

Since

\[
K_J(-\xi)=\overline{K_J(\xi)}
\]

when \(w_J\) is real, this has the same operator structure as the main branch.

The main-dual cross term is

\[
2\Re\left(
e^{-i\Theta_Z}
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)
\langle B^+(m_j),B^-(m_j)\rangle
\right).
\]

Expanding,

\[
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)
\langle B^+(m_j),B^-(m_j)\rangle
=
\sum_r
\sum_{\substack{x_n^+\in I_r\\ x_{n'}^-\in I_r}}
z_n^+\overline{z_{n'}^-}
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j(\log n+\log n')}.
\]

Hence the cross term is governed by kernels

\[
K_J(\log n+\log n').
\]

With gamma/folding phases, the kernel becomes schematically

\[
K_J(\log n+\log n'-\Theta_Z'(m_j))
\]

or, more carefully, a weighted sum

\[
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)
e^{-im_j(\log n+\log n')}
e^{-i\Theta_Z(m_j,\alpha)}
\]

which is a twisted zero-sampling kernel

\[
K_{J,\Theta}(\log n+\log n')
=
\sum_{m_j}w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j(\log n+\log n')}e^{-i\Theta_Z(m_j,\alpha)}.
\]

So the full degree-one zero-set large sieve needs control of two kernel classes:

\[
K_J(\log n-\log n')
\]

and

\[
K_{J,\Theta}(\log n+\log n').
\]

---

# 4. Required operator inequality

Let \(a_n\) denote the main-branch coefficients within cells. Define the same-cell matrix

\[
\mathcal K^+_{n,n'}
=
\mathbf 1_{x_n,x_{n'}\text{ in same cell}}
K_J(\log n-\log n').
\]

The needed lower-bound operator inequality is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{n,n'}
a_n\overline{a_{n'}}
\mathcal K^+_{n,n'}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_n|a_n|^2.
}
\]

Similarly for the dual branch.

For the full main+dual vector, define a block matrix

\[
\mathcal K_{\rm full}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal K^{++} & \mathcal K^{+-}\\
\mathcal K^{-+} & \mathcal K^{--}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal K^{++}_{n,n'}=
\mathbf 1_{\mathrm{same\ cell}}
K_J(\log n-\log n'),
\]

\[
\mathcal K^{--}_{n,n'}=
\mathbf 1_{\mathrm{same\ cell}}
K_J(-\log n+\log n'),
\]

\[
\mathcal K^{+-}_{n,n'}=
\mathbf 1_{\mathrm{folded\ same\ cell}}
e^{-i\Theta_Z}
K_{J,\Theta}(\log n+\log n'),
\]

and \(\mathcal K^{-+}\) is the adjoint.

The full theorem would follow from

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal K_{\rm full}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I
}
\]

on the coefficient subspace generated by the canonical AFE weights, after subtracting background/error perturbations.

This is the precise degree-one zero-set large-sieve operator estimate.

---

# 5. Can the argument principle estimate \(K_J(\xi)\)?

The formal identity is

\[
\sum_{Z_\alpha(s_j)=0}H(s_j)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
H(s)\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds,
\]

for \(H\) analytic in \(\Omega\), assuming zeros are counted with multiplicity.

Taking

\[
H(s)=w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\]

would give

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}
\,ds.
\]

For the twisted kernel,

\[
H(s)=w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}e^{-i\Theta_Z(s,\alpha)}.
\]

This is a valid route formally, but it needs strong bounds for

\[
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}
\]

on the contour. Specifically, to prove an operator estimate, one needs off-diagonal decay of \(K_J(\xi)\), for \(\xi\ne0\), of the form

\[
|K_J(\xi)|
\le
\eta(\xi)K_J(0),
\]

where the matrix formed from \(\eta(\log n-\log n')\) has operator norm \(<1-Q^{-A}\) on same-cell pairs.

This requires control of:

\[
\frac{Z_\alpha'}{Z_\alpha}
\]

near the contour, including avoidance of zeros too close to the contour, or Cartan-exceptional set management.

So the argument principle gives the correct formula, but not yet the required bound.

---

# 6. Resonance structure

For the main-main kernel,

\[
\xi=\log n-\log n'=\log(n/n').
\]

Same-cell means

\[
|\lambda(\log n-\log n')|
\lesssim R^{-1},
\]

so

\[
|\log(n/n')|
\lesssim \frac{Q}{R}.
\]

This range still contains many off-diagonal terms.

The exact resonance \(\xi=0\) occurs only when

\[
n=n'.
\]

So the diagonal is clean. But near-resonances \(\log(n/n')\) small can be numerous inside a cell.

For main-dual cross terms,

\[
\xi=\log n+\log n'=\log(nn').
\]

In packet-frequency support,

\[
\log n+\log n'\asymp Q,
\]

so this is far from zero. If \(K_J(\xi)\) has decay for \(|\xi|\asymp Q\), then main-dual cross terms are controllable.

Thus the most dangerous terms are same-branch, same-cell off-diagonals with small \(\log(n/n')\), not main-dual cross terms.

---

# 7. Candidate theorem

## Degree-one zero-set large sieve for cell vectors

Let \(\mathcal Z_J=\{m_j\in J:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0\}\). Suppose the zero-sampling kernel satisfies:

1. Diagonal size:

\[
K_J(0)\asymp N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

2. Same-branch operator bound:

For each branch \(\pm\),

\[
\left\|
\left[
\mathbf 1_{\mathrm{same\ cell}}
K_J(\pm(\log n-\log n'))
\right]_{n\ne n'}
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
(1-Q^{-A})K_J(0).
\]

3. Main-dual cross operator bound:

\[
\left\|
\left[
\mathbf 1_{\mathrm{folded\ same\ cell}}
K_{J,\Theta}(\log n+\log n')
\right]_{n,n'}
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
Q^{-A}K_J(0).
\]

Then

\[
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\cdot
\left(
\|z^+\|_2^2+\|z^-\|_2^2
\right)
-
\mathrm{Err}.
\]

After normalization of cell coefficients, this gives

\[
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
w_J(m_j)|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

This is the desired averaged cell theorem.

---

# 8. Does this give the pointwise theorem?

The averaged theorem gives

\[
\frac{1}{N_{Z_\alpha}(J)}
\sum_{m_j\in\mathcal Z_J}
|B(m_j)|_2^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It does **not** imply

\[
|B(m_j)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

for every zero.

To use it for Gate 1 at an arbitrary admissible \(m_0\), one needs either:

1. a local version with \(J\) so short that it contains only \(m_0\), or
2. a nonconcentration theorem preventing exceptional zeros with small cell mass, or
3. a way to choose \(m_0\) from a set of good zeros, which is not enough for the RH contradiction setup if the given off-line zero is arbitrary.

Therefore, the zero-set large sieve is a strong averaged precursor, but the pointwise theorem remains stronger.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{A degree-one zero-set large sieve is plausible as an averaged theorem.}
}
\]

The required kernel/operator estimates are now precise:

\[
K_J(\log n-\log n')
\]

for same-branch terms and

\[
K_{J,\Theta}(\log n+\log n')
\]

for main-dual terms.

The argument principle gives a formal expression for \(K_J\), but proving the necessary off-diagonal operator bounds requires strong control of

\[
Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha
\]

and zero distribution in \(J\). That is nontrivial actual-zeta input.

Most importantly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the averaged zero-set large sieve does not by itself give the pointwise cell theorem.}
}
\]

So the deliverable is a candidate averaged theorem plus a clear gap:

\[
\boxed{
\text{need local/pointwise zero nonconcentration to upgrade averaged cell mass to every admissible zero.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 4’s conclusion: this route is useful, but the pointwise cell nonrecurrence theorem is still the exact input needed for the Wronskian proof.

## Agent 4 / D — Easy \(\alpha\)-tilted branch and branch dominance

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: isolate the easier tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q
\]

and determine whether branch dominance proves main/dual cell nonalignment once same-branch mass is available. The prompt asks specifically for coefficient-ratio analysis, possible dominance, and whether this closes the tilted branch. 

---

# 1. Main/dual coefficient ratio

Work on fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

For the main branch,

\[
u=\log n\in[c_-Q,c_+Q].
\]

For the folded dual branch, write

\[
u^-=\log \frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

In ordinary scale, with conductor logarithm normalized as

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi}\asymp Q,
\]

the dual variable satisfies

\[
u^- \in [(1-c_+)Q,(1-c_-)Q].
\]

So the main and dual branches lie in separated packet-frequency intervals:

\[
x^+=\lambda u\in[c_-,c_+],
\]

\[
x^-=\lambda u^-\in[1-c_+,1-c_-].
\]

The schematic AFE coefficient magnitudes have the form

\[
|z_n^+|
\asymp
A_+(u,m,\alpha)\,
e^{-\alpha u}\,
W_+(u),
\]

\[
|z_n^-|
\asymp
A_-(u^-,m,\alpha)\,
e^{+\alpha u^-}\,
W_-(u^-),
\]

where \(W_\pm\) include the common \(n^{-1/2}\), log-power, smoothing, and gamma/amplitude factors after folding. On plateau blocks away from transition/saddle regions,

\[
A_\pm,W_\pm=Q^{O(1)}
\]

relative to each other. More precisely, the non-\(\alpha\) part of the ratio should satisfy

\[
Q^{-C_0}
\le
\frac{A_+(u)W_+(u)}
{A_-(u^-)W_-(u^-)}
\le
Q^{C_0}.
\]

Thus the dominant exponential part of the ratio is

\[
\frac{|z_n^-|}{|z_n^+|}
\asymp
Q^{O(1)}\,
e^{\alpha(u+u^-)}.
\]

Since

\[
u+u^-
=
\log n+\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
=
\log\frac{m}{2\pi}
\asymp Q,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z_n^-|}{|z_n^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)} e^{\alpha Q}.
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z_n^+|}{|z_n^-|}
=
Q^{O(1)} e^{-\alpha Q}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Branch dominance when \(|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q\)

Suppose

\[
\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q.
\]

Then

\[
e^{\alpha Q}\ge Q^{C_1}.
\]

Choosing \(C_1\) larger than the polynomial losses from smoothing, gamma folding, log powers, and basis/cell conditioning gives

\[
|z_n^-|\ge Q^{c}|z_n^+|
\]

uniformly on paired cells.

Summing cellwise, the expected dominance is

\[
\|B^-\|_2
\ge
Q^c\|B^+\|_2
\]

provided the dominant branch itself does not internally cancel cell by cell.

Similarly, if

\[
-\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q,
\]

then

\[
\|B^+\|_2
\ge
Q^c\|B^-\|_2.
\]

So the tilted branch admits the following conditional dominance theorem.

---

# 3. Conditional branch-dominance theorem

## Theorem candidate

Assume:

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q,
\]

with \(C_1\) large enough relative to canonical AFE polynomial losses.

Assume the AFE blocks are plateau-separated:

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12,
\]

so neither branch lies near a smoothing transition or saddle-overlap region.

Assume also a same-branch cell mass theorem for the dominant branch:

\[
\|B^{\rm dom}(m_0)\|_2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then the non-dominant branch satisfies

\[
\|B^{\rm sub}(m_0)\|_2
\le
Q^{-c}\|B^{\rm dom}(m_0)\|_2
\]

after absorbing canonical background/error into

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\le
Q^{-A_0-c}.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\begin{aligned}
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
&\ge
\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2
-
\|B^{\rm sub}\|_2
-
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2
-
\|B^E\|_2\\
&\ge
\frac12 Q^{-A_0}.
\end{aligned}
\]

Thus,

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|B\|_2\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

provided the dominant same-branch cell mass theorem holds.

---

# 4. What could defeat dominance?

There are four possible obstructions.

## 4.1 AFE transition or saddle weights

If either branch is near an AFE transition region, the non-\(\alpha\) ratio may not be merely polynomially controlled. This is avoided by requiring

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12
\]

and choosing plateau cells away from the saddle.

## 4.2 Cell pairing mismatch

The main cell coordinate is

\[
x^+=\lambda\log n,
\]

while the dual coordinate is

\[
x^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

The folded pairing reverses the interval. If cell partitions are not matched under

\[
x^-\approx 1-x^+,
\]

then local dominance may fail cell-by-cell. But global \(\ell^2\)-dominance survives as long as both cell systems cover corresponding fixed-width intervals and weights are comparable.

## 4.3 Internal cancellation in the dominant branch

Dominance does not prove

\[
\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It only says that if one branch has mass, it cannot be cancelled by the other. The same-branch theorem is still required:

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

In the tilted regime, it is enough to prove the dominant branch version.

## 4.4 Background/error terms

The background and \(E\)-terms must be smaller than the dominant cell mass:

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2\le \frac14\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2.
\]

This is a canonical error-budget condition, not a new arithmetic obstacle.

---

# 5. Combination with same-branch mass

Assume the combined same-branch mass theorem

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_1}.
\]

In the tilted regime, branch dominance implies that one branch supplies essentially all this mass. If

\[
\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q,
\]

then

\[
\|B^-\|_2
\ge
Q^c\|B^+\|_2
\]

unless \(\|B^-\|\) itself is tiny. But the combined mass lower bound then forces

\[
\|B^-\|_2\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Consequently,

\[
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2
\ge
\|B^-\|_2-\|B^+\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A_3}.
\]

Similarly, if

\[
-\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q,
\]

then the main branch dominates and

\[
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2
\ge Q^{-A_3}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-branch mass}
+
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\Rightarrow
\text{full cell mass}.
}
\]

---

# 6. The hard branch remains \(|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q\)

The above closes only the strongly tilted regime.

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q,
\]

and especially if

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

then

\[
e^{\alpha Q}=Q^{o(1)}
\]

or \(1+o(1)\), so branch dominance disappears.

In that case,

\[
\|B^+\|_2
\asymp
\|B^-\|_2
\]

is possible, and cellwise cancellation

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-
\]

is not ruled out by coefficient magnitudes.

Thus the hard uniform theorem remains:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll \log Q
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{need folded main/dual actual-orbit nonalignment.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Final theorem for the tilted regime

## Tilted-cell theorem

Let

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q.
\]

Assume:

1. plateau separation:

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12;
\]

2. polynomially controlled AFE weight ratios;

3. canonical background/error cell norms are \(Q^{-C}\)-small relative to branch mass;

4. same-branch mass:

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Consequently,

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{main/dual cell cancellation cannot occur.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Branch dominance is sufficient in the strongly tilted regime }|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q.
}
\]

But it is conditional on same-branch cell mass, and it does not address the central symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
\]

So the proof strategy should split:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q:
\quad
\text{same-branch mass} \Rightarrow \text{full cell mass by dominance.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q:
\quad
\text{need folded main/dual cell nonalignment / actual-orbit nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

Thus Agent 4’s tilted-branch result is positive but partial: it closes the easiest \(\alpha\)-regime modulo the same-branch mass theorem, while the hard symmetric branch remains the real obstacle.

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:10:48)

## Agent 4 / D — Tilted branch closure

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: close, if possible, the easier tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q.
\]

The prompt asks for the main/dual magnitude ratio, explicit loss accounting, dominance theorem, and whether the tilted regime closes modulo same-branch mass. 

---

# 1. Main/dual magnitude ratio

Work on fixed-width support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Let

\[
u=\log n,
\]

so the main branch lies in

\[
u\in[c_-Q,c_+Q].
\]

The folded dual coordinate is

\[
u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

Since the completed conductor scale satisfies

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi}\asymp Q,
\]

we have

\[
u^-\in[(1-c_+)Q,(1-c_-)Q].
\]

The schematic AFE coefficient magnitudes are

\[
|z_n^+|
\asymp
\mathcal A_+(u,m,\alpha)\,e^{-\alpha u},
\]

and

\[
|z_n^-|
\asymp
\mathcal A_-(u^-,m,\alpha)\,e^{+\alpha u^-},
\]

where \(\mathcal A_\pm\) include smoothing weights, gamma/folded amplitude factors, log powers, and the \(n^{-1/2}\)-type weights.

On plateau blocks away from the AFE transition and saddle overlap, assume the non-\(\alpha\) ratio is polynomially controlled:

\[
Q^{-C_0}
\le
\frac{\mathcal A_-(u^-,m,\alpha)}
{\mathcal A_+(u,m,\alpha)}
\le
Q^{C_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{|z_n^-|}{|z_n^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha(u+u^-)}.
\]

But

\[
u+u^-=
\log n+\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
=
\log\frac{m}{2\pi}
\asymp Q.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z_n^-|}{|z_n^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha Q}.
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z_n^+|}{|z_n^-|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{-\alpha Q}.
}
\]

This is the core tilted-branch asymmetry.

---

# 2. Explicit loss budget

The factor \(Q^{O(1)}\) absorbs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{AFE smoothing ratio}
}
\]

provided both branches stay on plateau support;

\[
\boxed{
\text{gamma/folding amplitude ratio}
}
\]

provided Stirling expansion is used away from saddle transition;

\[
\boxed{
\text{log-power ratio}
}
\]

such as powers of \(u,u^-\), all with \(u,u^-\asymp Q\);

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell normalization / basis normalization}
}
\]

which costs \(Q^{O(1)}\) at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

So choose \(C_1\) such that

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\]

dominates all polynomial losses. More concretely, if total non-\(\alpha\) losses are bounded by \(Q^{C_0}\), take

\[
C_1>C_0+C_{\rm margin}.
\]

Then the branch ratio is at least

\[
Q^{C_{\rm margin}}.
\]

---

# 3. Branch dominance theorem

## Theorem candidate — tilted branch dominance

Assume:

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q.
\]

Assume plateau separation:

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12,
\]

so both main and folded dual blocks are away from transition/saddle regions.

Assume canonical non-\(\alpha\) weight ratios satisfy

\[
Q^{-C_0}
\le
\frac{\mathcal A_-(u^-)}
{\mathcal A_+(u)}
\le
Q^{C_0}.
\]

Then:

If

\[
\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q,
\]

the dual branch dominates:

\[
\|B^-\|_2
\ge
Q^{c}\|B^+\|_2
\]

unless \(B^-\) itself has undergone internal same-cell cancellation. More precisely, after same-branch mass is known, one has

\[
\|B^-\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
\|B^+\|_2
\le
Q^{-c}\|B^-\|_2.
\]

If

\[
-\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q,
\]

the main branch dominates:

\[
\|B^+\|_2
\ge
Q^{c}\|B^-\|_2.
\]

This dominance is conditional on same-branch cell mass. The \(\alpha\)-tilt controls relative coefficient magnitudes, but it does not by itself stop internal cancellation inside the dominant branch.

---

# 4. Combining dominance with same-branch mass

Assume the same-branch theorem:

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Suppose \(\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q\), so the dual branch dominates. Then

\[
\|B^-\|_2\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

and

\[
\|B^+\|_2\le Q^{-c}\|B^-\|_2.
\]

Hence

\[
\begin{aligned}
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
&\ge
\|B^-\|_2-\|B^+\|_2-\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2-\|B^E\|_2.
\end{aligned}
\]

If canonical background/error terms obey

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\le
\frac14\|B^-\|_2,
\]

and \(Q^{-c}\le1/4\), then

\[
\|B\|_2
\ge
\frac12\|B^-\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A_2}.
\]

The case \(-\alpha Q\ge C_1\log Q\) is identical, with \(B^+\) dominant.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-branch mass}
+
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\Rightarrow
\text{full canonical cell mass}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Obstructions to dominance

The dominance proof can fail only if one of the following occurs.

## 5.1 AFE transition

If the support approaches the smoothing transition or saddle, then

\[
\mathcal A_-/\mathcal A_+
\]

may not be polynomially controlled. Avoid this by requiring

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12.
\]

## 5.2 Internal dominant-branch cancellation

Even if the dual branch coefficients dominate termwise, the cell vector \(B^-\) may itself be small:

\[
B_r^-\approx0
\quad\forall r.
\]

This is exactly the same-branch off-diagonal problem and must be handled separately.

## 5.3 Background/error terms

If

\[
B^{\rm bg}+B^E
\]

is comparable to the dominant branch, it could cancel it. The tilted theorem therefore requires a canonical error bound of the form

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\le Q^{-C}\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2.
\]

This is an error-budget assumption, not an arithmetic obstruction.

## 5.4 Cell matching

The main and dual cell coordinates are folded:

\[
x^+\in[c_-,c_+],
\qquad
x^-\in[1-c_+,1-c_-].
\]

The dominance estimate is global in \(\ell^2\), so exact cell-by-cell pairing is not essential. It suffices that both cell systems are fixed-width and have comparable \(M\asymp R\) discretization.

---

# 6. Final tilted-regime theorem

## Tilted-cell theorem

Let

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q.
\]

Assume:

1. fixed-width plateau support

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12;
\]

2. polynomial control of non-\(\alpha\) AFE weight ratios;

3. canonical background/error cell vector satisfies

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2\le Q^{-C}\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2;
\]

4. same-branch mass

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Consequently, in the tilted regime,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B(m_0)|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

modulo the same-branch cell mass theorem.

---

# 7. What remains open

This closes only the easy branch:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q.
}
\]

The hard branch remains:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q,
}
\]

especially

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

There, the exponential tilt disappears:

\[
e^{\pm\alpha Q}=Q^{o(1)}
\]

or

\[
1+o(1),
\]

and branch magnitudes can be comparable. In that case, the main/dual cell vector can still collapse through

\[
B^+\approx-e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-,
\]

unless one proves a folded actual-orbit nonalignment theorem.

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The tilted regime is closable modulo same-branch mass and canonical error control.}
}
\]

More precisely:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ge C_1\log Q
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{main/dual cancellation is impossible by branch dominance.}
}
\]

But:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the uniform cell theorem still reduces to hard-branch folded main/dual nonrecurrence for }|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
}
\]

So Agent 4’s result is positive but partial: it isolates and essentially closes the easy \(\alpha\)-tilted branch, while confirming that the central remaining cell-theorem difficulty lies in the symmetric regime.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:19:41)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 4 / D — Tilted branch closure

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: close the regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q
\]

for the fixed-width multiblock cell theorem, modulo the same-branch mass theorem. The latest prompt keeps the focus on the cell theorem and asks specifically for a tilted-regime branch-dominance theorem. 

---

# 1. Branch coefficient ratio

Use fixed-width plateau support

\[
c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

For the main branch, set

\[
u=\log n\in[c_-Q,c_+Q].
\]

For the folded dual branch,

\[
u^-=\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}.
\]

Since the conductor logarithm satisfies

\[
\log\frac{m}{2\pi}\asymp Q,
\]

the folded dual branch lies in

\[
u^-\in[(1-c_+)Q,(1-c_-)Q].
\]

The main and dual cell coefficients have schematic magnitudes

\[
|z_n^+|
=
\mathcal A_+(u,m,\alpha)e^{-\alpha u},
\]

\[
|z_n^-|
=
\mathcal A_-(u^-,m,\alpha)e^{+\alpha u^-},
\]

where \(\mathcal A_\pm\) include AFE smoothing, gamma/folding factors, log powers, normalization, and mild \(m,\alpha\)-dependence.

On plateau support away from the saddle and transition region, assume the non-\(\alpha\) ratio is polynomially controlled:

\[
Q^{-C_0}
\le
\frac{\mathcal A_-(u^-,m,\alpha)}
{\mathcal A_+(u,m,\alpha)}
\le
Q^{C_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{|z_n^-|}{|z_n^+|}
=
\frac{\mathcal A_-(u^-)}{\mathcal A_+(u)}
e^{\alpha(u+u^-)}.
\]

But

\[
u+u^-
=
\log n+\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
=
\log\frac{m}{2\pi}
\asymp Q.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z_n^-|}{|z_n^+|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{\alpha Q}.
}
\]

Similarly,

\[
\boxed{
\frac{|z_n^+|}{|z_n^-|}
=
Q^{O(1)}e^{-\alpha Q}.
}
\]

This is the basic tilted-branch separation.

---

# 2. Sources of the \(Q^{O(1)}\) loss

The polynomial loss in the ratio comes from the following sources:

\[
\boxed{\text{AFE smoothing weights}}
\]

provided both branches remain on plateau support;

\[
\boxed{\text{gamma/folding amplitude factors}}
\]

controlled by Stirling expansion away from saddle overlap;

\[
\boxed{\text{log-power factors}}
\]

since \(u,u^-\asymp Q\);

\[
\boxed{\text{cell normalization and basis normalization}}
\]

with cost at most \(Q^{O(1)}\) at safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q};
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{canonical background/error tolerances}}
\]

provided

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\]

is smaller than the dominant branch norm by a fixed polynomial margin.

Therefore choose \(C_{\rm tilt}\) larger than the total exponent in these polynomial losses.

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q,
\]

then the exponential tilt dominates all non-\(\alpha\) distortions.

---

# 3. Branch dominance theorem

## Theorem candidate — tilted branch dominance

Assume:

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q,
\]

with \(C_{\rm tilt}\) chosen larger than the polynomial AFE/gamma/log/basis/error loss.

Assume fixed-width plateau support

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12,
\]

and assume both main and folded-dual weights are away from transition/saddle regions.

If

\[
\alpha Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q,
\]

then the folded dual coefficients dominate:

\[
|z_n^-|\ge Q^c |z_n^+|
\]

uniformly on paired support, for some \(c>0\). Consequently, after summing over cells, the expected branch relation is

\[
\|B^-\|_2\ge Q^c\|B^+\|_2,
\]

provided the dominant branch has not internally collapsed.

If

\[
-\alpha Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q,
\]

then the main branch dominates:

\[
\|B^+\|_2\ge Q^c\|B^-\|_2.
\]

More precisely, the dominance conclusion should be stated conditionally on same-branch mass:

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then the dominant branch obeys

\[
\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

and the subordinate branch obeys

\[
\|B^{\rm sub}\|_2\le Q^{-c}\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2.
\]

---

# 4. Global dominance is sufficient

The dominance does **not** need to hold cellwise.

The desired full cell bound is

\[
\|B\|_2
=
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2.
\]

If one branch dominates globally in \(\ell^2\), then by the triangle inequality,

\[
\|B\|_2
\ge
\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2
-
\|B^{\rm sub}\|_2
-
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2
-
\|B^E\|_2.
\]

Assume

\[
\|B^{\rm sub}\|_2
\le
\frac14\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2,
\]

and

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\le
\frac14\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2.
\]

Then

\[
\|B\|_2
\ge
\frac12\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus global branch dominance is enough. Cellwise dominance is stronger than needed.

---

# 5. Tilted-regime closure modulo same-branch mass

Combining the same-branch mass theorem with branch dominance gives the tilted cell theorem.

Assume

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

If

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q,
\]

then one branch dominates after polynomial losses. Therefore

\[
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q
\quad+\quad
\text{same-branch mass}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{full canonical cell mass}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|\alpha|Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q
\Rightarrow
\|B(m_0,\alpha)\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

provided the same-branch theorem and canonical error budget hold.

This closes the tilted regime modulo same-branch mass.

---

# 6. What dominance does not prove

The dominance theorem does **not** prove the same-branch mass theorem:

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

If the dominant branch internally collapses cellwise,

\[
B_r^{\rm dom}\approx0
\quad\forall r,
\]

then branch dominance is irrelevant.

So the tilted branch still depends on the same-branch off-diagonal theorem:

\[
O^+ + O^-
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^+ + D^-).
\]

Dominance only eliminates the second obstruction:

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-.
\]

---

# 7. Remaining hard regime

The tilted theorem covers

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q.
\]

The hard branch is

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll \log Q,
\]

especially

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

In this symmetric regime,

\[
e^{\alpha Q}=Q^{o(1)}
\]

or

\[
1+o(1),
\]

so the branches can have comparable magnitude. Then cancellation

\[
B^+\approx -e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-
\]

is not ruled out by coefficient sizes.

Thus the hard branch still requires a folded main/dual actual-orbit nonalignment theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}(\|B^+\|_2+\|B^-\|_2)
}
\]

for

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
\]

---

# 8. Final deliverable

## Tilted-cell theorem

Let

\[
|\alpha|Q\ge C_{\rm tilt}\log Q.
\]

Assume:

1. fixed-width plateau support

\[
0<c_-<c_+<c_1<\frac12;
\]

2. polynomial control of non-\(\alpha\) AFE weight ratios;

3. canonical background/error cell norms satisfy

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2
\le Q^{-C}\|B^{\rm dom}\|_2;
\]

4. same-branch cell mass

\[
\|B^+\|_2^2+\|B^-\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|B^+ + e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-+B^{\rm bg}+B^E\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Consequently, the fixed-width multiblock cell theorem is proved in the tilted regime, modulo same-branch mass.

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Tilted branch: closed modulo same-branch mass and canonical error control.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dominance works globally in }\ell^2;\text{ cellwise dominance is unnecessary.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining main/dual nonalignment problem is confined to }|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
}
\]

So the next useful work should focus on:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-branch mass for all }\alpha
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{hard symmetric main/dual nonalignment for }|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:23:47)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 4 / D — Actual-orbit theorem naming and minimal hypotheses

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: turn the full cell theorem into the cleanest named actual-orbit avoidance theorem, with minimal hypotheses and black-box-ready formulation. 

---

# 1. Phase vector and cell projection

Define the canonical fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le \log n\le c_+Q\},
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

Use normalized packet coordinate

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n.
\]

For the folded dual branch use

\[
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m_0}{2\pi n},
\]

or the exact convention determined by the canonical AFE.

Define the phase/coefficient vector

\[
v(m_0,\alpha)
=
\left(
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n},
\ e^{i\Theta_Z(m_0,\alpha)}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n},
\ B^{\rm bg},
\ B^E
\right).
\]

The cell projection is

\[
P_{\rm cell}v
=
(B_r)_r,
\]

where

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

The cell-flat variety is

\[
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
=
\ker P_{\rm cell}.
\]

The desired nonrecurrence statement is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
v(m_0,\alpha),
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

with the distance measured in the coefficient-weighted \(\ell^2\) norm for which

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
v(m_0,\alpha),
\mathcal C_{\rm flat}
\right)
\asymp
\|P_{\rm cell}v(m_0,\alpha)\|_2
=
\|B(m_0,\alpha)\|_2.
\]

---

# 2. Minimal hypotheses

The theorem should be stated with the following hypotheses.

## H1. Ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

This is the ordinary Wronskian regime. Deep singular packets are excluded from this theorem.

## H2. Fixed-width plateau support

Use

\[
c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q,
\qquad
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12.
\]

The strict inequality \(c_+<1/2\) keeps the main and folded-dual branches away from saddle overlap.

## H3. Stable cell partition

Partition

\[
[x_-,x_+]=[\lambda c_-Q,\lambda c_+Q]
\]

into cells

\[
I_r,
\qquad
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

For the cleanest version, impose

\[
M_{\rm cell}\le R+2
\]

or use a projected-cell fallback. This avoids irrelevant high-cell-frequency leakage.

## H4. Canonical AFE fidelity

The cell sums use the full canonical AFE symbols:

\[
z_n^+,\quad z_n^-,
\quad \Theta_Z,
\quad B^{\rm bg},
\quad B^E.
\]

The error terms must satisfy

\[
\|B^{\rm bg}\|_2+\|B^E\|_2\le Q^{-C_{\rm err}}
\]

with \(C_{\rm err}\) large enough relative to the final exponent \(A\).

## H5. Admissible zero

The point \(m_0,\alpha\) must satisfy

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

and the usual ordinary-scale admissibility assumptions. Numerically, toy artifacts at \(m=0\) should be excluded; theorem-level statement can require

\[
m_0\ge m_{\rm min}
\]

or simply “\(m_0\) lies in the asymptotic ordinary regime.”

## H6. Branch-regime split

The theorem should acknowledge that

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q
\]

is easier: main/dual cancellation is prevented by branch dominance once same-branch mass is known.

The hard uniform branch is

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q,
\]

especially

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

The named theorem should cover the hard branch; otherwise the tilted branch can be listed as a corollary.

---

# 3. Final named theorem statement

## Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence Theorem

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Fix

\[
0<c_-<c_+<\frac12
\]

and define the fixed-width packet-frequency support

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm wide}
=
\{n:c_-Q\le\log n\le c_+Q\}.
\]

Let

\[
I_r
\]

be a stable partition of the normalized support into cells of width

\[
|I_r|\asymp R^{-1},
\qquad
M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

Let \(B(m,\alpha)=(B_r(m,\alpha))_r\) be the full canonical cell vector

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z(m,\alpha)}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E,
\]

where

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m)e^{+im\log n}.
\]

Assume canonical AFE errors satisfy the ordinary-scale cell error budget. Then there exist constants \(A,C>0\) such that, for every admissible ordinary-scale zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\|B(m_0,\alpha)\|_2^2
=
\sum_r |B_r(m_0,\alpha)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
v(m_0,\alpha),
\ker P_{\rm cell}
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the black-box input needed to prove

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

---

# 4. Raw versus projected version

There should also be a projected fallback.

Define

\[
\Pi_{\le R+1}
\]

as the projection onto the degree-\((R+1)\) polynomial modes on the cell centers, using a stable discrete orthonormal basis.

## Projected Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

Under the same hypotheses,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|\Pi_{\le R+1}B(m_0,\alpha)\|_2^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This version is closer to the direct jet statement

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Recommended final formulation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use raw cell mass as the primary theorem when }M_{\rm cell}\asymp R\text{ and }M_{\rm cell}\le R+2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use projected cell mass as fallback if the chosen partition has }M_{\rm cell}>R+2.
}
\]

---

# 5. Subtheorem decomposition

The named theorem decomposes into two still-unproved arithmetic inputs.

## Same-Branch Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|B^+(m_0)\|_2^2+\|B^-(m_0)\|_2^2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
O^+(m_0)+O^-(m_0)
\ge
-(1-Q^{-A})(D^+ + D^-).
\]

This rules out simultaneous same-cell self-cancellation in both branches.

## Folded Main/Dual Cell Nonalignment

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|B^+(m_0)+e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-(m_0)\|_2
\ge
Q^{-A}
\bigl(
\|B^+(m_0)\|_2+\|B^-(m_0)\|_2
\bigr).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|\langle B^+,B^-\rangle|
\le
(1-Q^{-A})\|B^+\|_2\|B^-\|_2.
\]

The tilted regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q
\]

is mostly handled by branch dominance, modulo same-branch mass. The hard branch is

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q.
\]

---

# 6. What this theorem buys

If the Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence Theorem holds, then the already-settled analytic package gives

\[
\|B(m_0,\alpha)\|_2^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\sup_{|t|\le R}
|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|
\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

Thus it closes the first Wronskian factor:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

It does **not** close Gate 1. The next theorem remains

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

followed by the angle/incidence theorem.

---

# 7. Final status

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence Theorem is the clean named input.}
}
\]

It is not proved by current local algebra. It is false in phase-relaxed models and must use actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.

The current cell-theorem phase should now either:

1. prove the two named subtheorems above, or  
2. park them as black-box inputs and move to the \(\mathbf M\) zero-set large-sieve theorem.

My recommendation: after one final check from Agents 1–3 on the two subtheorems, park this as the named input unless a genuinely new proof mechanism appears.
## User (2026-04-27 07:41:41)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Agent 4 / D — Pointwise-from-averaged \(\mathbf M\) theorem

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: determine whether an averaged \(\mathbf M\) zero-set large sieve can imply the required pointwise lower bound. The current shared background parks the cell theorem as a named input and moves the ordinary route to the cofactor-vector theorem \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\Rightarrow |\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}\). 

---

# 1. Averaged theorem versus pointwise theorem

The averaged theorem is

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

The required pointwise theorem is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The averaged theorem alone does **not** imply the pointwise theorem. It permits exceptional zeros \(m_0\) where

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A},
\]

as long as other zeros in \(J\) compensate.

Thus the averaged theorem is useful only if paired with an additional **bad-zero exclusion** or **local propagation** principle.

---

# 2. Bad-zero exclusion principle needed

A sufficient principle would be:

## Bad-zero exclusion principle

Let \(m_0\) be an admissible zero of \(Z_\alpha\). If

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\le Q^{-A_0},
\]

then for some local zero window

\[
J_0=[m_0-H,m_0+H],
\]

one has

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J_0\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\le Q^{-A_1}N_{Z_\alpha}(J_0).
\]

Then the averaged zero-set large sieve on \(J_0\) contradicts the bad zero.

This would upgrade average to pointwise.

The missing task is proving that one bad zero forces a local cluster of bad or semi-bad zeros. That is not automatic.

---

# 3. Can derivative bounds for \(\mathbf M\) propagate smallness?

Suppose

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\le Q^{-A_0}.
\]

If we have a derivative bound

\[
|\partial_m \mathbf M(m)|\le Q^{C}
\]

on a neighborhood of \(m_0\), then

\[
|\mathbf M(m)|\le 2Q^{-A_0}
\]

for

\[
|m-m_0|\le Q^{-A_0-C}.
\]

In normalized variables, with \(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\), one might instead have

\[
|\mathcal D\mathbf M|\le Q^C.
\]

Then smallness propagates over

\[
|m-m_0|\le \lambda Q^{-A_0-C}.
\]

This propagation interval is **microscopic**. To use the averaged theorem, this interval must contain enough zeros of \(Z_\alpha\). But zero spacing at height \(m_0\) is roughly logarithmic-scale, while \(\lambda\asymp Q^{-1}\). The propagated interval

\[
\lambda Q^{-A_0-C}
\]

is much smaller than a typical zero spacing unless \(A_0\) is extremely small.

So derivative propagation alone does not create enough nearby sampled zeros.

---

# 4. Can local zero density help?

If \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros were very dense near \(m_0\), then a small neighborhood might contain many sampled points, and propagation of \(\mathbf M\)-smallness could contradict the averaged theorem.

But the ordinary setting does not guarantee such density. In fact, earlier local amplitude/zero-crowding work treated excessive zero crowding as an exceptional phenomenon, not a guaranteed input.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local zero density does not upgrade averaged }\mathbf M\text{ mass to pointwise }\mathbf M\text{ mass.}
}
\]

The averaged theorem samples all zeros in \(J\); a single prescribed zero can still be exceptional.

---

# 5. Stronger averaged theorem that would imply pointwise

One could strengthen the averaged theorem to a **short-interval local average** around every zero:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j:\ |m_j-m_0|\le H\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
N_{Z_\alpha}([m_0-H,m_0+H])
\]

for every admissible \(m_0\), with \(H\) small enough that derivative propagation from \(m_0\) controls \(\mathbf M\) throughout the interval.

But this requires two simultaneous facts:

1. \(H\) is small enough for

\[
|\mathbf M(m_j)-\mathbf M(m_0)|
\]

to be controlled.

2. The interval contains enough zeros to activate the average.

These are in tension. If \(H\) is small enough for derivative propagation, there may be no other zeros. If \(H\) is large enough to contain many zeros, \(\mathbf M\) can vary substantially.

So this strengthened theorem is unlikely to be easier than pointwise nonrecurrence.

---

# 6. Comparison with the cell-theorem obstruction

This is the same structural issue seen in the cell theorem.

For the cell theorem, an averaged statement over zeros,

\[
\sum_{Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}|B(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha},
\]

did not imply the required pointwise statement

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\Rightarrow |B(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The same logic applies here, but more severely, because \(\mathbf M\) is a higher-degree subset-product object:

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+\cdots,
\qquad
\Omega_S=\log N_S.
\]

Its derivative complexity and oscillation are larger than the degree-one cell vector. Therefore averaged-to-pointwise transfer is at least as hard as in the cell case.

---

# 7. Conditional averaged-to-pointwise theorem

A valid but strong theorem is:

## Conditional averaged-to-pointwise theorem for \(\mathbf M\)

Assume:

1. **Local badness propagation**

   If \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) and

   \[
   |\mathbf M(m_0)|\le Q^{-A_0},
   \]

   then for every zero \(m_j\) in

   \[
   |m_j-m_0|\le H
   \]

   one has

   \[
   |\mathbf M(m_j)|\le Q^{-A_1}.
   \]

2. **Local zero abundance**

   \[
   N_{Z_\alpha}([m_0-H,m_0+H])\ge Q^{-C}H Q
   \]

   or at least enough zeros to make the local average meaningful.

3. **Local averaged sieve**

   \[
   \sum_{\substack{|m_j-m_0|\le H\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
   |\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
   \ge
   Q^{-A_2}
   N_{Z_\alpha}([m_0-H,m_0+H]).
   \]

Then

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This theorem is logically correct, but its hypotheses are nearly as strong as the desired pointwise theorem. In particular, local badness propagation plus local zero abundance is not currently available.

---

# 8. Better formulation: pointwise \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence

The more honest target is pointwise:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, define the cofactor-flat bad set

\[
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
=
\{u:\mathbf M(u)=0\}.
\]

Then prove actual-orbit avoidance:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}(u(m_0),\mathcal M_{\rm flat})\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The averaged zero-set large sieve remains useful as evidence and as a possible global theorem, but it is not enough for the RH contradiction unless the off-line zero can be chosen from a good set, which it cannot.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Averaged }\mathbf M\text{ zero-set large sieve does not imply the required pointwise lower bound.}
}
\]

To upgrade average to pointwise, one needs an additional bad-zero exclusion theorem. The natural candidates are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{local propagation of }\mathbf M\text{-smallness plus local zero abundance,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{direct actual-orbit avoidance of the cofactor-flat variety.}
}
\]

The first seems unlikely to be easier because propagation intervals are too small relative to zero spacing. Therefore the next theorem should be named directly:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem: }
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\Rightarrow |\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The zero-set large sieve is still useful, but as an averaged companion theorem, not as a substitute for pointwise \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence.
