## Agent 4 / D — Pointwise \(\mathbf M\) from averaged large sieve

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: determine whether an averaged \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve can imply the required pointwise lower bound

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The current round has moved from the parked cell theorem to the cofactor-vector theorem for \(\mathbf M\), with the averaged zero-set large sieve as the natural first formulation. 

---

# 1. Averaged theorem does not imply pointwise theorem

The averaged theorem is

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

The needed theorem is pointwise:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The averaged statement permits exceptional zeros. For example, one could have

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\]

at a specific zero \(m_0\), while

\[
|\mathbf M(m_j)|\gg Q^{-A}
\]

for most other zeros in \(J\). The average remains large.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A zero-set large sieve is not sufficient by itself.}
}
\]

It is an averaged nonconcentration theorem, not a pointwise exclusion theorem.

---

# 2. Bad-zero exclusion principle needed

To upgrade average to pointwise, we need a separate principle of the form:

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{many nearby }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros also have small }\mathbf M.
\]

A precise version:

## Bad-zero propagation principle

Let \(m_0\) satisfy

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\le Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J_0=[m_0-H,m_0+H]
\]

such that

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J_0\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\le
Q^{-A_1}N_{Z_\alpha}(J_0).
\]

Together with the averaged lower bound on \(J_0\), this would contradict the bad zero.

So the averaged theorem implies pointwise only if badness propagates from one zero to a local family of zeros.

---

# 3. Derivative propagation is too local

Suppose

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\le Q^{-A_0}.
\]

If we have a derivative bound

\[
|\partial_m \mathbf M(m)|\le Q^C,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf M(m)|\le 2Q^{-A_0}
\]

only for

\[
|m-m_0|\le Q^{-A_0-C}.
\]

With normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

a bound

\[
|\mathcal D \mathbf M|\le Q^C
\]

gives propagation over

\[
|m-m_0|\le \lambda Q^{-A_0-C}.
\]

Since ordinary scale has

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

this is roughly

\[
|m-m_0|\le Q^{-A_0-C-1}.
\]

That is far smaller than a typical zero spacing unless the zero set is extremely crowded.

Thus derivative propagation alone does not produce enough nearby \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros for an averaged theorem to contradict the bad zero.

---

# 4. Local zero density does not rescue the argument

One might hope \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros are dense enough near \(m_0\). But the previous local-amplitude/zero-crowding branch treated excessive microscopic zero crowding as an exceptional condition, not a guaranteed fact.

To use local density, we would need something like

\[
N_{Z_\alpha}([m_0-H,m_0+H])\ge Q^{-C}HQ
\]

for an \(H\) small enough that \(\mathbf M\)-smallness propagates.

But the propagation radius from derivative bounds is much smaller than natural zero spacing. Taking \(H\) large enough to contain many zeros allows \(\mathbf M\) to oscillate significantly, since \(\mathbf M\) has subset-product frequencies

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad |S|=R+1.
\]

So there is a tension:

\[
\boxed{
\text{short }H:\text{ badness propagates but there may be no other zeros;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{long }H:\text{ there are zeros but badness need not propagate.}
}
\]

This blocks a simple averaged-to-pointwise transfer.

---

# 5. Stronger local averaged theorem would still not be enough

A stronger local version would be

\[
\sum_{\substack{|m_j-m_0|\le H\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}
N_{Z_\alpha}([m_0-H,m_0+H])
\]

for every admissible \(m_0\).

But to imply pointwise, \(H\) must be so small that

\[
|\mathbf M(m_j)-\mathbf M(m_0)|
\]

is controlled for all zeros in the window.

That again requires \(H\) on the order of the derivative propagation scale. Such a window may contain only \(m_0\), or no other zeros. If it contains only \(m_0\), then the local averaged theorem is just the pointwise theorem in disguise.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a sufficiently local averaged theorem collapses back to the pointwise theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Comparison with the cell theorem

This is exactly the same obstruction seen in the degree-one cell-sum theorem.

There, an averaged theorem like

\[
\sum_{Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}|B(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}
\]

did not imply

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|B(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Here the situation is harder, because

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+\cdots
\]

has high-degree subset-product frequencies. It can oscillate more rapidly and with more complicated resonance structure than the degree-one cell vector.

So any averaged-to-pointwise upgrade for \(\mathbf M\) is at least as hard as the corresponding upgrade for the cell theorem.

---

# 7. Conditional averaged-to-pointwise theorem

A logically valid theorem would be:

## Conditional theorem

Assume:

1. **Averaged zero-set large sieve**

   \[
   \sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
   |\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
   \ge
   Q^{-A_1}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
   \]

2. **Bad-zero propagation**

   If

   \[
   Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
   \qquad
   |\mathbf M(m_0)|\le Q^{-A_2},
   \]

   then for some interval \(J_0\ni m_0\),

   \[
   |\mathbf M(m_j)|\le Q^{-A_3}
   \]

   for a positive proportion of zeros \(m_j\in J_0\).

3. **Local zero abundance**

   \[
   N_{Z_\alpha}(J_0)\ge1
   \]

   and preferably

   \[
   N_{Z_\alpha}(J_0)\gg Q^{-C}|J_0|Q.
   \]

Then

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But assumptions 2 and 3 are strong and currently unavailable. In practice, they are close to the pointwise theorem itself.

---

# 8. More honest pointwise theorem

The clean theorem to name is:

## Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem

For every admissible ordinary-scale zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the cofactor vector satisfies

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, if

\[
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
=
\{u:\mathbf M(u)=0\},
\]

then the actual prime-log orbit satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
u(m_0),
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

This is the true pointwise input needed after the parked cell theorem.

The averaged large sieve remains valuable as a companion theorem and diagnostic, but not as a substitute.

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Averaged }\mathbf M\text{ large sieve does not imply pointwise }\mathbf M\text{ nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

To upgrade average to pointwise, one needs a bad-zero exclusion principle. The natural route via derivative propagation fails because the propagation scale is too short relative to zero spacing.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pointwise Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence must be treated as a separate actual-orbit theorem.}
}
\]

The averaged theorem is still useful, especially for understanding typical behavior and for later zero-set spectral estimates, but the RH proof route needs the pointwise statement at the specific admissible \(Z_\alpha\)-zero.
## User (2026-04-27 07:48:00)

Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:48:09)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 4 / D — Direct pointwise \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: bypass the averaged large sieve and attack the pointwise theorem directly,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The prompt asks for a direct actual-orbit avoidance formulation, codimension/recurrence comparison, and a verdict on whether the cofactor structure gives stronger anti-recurrence than the degree-one cell theorem. 

---

# 1. Cofactor-flat variety

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

The parked cell theorem supplies

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

So the next pointwise target is

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Define the cofactor-flat variety in phase coordinates by

\[
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
=
\{u:\mathbf M(u)=0\}.
\]

The actual phase orbit is

\[
u(m)
=
\left(e^{-im\log n}\right)_n
\]

with folded dual and background phases included as prescribed by the canonical AFE.

Then the desired pointwise theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(u(m_0),\mathcal M_{\rm flat}\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the exact pointwise cofactor nonrecurrence statement.

---

# 2. Cofactor expansion and bad set

The cofactor vector has schematic expansion

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

with

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

Thus

\[
\mathbf M(m)\approx0
\]

is a vector-valued subset-product cancellation condition:

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im\log N_S}
+
\cdots
\approx0.
\]

The bad event is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\mathbf M(m_0)\approx0.
\]

The first equation is one complex scalar condition. The second is a vector condition whose effective dimension depends on the rank of the cofactor-vector coefficient system

\[
\{\mathbf A_S\}_S.
\]

---

# 3. Codimension estimate

If \(\mathbf M\) has effective rank \(d_M\), then

\[
\mathbf M(m)\approx0
\]

is approximately \(d_M\) complex conditions, i.e.

\[
2d_M
\]

real constraints.

Conditioning on

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\]

removes one complex condition. So the combined bad event has heuristic codimension

\[
2+2d_M.
\]

If \(d_M\asymp R\), then the recurrence cost to hit a \(Q^{-A}\)-tube is roughly

\[
Q^{2A(d_M+1)}
=
\exp\!\left(
O_A\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

If \(d_M\) is only \(O(1)\), the recurrence cost is merely polynomial in \(Q\), too cheap to prove a pointwise lower bound by recurrence heuristics.

Therefore, the cofactor route needs an **effective-rank theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{rank}_{\rm eff}
\{\mathbf A_S\}_S
\ge cR
}
\]

or at least enough rank to make cofactor-flatness a high-codimension event.

---

# 4. Comparison with the cell-flat variety

The fixed-width cell theorem dealt with the cell-flat condition

\[
B_r(m)\approx0,
\qquad 1\le r\le M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

That event imposed roughly \(R\) complex constraints and was therefore a plausible high-codimension actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

The cofactor-flat condition

\[
\mathbf M(m)\approx0
\]

may be similar or stronger if \(\mathbf M\) has many independent components.

But there is a danger:

\[
\mathbf M
\]

is not an arbitrary \(R\)-dimensional vector of independent sums. It is a cofactor vector, so its components are algebraically linked minors of the same jet block. Its effective rank may be smaller than its ambient dimension.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cofactor nonrecurrence is plausibly harder than cell nonrecurrence unless an effective-rank/coefficient-mass theorem is proved.}
}
\]

The exterior structure gives more equations, but also more algebraic dependence.

---

# 5. Does exterior/minor structure help?

The cofactor vector is the Hodge dual of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet row block. If the \(q''_{\can}\)-rows are well-conditioned, then \(\mathbf M\) should have nontrivial exterior volume.

Coefficient-level evidence should take the form

\[
\sum_S |\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is a diagonal/exterior-mass statement. It says the cofactor vector is not symbolically zero.

But pointwise nonrecurrence requires more:

\[
\left|
\sum_S\mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The exterior structure therefore helps in two ways:

1. It supplies a plausible large coefficient mass.
2. It may increase effective vector rank.

But it does **not** by itself prevent subset-product phase cancellation at a specific \(m_0\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exterior structure improves the target but does not close pointwise nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Direct proof mechanism attempt

A direct proof would need one of the following.

## 6.1 Effective-rank plus actual-orbit avoidance

Show:

\[
\mathbf M(m)=
\sum_{\nu}
\mathbf A_\nu e^{-im\Omega_\nu}
\]

has effective vector rank

\[
d_M\ge cR,
\]

and prove the actual orbit avoids the cofactor-flat tube:

\[
\left\{
m:
\left|
\sum_\nu \mathbf A_\nu e^{-im\Omega_\nu}
\right|
\le Q^{-A}
\right\}
\]

at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

This is the cleanest pointwise formulation.

## 6.2 Deterministic lower bound from dominant exterior minor

If one exterior minor family dominates all others, then

\[
|\mathbf M(m)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

could follow from coefficient dominance.

But previous Wronskian/minor-isolation analysis found no local dominance mechanism: subset-product phases are dense, and filtering a single minor is nonlocal.

So this route is unlikely.

## 6.3 Positivity or norm structure

If \(|\mathbf M|^2\) had a positive diagonal representation that survived pointwise, it might be possible to prove a lower bound.

But \(\mathbf M(m)\) itself is a vector exponential sum. Its norm squared has positive diagonal only after averaging or summing over \(m\). Pointwise, off-diagonal cancellation remains.

So this route again becomes nonrecurrence.

---

# 7. Averaged theorem is weaker

Averaged large sieve:

\[
\sum_{m_j:Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}
\]

would establish typical non-smallness. But it allows isolated bad zeros.

For the RH contradiction, the off-line zero \(m_0\) is arbitrary; we cannot replace it by a good zero. Therefore the averaged theorem is insufficient unless paired with a bad-zero exclusion principle.

As argued before, derivative propagation of \(\mathbf M\)-smallness is too local relative to zero spacing. So averaged-to-pointwise transfer is not currently viable.

---

# 8. Named theorem needed

The direct pointwise theorem should now be named.

## Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem

Let \(m_0,\alpha\) be an admissible ordinary-scale \(Z_\alpha\)-zero:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)
\]

be the canonical cofactor vector built from the full source curvature

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

using the basis-normalized Wronskian rows

\[
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

Then there exists \(A>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
u(m_0),
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the pointwise theorem needed after the parked cell theorem.

---

# 9. Supporting subtheorems

The named theorem should be decomposed into two supporting inputs.

## A. Exterior coefficient mass

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is coefficient-level and likely Green-feasible via basis normalization and source-row rank.

## B. Actual subset-product cofactor nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\left|
\sum_S\mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+
\cdots
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is the true arithmetic input.

The first is structural. The second is actual-orbit arithmetic.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No direct pointwise proof of }|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}\text{ is currently available.}
}
\]

The exterior/minor structure makes the theorem plausible by increasing effective codimension, but it does not by itself prevent pointwise subset-product cancellation.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence should be named as the next black-box arithmetic input unless a new proof mechanism appears.}
}
\]

It is narrower than the final Wronskian angle/incidence theorem, but harder than the degree-one cell theorem because its frequencies are subset products of degree \(R+1\).
## User (2026-04-27 07:53:26)

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:53:32)

_Thought for 4s_

## Agent 4 / D — Pointwise Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

Executing the assigned Agent 4 task: attack the pointwise theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

rather than relying on an averaged zero-set large sieve. The prompt asks for an actual-orbit avoidance formulation, codimension comparison, recurrence-cost analysis, and a decision whether this should become a named black-box theorem. 

---

# 1. Cofactor-flat variety

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the basis-normalized Wronskian expands as

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

The parked cell theorem gives

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_z}.
\]

The next necessary input is

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A_M}.
\]

Define the cofactor-flat variety

\[
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
=
\{u:\mathbf M(u,\alpha)=0\},
\]

where \(u\) denotes the full actual prime-log phase vector, including main, folded-dual, background, and canonical error coordinates as needed.

The pointwise theorem is therefore the actual-orbit avoidance statement

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(u(m_0),\mathcal M_{\rm flat}\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the **Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem**.

---

# 2. Expansion of \(\mathbf M\)

The cofactor vector has schematic expansion

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

where

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

For a full canonical model,

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

the expansion contains pure-main, pure-dual, mixed main/dual, \(B_2\)-containing, and \(E_2\)-perturbed minors. Thus the true phase set is larger than the displayed pure-main subset-product family.

The flat event is

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+
\cdots
\approx0.
\]

This is a vector-valued subset-product cancellation condition.

---

# 3. Codimension estimate

Let

\[
d_{\rm eff}
=
\operatorname{rank}_{\rm eff}\{\mathbf A_S\}_S
\]

be the effective complex dimension of the cofactor vector.

The event

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)\approx0
\]

has heuristic real codimension

\[
2d_{\rm eff}.
\]

Together with

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the full bad event has heuristic real codimension

\[
2+2d_{\rm eff}.
\]

If

\[
d_{\rm eff}\asymp R,
\]

then a \(Q^{-A}\)-tube around the bad set has recurrence cost roughly

\[
Q^{2A(R+1)}
=
\exp\left(
O_A\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is much more expensive than the scalar Wronskian-incidence event

\[
Z_\alpha\approx0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0,
\]

which has only codimension four and generic recurrence cost \(Q^{O(A)}\).

So the cofactor theorem is plausibly easier than final angle/incidence **if** \(d_{\rm eff}\asymp R\).

But this codimension heuristic is not proof.

---

# 4. Comparison with the cell-flat event

The parked cell theorem had bad event

\[
B_r(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
1\le r\le M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

That was also an \(R\)-complex-constraint event.

The cofactor-flat event is similar in spirit, but harder in two ways:

1. The frequencies are subset-product frequencies

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad |S|=R+1,
\]

rather than degree-one prime-log frequencies.

2. The coefficients \(\mathbf A_S\) are exterior/cofactor coefficients, not simple AFE coefficients. They contain determinant signs, basis-normalization factors, and mixed canonical contributions.

The cofactor-flat event may therefore have high codimension, but its resonance structure is much more complicated.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cofactor nonrecurrence is higher-degree and harder than cell nonrecurrence, but still narrower than final Wronskian angle/incidence.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Does exterior/minor structure help?

The exterior structure gives a plausible diagonal mass statement:

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is a structural input, likely accessible through basis-normalized Gram/exterior-volume estimates.

But diagonal mass does not imply pointwise nonvanishing. The actual value is

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)
=
\sum_S \mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+\cdots.
\]

Even if the coefficient mass is large, the phases may cancel.

Thus exterior structure helps by ensuring that \(\mathbf M\) is not symbolically zero, but it does not prove

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A pointwise nonrecurrence theorem is still required.

---

# 6. Direct proof routes considered

## 6.1 Dominant minor

If one subset family \(S_0\) dominated all others, then

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

could follow from coefficient dominance.

But previous filtered-minor analysis showed that isolating a single subset-product minor is nonlocal, and no dominance mechanism is visible in packet-frequency support.

So this route is currently unavailable.

## 6.2 Positivity

If \(\mathbf M\) admitted a positive-energy representation pointwise, one could obtain lower bounds from diagonal mass. But \(\mathbf M\) is an exterior cofactor vector, not a positive quadratic form.

The positive diagonal appears only after averaging:

\[
\int |\mathbf M(m)|^2dm.
\]

Pointwise, the off-diagonal subset-product phases remain.

So positivity does not close the pointwise theorem.

## 6.3 Actual-orbit avoidance

The cleanest possible proof is a direct avoidance theorem:

\[
u(m_0)
\notin
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}^{(Q^{-A})}
\quad
\text{whenever }
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

This must use actual prime-log arithmetic, not relaxed phase geometry.

This is the correct final formulation.

---

# 7. Averaged large sieve is insufficient

The averaged zero-set large sieve would state

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

This proves typical non-smallness of \(\mathbf M\) on \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

It does not exclude an isolated bad zero

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Derivative propagation of \(\mathbf M\)-smallness is too local relative to the expected spacing of \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros. Therefore averaged-to-pointwise transfer requires an additional bad-zero exclusion theorem, which is essentially another pointwise nonrecurrence input.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The averaged large sieve is useful, but not sufficient for the RH route.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Named theorem statement

## Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let

\[
\mathbf M(m,\alpha)
\]

be the canonical cofactor vector formed from the basis-normalized \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block

\[
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R,
\]

with

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

For every admissible ordinary-scale zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

there exists \(A>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
u(m_0),
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem is the second black-box arithmetic input in the ordinary Wronskian route, after Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence.

---

# 9. Supporting subtheorems

A natural decomposition is:

## A. Exterior Mass Theorem

\[
\boxed{
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is structural and likely Green-feasible.

## B. Subset-Product Cofactor Nonrecurrence

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\left|
\sum_S\mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+\cdots
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the genuine actual-orbit arithmetic theorem.

## C. Canonical Transfer

Any model theorem must transfer to

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

with derivative control through approximately \(2R+1\) normalized derivatives.

---

# 10. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No pointwise proof is currently available.}
}
\]

The cofactor theorem should be named as a black-box input unless Agents 1–3 find a real proof mechanism through the zero-set kernel/resonance route.

The current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence is structurally plausible, but arithmetically open.}
}
\]

It is narrower than final angle/incidence but harder than the degree-one cell theorem because it involves degree-\((R+1)\) subset-product frequencies.

## Agent 4 / D — Pointwise Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: attack or formally name the pointwise cofactor theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The current prompt asks specifically for the cofactor-flat variety, actual-orbit avoidance formulation, effective codimension, recurrence comparison, and whether exterior/minor structure gives a deterministic pointwise lower bound. 

---

# 1. Cofactor-flat variety

Let \(u(m)\) denote the actual phase vector entering the canonical \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block, including main, folded-dual, \(B_2\), and controlled \(E_2\) components as appropriate.

Define

\[
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
=
\{u:\mathbf M(u)=0\}.
\]

The pointwise target is the actual-orbit avoidance theorem

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}(u(m_0),\mathcal M_{\rm flat})\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Here

\[
\mathbf M(m)
=
\sum_{|S|=R+1}
\mathbf A_S e^{-im\Omega_S}
+
\text{dual/background/error},
\]

with

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

---

# 2. Effective codimension

Let

\[
d_{\rm eff}
=
\operatorname{rank}_{\rm eff}\{\mathbf A_S\}
\]

be the effective complex rank of the vector coefficient family.

The event

\[
\mathbf M(m)\approx0
\]

has heuristic real codimension

\[
2d_{\rm eff}.
\]

Conditioning additionally on

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\]

adds two real conditions, so the combined bad event has heuristic codimension

\[
2(d_{\rm eff}+1).
\]

If

\[
d_{\rm eff}\asymp R,
\]

then a \(Q^{-A}\)-tube recurrence cost is roughly

\[
Q^{2A(d_{\rm eff}+1)}
=
\exp\left(
O_A\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

This is comparable in type to the fixed-width cell-flat event and much more expensive than the scalar angle/incidence event

\[
Z_\alpha\approx0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0,
\]

which has only codimension four and recurrence cost \(Q^{O(A)}\).

So the cofactor theorem is plausibly a meaningful intermediate input, provided

\[
d_{\rm eff}\asymp R
\]

is actually true.

---

# 3. Comparison with degree-one cell-flatness

The parked cell theorem concerned

\[
B_r(m)\approx0,
\qquad 1\le r\le M_{\rm cell}\asymp R.
\]

That is a degree-one vector smallness condition with about \(R\) complex constraints.

The cofactor theorem concerns

\[
\mathbf M(m)\approx0,
\]

where \(\mathbf M\) is a degree-\((R+1)\) exterior/cofactor object.

Similarities:

\[
\boxed{
\text{both are high-codimension vector nonrecurrence statements;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{both are false in relaxed phase models;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{both require actual one-parameter prime-log arithmetic.}
}
\]

Differences:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cell-flatness uses degree-one frequencies }\log n;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf M\text{-flatness uses subset-product frequencies }\Omega_S=\log N_S.
}
\]

Thus the cofactor theorem is structurally analogous to the cell theorem but arithmetically harder because of subset-product resonances and mixed canonical minors.

---

# 4. Does exterior/minor structure give a deterministic pointwise lower bound?

It gives a strong coefficient-level statement, not a pointwise one.

The exterior coefficient mass theorem is expected to be Green-feasible:

\[
\sum_S |\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This follows from basis-normalized row rank / exterior volume, assuming the canonical jet rows are not degenerate.

But pointwise,

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)
=
\sum_S \mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+\cdots.
\]

Large coefficient mass does not prevent cancellation at one specified \(m_0\). Therefore exterior/minor structure alone gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nonzero symbolic/coefficient mass}
}
\]

but not

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise nonvanishing.}
}
\]

No deterministic lower bound follows without an actual-orbit nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 5. Why averaged large sieve is insufficient

The averaged theorem

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\]

allows isolated bad zeros. Since the off-line zero \(m_0\) is fixed by the contradiction setup, a typical-zero theorem is not enough.

An averaged-to-pointwise upgrade would need a bad-zero propagation theorem:

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_j)|\ll Q^{-A'}
\quad\text{for many nearby }Z_\alpha\text{-zeros}.
\]

But derivative propagation is too local relative to zero spacing, and \(\mathbf M\) has high subset-product frequency complexity. Thus no such upgrade is currently available.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the pointwise theorem must be treated as a separate input.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Possible proof mechanisms and their status

## 6.1 Dominant minor

A dominant exterior minor would give a pointwise lower bound if it were isolated. But previous filtering/minor-isolation work showed that subset-product frequencies are too dense for local isolation.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{No viable dominant-minor proof.}}
\]

## 6.2 Positivity

A pointwise positive representation of \(|\mathbf M|\) is not visible. Positivity appears only after averaging \(|\mathbf M|^2\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{No pointwise positivity mechanism.}}
\]

## 6.3 Actual-orbit high-codimension avoidance

This is the only clean route:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
u(m_0)\notin \mathcal M_{\rm flat}^{(Q^{-A})}.
\]

This is a genuine actual-zeta nonrecurrence theorem for subset-product frequencies.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{Plausible but unproved.}}
\]

---

# 7. Final named theorem

## Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(\mathbf M(m,\alpha)\) be the canonical cofactor vector formed from the basis-normalized \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block

\[
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad 0\le j\le R,
\]

with

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

For every admissible ordinary-scale zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

there is a constant \(A>0\) such that

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
u(m_0),
\mathcal M_{\rm flat}
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the next black-box arithmetic theorem after Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence.

---

# 8. Supporting named inputs

The theorem can be decomposed into:

## A. Exterior Coefficient Mass

\[
\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Likely structural / Green-feasible.

## B. Subset-Product Cofactor Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\left|
\sum_S\mathbf A_S e^{-im_0\Omega_S}
+\cdots
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is the true arithmetic input.

## C. Canonical Transfer

Any proof in a model must transfer to the full

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

cofactor vector with derivative control through approximately \(2R+1\).

---

# 9. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pointwise Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence is not proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{It should now be named as a black-box input unless Agents 1–3 produce a genuine zero-kernel/resonance proof.}
}
\]

The cofactor theorem is narrower than final angle/incidence, but it is still a new actual-zeta arithmetic nonrecurrence theorem over degree-\((R+1)\) subset-product frequencies.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:14:24)

_Thought for 8s_

## Agent 4 / D — Exterior algebra / Hodge-dual geometry

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: test whether the Wronskian matrix geometry itself gives an intrinsic lower bound for

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

The current shared background says the cell theorem and \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence are now parked as named inputs, and the active target is the final angle/incidence theorem. 

---

# 1. Exterior-algebra setup

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block rows be

\[
Q_j
=
\left(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(m_0)\right)_{\ell=0}^{R+1},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

These span a subspace

\[
V=\operatorname{span}\{Q_0,\ldots,Q_R\}
\subset \mathbb C^{R+2}.
\]

The cofactor vector is the Hodge dual

\[
\mathbf M
=
\star(Q_0\wedge Q_1\wedge\cdots\wedge Q_R).
\]

Thus

\[
\mathbf M\perp V.
\]

The first Wronskian row at \(Z_\alpha=0\) is

\[
\mathbf z'
=
\left(
C_1(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha,
\ldots,
C_{R+1}(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha
\right)(m_0,\alpha)
\]

up to the column convention and signs.

Then

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

Therefore the bad event is

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0,
\]

equivalently

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf z'\in V.
}
\]

So the final angle theorem is exactly a quantitative lower bound on the distance from the \(Z_\alpha\)-derivative row to the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet subspace:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V)
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|.
}
\]

Since

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
=
\|\mathbf M\|\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V),
\]

the desired angle bound is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V)}{\|\mathbf z'\|}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Relation to previous \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol-rank results

Earlier symbol-rank work showed, in packet-frequency coordinates, that the \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol ratio is not polynomially approximable by the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols. Schematically,

\[
\frac{z_n(\alpha)}{c_n}
\not\approx
P(x_n),
\qquad
\deg P\le R.
\]

This proves a **coefficient-symbol transversality** statement.

It says the formal \(Z_\alpha\)-row is not contained in the formal polynomial span of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows on the active packet-frequency block.

But the final angle theorem is stronger. It asks for pointwise phase-weighted nonalignment at the actual \(m_0\):

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0)
\not\approx
V(m_0).
\]

The rows \(Q_j(m_0)\) and \(\mathbf z'(m_0)\) are not just coefficient symbols; they are sums over actual phases:

\[
e^{-im_0\log n},
\]

with main/dual/gamma/canonical weights.

Thus symbol-rank gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not identically dependent as symbols}
}
\]

but does not give:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise distance from the actual phase-summed vector to }V(m_0).
}
\]

A phase-relaxed model can have symbol rank and still arrange

\[
\mathbf z'\in V
\]

at a particular phase point.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{previous }Z_\alpha\text{-symbol rank is necessary but not sufficient for the final angle theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Can Hodge-dual geometry alone give an angle lower bound?

No.

For arbitrary vectors \(Q_0,\ldots,Q_R\) and \(\mathbf z'\), even if

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

one can still have

\[
\mathbf z'\in V,
\]

so

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

Exterior algebra gives the identity

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
=
\operatorname{Vol}_{R+2}(\mathbf z',Q_0,\ldots,Q_R),
\]

but it does not lower-bound this volume from the lower bounds on

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|
\quad\text{and}\quad
\|Q_0\wedge\cdots\wedge Q_R\|.
\]

One also needs an angle lower bound:

\[
\sin\angle(\mathbf z',V)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus Hodge geometry identifies the missing input but does not provide it.

---

# 4. Quantitative exterior-angle theorem candidate

The strongest valid theorem form is:

## Exterior-Angle Nonalignment Theorem

Let

\[
V(m_0)
=
\operatorname{span}
\left\{
(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(m_0))_{\ell=0}^{R+1}
:
0\le j\le R
\right\}.
\]

Let

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0)
=
(C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0))_{\ell=1}^{R+1}.
\]

Assume:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z'(m_0),V(m_0))
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'(m_0)\|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|\|\mathbf M\|.
}
\]

This is exactly the Wronskian angle theorem.

---

# 5. Does the angle theorem reduce to prior inputs?

No. The prior named inputs give:

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

They do not give

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V)\ge Q^{-A}\|\mathbf z'\|.
\]

Indeed, \(\mathbf M\) is the normal to \(V\), so

\[
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

means \(V\) is well-defined and the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block has exterior volume. It does not prevent \(\mathbf z'\) from lying almost exactly in \(V\).

Thus the final angle theorem is genuinely independent.

---

# 6. Actual-orbit formulation

The bad event is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\mathbf z'(m_0)\in V(m_0).
\]

In phase coordinates, this is an actual-orbit incidence condition:

\[
u(m_0)
\in
\mathcal A_{\rm angle}
:=
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \mathbf z'(u)\in V(u)\}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u)=0.
\]

So the final theorem can also be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
(u(m_0),\mathcal A_{\rm angle})
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is a higher-order actual-zeta incidence theorem.

It is not a purely linear algebraic fact.

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed countermodel

In a phase-relaxed model, allow the prime phases to vary freely. Then one can impose:

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\]

\[
\|\mathbf z'\|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
\|\mathbf M\|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf z'\in V.
\]

These are finitely many real constraints in a high-dimensional torus. With enough active phases, the solution set is expected to be nonempty.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exterior-angle theorem is false in relaxed phase models.}
}
\]

It must use the actual one-parameter orbit

\[
m\mapsto e^{-im\log n}.
\]

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exterior/Hodge geometry gives the exact form of the missing theorem, not a proof.}
}
\]

The final ordinary Wronskian theorem should now be named:

## Wronskian Angle Nonalignment Theorem

At every admissible ordinary-scale zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),
V(m_0,\alpha)
\right)
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}
\|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)\|\,
\|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This theorem is not implied by:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It is the third and final ordinary-route actual-zeta incidence input.

## Agent 4 / D — Actual-orbit incidence variety

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: formulate the final angle theorem as avoidance of the bad incidence variety

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}
=
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0\},
\]

and determine whether actual zeta arithmetic supplies a mechanism excluding that incidence. The shared prompt identifies this as the final ordinary Wronskian incidence theorem after parking Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence and Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence. 

---

# 1. Actual phase orbit

Let \(u(m)\) denote the full finite phase coordinate system needed by the canonical Wronskian. At minimum this includes main AFE phases

\[
u_n^+(m)=e^{-im\log n},
\]

folded dual phases

\[
u_n^-(m)=e^{+im\log n},
\]

with gamma/folding factors absorbed into the coefficients, and deterministic smooth coordinates for \(B_2\), \(E_2\), and any amplitude derivatives.

Thus the actual orbit is

\[
m\mapsto u(m)
=
\left(
e^{-im\log n},
e^{+im\log n},
B_2^{(k)}(m),
E_2^{(k)}(m),
\ldots
\right).
\]

The important part is the one-parameter prime-log trajectory

\[
m\mapsto
(e^{-im\log n})_n.
\]

The bad incidence variety is

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}(\alpha)
=
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0\}.
\]

The desired theorem is

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
u(m_0),
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}(\alpha)
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Incidence geometry

The two equations defining \(\mathcal I_{\rm bad}\) are:

\[
Z_\alpha(u)=0,
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0.
\]

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
=
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle.
\]

So the second equation is

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0.
\]

Assuming the parked inputs

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

the remaining bad event is pure angle cancellation:

\[
\mathbf z'\perp \mathbf M.
\]

Equivalently, if

\[
V=\operatorname{span}\{\text{\(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows}\},
\]

then

\[
\mathbf M\perp V,
\]

and

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\mathbf z'\in V.
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}
=
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \mathbf z'(u)\in V(u)\}.
\]

---

# 3. Codimension in relaxed phase space

In a relaxed phase space with many independent phase coordinates, the condition

\[
Z_\alpha=0
\]

is one complex equation, i.e. two real constraints.

The angle condition

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=0
\]

is another complex equation, i.e. two more real constraints.

Thus the naive bad incidence has real codimension

\[
4.
\]

This is much smaller than:

\[
\text{cell-flatness},
\]

which imposed roughly \(R\) complex constraints, and smaller than:

\[
\mathbf M\text{-flatness},
\]

which also has high effective codimension if the cofactor vector has rank \(\asymp R\).

Therefore the final angle theorem is intrinsically harder by recurrence heuristics: it is a low-codimension incidence condition.

---

# 4. Why generic codimension is insufficient

A generic one-parameter orbit can hit a codimension-four tube at polynomial cost.

For threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A},
\]

a random codimension-four small-value event has probability approximately

\[
\varepsilon^4=Q^{-4A}.
\]

The recurrence time is therefore roughly

\[
Q^{4A}.
\]

This is far too cheap to exclude over the relevant height range if

\[
Q\sim\log m.
\]

Thus the lower bound

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

cannot follow from generic transversality or codimension.

It requires special actual-zeta arithmetic.

---

# 5. Can exact AFE structure make \(\mathcal I_{\rm bad}\) empty?

In relaxed phase space, no.

The phase-relaxed model has enough degrees of freedom to solve

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R=0
\]

while keeping

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The two parked norm lower bounds do not prevent orthogonality.

So the bad variety is expected to be nonempty in relaxed phase space.

The theorem must say not that

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}=\varnothing,
\]

but that the actual orbit

\[
m\mapsto u(m)
\]

does not approach it at polynomial scale at admissible zeros.

---

# 6. Candidate actual-zeta mechanisms

## 6.1 Euler-product rigidity

A possible mechanism would assert that the actual prime-log orbit

\[
m\mapsto(e^{-im\log n})_n
\]

cannot satisfy both:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)\approx0
\]

and

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)\approx0.
\]

This would be a genuine Euler-product rigidity theorem.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No such rigidity theorem is known in this framework.}
}
\]

It would need to exploit actual coefficient structure, not just rational independence of \(\log p\).

---

## 6.2 Functional-equation coupling

The folded dual branch imposes the relation

\[
u_n^-=e^{+im\log n}
\]

up to gamma factors, so main and dual phases are not independent.

This improves canonical fidelity and sometimes gives branch dominance in tilted regimes. But prior analysis found no uniform sign, positivity, or commutator invariant in the hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1.
\]

So functional-equation coupling alone has not produced an incidence lower bound.

---

## 6.3 Explicit-formula obstruction

A successful explicit-formula route would show:

\[
Z_\alpha\approx0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0
\]

force incompatible prime/zero statistics.

The obstacle is that \(Z_\alpha\) is essentially linear in AFE phases, while

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R
\]

is an exterior determinant / subset-product object. The explicit formula naturally controls linear statistics, not the determinant cancellation.

Thus this route currently reduces to folded subset-product nonrecurrence.

---

## 6.4 Zero-repulsion

One might try to prove that zeros of \(Z_\alpha\) repel zeros of \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\):

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)\ne0.
\]

But quantitative repulsion

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

requires a strong common-zero exclusion theorem for actual exponential polynomials.

No soft zero-repulsion law is visible.

---

# 7. Final incidence theorem candidate

The clean theorem is:

## Wronskian Incidence Avoidance Theorem

Let

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\) be the full canonical basis-normalized Wronskian with

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

For every admissible ordinary-scale zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl(
u(m_0),
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}(\alpha)
\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, assuming the parked norm inputs,

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

---

# 8. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No proof from generic geometry, Hodge duality, or codimension.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No current sign, positivity, commutator, or functional-equation invariant closes the theorem.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The theorem is false in phase-relaxed models and must use actual one-parameter zeta arithmetic.}
}
\]

Therefore the final angle/incidence statement should be named as the third ordinary-route black-box input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence Theorem}.
}
\]

This is the remaining ordinary-scale arithmetic obstruction after:

\[
\text{Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence}
\]

and

\[
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence}.
\]

Final Agent 4 conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The final ordinary incidence theorem is cleanly formulated but not proved.}
}
\]

## Agent 4 / D — Canonical audit of all named inputs

Executing the assigned canonical audit. The current architecture has stopped decomposing the ordinary Wronskian route and now uses three named ordinary-route inputs, plus a separate singular branch and downstream Gate 2 / row-conversion audit. 

---

# 1. Canonical object and mandatory convention

The canonical curvature throughout must be

\[
q''_{\can}
=
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The finalized background term is

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}
\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

Any proof that uses only one of

\[
P_2,\qquad D_2,\qquad B_2,
\]

or a proxy zero kernel, is not canonical unless a transfer theorem is supplied.

The ordinary Wronskian rows must be

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R,
\]

with

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

---

# 2. Audit of Input 1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

## Named input

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is obtained through the parked theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r|B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where the full canonical cell vector is

\[
B_r
=
B_r^+
+
e^{i\Theta_Z}B_r^-
+
B_r^{\rm bg}
+
B_r^E.
\]

## Canonical requirements

This input is canonical only if:

\[
B_r^+
=
\sum_{x_n^+\in I_r}
z_n^+(\alpha,m_0)e^{-im_0\log n}
\]

and

\[
B_r^-
=
\sum_{x_n^-\in I_r}
z_n^-(\alpha,m_0)e^{+im_0\log n}
\]

use the same AFE convention as the canonical \(Z_\alpha\).

The proof must include:

\[
B_r^{\rm bg}
\]

from completed/gamma/background terms, and

\[
B_r^E
\]

from the AFE error/tail.

A main-only theorem

\[
\sum_r |B_r^+|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

is insufficient unless paired with both:

\[
\|B^++e^{i\Theta_Z}B^-\|_2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and error/background transfer.

## Transfer needed

A model theorem

\[
\sum_r |B_{r,\model}|^2\ge Q^{-A}
\]

transfers to canonical if

\[
\|B_{\can}-B_{\model}\|_2
\le
\frac12Q^{-A/2}.
\]

Equivalently, one needs cellwise AFE/background/error control:

\[
\left(
\sum_r|B_r^{\rm bg}+B_r^E+\Delta B_r^{\rm model}|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\le
Q^{-A'}
\]

with \(A'\) larger than the final cell exponent.

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 1 is canonically acceptable only in full main+dual+background+error cell form.}
}
\]

It must not be cited from a plus-only, main-only, or low-prime proxy cell theorem.

---

# 3. Audit of Input 2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

## Named input

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Here \(\mathbf M\) is the cofactor/Hodge-dual vector of the canonical \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block.

## Canonical definition

Let

\[
Q_j
=
\left(
C_\ell(\mathcal D)\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right)_{\ell=0}^{R+1},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\star(Q_0\wedge Q_1\wedge\cdots\wedge Q_R).
\]

Equivalently, \(\mathbf M_{\can}\) is multilinear in the \(R+1\) canonical source rows.

Since

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

we have the multilinear expansion

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\sum_{\sigma\in\{B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\}^{R+1}}
\mathbf M[\sigma_0,\ldots,\sigma_R].
\]

This means mixed minors are structurally unavoidable.

## What cannot be done

One cannot prove only

\[
|\mathbf M[P_2,\ldots,P_2]|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and treat that as canonical.

One also cannot prove a prime-only cofactor theorem unless one proves

\[
\mathbf M_{\prime}\to \mathbf M_{\can}
\]

by a robust transfer estimate.

A \(B_2\)-only cofactor is diagnostic only. It must never be classified as proof-level Gate 1 evidence.

## Leading model

The safest canonical leading model is

\[
\mathbf M_{\lead}
=
\mathbf M[B_2+P_2+D_2],
\]

with

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\mathbf M_{\lead}
+
\mathbf M_{\pert}[E_2].
\]

This is safer than pure \(P_2\), pure \(D_2\), prime-only, or \(B_2\)-only models.

## Transfer needed

A lower bound

\[
|\mathbf M_{\lead}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

transfers if

\[
|\mathbf M_{\can}(m_0)-\mathbf M_{\lead}(m_0)|
\le
\frac12Q^{-A}.
\]

Because \(\mathbf M\) is multilinear in \(R+1\) rows, if each row perturbation is bounded by \(\varepsilon_E\), the cofactor perturbation has schematic size

\[
|\Delta \mathbf M|
\le
Q^{A_L}\varepsilon_E,
\]

where \(Q^{A_L}\) includes row norms, basis norms, and exterior-power combinatorics.

Thus one needs

\[
Q^{A_L}\varepsilon_E
\le
\frac12Q^{-A}.
\]

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 2 is canonical only if }\mathbf M\text{ is formed from }B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\text{ or transferred from }B_2+P_2+D_2.
}
\]

---

# 4. Audit of Input 3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence

## Named input

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'|\,|\mathbf M|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## Canonical determinant

The full determinant must be

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{R,\can}(m,\alpha)
=
\det
\left(
C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)
\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1},
\]

with

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\]

and

\[
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R.
\]

At \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\),

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{R,\can}(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'_{\can},\mathbf M_{\can}\rangle.
\]

## Canonical dependencies

Input 3 depends simultaneously on:

\[
\mathbf z'_{\can},
\qquad
\mathbf M_{\can},
\qquad
\text{and their angle}.
\]

Even if model versions satisfy

\[
|\mathbf z'_{\model}|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M_{\model}|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

a model angle theorem transfers only if both vectors and the inner product are stable:

\[
\|\mathbf z'_{\can}-\mathbf z'_{\model}\|
\le Q^{-A_z'},
\]

\[
\|\mathbf M_{\can}-\mathbf M_{\model}\|
\le Q^{-A_M'},
\]

and

\[
|\langle\mathbf z'_{\can},\mathbf M_{\can}\rangle
-
\langle\mathbf z'_{\model},\mathbf M_{\model}\rangle|
\le
\frac12Q^{-A}.
\]

The last bound follows from

\[
|\Delta\langle z,M\rangle|
\le
\|\Delta z\|\|M_{\model}\|
+
\|z_{\model}\|\|\Delta M\|
+
\|\Delta z\|\|\Delta M\|.
\]

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 3 is canonical only as a theorem about the full determinant with }G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}.
}
\]

A model angle theorem is not proof-level without vector and determinant transfer.

---

# 5. \(E_2\) derivative requirements

The Wronskian uses rows

\[
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\qquad
0\le j\le R,
\]

and columns

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D),
\qquad
0\le \ell\le R+1.
\]

Thus entries can involve

\[
\mathcal D^{j+\ell}q''_{\can}
\]

with

\[
0\le j\le R,
\qquad
0\le \ell\le R+1.
\]

The maximum normalized derivative order of \(q''_{\can}\) required is therefore

\[
2R+1.
\]

For \(q_\zeta\) itself this corresponds to physical source derivatives up to the corresponding shifted order, depending on the convention \(q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''\) or \(\Phi_\zeta'''\). The audit requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-A_E}
}
\]

on the relevant thickened ordinary packet interval.

This same \(2R+1\) order suffices for:

\[
\mathbf M,
\]

and the full determinant, since the determinant entries are the same row/column evaluations.

No stronger derivative order appears unless the proof differentiates the determinant itself after construction.

---

# 6. Required transfer theorems

## Transfer 1 — \(\mathbf z'\)

If a model \(Z_{\alpha,\model}\) is used, require

\[
\|\mathbf z'_{\can}-\mathbf z'_{\model}\|
\le Q^{-A_z}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf z'_{\model}|\ge Q^{-B_z}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'_{\can}|\ge Q^{-B_z'}
\]

with \(A_z\) larger than \(B_z\).

## Transfer 2 — \(\mathbf M\)

If a model \(\mathbf M_{\model}\) is used, require

\[
\|\mathbf M_{\can}-\mathbf M_{\model}\|
\le Q^{-A_M}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf M_{\model}|\ge Q^{-B_M}
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M_{\can}|\ge Q^{-B_M'}.
\]

## Transfer 3 — determinant / angle

If a model Wronskian theorem is used, require

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\can}
-
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\model}|
\le Q^{-A_W}
\]

and

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\model}|\ge Q^{-B_W}
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\can}|\ge Q^{-B_W'}.
\]

A convenient sufficient bound is rowwise perturbation with determinant Lipschitz control:

\[
|\Delta \det|
\le
Q^{A_{\det}}
\max_{j,\ell}|\Delta M_{j\ell}|,
\]

where \(A_{\det}\) is controlled by row-normalization, basis-conditioning, and the safe depth

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

---

# 7. Canonical guardrail theorem

## Canonical Gate 1 Transfer Guardrail

Assume ordinary scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Suppose a model theorem package proves:

\[
|\mathbf z'_{\model}|\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

\[
|\mathbf M_{\model}|\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and

\[
|\langle\mathbf z'_{\model},\mathbf M_{\model}\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A_3}.
\]

Assume canonical transfer bounds:

\[
\|\mathbf z'_{\can}-\mathbf z'_{\model}\|\le Q^{-A_1-C},
\]

\[
\|\mathbf M_{\can}-\mathbf M_{\model}\|\le Q^{-A_2-C},
\]

and

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\can}-\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\model}|
\le Q^{-A_3-C}.
\]

Then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_{\can}|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

for some \(A\), hence the canonical ordinary Wronskian lower bound follows.

This transfer requires

\[
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-A_E}
\]

and all tail/truncation/model errors small enough after determinant Lipschitz amplification.

---

# 8. What must never be treated as proof-level

The following are diagnostic only unless accompanied by a transfer theorem:

\[
\boxed{B_2\text{-only rows};}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{pure }P_2\text{-only cofactors};}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{pure }D_2\text{-only cofactors};}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{prime-only packet models};}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{zero-kernel proxies};}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{AFE truncations without }E_2\text{ derivative control};}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{main-only cell or cofactor lower bounds without folded dual/background/error control}.}
\]

---

# 9. Final audit verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The ordinary-route named inputs are canonically valid only if stated for the full completed AFE object.}
}
\]

The canonical proof package must use:

\[
Z_\alpha,
\qquad
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}.
\]

The derivative budget

\[
2R+1
\]

for \(E_2\) and tail control is the central analytic transfer requirement.

With those guardrails, a model theorem package can imply a canonical Gate 1 package. Without those guardrails, results remain proxy diagnostics, not proof-level statements.

## Agent 4 / D — \(q_0\)-wall and source-robust row search

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: attack the downstream \(q_0\)-wall after Gate 1/Gate 2, and determine whether the existing row architecture can survive the wall or needs a new source-robust row/input. The prompt defines the known row structure \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G\), \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}\), with \(H\sim -q_0(q''_{\can})^3/288\), and asks whether Gate 2 can force \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy or whether another row is needed. 

---

# 1. Current downstream obstruction

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives source mass:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Gate 2 is expected to give anisotropy-weighted source mass:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u(m)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

The known row architecture is

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

where

\[
H=yq''_{\can}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Thus even if Gate 2 gives

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}
\]

at some point, the currently known rows still carry the additional factor

\[
q_0u^2.
\]

So a row lower bound from \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) requires something like

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and enough pointwise lower control on \(u\).

The obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
q_0\approx0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
H\approx0,
}
\]

so all known \(H\)-divisible rows can collapse even when source and anisotropy remain live.

---

# 2. The \(q_0=0\) local model

The prompt gives

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we get

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Thus a clean wall model is:

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
u\ne0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u\ne0.
\]

If \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is not forced to cancel simultaneously, then Gate 2 can remain live:

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\ge
|u|^4.
\]

But the \(H\)-driven rows satisfy

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G=0,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

So the implication

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\text{known row lower bound}
\]

is false without an additional \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy theorem or a non-\(H\)-divisible row.

This is not a technical edge case; it is an algebraic wall.

---

# 3. Can Gate 2 force \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy?

The hoped-for theorem would be:

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast\in I_\rho:
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

But Gate 2 only controls

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u,
\]

Gate 2 is compatible with

\[
q_0\equiv0,
\qquad
u\not\equiv0.
\]

A model with

\[
q_0(m)=0+O(Q^{-N}),
\]

\[
u(m)\asymp Q^{-B},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G(m)\asymp u(m)
\]

has nontrivial Gate 2 mass while keeping

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C}
\]

for arbitrary fixed \(C\), if \(N\) is large.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 alone cannot force }|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

To get \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy, one would need an extra structural equation coupling \(q_0\) to \(u\), \(\Gamma_G\), or the off-line zero geometry. It is not contained in Gate 1/Gate 2 as currently stated.

---

# 4. Known Gram tower does not rescue the wall

The known pattern is

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

If every usable projected row has a leading factor \(H\), then at

\[
q_0=0
\]

all such rows vanish to leading order:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim0.
\]

Since

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288},
\]

the tower carries the same wall:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Adding more \(\Gamma_{G,k}\) channels may help if \(q_0\) is non-small, because one may find some live anisotropy direction. But it does not help if

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The known }H\text{-divisible Gram tower cannot by itself cross the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Source-robust row requirement

A source-robust row must have leading behavior

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
u^a \mathcal A(q_0,u,\ldots)
+
\text{controlled corrections},
\]

with

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The minimal useful form would be something like

\[
R_{\rm rob}
\sim
u^p\Gamma_G
\]

or

\[
R_{\rm rob}
\sim
u^p(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2},
\]

without an overall \(q_0\) or \(H\) factor.

At \(q_0=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u,
\]

so such a row would satisfy

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0}
\sim
u^{p+1},
\]

which is live whenever source is live.

The necessary theorem would be:

## Source-Robust Row Theorem

There exists a row/invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) in the local jet/scattering/Gram architecture such that

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
u^p\mathcal R(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Correction},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
|\mathrm{Correction}|
\le
\frac12|u^p\mathcal R|.
\]

Then Gate 1/Gate 2 mass would imply a row lower bound even on the \(q_0\)-wall.

No such row is currently identified in the known \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\) tower.

---

# 6. Candidate row families to inspect

The wall search should not continue inside rows already known to be \(H\)-divisible. It should inspect row families before or outside the \(H\)-projection mechanism.

Potential sources:

## 6.1 Raw scattering rows

Projected rows may acquire the \(H\) factor through normalization/projection. Raw or less-projected scattering rows might retain a term live at \(q_0=0\).

Target:

\[
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Needed audit:

\[
R_{\rm raw}
=
u^p\Gamma_G
+
q_0(\cdots)
+
\text{higher corrections}.
\]

## 6.2 Ambient/unprojected Gram rows

The projection onto \(\mathfrak f\) may be responsible for source-divisibility. Ambient Gram entries may contain source terms not multiplied by \(H\).

Target:

\[
G_{\rm amb}^{(k)}|_{q_0=0}
\sim u^p\ne0.
\]

## 6.3 Correction rows

Some correction terms discarded as lower-order in the nondegenerate branch may become leading on the wall. A row that is “correction” off-wall may be the wall-leading invariant.

Target:

\[
R_{\rm corr}
=
u^p
+
q_0(\cdots),
\]

so

\[
R_{\rm corr}|_{q_0=0}=u^p.
\]

## 6.4 Higher-order wall transport terms

If every low-order projected row is \(H\)-divisible, a higher-order transport term might break the \(q_0\) factor.

But if the all-order architecture is truly

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\]

then higher order will not help within that family.

---

# 7. Wall theorem alternatives

There are only three viable downstream options.

## Option A — \(q_0\)-wall exclusion theorem

Prove

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast:
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{false under the present Gate 1/Gate 2 information alone.}
}
\]

It would need a new structural relation involving \(q_0\).

## Option B — Source-robust row theorem

Find \(R_{\rm rob}\) with

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{plausible target, but no row currently identified.}
}
\]

This is the most promising wall-specific task.

## Option C — Wall-specific contradiction

Show that

\[
q_0\approx0,
\qquad
u\not\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G\approx u
\]

contradicts some other geometric, scattering, or global consistency condition.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no such contradiction identified.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Nondegenerate branch theorem

For completeness, if

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q}
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then the known rows give

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|
\sim
|H|(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
\]

with

\[
|H|\sim |q_0||u|^3.
\]

Thus

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|
\gtrsim
|q_0||u|^3
(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|).
\]

This is useful only if \(u\) also has a pointwise lower bound at the selected \(m_\ast\), not merely \(L^2\)-mass. A sampling lemma must choose \(m_\ast\) where source and anisotropy are simultaneously live.

This branch is conditionally viable, but it is not enough globally because of the wall.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }q_0\text{-wall is real.}
}
\]

Gate 1/Gate 2 do not force

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0,
\]

Gate 2 may remain live while all known \(H\)-divisible rows collapse.

The known Gram tower

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}
\]

does not rescue the wall.

Therefore the downstream proof needs a new input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{either a Source-Robust Row Theorem or a }q_0\textbf{-Wall Exclusion Theorem.}
}
\]

Given the current algebra, the source-robust row search is the more plausible next target.

## Agent 4 / D — Source-robust row / invariant search

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: search for a downstream row or invariant that remains visible at the \(q_0\)-wall, where the known \(H\)-divisible rows collapse. The prompt gives the known row architecture \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G\), \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}\), with \(H\sim -q_0u^3/288\), and asks whether any known row family escapes that factor. 

---

# 1. Wall condition

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Known rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

At the wall

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
H=0.
\]

But also

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Thus at

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0,
\]

the anisotropy channel can remain live while all known \(H\)-divisible rows vanish.

This is the core obstruction.

---

# 2. Higher Gram tower rows

The known tower has schematic form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

If this pattern is exact at leading order for all usable projected rows, then every such row contains the same factor

\[
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0
\]

for every \(k\), regardless of whether \(\Gamma_{G,k}\) is nonzero.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No row in the known }A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\text{ tower rescues the }q_0\text{-wall if all rows are }H\text{-divisible.}
}
\]

The higher tower may help choose a live anisotropy direction off-wall, but it cannot remove the wall itself.

---

# 3. What a source-robust row must look like

A row \(R_{\rm rob}\) can rescue the wall only if its leading term is not divisible by \(q_0\) or \(H\).

A sufficient schematic form is

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
u^p\mathcal R(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Correction},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

For example, if

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

then at \(q_0=0\),

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^{p+1},
\]

which is live whenever \(u\ne0\).

Similarly, a row of the type

\[
R_{\rm rob}\sim u^p(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}
\]

would survive on the wall if Gate 2 mass is live.

So the required theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists R_{\rm rob}
\quad\text{such that}\quad
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
}
\]

No known \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\)-row currently satisfies this.

---

# 4. Candidate families to inspect

## 4.1 Raw scattering rows

The \(H\)-factor may be introduced by the projection to the \(\mathfrak f\)-row or by a normalization step. Therefore raw scattering rows should be inspected before the \(H\)-projection.

Target form:

\[
R_{\rm raw}
=
u^p\Gamma_G
+
q_0(\cdots)
+
\text{higher terms}.
\]

Then

\[
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}=u^{p+1}.
\]

This is the most plausible source-robust candidate family.

Required audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute raw scattering rows before }\mathfrak f\text{-projection and check divisibility by }q_0.
}
\]

---

## 4.2 Ambient / unprojected Gram rows

The \(\mathfrak f\)-projection may remove source-robust components. Ambient Gram entries might contain wall-live terms.

Target form:

\[
G_{\rm amb}^{(k)}
=
u^p
+
q_0(\cdots).
\]

If

\[
G_{\rm amb}^{(k)}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

then the problem becomes whether this ambient row can be converted into a valid downstream contradiction without reintroducing \(H\)-divisibility.

Required audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Check ambient Gram rows for non-}q_0\text{-divisible source terms before projection.}
}
\]

---

## 4.3 Correction rows

Terms treated as lower order off-wall may become leading on the wall.

Suppose

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_G
+
C_7,
\]

where

\[
C_7
=
u^p
+
q_0(\cdots).
\]

Off-wall, \(C_7\) may be lower order relative to \(H\Gamma_G\). On the wall, \(H\Gamma_G\) vanishes and \(C_7\) becomes leading.

So each “correction” must be audited at \(q_0=0\), not only estimated relative to the off-wall leading term.

Required theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\exists C_k\text{ with }C_k|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0
}
\]

and correction cancellation must be controlled against other wall-leading terms.

---

## 4.4 Higher-order transport terms

If the all-order projected tower remains

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\]

then higher order does not help within the same projected family.

However, higher-order transport may contain wall-live pieces before projection or inside correction sectors.

So higher order is worth checking only outside the already-known \(H\)-divisible leading tower.

---

# 5. No-go inside the known projected tower

Assume:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
\text{terms also divisible by }H
\]

for all \(k\) in the accessible tower.

Then at

\[
q_0=0,
\]

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]

for all \(k\).

Under this assumption:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the known projected Gram tower cannot produce a source-robust row.}
}
\]

Therefore a wall solution must come from one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw rows, ambient rows, correction rows, or a new invariant.}
}
\]

---

# 6. \(q_0\)-wall exclusion is unlikely from Gate 2 alone

Could one instead prove

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

somewhere?

No, not from Gate 2 alone. At \(q_0=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Thus if

\[
u\ne0,
\]

then

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2=|u|^4
\]

can be nonzero, so Gate 2 mass is compatible with \(q_0=0\).

A local model

\[
q_0\equiv0,\qquad u\not\equiv0
\]

does not violate the Gate 2 integrand algebraically.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 does not exclude the wall without an extra equation coupling }q_0\text{ to }u.
}
\]

This makes the source-robust row search the more plausible route.

---

# 7. Source-robust row theorem candidate

## Source-Robust Row Theorem

There exists a canonical row or invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) in the local scattering/Gram architecture such that, in the wall regime,

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
u^p\mathcal R(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Err},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le
\frac12
|u^p\mathcal R|.
\]

Consequently, Gate 1/Gate 2 mass implies a nonzero downstream row even when

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

Required next calculation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute raw/ambient/correction row expansions at }q_0=0
\text{ and identify whether any contain }u^p\text{ or }u^p\Gamma_G\text{ without }q_0.
}
\]

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{No source-robust row is currently identified.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The known projected tower }A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}
\text{ cannot rescue }q_0=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass alone does not force }q_0\text{-nondegeneracy.}
}
\]

Therefore the downstream branch requires a new named input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row Theorem}
}
\]

or, less likely,

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(q_0\)-Wall Exclusion Theorem}.
}
\]

Given the current algebra, the Source-Robust Row Theorem is the better target.

## Agent 4 / D — Correction-row wall-leading audit

Executing the assigned task: audit whether correction terms in

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9
\]

can survive the \(q_0\)-wall and provide a source-robust downstream row. The current downstream status is that exact interval base-locus rigidity is useful, but Gate 2 propagation and the \(q_0\)-wall remain open; known projected rows \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}\) vanish when \(q_0=0\). 

---

# 1. Wall expansion to audit

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Known leading rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9,
\]

with

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

At the wall

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
H=0,
\]

but

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

gives

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Thus the nominal leading pieces vanish:

\[
H\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=0,
\]

\[
H\Gamma_{G,2}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

So the only possible rescue inside \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) is:

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0
\]

or

\[
C_9|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

---

# 2. What kind of correction would rescue the wall?

A wall-live correction must contain at least one term not divisible by

\[
q_0,\qquad H,\qquad q_0u^3.
\]

Useful forms include:

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p,
\]

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

or

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p(q')^a,
\]

with nonzero coefficient \(c\), and with the term not cancelled by other wall-leading pieces.

At \(q_0=0\),

\[
u^p\Gamma_G=u^{p+1},
\]

so such a term would be live whenever

\[
u\ne0.
\]

A correction-row wall theorem would have the shape:

\[
C_{\rm wall}
=
c\,u^p\mathcal R(u,q',q'',\ldots)
+
O(Q^{-C}|u|^p|\mathcal R|)
\]

with

\[
\mathcal R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Then

\[
|C_{\rm wall}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

could replace the \(H\)-divisible row on the wall.

---

# 3. Necessary divisibility audit

Each correction sector must be classified by its divisibility ideal.

Define the wall ideal

\[
\mathfrak I_{\rm wall}:=(q_0)
\]

and the stronger \(H\)-ideal

\[
\mathfrak I_H:=(H)\sim(q_0u^3).
\]

For every monomial term \(T\) in \(C_7,C_9\), classify:

\[
T\in(q_0),
\]

\[
T\in(H),
\]

or

\[
T\notin(q_0).
\]

The correction sector rescues the wall only if

\[
C_7\notin(q_0)
\quad\text{or}\quad
C_9\notin(q_0)
\]

after all internal cancellations are applied.

If instead

\[
C_7,C_9\in(q_0),
\]

then

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0}=C_9|_{q_0=0}=0,
\]

and the correction sector does not rescue the wall.

If still stronger,

\[
C_7,C_9\in(H),
\]

then the entire known projected row architecture remains \(H\)-divisible.

---

# 4. Candidate wall-leading terms

The terms worth searching for are:

## 4.1 Pure source terms

\[
u^p,\qquad p\ge1.
\]

At \(q_0=0\), these remain live.

If found in a correction row, the row can convert Gate 1 source mass directly, perhaps even without Gate 2 anisotropy.

## 4.2 Source-anisotropy terms without \(q_0\)

\[
u^p\Gamma_G,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
u^p\Gamma_G=u^{p+1}.
\]

These would be ideal: Gate 2 supplies anisotropy, while the row avoids \(H\).

## 4.3 Derivative-wall terms

\[
u^p(q')^a,
\qquad
u^p q' q'',
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G' .
\]

These may survive at \(q_0=0\), but they need extra control. If the row depends on \(q'\), it may vanish on subcases where \(q'=0\). Such a row is useful only if paired with base-locus or ODE rigidity.

## 4.4 Gamma-background corrections

Terms involving \(B_2\) or smooth background may survive \(q_0=0\), but they are dangerous: they may be diagnostics rather than source-driven rows. A background-only surviving term is not automatically useful for Gate 1/Gate 2 unless it is coupled to \(u\).

---

# 5. Possible cancellation among wall-leading corrections

Even if

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0}
\]

contains a live term, it may cancel with another wall-leading correction.

The needed correction-row theorem is therefore vector-valued:

\[
\left(
C_7|_{q_0=0},
C_9|_{q_0=0},
C_{11}|_{q_0=0},
\ldots
\right)
\]

must contain at least one component bounded below:

\[
\max_k |C_k|_{q_0=0}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

under Gate 1/Gate 2 mass.

A scalar correction term is not enough unless its coefficient and sign are fixed and no same-order cancellation exists.

So the correct target is:

## Wall-leading correction vector theorem

There exists a finite correction-row vector

\[
\mathbf C_{\rm wall}
=
(C_{k_1},\ldots,C_{k_s})
\]

such that

\[
\mathbf C_{\rm wall}|_{q_0=0}
=
u^p\mathbf R(u,q',\ldots)
+
\mathrm{higher}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R(u,q',\ldots)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on the Gate 2 wall branch.

---

# 6. Conditional correction-row theorem

The best theorem candidate is:

## Correction-Row Wall Theorem

Assume the known row expansion has

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}+C_{2k+1}.
\]

Suppose for some finite set of \(k\)’s,

\[
\mathbf C
=
(C_{2k_1+1},\ldots,C_{2k_s+1})
\]

satisfies

\[
\mathbf C|_{q_0=0}
=
u^p\mathbf R(q,u,q',\ldots)
\]

with

\[
|\mathbf R|\ge Q^{-A_R}
\]

whenever

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_G}
\]

and

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Assume further that higher-order correction errors satisfy

\[
|\mathrm{Err}_{\mathbf C}|
\le
\frac12 |u^p\mathbf R|.
\]

Then on the \(q_0\)-wall branch,

\[
|\mathbf C|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and downstream row conversion survives the wall.

This theorem would close the wall if such \(\mathbf C\) exists.

---

# 7. Current audit verdict

From the supplied structure, all **known projected leading rows** have the form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Therefore their nominal leading terms are all \(H\)-divisible.

No explicit correction term has yet been identified with

\[
C_k|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

So the present status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No correction-row wall rescue is currently certified.}
}
\]

The correction sector remains a plausible search space, but it must be audited term-by-term for \(q_0\)-divisibility.

---

# 8. No-go condition

If a direct calculation shows that every correction satisfies

\[
C_{2k+1}\in(q_0)
\]

for all accessible rows, then:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0
\]

for the full known row family.

If, more strongly,

\[
C_{2k+1}\in(H),
\]

then the entire projected row architecture is \(H\)-divisible to that order.

Under either condition, the wall cannot be rescued inside known projected correction rows.

Then the only viable options are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw scattering rows, ambient/unprojected rows, or a new invariant.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final answer

The correction-row audit does not currently close the \(q_0\)-wall.

The next concrete calculation should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{expand }C_7,C_9,\text{ and if available }C_{11},C_{13},\ldots
\text{ at }q_0=0
}
\]

and classify every term by divisibility in \(q_0\) and \(H\).

If one finds

\[
C_k|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

then formulate a Correction-Row Wall Theorem.

If all correction terms are \(q_0\)- or \(H\)-divisible, then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{known correction sectors do not rescue the }q_0\text{-wall}.
}
\]

At present, the downstream architecture still requires one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-Robust Row Theorem}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
q_0\text{-Wall Exclusion Theorem}.
}
\]

The current evidence favors the former as the more plausible target.
