## Agent 4 / D — Correction-row wall-leading expansion

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: audit whether correction terms \(C_7,C_9\) can rescue the \(q_0\)-wall when the nominal \(H\)-leading rows vanish. The current downstream focus is Gate 2 propagation and the source-robust row search at \(q_0=0\). 

---

# 1. Wall setup

Known projected rows have the form

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9,
\]

with

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288},
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
H=0.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Therefore

\[
(H\Gamma_G)|_{q_0=0}=0,
\]

\[
(H\Gamma_{G,2})|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

The correction-row question is exactly:

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\stackrel{?}{\ne}0
\]

or

\[
C_9|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\stackrel{?}{\ne}0.
\]

---

# 2. Divisibility audit needed

For every monomial term \(T\) in \(C_7,C_9\), classify it into one of:

\[
T\in(q_0),
\]

\[
T\in(H),
\]

\[
T\in(q_0u^3),
\]

or

\[
T\notin(q_0).
\]

Only terms in the final category can rescue the wall.

Terms that would survive include:

\[
u^p,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no \(q_0\)-factor and no \(H\)-factor.

At \(q_0=0\),

\[
u^p\Gamma_G=u^{p+1},
\]

so a term \(u^p\Gamma_G\) is wall-live whenever \(u\ne0\).

---

# 3. Candidate correction structures

## 3.1 Pure source correction

If

\[
C_7\supset c\,u^p
\]

or

\[
C_9\supset c\,u^p,
\]

then at the wall

\[
C_k|_{q_0=0}=c\,u^p.
\]

This would be the strongest possible rescue, because it would convert Gate 1 source mass directly.

No such term is currently known.

## 3.2 Source-anisotropy correction

If

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p\Gamma_G
\]

or

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

then Gate 2 can feed into the correction row without the \(q_0\)-factor.

At \(q_0=0\),

\[
u^p\Gamma_G=u^{p+1}.
\]

A \(u^p\Gamma_{G,2}\) term is useful if \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) remains live. If \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) vanishes but \(\Gamma_G=u\) is live, then \(u^p\Gamma_G\) is better.

No such term is currently certified.

## 3.3 Derivative correction

If

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p(q')^a
\]

or

\[
C_k\supset c\,u^p\Gamma_G',
\]

the term may survive at \(q_0=0\), but it is not automatically useful. It could vanish on subbranches such as

\[
q'=0.
\]

Such corrections need to be paired with interval/base-locus rigidity or a multi-row vector lower bound.

---

# 4. Internal correction cancellation

Even if a wall-live term appears in \(C_7\) or \(C_9\), it may cancel against another wall-live correction.

Therefore the right object is not a scalar correction but a correction vector:

\[
\mathbf C_{\rm wall}
=
(C_7,C_9,C_{11},\ldots)|_{q_0=0}.
\]

The desired lower bound is

\[
|\mathbf C_{\rm wall}|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

under the wall-branch Gate 2 assumptions.

A single wall-live monomial is not enough unless its coefficient cannot cancel with other monomials of the same order.

The correction-row theorem must therefore be vector-valued.

---

# 5. Conditional correction-row theorem

A usable theorem would be:

## Correction-Row Wall Theorem

Assume the projected row expansions satisfy

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}+C_{2k+1}.
\]

Suppose that for a finite set of indices \(k_1,\ldots,k_s\),

\[
\mathbf C_{\rm wall}
=
(C_{2k_1+1},\ldots,C_{2k_s+1})|_{q_0=0}
\]

has expansion

\[
\mathbf C_{\rm wall}
=
u^p\mathbf R(q,u,q',\ldots)+\mathrm{Err},
\]

where

\[
|\mathbf R|\ge Q^{-A_R}
\]

whenever the wall branch has Gate 2 mass:

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_G},
\]

and

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le \frac12 |u^p\mathbf R|,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf C_{\rm wall}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This would provide a source-robust downstream row on the wall.

---

# 6. No-go condition

If the correction expansions satisfy

\[
C_7,C_9,C_{11},\ldots \in(q_0),
\]

then

\[
C_k|_{q_0=0}=0
\]

for every known correction row.

If stronger,

\[
C_k\in(H)
\]

for every \(k\), then the entire known projected row family remains \(H\)-divisible.

Under either condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{known correction rows cannot rescue the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

Then the only remaining candidates are:

\[
\text{raw scattering rows,}
\]

\[
\text{ambient/unprojected rows,}
\]

or

\[
\text{a new invariant.}
\]

---

# 7. Present verdict

No explicit correction term has yet been shown to satisfy

\[
C_k|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

So the correction-row branch is not closed.

The correct next calculation is not another conceptual pass. It is a termwise expansion audit:

\[
C_7,\ C_9,\ C_{11},\ldots
\quad
\text{at}
\quad
q_0=0,\ u\ne0.
\]

For each term, record whether it lies in

\[
(q_0),
\quad
(H),
\quad
(q_0u^3),
\]

or survives the wall.

---

# 8. Final answer

\[
\boxed{
\text{Correction rows may rescue the wall only if some correction term is not }q_0\text{-divisible.}
}
\]

At present,

\[
\boxed{
\text{no such wall-live correction is certified.}
}
\]

Therefore the wall branch still needs one of:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Correction-Row Wall Theorem},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row Theorem},
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(q_0\)-Wall Exclusion Theorem}.
}
\]

Given the current algebra, the most concrete next step is the correction/raw/ambient row expansion audit at

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0.
\]

## Agent 4 / D — Raw/ambient \(q_0\)-wall row search

Executing Agent 4’s task: search outside the known projected \(H\)-divisible tower for a wall-live row or invariant. The downstream state is that Gate 2 still needs thick-set-to-interval propagation, and the \(q_0\)-wall remains real because known projected rows vanish when \(q_0=0\). 

---

# 1. Wall criterion

Known projected tower:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
H=0.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

so

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Therefore a row \(R\) is wall-live only if

\[
R|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

A useful wall-live leading term would have one of the forms

\[
u^p,\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no factor of

\[
q_0,\qquad H,\qquad q_0u^3.
\]

---

# 2. Projected tower no-go

If the projected tower has the structural form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
\text{terms divisible by }H
\]

or even merely

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in(q_0),
\]

then

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0
\]

for every accessible \(k\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No row inside the known projected }A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\text{ tower rescues the wall unless a correction term escapes }(q_0).
}
\]

So the search must move to:

\[
\text{raw scattering rows, ambient/unprojected Gram rows, or wall-leading correction sectors.}
\]

---

# 3. Raw scattering row candidate

The best candidate class is a raw row before \(\mathfrak f\)-projection.

The reason is structural: the \(H\)-factor may be introduced by projection, normalization, or quotienting. A pre-projection row may contain a source-visible term such as

\[
R_{\rm raw}
=
c\,u^p\Gamma_G
+
q_0(\cdots)
+
\mathrm{higher}.
\]

At the wall this becomes

\[
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}
=
c\,u^{p+1}
+
\mathrm{higher}.
\]

If the higher terms are perturbative, then

\[
|R_{\rm raw}|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

whenever \(u\) is live.

This would be stronger than the current \(H\)-tower rows because it would convert Gate 1 source mass, or Gate 2 mass through \(\Gamma_G\), without needing \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy.

## Required calculation

For each raw scattering row \(R_{\rm raw}^{(k)}\), compute the expansion modulo the wall ideal \((q_0)\):

\[
R_{\rm raw}^{(k)}
\equiv
\sum_{p,a,b} c_{pab}u^p(\Gamma_G)^a(\Gamma_{G,2})^b
+
\sum_{p,a}d_{pa}u^p(q')^a
\pmod{(q_0)}.
\]

If any coefficient survives, i.e.

\[
R_{\rm raw}^{(k)}\not\equiv0\pmod{(q_0)},
\]

then the raw row is a candidate source-robust row.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No raw row is certified wall-live yet, because the needed pre-projection expansion has not been computed.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Ambient / unprojected Gram row candidate

The second candidate class is an ambient Gram row before the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection.

A useful ambient row would satisfy

\[
G_{\rm amb}^{(k)}
=
c\,u^p
+
q_0(\cdots)
+
\mathrm{higher}
\]

or

\[
G_{\rm amb}^{(k)}
=
c\,u^p\Gamma_G
+
q_0(\cdots)
+
\mathrm{higher}.
\]

At \(q_0=0\),

\[
G_{\rm amb}^{(k)}|_{q_0=0}
=
c\,u^p
\quad\text{or}\quad
c\,u^{p+1}.
\]

This would solve the wall if the ambient row is admissible for the downstream contradiction and if correction terms are controlled.

But there is a possible obstruction: if the geometry forces every invariant row that survives the quotient/projection to lie in the ideal

\[
(q_0),
\]

then all ambient source terms may be killed when passing to the proof-relevant row space.

So the key audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the }H\text{-factor appear before projection, or only after projection to }\mathfrak f?
}
\]

If it appears only after projection, ambient rows may rescue the wall. If it is intrinsic to all invariant rows, they do not.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ambient rows remain a plausible search space, but no wall-live ambient invariant is identified.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Candidate classification table

For each candidate row \(R\), the audit should produce:

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}
\]

and classify it as follows.

| Class | Algebraic condition | Wall status |
|---|---|---|
| Wall-live | \(R\notin(q_0)\) | candidate |
| \(q_0\)-divisible | \(R\in(q_0)\) | wall-dead |
| \(H\)-divisible | \(R\in(H)\sim(q_0u^3)\) | wall-dead |
| Projection-dead | raw \(R\notin(q_0)\), projected \(R^{\mathfrak f}\in(q_0)\) | raw/ambient only |
| Cancellation-dead | wall-live monomials cancel in row vector | needs higher vector audit |

A source-robust theorem needs at least one row or row vector in the first class.

---

# 6. Source-robust row theorem candidate

The clean theorem to prove is:

## Source-Robust Row Theorem

There exists a canonical raw, ambient, or correction row vector

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}
=
(R_1,\ldots,R_s)
\]

such that, on the \(q_0\)-wall,

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0}
=
u^p\mathbf R_0(u,q',\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Err},
\]

with

\[
|\mathbf R_0|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

whenever Gate 1/Gate 2 source-anisotropy is live, and

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le \frac12 |u^p\mathbf R_0|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on the wall branch, giving downstream row conversion without requiring

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This theorem is the correct wall replacement for the nondegenerate \(A_7,A_9\) row-conversion branch.

---

# 7. No-go theorem if raw/ambient rows are also divisible

If a direct computation shows that every proof-relevant raw, ambient, and correction row satisfies

\[
R\in(q_0),
\]

then the wall cannot be solved by row search.

The resulting no-go is:

## Row-Architecture Wall No-Go

Assume every proof-relevant downstream row or invariant satisfies

\[
R(q_0,u,q',\ldots)\in(q_0).
\]

Then for any local model with

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0,
\]

all downstream rows vanish even though

\[
\Gamma_G=u
\]

and Gate 2 mass may be nonzero.

Therefore Gate 1/Gate 2 cannot imply row conversion without a new external wall-exclusion theorem.

This would force the project to seek a genuinely new invariant, not merely a different row in the current architecture.

---

# 8. Final verdict

No source-robust row is currently certified.

The known projected tower is wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

The only viable search spaces are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw scattering rows, ambient/unprojected Gram rows, correction rows, or a new invariant.}
}
\]

The next concrete calculation is termwise:

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}
\]

for every raw/ambient/correction candidate. If all such candidates lie in \((q_0)\), then the \(q_0\)-wall becomes a named downstream input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row Theorem / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

At present, the wall remains open.

## Agent 4 / D — Full conditional Gate 2 theorem

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: assemble the Gate 2 proof from set extraction, thick-set/Remez propagation, derivative propagation, and interval rigidity. The current bottleneck is no longer the set extraction step; it is converting the polynomial-measure approximate base-locus into an interval-scale approximate base-locus with enough derivative control. 

---

# 1. Target theorem

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 asks for

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

The known identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

with the established normalized derivative convention.

The exact interval rigidity theorem says

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\quad\text{on an interval}
\]

implies

\[
u\equiv0.
\]

The conditional Gate 2 proof must turn Gate 2 failure into an approximate version of that interval rigidity setting.

---

# 2. Contrapositive structure

Assume Gate 1 holds:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

For \(A\) sufficiently large relative to \(B\), a standard Chebyshev/energy extraction gives a set

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

such that on \(E\),

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

This step is Green. The issue is that \(E\) may be dust-like.

---

# 3. Required propagation input

The missing propagation theorem must have the following form.

## Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and finite analytic complexity

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|
\]

such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-C_1}.
\]

For Gate 2, this is not enough by itself. The output must also include one of:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}
\]

on a shrunken interval

\[
J'\subset J,
\]

or directly

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

Thus the exact needed black box is:

\[
\boxed{
E\text{ polynomial-measure approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus plus derivative/base-locus derivative control.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Why plain positive measure is insufficient

The extraction gives

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

but this alone does not imply interval smallness. A set of polynomial measure can be distributed as many tiny pieces. With only finite derivative upper bounds, a function can be small on such a dust-like set and still large between pieces unless one has a Remez/Cartan-type complexity theorem with acceptable loss.

The dangerous loss is:

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

if the effective complexity is \(R\). This is too expensive unless the extracted smallness exponent is made correspondingly enormous.

Therefore the propagation theorem must use one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{low effective complexity;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{relative density of }E\text{ at controlled scales;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{a Cartan/Remez theorem with only polynomial loss;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{additional structure of }\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ beyond generic finite degree.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Insert derivative propagation

Assume the propagation theorem first gives

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1}.
\]

To use interval rigidity quantitatively, we need either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2},
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

The identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

shows why this is necessary. Smallness of

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

alone allows cancellation between

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

and

\[
-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

So the derivative propagation theorem must supply one of the following.

## Version A — derivative control

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}
\]

under a complex-tube or Bernstein-type finite-complexity hypothesis.

## Version B — direct base-locus control

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

Version B would be stronger and more direct, but it appears harder because of the cancellation possibility above.

---

# 6. Apply approximate interval rigidity

Assume we have an interval

\[
J'
\]

such that

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

and

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

Then from

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

we get

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1}).
\]

From

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

we get

\[
2q(q')^2=O(Q^{-C_1})+O(Q^{-C_2}).
\]

Thus

\[
q(q')^2=O(Q^{-C_3}).
\]

On regions where

\[
|q|\ge \delta,
\]

this gives

\[
|q'|^2\le Q^{-C_3}\delta^{-1}.
\]

So \(q\) is nearly constant there. Combining with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1}),
\]

the near-constant values must approximately solve

\[
6q-2q^3=0,
\]

i.e.

\[
q\approx0,\quad q\approx\sqrt3,\quad q\approx-\sqrt3.
\]

In all three cases,

\[
u=q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1})
\]

is small on a shrunken interval:

\[
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-C_4}.
\]

This contradicts the retained lower bound

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

on the propagated interval if the exponents are chosen with

\[
C_4>C_u.
\]

Thus Gate 2 follows.

---

# 7. Conditional Gate 2 theorem

## Conditional Gate 2 Theorem

Assume:

1. **Gate 1**

\[
\int_I|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. **Finite complexity**

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0.
\]

3. **Set extraction**

Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives

\[
E\subset I,
\qquad
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\]

on \(E\).

4. **Thick-set-to-interval propagation**

Such an \(E\) yields an interval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|
\]

and

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

while preserving nontrivial source size on a subinterval or point.

5. **Derivative propagation**

On a shrunken interval \(J'\subset J\),

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}
\]

or equivalently

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

6. **Approximate interval rigidity**

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-C}
\]

implies

\[
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-C'}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(J''\subset J'\).

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 8. Open sublemmas

The conditional theorem reduces Gate 2 to two still-open analytic sublemmas.

## D1. Thick-set-to-interval propagation

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\quad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C}
\text{ on }E
\]

must imply interval-scale smallness.

Positive measure alone is insufficient. Need relative density, low-complexity Remez, or Cartan propagation with polynomial loss.

## D2. Derivative propagation

Interval smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

must imply either

\[
\Gamma_G''\text{ small}
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2\text{ small}.
\]

This is not automatic because

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

allows cancellation.

---

# 9. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is conditionally reduced but not proved.}
}
\]

The complete proof is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{set extraction}
+
\text{thick-set-to-interval propagation}
+
\text{derivative propagation}
+
\text{approximate interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Set extraction and interval rigidity are in good shape.

The active missing inputs are:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation for }\Gamma_G''\text{ or }q(q')^2.
}
\]

These should remain the main Gate 2 targets.

## Agent 4 / D — Full Gate 2 conditional theorem

Executing Agent 4’s task: assemble Gate 2 as a conditional theorem from set extraction, density/Remez propagation, derivative propagation, and interval rigidity. The current downstream state is that Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives a polynomial-measure bad set, but an interval-scale approximate base-locus still requires a density/Remez/Cartan propagation input. 

---

# 1. Target

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Gate 2 should prove

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

The relevant identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

under the established normalized derivative convention.

The exact interval rigidity theorem is:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\quad\text{on an interval}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
u\equiv0.
\]

The approximate version needs smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and either

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or directly

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

---

# 2. Contrapositive proof structure

Assume Gate 1 holds:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

By energy decomposition and Chebyshev, for \(A\) sufficiently large relative to \(B\), there exists a set

\[
E\subset I
\]

such that

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

and on \(E\),

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

This set extraction is already structurally sound. The obstruction is that \(E\) may be dust-like and need not contain an interval.

---

# 3. Required density/Remez propagation theorem

The first black-box input needed is:

## Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Let

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Assume

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

and a finite-complexity package

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0.
\]

Then there exists an interval

\[
J\subset I,
\qquad
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-C_1}.
\]

The theorem must have polynomial loss only. If the Remez/Cartan complexity is effectively \(N\asymp R\), the loss

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\left(O\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right)
\]

is too large unless the extracted smallness exponent is chosen far stronger. Therefore a usable version needs one of:

\[
\boxed{\text{relative density of }E\text{ at controlled scales}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{low effective complexity}},
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Cartan exceptional-set structure with polynomial loss}},
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{additional ODE structure of }(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})}.
\]

Without such a theorem, Gate 2 is not proved.

---

# 4. Required derivative propagation theorem

The second black-box input must bridge from smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

to the approximate interval rigidity hypotheses.

There are two acceptable versions.

## Version A — \(\Gamma_G''\)-propagation

If

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1},
\qquad
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

then on a shrunken interval

\[
J'\subset J
\]

one has

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

This may follow from either:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1}
\]

on a complex tube \(\mathcal T_\rho(J)\), via Cauchy estimates, with

\[
\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho},
\]

or a real Bernstein inequality of the form

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

## Version B — direct \(q(q')^2\)-propagation

Alternatively, one proves directly

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

This is enough because the exact base-locus proof uses the vanishing of

\[
2q(q')^2.
\]

But this does **not** follow merely from

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

being small, since \(2q(q')^2\) may cancel with \(-\Gamma_G''/6\). So either \(\Gamma_G''\)-smallness or a special no-cancellation argument is needed.

Thus the derivative input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}
}
\]

in either \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\) form.

---

# 5. Approximate interval rigidity

Assume we obtain an interval \(J'\) such that

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

and either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

Then from

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

we get

\[
u=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1}).
\]

Since \(u=q''\), this gives

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1}).
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

gives

\[
q(q')^2=O(Q^{-C_3}).
\]

Split \(J'\) into regions

\[
|q|\le \delta
\]

and

\[
|q|>\delta.
\]

On \(|q|>\delta\),

\[
(q')^2\le Q^{-C_3}\delta^{-1},
\]

so \(q\) is nearly constant on a shrunken subinterval. The approximate ODE

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1})
\]

then forces that near-constant value to be close to a root of

\[
6q-2q^3=0,
\]

namely

\[
q\approx0,\qquad q\approx \sqrt3,\qquad q\approx-\sqrt3.
\]

In all cases,

\[
u=q''=6q-2q^3+O(Q^{-C_1})
\]

is small on a shrunken interval:

\[
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-C_4}.
\]

This contradicts the propagated source non-smallness

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

if exponents are chosen so that

\[
C_4>C_u.
\]

So approximate interval base-locus rigidity gives the contradiction.

---

# 6. Full conditional Gate 2 theorem

## Conditional Gate 2 Theorem

Assume:

### (i) Gate 1

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

### (ii) Finite analytic complexity

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0.
\]

At least \(k_0=6\) is plausible because the expressions involve \(q,q',q'',\Gamma_G'',\Gamma_{G,2}\), and the propagation/rigidity step may differentiate further. The exact \(k_0\) depends on the chosen Remez/Bernstein mechanism.

### (iii) Set extraction

Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure yields

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C_E}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\]

on \(E\).

### (iv) Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

From this \(E\), obtain an interval

\[
J\subset I
\]

such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^{-C_1},
\]

and the non-smallness of \(u\) is retained somewhere or on a controlled subset.

### (v) Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

On a shrunken interval

\[
J'\subset J,
\]

obtain either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-C_2}.
\]

### (vi) Approximate interval rigidity

Smallness of

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2},\quad \Gamma_G''
\]

or equivalently of

\[
\Gamma_G,\quad q(q')^2
\]

implies

\[
\sup_{J''}|u|\le Q^{-C_4}
\]

on a shrunken interval \(J''\), contradicting retained \(u\)-mass.

Then Gate 2 holds:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. Current status of components

| Component | Status |
|---|---|
| Set extraction from Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure | Green |
| Exact interval base-locus rigidity | Green |
| Approximate interval rigidity | Conditional / mostly structured |
| Thick-set-to-interval propagation | Open |
| Derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\) | Open |
| Gate 2 as a whole | Conditional, not proved |

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is not yet proved.}
}
\]

It is conditionally reduced to two named analytic inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}.
}
\]

Together with the already established set extraction and interval rigidity, these imply Gate 2.

So the complete dependency is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Set extraction}
+
\text{Density/Remez propagation}
+
\text{Derivative propagation}
+
\text{Approximate interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

## Agent 4 / D — Final \(q_0\)-wall source-robust row audit

Executing Agent 4’s task: settle whether currently known row families contain a source-robust wall row, or whether this must be named as a downstream black-box input. The current downstream stop-condition round asks specifically for the projected tower no-go, the raw/ambient/correction audit table required, and the final named wall-resolution input if no certified row is available. 

---

# 1. Projected tower no-go

Known projected rows have leading form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\]

with

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

At the wall

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we get

\[
H=0.
\]

Therefore every row whose proof-relevant leading term is \(H\)-divisible is wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

This includes the known rows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

So the wall model

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
u\ne0
\]

can have live Gate 2 anisotropy while all known \(H\)-divisible projected rows vanish.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The known projected }A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\text{ tower does not rescue the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

---

# 2. What counts as a wall-live row

A row or invariant \(R\) is wall-live if

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Acceptable leading forms include

\[
u^p,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

provided they are **not** multiplied by

\[
q_0,
\qquad
H,
\qquad
q_0u^3.
\]

At the wall,

\[
u^p\Gamma_G=u^{p+1},
\]

so a row with leading term \(u^p\Gamma_G\) is source-robust.

A row with leading term \(u^p\Gamma_{G,2}\) is useful if \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) is live on the wall branch. A row with \(u^p(q')^a\) is weaker because it may vanish on subbranches where \(q'=0\), unless paired with Gate 2/base-locus rigidity.

---

# 3. Required audit tables

The wall cannot be settled conceptually from the known leading tower. It requires finite algebraic expansion modulo the wall ideal \((q_0)\).

## 3.1 Raw scattering rows

For every raw scattering row \(R_j^{\rm raw}\), compute

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0).
\]

Required output table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{row} & R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0) & \text{classification}\\
\hline
R_1^{\rm raw} & \cdots & \text{wall-live / }q_0\text{-divisible / }H\text{-divisible}\\
R_2^{\rm raw} & \cdots & \cdots
\end{array}
\]

A usable row has

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}.
\]

Target examples:

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\equiv c\,u^p,
\]

or

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\equiv c\,u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

or

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\equiv c\,u^p\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

## 3.2 Ambient / unprojected Gram rows

For every ambient or unprojected Gram row \(R_j^{\rm amb}\), compute

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
\]

The important diagnostic is whether the \(H\)-factor appears **before** projection or is introduced by the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection.

If

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\notin(q_0)
\]

but

\[
R_j^{\mathfrak f}\in(q_0),
\]

then the source-visible component exists but is killed by projection. That would suggest the need for an ambient/unprojected downstream invariant.

## 3.3 Correction sectors

For the known projected rows, write

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9.
\]

Then compute

\[
C_7\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
C_9\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
C_{11}\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
C_{13}\bmod(q_0),
\ldots
\]

A wall rescue exists if for some \(k\),

\[
C_{2k+1}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}.
\]

If instead

\[
C_{2k+1}\in(q_0)
\]

for all accessible correction sectors, then corrections do not rescue the wall.

---

# 4. Classification rules

Each candidate row or correction term should be classified as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall-live}
}
\]

if

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

\[
\boxed{
q_0\text{-divisible}
}
\]

if

\[
R\in(q_0).
\]

\[
\boxed{
H\text{-divisible}
}
\]

if

\[
R\in(H)\sim(q_0u^3).
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero only after cancellation}
}
\]

if individual terms survive modulo \((q_0)\), but cancel in the full row. This case requires vector-row analysis, because another row may retain the surviving direction.

The ideal audit should therefore be vector-valued:

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm wall}
=
(R_{j_1},\ldots,R_{j_s})\bmod(q_0).
\]

A wall theorem needs

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm wall}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

under Gate 2 wall-branch hypotheses.

---

# 5. Source-Robust Row Theorem candidate

If the audit finds a wall-live row vector, the theorem should be stated as follows.

## Source-Robust Row Theorem

There exists a canonical row or finite row vector

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}
\]

from the raw, ambient, or correction sector such that

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0}
=
u^p\mathbf R_0(u,q',\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Err},
\]

where

\[
|\mathbf R_0|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

whenever the wall branch has Gate 2 pointwise mass

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_1},
\]

and

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|\le \frac12 |u^p\mathbf R_0|,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This would close the \(q_0\)-wall branch of row conversion.

---

# 6. Final no-go if no wall-live row is found

If the finite audit proves

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\in(q_0),
\]

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\in(q_0),
\]

and

\[
C_{2k+1}\in(q_0)
\]

for all proof-relevant rows/corrections, then the current row architecture cannot cross the wall.

The resulting no-go is:

## Row-Architecture Wall No-Go

If every proof-relevant downstream row satisfies

\[
R\in(q_0),
\]

then for local configurations with

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
u\ne0,
\]

all known downstream rows vanish, even though

\[
\Gamma_G=u
\]

and Gate 2 mass may be live.

Therefore Gate 1 + Gate 2 cannot imply row conversion without a new invariant or external wall-exclusion theorem.

---

# 7. Final answer

No certified source-robust row is currently available.

The known projected tower is wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

Thus the downstream proof currently requires one of the following named inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(q_0\)-Wall Exclusion Theorem}.
}
\]

The more plausible route is the first: find a raw, ambient, or correction row whose reduction modulo \((q_0)\) is nonzero.

The next concrete calculation is exactly:

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0)
\]

for all proof-relevant rows. If all vanish, the wall becomes a named black-box obstruction.

## Agent 4 / D — D3: Source-robust row / \(q_0\)-wall resolution

Executing Agent 4’s assignment: attack the \(q_0\)-wall structurally by checking whether any raw, ambient, or unprojected row can survive where the known projected tower vanishes. The current downstream layer is explicitly reduced to D1/D2 propagation inputs plus D3 wall resolution and D4 nondegenerate row conversion. 

---

# 1. Projected tower no-go

Known projected rows have leading form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\]

with

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

At the \(q_0\)-wall,

\[
q_0=0,
\]

so

\[
H=0.
\]

Therefore every projected row whose leading term is \(H\)-divisible satisfies

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

In particular,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are wall-dead.

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Thus the local wall model

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0
\]

can retain Gate 2 mass while all known \(H\)-driven projected rows vanish.

So the projected tower cannot solve D3 unless a correction term or a nonprojected row escapes the \(q_0\)-factor.

---

# 2. What must be checked

The required finite algebraic audit is modulo the wall ideal

\[
(q_0).
\]

For each proof-relevant row or invariant \(R\), compute

\[
R\bmod(q_0).
\]

Classify:

\[
R\not\equiv0 \pmod{q_0}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{wall-live candidate},
\]

\[
R\equiv0 \pmod{q_0}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{wall-dead}.
\]

A wall-live term may have form

\[
u^p,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no multiplicative factor

\[
q_0,\qquad H,\qquad q_0u^3.
\]

At the wall,

\[
u^p\Gamma_G=u^{p+1},
\]

so \(u^p\Gamma_G\) is especially useful: it remains nonzero whenever \(u\ne0\).

---

# 3. Raw scattering rows

For raw scattering rows before \(\mathfrak f\)-projection, the needed audit table is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{raw row} & R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0) & \text{classification}\\
\hline
R_1^{\rm raw} & \cdots & \text{wall-live / }q_0\text{-divisible / }H\text{-divisible}\\
R_2^{\rm raw} & \cdots & \cdots
\end{array}
\]

The key question is whether the \(H\)-factor is intrinsic or introduced only by the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection.

If a raw row has

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\equiv c\,u^p\Gamma_G \pmod{q_0},
\qquad c\ne0,
\]

then

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}=c\,u^{p+1},
\]

and this row is source-robust.

If every raw row satisfies

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\in(q_0),
\]

then raw rows do not solve the wall.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No raw scattering row is certified wall-live yet.}
}
\]

The next required calculation is exactly

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0)
\]

for the finite set of rows used in the downstream architecture.

---

# 4. Ambient / unprojected Gram rows

For ambient or unprojected Gram rows, compute

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
\]

The important diagnostic is whether source-visible terms exist before projection:

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\equiv c\,u^p
\quad\text{or}\quad
c\,u^p\Gamma_G
\pmod{q_0}.
\]

If yes, then the ambient object contains wall-live source information, but the \(\mathfrak f\)-projection may be killing it.

This would create a new downstream route:

\[
\text{use ambient/unprojected invariant instead of }A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

If instead every proof-relevant ambient row satisfies

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\in(q_0),
\]

then the wall-deadness is intrinsic to the known row architecture.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No ambient/unprojected Gram row is certified wall-live yet.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Source-robust row theorem candidate

If the audit finds a row vector \(\mathbf R_{\rm rob}\), the theorem should be:

## Source-Robust Row Theorem

There exists a canonical raw, ambient, correction, or newly defined row vector

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}
\]

such that, modulo the wall ideal,

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}
=
u^p\mathbf R_0(u,q',\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots)
+
q_0(\cdots),
\]

with

\[
|\mathbf R_0|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

whenever

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_1}
\]

and

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q}.
\]

If the remaining error satisfies

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le \frac12 |u^p\mathbf R_0|,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on the \(q_0\)-wall branch.

This would close D3.

---

# 6. If no wall-live row exists

If the finite audit proves

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\in(q_0),
\]

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\in(q_0),
\]

and

\[
C_{2k+1}\in(q_0)
\]

for all proof-relevant raw, ambient, and correction rows, then the known row architecture cannot cross the wall.

Then one must name the downstream input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}
}
\]

or replace it by a stronger

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(q_0\)-Wall Exclusion Theorem}.}
\]

But the wall-exclusion route is currently less plausible, since Gate 2 is compatible with

\[
q_0\approx0,\qquad u\ne0,\qquad \Gamma_G\approx u.
\]

---

# 7. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 is not closed.}
}
\]

The known projected tower is wall-dead. No raw, ambient, or correction row has yet been certified wall-live.

The exact next algebraic task is finite and concrete:

\[
\boxed{
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),\quad
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0),\quad
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0)
}
\]

for all proof-relevant rows.

Until such a row is found, D3 should be treated as the named input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

## Agent 4 / D — Final D3 \(q_0\)-wall resolution statement

Executing Agent 4’s assignment: finalize D3 as a named input unless a concrete wall-live row is available. The latest update confirms D1 remains a named density/Remez input without a low-complexity/doubling theorem, and the downstream layer is now being reduced to D1–D4. 

---

# 1. Projected tower no-go

Known projected rows have the form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\]

with

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

At the wall

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
H=0.
\]

Therefore the known projected tower is wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

In particular,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

cannot produce a downstream row lower bound at \(q_0=0\), even if Gate 2 mass is live.

This is not just a smallness problem. It is algebraic divisibility by the wall factor \(q_0\).

---

# 2. Wall-live criterion

A row or invariant \(R\) is wall-live if

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Acceptable leading forms include

\[
u^p,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
u^p(q')^a,
\]

provided the term has no factor of

\[
q_0
\]

or

\[
H.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Thus a row with leading term

\[
u^p\Gamma_G
\]

becomes

\[
u^{p+1}
\]

on the wall and is source-robust.

A row with leading term

\[
u^p\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

is wall-live if the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel is non-small. A row with

\[
u^p(q')^a
\]

may need an additional nonvanishing argument for \(q'\).

---

# 3. Required finite algebraic residue audit

The exact audit needed to prove or refute D3 is finite and algebraic. Compute the following reductions modulo the wall ideal \((q_0)\).

## Raw rows

For proof-relevant raw scattering rows,

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0).
\]

A raw row is a candidate if

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}.
\]

## Ambient rows

For ambient or unprojected Gram rows,

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
\]

If some ambient row is wall-live but its projected version is wall-dead, then the existing projection is discarding the needed wall information. That would suggest a new ambient downstream invariant.

## Correction sectors

For projected row corrections,

\[
C_7\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
C_9\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
C_{11}\bmod(q_0),
\ldots
\]

where

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9.
\]

A correction sector rescues the wall only if

\[
C_{2k+1}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

for at least one proof-relevant \(k\), after cancellations.

---

# 4. Source-Robust Row theorem

The named D3 input should be:

## Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

Assume

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}
\]

and Gate 2 pointwise mass

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then there exists a canonical row or finite row vector

\[
R_{\rm rob}
\]

such that

\[
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and whose leading expansion is not divisible by

\[
q_0
\]

or

\[
H.
\]

A sufficient explicit form is

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
u^p\mathcal R(u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},q',\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Err},
\]

with

\[
\mathcal R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le
\frac12 |u^p\mathcal R|.
\]

This theorem closes the wall branch of row conversion.

---

# 5. Current status

No certified wall-live row is currently available.

The known projected tower is wall-dead. Raw rows, ambient rows, and correction rows remain unverified until the finite residue audit is performed.

Therefore D3 is not proved.

---

# 6. Final D3 statement

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3: Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}
}
\]

is now a named downstream input.

It consists of the assertion that the \(q_0\)-wall branch

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}
\]

admits a proof-relevant row/invariant satisfying

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

with correction control strong enough to give

\[
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

under Gate 2 mass.

If future computation shows

\[
R_j^{\rm raw},\ R_j^{\rm amb},\ C_{2k+1}\in(q_0)
\]

for all proof-relevant rows, then the current row architecture cannot resolve the wall and a genuinely new invariant or wall-exclusion theorem is required.

## Agent 4 / D — Final handoff: row conversion D3/D4

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: finalize the row-conversion layer, including the nondegenerate branch D4 and the \(q_0\)-wall branch D3. The current architecture is conditional and the downstream layer is reduced to named local inputs. 

---

# 1. Known row architecture

The proof-relevant projected rows currently available are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

with

\[
H
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\mathcal R_H,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The leading row vector is therefore

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

The correction vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm corr}
=
\left(
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\;
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9
\right).
\]

---

# 2. D4 — Nondegenerate row conversion

## D4 statement

Assume there is a point \(m_\ast\) such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and Gate 2 pointwise mass holds:

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G(m_\ast)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Assume also either

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

or an anisotropy upper bound

\[
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}(m_\ast)
\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

which, together with the Gate 2 product lower bound, implies a polynomial lower bound for \(|u(m_\ast)|\).

Assume correction control:

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}(m_\ast)|
\le
\frac12
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_\ast)|.
\]

Then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|
+
|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

## Proof sketch

From the leading vector,

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\asymp
|q_0|\,|u|^3
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Gate 2 pointwise mass gives

\[
|u|
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}
\ge Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\asymp
|q_0|\,|u|^2
\left[
|u|
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}
\right].
\]

If \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\), then

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q}
Q^{-2C_u}
Q^{-A_2/2}
=
Q^{-C}.
\]

If \(|u|\) is not separately known but anisotropy is bounded above by \(Q^{C_\Gamma}\), then

\[
|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-A_2}Q^{-2C_\Gamma},
\]

so

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-A_2/2-C_\Gamma},
\]

and the same lower bound follows with a different exponent.

Correction control gives

\[
|(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})|
\ge
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|-|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\ge
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Using the vector norm avoids cancellation between the \(A_7\) and \(A_9\) channels.

## D4 status

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 is conditionally closeable.}
}
\]

It still requires:

\[
\boxed{
\text{sampling a point where } |q_0|,\ |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\text{ are simultaneously non-small,}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
}
\]

---

# 3. D3 — \(q_0\)-wall branch

The nondegenerate theorem does not handle

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3=u.
\]

So Gate 2 mass can be live:

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2=|u|^4,
\]

while

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H
\]

vanishes to leading order.

Thus all rows whose leading term is \(H\)-divisible collapse on the wall.

The known projected tower has the schematic form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Therefore the projected tower is wall-dead unless correction terms or unprojected structures contain wall-live components.

---

# 4. Wall-live row criterion

A source-robust row \(R_{\rm rob}\) must satisfy

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Acceptable leading forms include

\[
u^p,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no factor of

\[
q_0,
\qquad
H,
\qquad
q_0u^3.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u,
\]

a term

\[
u^p\Gamma_G
\]

becomes

\[
u^{p+1},
\]

which is live whenever \(u\ne0\).

---

# 5. Required finite audits

D3 is not proved until the following finite algebraic audits are done.

## Raw scattering rows

Compute

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0)
\]

for every proof-relevant raw row.

Classify each row as:

\[
\text{wall-live},
\quad
q_0\text{-divisible},
\quad
H\text{-divisible},
\quad
\text{or cancellation-dead}.
\]

## Ambient / unprojected Gram rows

Compute

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
\]

If

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

but the projected row is \(q_0\)-divisible, then the proof may need an ambient or unprojected invariant.

## Correction rows

For projected-row corrections, compute

\[
C_7\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_9\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_{11}\bmod(q_0),
\ldots
\]

where

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
C_{2k+1}.
\]

If every correction satisfies

\[
C_{2k+1}\in(q_0),
\]

then known correction sectors do not rescue the wall.

---

# 6. D3 statement

## Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

Assume

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q},
\]

and Gate 2 wall mass holds at a point:

\[
|u|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then there exists a proof-relevant canonical row or invariant

\[
R_{\rm rob}
\]

such that

\[
|R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

A sufficient structural form is

\[
R_{\rm rob}
=
u^p\mathcal R(u,\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},q',\ldots)
+
\mathrm{Err},
\]

with

\[
\mathcal R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

and

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le
\frac12|u^p\mathcal R|.
\]

## D3 status

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 is open.}
}
\]

No source-robust row has been certified. The known projected tower is wall-dead. The next step is the finite residue audit above.

---

# 7. Final D3/D4 classification

| Layer | Statement | Status |
|---|---|---|
| D4 nondegenerate branch | \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}\) + Gate 2 pointwise mass + correction control \(\Rightarrow |A_7|+|A_9|\ge Q^{-C}\) | Conditional / closeable |
| D3 wall branch | \(|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}\) + Gate 2 wall mass \(\Rightarrow\) source-robust row lower bound | Open named input |
| Projected tower | \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}\) | wall-dead |
| Raw/ambient/correction audit | compute modulo \((q_0)\) | required, not done |

Final conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Row conversion is conditional on D4 off the wall and D3 on the wall.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The nondegenerate branch is structurally clear; the }q_0\text{-wall remains the structural blocker.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-27 09:39:33)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 4 / D — D4 correction-control theorem

Executing **Agent 4 / D**: finalize the nondegenerate row-conversion theorem and isolate the remaining correction estimates. The assigned lane is D4: **Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control**. 

---

# 1. Nondegenerate branch assumptions

Work at a sampled point \(m_\ast\). Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Assume the non-wall branch:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Assume pointwise Gate 2 mass:

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G(m_\ast)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)^2
\right)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Known row expansions:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\mathcal R_H.
\]

---

# 2. Leading row vector

Define

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

Then

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\asymp
|q_0|\,|u|^3
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}
\]

provided

\[
|c_7|+|c_9|\asymp 1
\]

and the row normalization has already been absorbed into the \(Q^{O(1)}\)-constants.

From pointwise Gate 2 mass,

\[
|u|
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}
\ge Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\gtrsim
|q_0|\,|u|^2 Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Using

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\gtrsim
Q^{-C_q}|u|^2Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

So the lower bound now depends on obtaining a polynomial lower bound for \(|u|\).

---

# 3. Two ways to lower-bound \(u\)

## Route A — explicit pointwise source lower bound

If sampling provides

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

then

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\gtrsim
Q^{-C_q}
Q^{-2C_u}
Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\ge Q^{-C_{\rm lead}},
\]

with

\[
C_{\rm lead}=C_q+2C_u+\frac{A_2}{2}+O(1).
\]

## Route B — anisotropy upper bound

If instead one has

\[
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}
\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

then pointwise Gate 2 mass gives

\[
|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-A_2}Q^{-2C_\Gamma}.
\]

So

\[
|u|
\ge
Q^{-A_2/2-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Plugging into the leading vector estimate:

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\gtrsim
Q^{-C_q}
Q^{-A_2-2C_\Gamma}
Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Hence

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\ge
Q^{-C_{\rm lead}'},
\]

where

\[
C_{\rm lead}'=C_q+\frac{3A_2}{2}+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Thus either an explicit \(|u|\)-sample or a polynomial anisotropy upper bound suffices.

---

# 4. Correction vector

Substitute

\[
H
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\mathcal R_H
\]

into \(A_7,A_9\). The correction vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm corr}
=
\left(
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\;
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9
\right).
\]

The exact correction-control requirement is

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Equivalently, it is enough to prove the two bounds

\[
|c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7|
\le
\frac{1}{2\sqrt2}|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|,
\]

\[
|c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9|
\le
\frac{1}{2\sqrt2}|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

A more invariant sufficient condition is

\[
|\mathcal R_H|
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}
+
\left(
|\mathcal R_7|^2+|\mathcal R_9|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\le
\frac12
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Using

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\asymp
|q_0|\,|u|^3
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2},
\]

it is enough that

\[
|\mathcal R_H|
\le
c\,|q_0|\,|u|^3,
\]

and

\[
\left(
|\mathcal R_7|^2+|\mathcal R_9|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\le
c\,|q_0|\,|u|^3
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)^{1/2}.
\]

---

# 5. Correction sources to control

The correction terms must include all of the following.

## 5.1 \(E_2\) and canonical tail error

Since

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

all row expansions must control errors caused by \(E_2\). The needed form is

\[
\max_{k\le k_{\rm row}}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-A_E}.
\]

For the full Wronskian system, previous audits placed the safe derivative budget near

\[
k_{\rm row}\le 2R+1.
\]

For D4 alone, the exact row-expansion depth may be smaller, but using the global \(2R+1\) budget is the safest canonical guardrail.

## 5.2 Projection and gauge errors

If \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) are projected or gauge-normalized rows, then the expansion must include errors from:

\[
\mathfrak f\text{-projection},
\]

row normalization,

basis conditioning,

and gauge/coordinate changes.

These must be bounded in the same vector norm as \(\mathcal A_{\rm lead}\).

## 5.3 Lower-order row terms

Terms lower-order away from the wall can still be comparable in small-source regimes. In the nondegenerate branch, they must satisfy

\[
|\mathrm{lower\ order}|
\le
\frac14|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\]

or be included in the leading vector if not perturbative.

## 5.4 Error in \(H\)

The approximation

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H
\]

must be controlled multiplicatively:

\[
|\mathcal R_H|
\le
c|q_0||u|^3.
\]

An absolute bound on \(\mathcal R_H\) is not enough unless combined with lower bounds on \(q_0,u\).

---

# 6. Final D4 theorem

## Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

Assume at \(m_\ast\):

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

or

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Assume row expansions

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H,
\]

with

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|
\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

for some polynomial exponent \(C\) depending on

\[
C_q,\ C_u,\ A_2
\]

or alternatively on

\[
C_q,\ C_\Gamma,\ A_2.
\]

Using the vector norm,

\[
\left(
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|^2+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is cleaner and avoids any cancellation issue between the two rows.

---

# 7. What remains open

D4 is closeable but conditional. The remaining tasks are local/canonical estimates:

1. prove exact row expansions with nonzero constants \(c_7,c_9\);

2. prove

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H;
\]

3. prove multiplicative \(H\)-error control

\[
|\mathcal R_H|\le c|q_0||u|^3;
\]

4. prove

\[
|\mathcal R_7|^2+|\mathcal R_9|^2
\le
c^2|q_0|^2|u|^6(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2);
\]

5. account for all canonical errors:

\[
E_2,\quad\text{tails},\quad\text{projection/gauge},\quad\text{row normalization},\quad\text{lower-order row terms}.
\]

---

# 8. Final status

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 is a conditional local theorem, not the main structural blocker.}
}
\]

It closes the non-wall branch once correction control and sampling are supplied.

It does not address

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Therefore the downstream split remains:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}
\Rightarrow
\text{D4 handles row conversion,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}
\Rightarrow
\text{need D3 Source-Robust Row / Wall Resolution.}
}
\]

## Agent 4 / D — D3 targeted attack: actual row residue audit protocol

Executing Agent 4 / D: make the \(q_0\)-wall audit executable by defining the wall ideal, the residue map, the first rows to audit, and the classification table needed to find or rule out a source-robust row. The relevant assigned prompt asks specifically for a finite algebraic protocol for \(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}\), including raw, ambient, projected, and correction forms. 

---

# 1. Wall ideal and residue map

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The wall is

\[
q_0=0.
\]

Define the wall ideal

\[
\mathfrak I_{\rm wall}:=(q_0).
\]

For any row, invariant, correction term, or expansion term \(R\), define its wall residue by

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{\rm wall}(R)
=
R\bmod(q_0).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{\rm wall}(R)
=
R|_{q_0=0}.
\]

A row is wall-live if

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{\rm wall}(R)
\not\equiv0
\]

as a polynomial/differential expression, and more specifically if

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

A row is wall-dead if

\[
R\in(q_0).
\]

A row is \(H\)-dead if

\[
R\in(H),
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

Since

\[
H\in(q_0),
\]

\(H\)-divisibility implies wall-deadness.

---

# 2. Wall-live monomial criterion

The audit should search for leading monomials of the form

\[
u^p,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no factor of

\[
q_0,
\qquad
H,
\qquad
q_0u^3.
\]

At the wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

becomes

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Therefore

\[
u^p\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u^{p+1},
\]

which is wall-live whenever

\[
u\ne0.
\]

By contrast,

\[
H\Gamma_{G,k}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Thus every row whose leading and correction terms remain in the ideal \((H)\) or \((q_0)\) cannot solve the wall.

---

# 3. Rows to audit first

The first finite audit set should be

\[
A_7,\quad A_9,\quad A_{11},\quad A_{13}.
\]

For each \(A_{2k+1}\), audit four versions:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\rm raw},
\]

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\rm amb},
\]

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]

and its correction sector

\[
C_{2k+1}
\]

defined by

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
C_{2k+1}.
\]

Here

\[
\Gamma_{G,1}=\Gamma_G,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

and higher \(\Gamma_{G,k}\) follow the existing tower convention.

The audit should not stop at \(A_7,A_9\), because a term that is lower-order off-wall may become leading at the wall.

---

# 4. Audit table

For each row, compute:

\[
R^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
R^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
R^{\mathfrak f}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
C\bmod(q_0).
\]

Use the following table format.

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c|c}
\text{row} &
R^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0) &
R^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0) &
R^{\mathfrak f}\bmod(q_0) &
C\bmod(q_0) &
\text{classification}
\\
\hline
A_7 &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots
\\
A_9 &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots
\\
A_{11} &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots
\\
A_{13} &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots &
\cdots
\end{array}
\]

Classifications:

\[
\boxed{\text{wall-live}}
\]

if some residue is nonzero at \(q_0=0,u\ne0\);

\[
\boxed{q_0\text{-divisible}}
\]

if all relevant residues vanish modulo \((q_0)\);

\[
\boxed{H\text{-divisible}}
\]

if the row lies in \((H)\);

\[
\boxed{\text{projection-killed}}
\]

if

\[
R^{\rm raw}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

or

\[
R^{\rm amb}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0},
\]

but

\[
R^{\mathfrak f}\equiv0\pmod{q_0};
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{cancellation-dead}}
\]

if wall-live monomials occur before summation but cancel in the full row.

---

# 5. Known projected tower diagnosis

The known projected tower has leading form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\equiv C_{2k+1}\pmod{q_0}.
\]

If

\[
C_{2k+1}\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

for all accessible \(k\), then

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

for the full projected tower. In that case, no projected row solves D3.

So the projected-row wall audit reduces to the correction residues

\[
C_7\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_9\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_{11}\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_{13}\bmod(q_0).
\]

---

# 6. Raw and ambient diagnostic logic

The raw and ambient rows answer whether wall information exists before projection.

## Case A — raw or ambient wall-live

Suppose

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

or

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}.
\]

For example,

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}
\equiv
c\,u^p\Gamma_G
\pmod{q_0},
\qquad c\ne0.
\]

Then

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0}
=
c\,u^{p+1}.
\]

This gives a candidate source-robust row.

If the projected row is wall-dead, then the current projection is killing the wall-live component. The new target becomes an ambient or raw downstream invariant.

## Case B — raw and ambient wall-dead

If

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

and

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

for every proof-relevant row, then the wall-deadness is intrinsic to the known row architecture, not an artifact of projection.

Then D3 cannot be solved without a new invariant or a \(q_0\)-wall exclusion theorem.

---

# 7. Correction-sector diagnostic logic

Write

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
C_{2k+1}.
\]

Since

\[
H\equiv0\pmod{q_0},
\]

we have

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\bmod(q_0)
=
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0).
\]

So corrections rescue the wall exactly when

\[
C_{2k+1}\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

for at least one \(k\), or for a finite vector of \(k\)'s.

A single correction term should be treated cautiously. The correct object is the correction vector

\[
\mathbf C_{\rm wall}
=
\left(
C_7,\ C_9,\ C_{11},\ C_{13},\ldots
\right)\bmod(q_0).
\]

The desired wall theorem is

\[
|\mathbf C_{\rm wall}|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

under wall-branch Gate 2 mass.

---

# 8. Theorem proved by a wall-live residue

If the audit finds a wall-live row, the resulting theorem should be stated as follows.

## Source-Robust Row Theorem

Assume the wall branch:

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Assume Gate 2 pointwise mass:

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Suppose there exists a canonical raw, ambient, projected-correction, or newly defined row vector

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}
\]

such that

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm rob}\bmod(q_0)
=
u^p\mathbf R_0(u,q',\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\ldots),
\]

with

\[
|\mathbf R_0|\ge Q^{-A_0}
\]

on the wall-branch Gate 2 set, and with error bound

\[
|\mathrm{Err}|
\le
\frac12|u^p\mathbf R_0|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

on the \(q_0\)-wall branch, closing D3.

---

# 9. No-go proved by a fully vanishing residue audit

If the audit proves

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\equiv0\pmod{q_0},
\]

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\equiv0\pmod{q_0},
\]

and

\[
C_{2k+1}\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\]

for

\[
A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}
\]

and all other proof-relevant rows, then the known architecture cannot cross the wall.

The no-go theorem is:

## Known Row Architecture Wall No-Go

If every proof-relevant raw, ambient, projected, and correction row lies in the ideal \((q_0)\), then for local configurations with

\[
q_0=0,\qquad u\ne0,
\]

all known downstream rows vanish even though

\[
\Gamma_G=u
\]

and Gate 2 mass may be nonzero.

Therefore the downstream proof requires either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a genuinely new source-robust invariant}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a }q_0\text{-wall exclusion theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 10. Final protocol

The D3 finite audit is now executable as follows:

1. Compute

\[
A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}
\]

in raw, ambient, projected, and correction forms.

2. Reduce every expression modulo

\[
(q_0).
\]

3. Identify whether any residue contains a nonzero term of type

\[
u^p,\quad
u^p\Gamma_G,\quad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\quad
u^p(q')^a.
\]

4. If yes, formulate the Source-Robust Row Theorem for that row/vector.

5. If no, name D3 as a black-box wall-resolution input.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No wall-live row is currently certified.}
}
\]

But the audit is finite, algebraic, and now sharply specified.

## Agent 4 / D — Attack on D4 correction-control / wall-adjacent row conversion

I am executing the Agent 4 lane from the latest prompt set: sharpen the downstream row-conversion layer around the nondegenerate branch and the \(q_0\)-wall, looking for a real mechanism rather than only restating D4. The current framework identifies D1–D4 as the downstream named inputs, with D3/D4 specifically controlling the \(q_0\)-wall and nondegenerate row conversion. 

---

# 1. Start from the known row structure

We have

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

with

\[
H=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\mathcal R_H,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

So the leading vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

The correction vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm corr}
=
\left(
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,\,
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9
\right).
\]

The basic nondegenerate theorem is therefore:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}
+
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2}
+
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This branch is structurally clear. The obstruction is the wall:

\[
q_0=0.
\]

---

# 2. The wall quotient calculation

Reduce the leading rows modulo the wall ideal

\[
(q_0).
\]

Since

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\]

we get

\[
H\equiv 0\pmod{q_0}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\equiv
\mathcal R_7
\pmod{q_0},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\equiv
\mathcal R_9
\pmod{q_0}.
\]

So the projected rows survive the wall **if and only if**

\[
\mathcal R_7\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal R_9\not\equiv0\pmod{q_0}.
\]

If

\[
\mathcal R_7,\mathcal R_9\in(q_0),
\]

then

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}
=
A_9^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}
=
0.
\]

Thus the first finite audit is exact:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute }\mathcal R_7\bmod(q_0),\quad \mathcal R_9\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

The same test should then be applied to

\[
C_{11},C_{13},\ldots
\]

where

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
C_{2k+1}.
\]

---

# 3. A new possible mechanism: wall blow-up rows

There is one nontrivial attack that is not just “find a correction.”

Although

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\]

vanishes at \(q_0=0\), its **first wall-normal quotient** does not.

Formally define the blow-up row

\[
\widehat A_7
:=
\frac{A_7^{\mathfrak f}}{q_0}
\]

where this quotient is interpreted algebraically before restriction to \(q_0=0\). Using the leading expansion,

\[
\frac{A_7^{\mathfrak f}}{q_0}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^3\Gamma_G
+
\frac{\mathcal R_7}{q_0}
+
c_7\frac{\mathcal R_H}{q_0}\Gamma_G.
\]

At the wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

gives

\[
\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}=u.
\]

Therefore the leading blow-up residue is

\[
\widehat A_7|_{q_0=0}
\sim
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^4
\]

provided

\[
\frac{\mathcal R_7}{q_0}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\frac{\mathcal R_H}{q_0}\Gamma_G
\]

are controlled.

Similarly,

\[
\widehat A_9
:=
\frac{A_9^{\mathfrak f}}{q_0}
\]

has leading residue

\[
\widehat A_9|_{q_0=0}
\sim
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

So the wall has a natural candidate invariant:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathbf A}_{\rm wall}
=
\left(
\frac{A_7^{\mathfrak f}}{q_0},
\frac{A_9^{\mathfrak f}}{q_0}
\right)_{\text{algebraic wall blow-up}}.
}
\]

This vector is source-robust at \(q_0=0\), because

\[
\widehat A_7|_{q_0=0}
\sim u^4.
\]

This is the strongest concrete candidate I see.

---

# 4. Why this is not automatically valid

The wall-blow-up row is not yet a proof-level row. It requires one of the following:

## Option A — Algebraic divisibility

Show that

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}, A_9^{\mathfrak f}\in(q_0)
\]

as exact row expressions, so the quotients

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}/q_0,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\]

are regular row/invariant functions.

Then the blow-up is legitimate.

## Option B — Wall-normal derivative

Define instead

\[
\partial_{q_0}A_7^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0}.
\]

From the leading term,

\[
\partial_{q_0}
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G
\right)_{q_0=0}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^3\Gamma_G|_{q_0=0}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^4.
\]

Likewise,

\[
\partial_{q_0}A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\Gamma_{G,2}|_{q_0=0}.
\]

This gives a wall-normal derivative invariant.

But it is useful only if the local geometry gives access to this transverse derivative as a proof-relevant row or invariant. If the downstream argument only permits values of rows, not derivatives with respect to \(q_0\), this is not enough.

## Option C — Blow-up compactification

Treat the wall as a blow-up chart and prove the downstream row conversion in the blown-up coordinate

\[
\widetilde A_{2k+1}=\frac{A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}}{q_0}.
\]

This is conceptually clean, but it changes the row architecture. It requires proof that the blown-up row is canonical and admissible.

---

# 5. Conditional wall-blow-up theorem

The promising theorem is:

## Wall-Blow-Up Row Theorem

Assume \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) are algebraically divisible by \(q_0\), and define

\[
\widehat A_7=A_7^{\mathfrak f}/q_0,
\qquad
\widehat A_9=A_9^{\mathfrak f}/q_0.
\]

Assume

\[
\widehat A_7
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^3\Gamma_G+\widehat{\mathcal R}_7,
\]

\[
\widehat A_9
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\Gamma_{G,2}+\widehat{\mathcal R}_9,
\]

with

\[
|\widehat{\mathcal R}_7|^2+|\widehat{\mathcal R}_9|^2
\le
\frac14
u^6(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

Then

\[
|\widehat A_7|+|\widehat A_9|
\ge
Q^{-A}
\]

whenever Gate 2 pointwise mass holds and \(u\) is polynomially non-small.

At the exact wall \(q_0=0\), this gives

\[
|\widehat A_7|
\sim
|u|^4
\]

because

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Thus the wall is solved if the blow-up row is allowed.

---

# 6. Interaction with Gate 2 pointwise mass

Gate 2 pointwise mass says

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

For the blow-up row,

\[
|\widehat{\mathcal A}_{\rm lead}|
\asymp
|u|^3
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

This equals

\[
|u|^2
\cdot
\left[
|u|
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}
\right].
\]

The bracket is bounded below by

\[
Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

So we still need either:

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

or an anisotropy upper bound to recover a pointwise source lower bound from the Gate 2 product.

At the exact wall, since

\[
\Gamma_G=u,
\]

we have

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2=|u|^4,
\]

so Gate 2 pointwise mass implies

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-A_2/4}
\]

if the \(\Gamma_G\) channel supplies the mass. If the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) channel dominates, use the standard anisotropy upper bound route.

Thus the blow-up row is compatible with the existing nondegenerate row-conversion logic.

---

# 7. If blow-up rows are disallowed

If the proof architecture only permits ordinary row values and forbids division by \(q_0\) or wall-normal derivatives, then the blow-up mechanism is not admissible.

In that case, the wall still requires an ordinary row satisfying

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The finite audit remains:

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0).
\]

If every proof-relevant row is in \((q_0)\), then no ordinary row solves the wall.

---

# 8. Final D4/D3 attack result

The nondegenerate branch D4 is local and closeable with correction control:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}
+
\text{Gate 2 pointwise mass}
+
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\Rightarrow
|A_7|+|A_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

For the wall branch, I see one concrete new possible route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall-blow-up rows }A_7/q_0,\ A_9/q_0
}
\]

or equivalently

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall-normal derivatives }\partial_{q_0}A_7,\ \partial_{q_0}A_9.
}
\]

These are source-robust because their residues at \(q_0=0\) contain

\[
u^4
\]

and

\[
u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

But they are only valid if the architecture admits blow-up/normal-derivative rows as proof-relevant invariants.

So the next algebraic question is now sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}/q_0\text{ a legitimate canonical row/invariant?}
}
\]

If yes, D3 has a plausible solution.

If no, D3 remains the named input:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]
