## Agent 4 / D — Continued attack: \(q_0\)-wall escape by Taylor displacement

I’m continuing the D4/D3 attack around the \(q_0\)-wall. The previous obstruction was:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288},
\]

so at

\[
q_0=0
\]

the known projected rows vanish even though

\[
\Gamma_G=u
\]

can remain live. The current D4 task is to sharpen row conversion and correction control in the nondegenerate branch; this attack tries to reduce the wall branch back to the nondegenerate branch by moving slightly off the wall. 

---

# 1. Core observation

The wall is dangerous only if we are forced to sample exactly where

\[
q_0=0.
\]

But if

\[
u=q_0''=q''_{\can}
\]

is non-small at the wall, then \(q_0\) cannot remain small on both sides of that point unless it has impossible Taylor behavior.

At a point \(m_0\) with

\[
q_0(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
u(m_0)=q_0''(m_0)\not\approx0,
\]

Taylor expansion gives

\[
q_0(m_0+t)
=
q_0(m_0)
+
q_0'(m_0)t
+
\frac12u(m_0)t^2
+
O(Mt^3),
\]

where

\[
M=\sup_{|s-m_0|\le h}|q_0'''(s)|.
\]

Therefore, for polynomially small \(h\), \(q_0\) should become polynomially non-small at a nearby point unless \(u\) is also small.

This suggests a new wall-escape theorem:

\[
\boxed{
q_0\approx0,\quad u\not\approx0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\exists m_1\text{ nearby with }|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}
\text{ and }u,\Gamma_G\text{ still live.}
}
\]

Then the nondegenerate row-conversion theorem D4 applies at \(m_1\).

---

# 2. Quadratic wall-escape lemma

Let \(q=q_0\), \(u=q''\). Suppose on

\[
[m_0-h,m_0+h]
\]

we have

\[
|q'''|\le M.
\]

Assume

\[
|q(m_0)|\le \eta,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge \delta.
\]

Then for \(h\) satisfying

\[
Mh^3\le \frac18\delta h^2,
\]

one has

\[
\max_{\sigma\in\{-1,0,1\}}
|q(m_0+\sigma h)|
\ge
c\,\delta h^2-\eta
\]

for an absolute constant \(c>0\).

Proof sketch:

\[
q(m_0+h)+q(m_0-h)-2q(m_0)
=
u(m_0)h^2+O(Mh^3).
\]

Therefore, if all three values \(q(m_0-h),q(m_0),q(m_0+h)\) were too small, the second difference could not be as large as \(\delta h^2\).

Choose

\[
h\asymp \sqrt{\frac{\eta_\ast}{\delta}}
\]

with

\[
\eta_\ast\gg \eta,
\qquad
M h\ll \delta.
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_1\in\{m_0-h,m_0,m_0+h\}
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge \eta_\ast.
\]

Taking

\[
\eta_\ast=Q^{-C_q}
\]

gives a polynomial \(q_0\)-nondegenerate point.

---

# 3. Keeping \(u\) and \(\Gamma_G\) live after displacement

We also need row conversion at \(m_1\). So we must preserve source and anisotropy.

Assume

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge \delta,
\]

and

\[
|u'(m)|\le M_u
\]

on the same interval. If

\[
M_u h\le \frac12\delta,
\]

then

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\delta.
\]

Next,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

If at \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\eta_\ast
\]

and

\[
\eta_\ast\ll \delta,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q_0(m_1)|-2|q_0(m_1)|^3
\ge
c\delta.
\]

Thus the \(\Gamma_G\) channel remains live.

So under derivative bounds, wall escape gives a nearby point satisfying

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is exactly the pointwise input needed by D4.

---

# 4. Consequence: a possible wall-exclusion theorem

This gives a stronger and more concrete version of the \(q_0\)-wall exclusion theorem:

## Local Wall-Escape Theorem

Assume on an interval \(I\):

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le Q^{-C_0},
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|=|q_0''(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and derivative bounds

\[
|q_0'''|\le Q^{C_3},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_u'}
\]

on a polynomial neighborhood of \(m_0\).

Then there exists

\[
m_1
\quad\text{with}\quad
|m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C_h}
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u'},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Consequently, if D4 correction control holds at \(m_1\), then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This would resolve the wall branch **without** finding a new source-robust row.

---

# 5. Interaction with Gate 2 mass

Gate 2 pointwise mass gives

\[
|u(m_0)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_0)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

On the exact wall,

\[
q_0(m_0)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G(m_0)=u(m_0).
\]

Therefore, if the Gate 2 mass at \(m_0\) is carried by the \(\Gamma_G\)-channel, then

\[
|u(m_0)|^4\ge Q^{-A},
\]

so

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A/4}.
\]

Then the wall-escape lemma applies.

If instead the Gate 2 mass is carried mostly by \(\Gamma_{G,2}\), we need either:

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}
\]

to recover a lower bound for \(u\), or a variant using \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) directly.

But in the strict \(q_0=0\) wall case, \(\Gamma_G=u\), so unless \(u\) is tiny, the \(\Gamma_G\)-channel is already live.

Thus the wall is less fatal than it first appeared: \(q_0=0\) plus \(u\neq0\) creates curvature that moves \(q_0\) off the wall quadratically.

---

# 6. Applying D4 after displacement

At the nearby point \(m_1\), D4 gives:

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)(m_1).
\]

Using

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}(m_1)|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|,
\]

then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the entire wall problem can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can row conversion sample at a nearby }m_1\text{ instead of the original wall point }m_0?
}
\]

If yes, D3 may reduce to D4 plus local Taylor control.

---

# 7. Remaining obstruction: admissible displacement

The new issue is whether downstream row conversion requires the row lower bound at the exact Gate 2 sample point, or whether it suffices to find a nearby point.

If the downstream contradiction only needs

\[
\exists m\in I_\rho
\]

with a row lower bound, then wall escape works.

If the proof requires the same point selected by Gate 2 and cannot move, then wall escape does not help.

Thus the next required theorem is:

## Row Sampling Stability Theorem

If Gate 2 mass gives a point \(m_0\) with wall-live source mass, and if the local Taylor wall-escape lemma produces \(m_1\) with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C}|I_\rho|,
\]

then the downstream row lower bound at \(m_1\) is admissible for the contradiction layer.

This is likely true if the downstream argument is existential over the packet interval.

---

# 8. What this means for D3

Previously, D3 was:

\[
\text{find source-robust row at }q_0=0.
\]

The new attack suggests an alternative:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3': Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem}
}
\]

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\text{ nearby with }|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}
\text{ and Gate 2 mass still live}.
\]

Then D4 handles \(m_1\).

So D3 has two possible solutions:

1. **Source-Robust Row Theorem**: find a row live at the wall.
2. **Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem**: move off the wall and use D4.

The second is now the more concrete attack.

---

# 9. Final attack result

The strongest new mechanism is:

\[
\boxed{
q_0=0,\quad u=q_0''\neq0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q_0\text{ becomes polynomially nonzero at nearby points.}
}
\]

Therefore, the \(q_0\)-wall may be avoidable without a new row if the proof permits nearby sampling.

The next exact theorem to prove is:

## \(q_0\)-Wall Escape Theorem

Assume on \(I_\rho\):

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le Q^{-C_0},
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and derivative bounds

\[
\sup_{I_\rho}|q_0'''|+\sup_{I_\rho}|u'|\le Q^C.
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_1\in I_\rho
\]

with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C'}
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u'},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma'}.
\]

Consequently D4 yields a row lower bound at \(m_1\), provided correction control holds.

This is a concrete route to resolving the \(q_0\)-wall.

## Agent 4 / D — Continuing attack: turn the \(q_0\)-wall into a nearby non-wall sample

The strongest route I now see is **not** to find a row that survives exactly at \(q_0=0\), but to prove that if \(q_0\approx0\) while \(u=q''_{\can}\) is live, then one can move a polynomially small distance inside the same packet to a point where \(q_0\) is polynomially nonzero and the Gate 2 signal remains live. Then D4 handles the displaced point.

This would replace the hard wall input

\[
\text{Source-Robust Row at }q_0=0
\]

by a more analytic theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem}
}
\]

which may be easier.

---

# 1. The key Taylor identity

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q''.
\]

Assume at a point \(m_0\),

\[
|q(m_0)|\le \eta,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|=|q''(m_0)|\ge \delta.
\]

Let

\[
M_3=\sup_{|t-m_0|\le h}|q'''(t)|.
\]

Then

\[
q(m_0+h)+q(m_0-h)-2q(m_0)
=
u(m_0)h^2+O(M_3h^3).
\]

Choose

\[
h\le c\,\frac{\delta}{M_3}.
\]

Then

\[
\left|
q(m_0+h)+q(m_0-h)-2q(m_0)
\right|
\ge c_1\delta h^2.
\]

Therefore at least one of the three points

\[
m_0-h,\quad m_0,\quad m_0+h
\]

satisfies

\[
|q(m)|\ge c_2\delta h^2-\eta.
\]

So if

\[
\eta\le \frac12c_2\delta h^2,
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_1,\ |m_1-m_0|\le h:
\quad
|q_0(m_1)|\ge c\,\delta h^2.
}
\]

This is the basic wall escape.

---

# 2. Polynomial exponent bookkeeping

Assume polynomial bounds

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le Q^{-C_0},
\]

\[
\sup |q'''|\le Q^{C_3}.
\]

Choose

\[
h=Q^{-C_h}
\]

with

\[
C_h>C_3+C_u+10
\]

large enough that

\[
Q^{C_3}h\ll Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Then

\[
\delta h^2
=
Q^{-C_u-2C_h}.
\]

If

\[
C_0>C_u+2C_h+10,
\]

then

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\ll \delta h^2.
\]

Hence there is a nearby point

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C_h}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q}
}
\]

where

\[
C_q=C_u+2C_h+O(1).
\]

This is exactly the nondegenerate hypothesis needed for D4, with a possibly large but still polynomial exponent.

---

# 3. Preserve \(u\) after displacement

We also need \(u\) live at \(m_1\).

Let

\[
M_u=\sup_{|t-m_0|\le h}|u'(t)|.
\]

If

\[
M_u h\le \frac12 |u(m_0)|,
\]

then

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12|u(m_0)|.
\]

With polynomial bounds

\[
M_u\le Q^{C_{u'}},
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

it suffices to choose

\[
h\le Q^{-C_{u'}-C_u-10}.
\]

Thus, by choosing

\[
C_h
\]

large enough, we get

\[
\boxed{
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u'}
}
\]

for another polynomial exponent.

---

# 4. Preserve the Gate 2 anisotropy signal

At the wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

At the displaced point \(m_1\),

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q_0(m_1)|-2|q_0(m_1)|^3.
\]

To keep \(\Gamma_G\) live, choose the escape threshold so that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ll |u(m_1)|.
\]

This requires

\[
Q^{-C_q}\ll Q^{-C_u'},
\]

i.e.

\[
C_q>C_u'.
\]

But the Taylor escape gives a **lower** bound

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

not an upper bound. We also need an upper bound on \(q_0\) in the neighborhood.

Taylor gives

\[
|q_0(m_1)|
\le
|q_0(m_0)|+|q_0'(m_0)|h+\frac12M_2h^2,
\]

where

\[
M_2=\sup |q_0''|=\sup |u|.
\]

If \(q_0'\) is huge, \(q_0\) may become much larger than \(u\), and then \(\Gamma_G\) could be dominated by \(-6q_0\), which is still not necessarily bad: \(\Gamma_G\) remains nonzero unless it finely cancels \(u\).

Actually, for D4 we only need

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

If \(q_0\) becomes larger, then

\[
|\Gamma_G|
=
|u-6q_0+2q_0^3|
\]

is typically still polynomially nonzero. The only dangerous case is

\[
u-6q_0+2q_0^3\approx0.
\]

But if \(q_0\) is near zero and \(u\) is live, this cannot happen unless

\[
q_0\approx \frac{u}{6}.
\]

That value is also polynomially nonzero, so D4 can still use the \(q_0\)-factor. If \(\Gamma_G\) cancels, then one must rely on \(\Gamma_{G,2}\), or move to a nearby point again.

So the correct statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall escape gives }q_0\text{ nonzero and }u\text{ live.}
}
\]

To guarantee Gate 2 pointwise mass at the displaced point, add a mild anisotropy-stability condition:

\[
\sup_{|t-m_0|\le h}
|\partial_t\Gamma_G|+
|\partial_t\Gamma_{G,2}|
\le Q^C.
\]

Then choose \(h\) small enough so that

\[
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\]

does not fall from \(Q^{-A}\) to below every polynomial threshold.

---

# 5. Wall-escape theorem, proof-ready form

## D3′ — Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

Let \(m_0\in I_\rho\). Suppose:

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le Q^{-C_0},
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_0)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_0)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_0)^2\right)
\ge Q^{-A_G}.
\]

Assume local derivative bounds on a neighborhood of radius \(Q^{-C_h}\):

\[
|q_0'''|\le Q^{C_3},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_1\in I_\rho,
\qquad
|m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C_h},
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u'},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2\right)
\ge Q^{-A_G'}.
\]

Consequently D4 applies at \(m_1\), assuming correction control.

---

# 6. Boundary issue

If \(m_0\) is too close to the edge of \(I_\rho\), the symmetric points

\[
m_0\pm h
\]

may leave the packet.

Use a one-sided second-difference variant.

If

\[
[m_0,m_0+2h]\subset I_\rho,
\]

then

\[
q(m_0+2h)-2q(m_0+h)+q(m_0)
=
u(m_0)h^2+O(M_3h^3).
\]

Therefore one of

\[
m_0,\quad m_0+h,\quad m_0+2h
\]

has

\[
|q|\ge c\delta h^2-\eta.
\]

Similarly on the left side.

So the theorem only needs

\[
\operatorname{dist}(m_0,\partial I_\rho)\ge 2h
\]

or a one-sided interval of length \(2h\). Since \(h\) is polynomially small, this is harmless unless the Gate 2 mass is concentrated exactly at the boundary. A standard packet-shrinking or interior-selection lemma can handle this.

---

# 7. Integrated version

If Gate 2 gives only integral mass on the wall region, not a point \(m_0\), we need a sampling lemma.

Let

\[
W=\{m\in I: |q_0(m)|\le Q^{-C_0}\}.
\]

Suppose

\[
\int_W |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then by Chebyshev, there is a point \(m_0\in W\) with

\[
|u(m_0)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_0)\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and, assuming anisotropy upper bounds, also

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Apply the wall-escape theorem to get \(m_1\) off the wall.

Thus D3′ can be used at the integral level.

---

# 8. Why this may beat source-robust row search

The previous D3 route required finding a row with

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The wall-escape route instead says:

\[
q_0=0,\ u\ne0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
q_0\ne0
\text{ nearby}.
\]

Then the already-understood nondegenerate rows \(A_7,A_9\) work.

So the wall branch may not require a new invariant. It may require only:

1. derivative bounds;
2. sampling stability;
3. permission to move the row-conversion point.

These are analytic/local conditions, not new arithmetic inputs.

---

# 9. Remaining critical question

The key issue is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the downstream contradiction require the row lower bound at the original sampled point, or merely somewhere in }I_\rho?
}
\]

If merely somewhere in the packet, wall escape is a viable proof path.

If the exact point matters, wall escape does not solve D3, and we still need a source-robust row.

Given the row-conversion goal is usually existential—find a row lower bound somewhere where source/anisotropy is live—the nearby-point version should be acceptable, but this must be checked against the final contradiction architecture.

---

# 10. Final conclusion of the continued attack

I now recommend replacing D3 with a more concrete fork:

## D3a — Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\text{ nearby with }q_0(m_1)\text{ polynomially nonzero and Gate 2 mass still live.}
\]

Then D4 handles \(m_1\).

## D3b — Source-Robust Row Theorem

If row conversion must occur at the exact wall point, find

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The wall-escape route is more concrete and should be attacked first.

## Agent 4 / D — \((q_0)\)-adic wall quotient and anisotropy ideal

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: formalize the wall quotient algebra and reduce D3 to an ideal-membership / row-generation problem. The current downstream update identifies the strongest concrete wall routes as wall escape and \((q_0)\)-adic row-pencil / ideal-generation at \(q_0=0\). 

---

# 1. Wall quotient identities

Let

\[
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The first anisotropy factor is

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

Modulo the wall ideal

\[
(q_0),
\]

we immediately get

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\equiv u\pmod{(q_0)}.
}
\]

The second anisotropy factor is

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q_0(q_0')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Modulo \((q_0)\), the first term vanishes:

\[
2q_0(q_0')^2\equiv0\pmod{(q_0)}.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_G''
=
(u-6q_0+2q_0^3)''
=
u''-6q_0''+2(q_0^3)''.
\]

Since

\[
q_0''=u,
\]

and

\[
(q_0^3)''=6q_0(q_0')^2+3q_0^2q_0'',
\]

we have

\[
(q_0^3)''\equiv0\pmod{(q_0)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\Gamma_G''
\equiv u''-6u\pmod{(q_0)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\equiv
-\frac16(u''-6u)
=
u-\frac16u''
\pmod{(q_0)}.
\]

Define

\[
\boxed{
\eta:=u-\frac16u''.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv \eta\pmod{(q_0)}.
}
\]

So the wall quotient of the Gate 2 anisotropy vector is

\[
\boxed{
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\equiv
(u,\eta)
\pmod{(q_0)}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Wall anisotropy ideal

Define the wall anisotropy ideal

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak I_{\rm G2,wall}:=(u,\eta)
}
\]

inside the local differential-polynomial ring after quotienting by \((q_0)\).

At the wall, Gate 2 pointwise mass becomes

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\equiv
|u|^2(u^2+\eta^2)
=
|u|^2|W|^2,
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
W=(u,\eta).
}
\]

Thus the wall branch is live precisely when

\[
\boxed{
|u|^2|W|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Any row architecture that resolves the wall should generate a nontrivial element of the ideal generated by \(u\) and \(\eta\), without an extra \(q_0\)-factor.

---

# 3. Wall row ideal

Let

\[
\mathbf R_N=(R_1,\ldots,R_s)
\]

be a finite row vector, for example

\[
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})
\]

or their raw / ambient / correction variants.

Define the wall residues

\[
\overline R_j:=R_j\bmod(q_0).
\]

Then define the wall row ideal

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_{\rm wall}:=(\overline R_1,\ldots,\overline R_s).
}
\]

The wall branch is resolved if \(\mathcal I_{\rm wall}\) controls a positive power of the anisotropy ideal:

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N\subset \mathcal I_{\rm wall}
}
\]

for some finite \(N\), with polynomially bounded certificate coefficients.

Concretely, for every monomial

\[
u^a\eta^b,\qquad a+b=N,
\]

one needs identities

\[
\boxed{
u^a\eta^b
=
\sum_{j=1}^s C_{ab,j}\,\overline R_j
}
\]

with coefficient bounds

\[
\boxed{
|C_{ab,j}|\le Q^C
}
\]

on the relevant local packet.

---

# 4. Why ideal generation implies a row lower bound

Assume

\[
(u,\eta)^N\subset \mathcal I_{\rm wall}
\]

with polynomial certificate bounds. Suppose for contradiction that every row is small:

\[
|\overline R_j|\le \varepsilon.
\]

Then every degree-\(N\) anisotropy monomial satisfies

\[
|u^a\eta^b|
\le
Q^C s\,\varepsilon.
\]

Taking the largest monomial among \(u^a\eta^b\) gives

\[
(|u|+|\eta|)^N
\le
Q^{C'}\varepsilon.
\]

Thus

\[
|W|
=
(|u|^2+|\eta|^2)^{1/2}
\le
Q^{C''}\varepsilon^{1/N}.
\]

But wall Gate 2 mass gives

\[
|u|^2|W|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

If \(|u|\le Q^{-A/2}\), Gate 2 already fails. Hence on the wall-live branch,

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-A_u},
\qquad
|W|\ge Q^{-A_W}.
\]

So at least one row must obey

\[
\boxed{
\max_j|\overline R_j|\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for a polynomial exponent \(A'\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N\subset\mathcal I_{\rm wall}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{wall row lower bound under Gate 2 mass}.
}
\]

This is the finite algebra certificate needed for D3.

---

# 5. Apply to known projected rows

For the known projected leading tower,

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

Modulo \((q_0)\),

\[
H\equiv0.
\]

Hence the leading tower contributes nothing:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\equiv
C_{2k+1}
\pmod{(q_0)},
\]

where \(C_{2k+1}\) denotes the correction sector.

Thus the projected tower resolves the wall only if the correction residues satisfy

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N
\subset
(C_7,C_9,C_{11},C_{13},\ldots)\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

If all correction residues vanish modulo \(q_0\),

\[
C_{2k+1}\equiv0\pmod{(q_0)},
\]

then

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm wall}=0
\]

for the known projected tower, and no wall resolution is possible inside that tower.

---

# 6. Raw / ambient row audit in ideal form

For raw rows, define

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm raw,wall}
=
(R^{\rm raw}_1,\ldots,R^{\rm raw}_s)\bmod(q_0).
\]

For ambient rows,

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm amb,wall}
=
(R^{\rm amb}_1,\ldots,R^{\rm amb}_s)\bmod(q_0).
\]

The audit target is:

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N\subset \mathcal I_{\rm raw,wall}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N\subset \mathcal I_{\rm amb,wall}.
}
\]

If one of these holds, then there is wall-live information before or outside \(\mathfrak f\)-projection.

If neither holds, and the projected correction ideal also fails, then the current row system cannot resolve the wall.

---

# 7. Minimal cases to test

## Case \(N=1\)

Need

\[
u,\eta\in\mathcal I_{\rm wall}.
\]

This is strongest. It means the rows directly generate both wall anisotropy channels.

Equivalent certificate:

\[
u=\sum_j a_j\overline R_j,
\qquad
\eta=\sum_j b_j\overline R_j.
\]

If true, wall resolution is immediate.

## Case \(N=2\)

Need

\[
u^2,\quad u\eta,\quad \eta^2
\in\mathcal I_{\rm wall}.
\]

This still suffices because Gate 2 gives

\[
|u|^2(u^2+\eta^2)\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

In fact, a slightly weaker ideal is enough:

\[
\boxed{
u(u,\eta)\subset\mathcal I_{\rm wall},
}
\]

i.e.

\[
u^2,\quad u\eta\in\mathcal I_{\rm wall}.
\]

Because wall Gate 2 mass is

\[
|u|^2|W|^2,
\]

the natural ideal target is

\[
\boxed{
u\cdot(u,\eta)=(u^2,u\eta).
}
\]

If the rows generate \(u^2\) and \(u\eta\), then

\[
|\mathbf R|\gtrsim Q^{-A}
\]

under Gate 2 wall mass.

## Case \(N=3\) or higher

Higher \(N\) still works but worsens exponents. It may be necessary if the first nonzero row residues are cubic or quartic in \(u,\eta\).

---

# 8. Relation to wall-blow-up rows

Earlier, the wall-blow-up row

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\]

had wall residue

\[
\left(A_7^{\mathfrak f}/q_0\right)\big|_{q_0=0}
\sim u^3\Gamma_G
\equiv u^4.
\]

Similarly,

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\]

has residue

\[
u^3\eta.
\]

So the blow-up rows generate

\[
(u^4,u^3\eta)=u^3(u,\eta).
\]

Thus, in the wall quotient, blow-up rows certify

\[
\boxed{
u^3(u,\eta)\subset \mathcal I_{\rm blowup,wall}.
}
\]

Because Gate 2 wall mass gives

\[
|u|^2|W|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and if \(u\) is polynomially non-small, then \(u^3W\) is polynomially non-small. Therefore blow-up rows solve the wall algebraically.

The open architectural question is whether the quotients

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\]

are legitimate downstream rows/invariants.

---

# 9. Finite algebra protocol

To execute D3:

1. Choose row family:

\[
\mathbf R_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})
\]

and include raw / ambient / correction variants.

2. Reduce modulo \((q_0)\):

\[
\overline R_j=R_j\bmod(q_0).
\]

3. Express each residue in variables

\[
u,\quad \eta=u-\frac16u'',\quad q',\quad u',\ldots
\]

4. Check ideal inclusion:

\[
u(u,\eta)\subset(\overline R_j)
\]

first.

5. If false, check

\[
(u,\eta)^N\subset(\overline R_j)
\]

for small \(N=2,3,4\).

6. If all fail, test blow-up residues:

\[
\overline{A_{2k+1}/q_0}.
\]

7. If blow-up works, decide whether blow-up rows are admissible. If not, D3 remains open.

---

# 10. Final deliverable

The wall quotient algebra reduces D3 to a finite ideal-generation test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find rows }R_j\text{ such that }
(u,\eta)^N\subset (R_j\bmod q_0).
}
\]

The most natural target is the smaller ideal

\[
\boxed{
u(u,\eta)=(u^2,u\eta).
}
\]

If this inclusion holds with polynomial certificates, then D3 is proved.

If not, the known row architecture is insufficient unless wall-escape sampling or blow-up rows are admitted.

Current best candidate:

\[
\boxed{
A_7/q_0,\ A_9/q_0
}
\]

because they generate

\[
u^3(u,\eta)
\]

at the wall.

But without admissibility of \(q_0\)-divided rows, D3 remains a named input.

_Thought for 12s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continued attack: replace wall rows by a saturated wall ideal or wall-escape sampling

Continuing the \(q_0\)-wall attack. The last useful reduction was:

\[
\Gamma_G\bmod(q_0)=u,\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\bmod(q_0)=\eta:=u-\frac16u'',
\]

so the wall Gate 2 signal is controlled by

\[
|u|^2(u^2+\eta^2).
\]

The row problem is now algebraic:

\[
\text{find proof-relevant rows }R_j\text{ such that }
(u,\eta)^N\subset (R_j\bmod q_0).
\]

The most promising candidate remains the saturated/blow-up row family:

\[
A_7/q_0,\qquad A_9/q_0,
\]

because modulo \(q_0\) they generate

\[
u^3(u,\eta).
\]

The issue is whether these divided rows are legitimate downstream invariants. 

---

# 1. Saturated row ideal: the clean algebraic object

Let \(\mathcal I_{\rm row}\) be the ideal generated by the proof-relevant downstream rows:

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm row}=(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},A_{11}^{\mathfrak f},\ldots).
\]

The ordinary row ideal is wall-dead if

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm row}\subset(q_0).
\]

But if all rows vanish **only because of a common removable \(q_0\)-factor**, the right algebraic object is the saturation:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_{\rm sat}
:=
(\mathcal I_{\rm row}:q_0^\infty)
=
\{F:\exists k,\ q_0^kF\in\mathcal I_{\rm row}\}.
}
\]

If

\[
u(u,\eta)\subset \mathcal I_{\rm sat}\bmod(q_0),
\]

then the wall information is present in the row architecture, but hidden behind a common \(q_0\)-factor.

For the known leading rows,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Therefore

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\sim
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^3\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\sim
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Modulo \(q_0\),

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\equiv
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^4,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}/q_0
\equiv
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\eta.
\]

Thus the saturated row ideal contains

\[
\boxed{
u^3(u,\eta)=(u^4,u^3\eta).
}
\]

This is enough under wall Gate 2 plus a polynomial lower bound for \(|u|\).

---

# 2. Saturated-row theorem

The theorem to try to prove is:

## Saturated Wall Row Theorem

Assume the downstream row ideal satisfies

\[
q_0\,\widehat A_7=A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
q_0\,\widehat A_9=A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

with regular saturated rows \(\widehat A_7,\widehat A_9\), and

\[
\widehat A_7
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^3\Gamma_G+\widehat{\mathcal R}_7,
\]

\[
\widehat A_9
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\Gamma_{G,2}+\widehat{\mathcal R}_9.
\]

Assume correction control

\[
\left(
|\widehat{\mathcal R}_7|^2+
|\widehat{\mathcal R}_9|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\le
\frac12
u^3
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Then

\[
\left(
|\widehat A_7|^2+|\widehat A_9|^2
\right)^{1/2}
\ge
c\,|u|^3
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

If Gate 2 pointwise mass holds,

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

then

\[
|\widehat A_7|+|\widehat A_9|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

At \(q_0=0\), this becomes especially strong because

\[
\Gamma_G=u,
\]

so

\[
|\widehat A_7|\sim |u|^4.
\]

---

# 3. The key legitimacy question

The saturated rows are algebraically natural, but proof relevance is not automatic.

The decisive question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the downstream contradiction allow saturated rows }A/q_0,
\text{ or only original rows }A?
}
\]

There are three possible answers.

## Case 1 — Saturated rows are legitimate invariants

Then D3 is essentially solved by \((A_7/q_0,A_9/q_0)\), modulo correction control.

This would be the best outcome.

## Case 2 — Saturated rows are not rows, but wall-normal derivatives are legitimate

Then use

\[
\partial_{q_0}A_7^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0},
\qquad
\partial_{q_0}A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0}.
\]

From the leading terms,

\[
\partial_{q_0}A_7^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^3\Gamma_G
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}u^4,
\]

\[
\partial_{q_0}A_9^{\mathfrak f}\big|_{q_0=0}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}u^3\eta.
\]

So the wall-normal derivative has the same content as the saturated row.

But it must be an admissible invariant in the downstream geometry.

## Case 3 — Only original rows are permitted

Then \(A_7,A_9\) cannot help at the wall, because both vanish like \(q_0\). In that case, D3 needs either:

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0
\]

for some different raw/ambient/correction row, or the wall-escape sampling theorem.

---

# 4. Wall-escape is the fallback if saturation is illegal

If saturated rows are not permitted, use the nearby-sampling route.

Suppose

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le \eta,
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|=|q_0''(m_0)|\ge \delta,
\]

and

\[
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le h}|q_0'''(m)|\le M_3.
\]

Then

\[
q_0(m_0+h)+q_0(m_0-h)-2q_0(m_0)
=
u(m_0)h^2+O(M_3h^3).
\]

If

\[
M_3h\le c\delta,
\qquad
\eta\le c\delta h^2,
\]

then there is

\[
m_1\in\{m_0-h,m_0,m_0+h\}
\]

with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge c\delta h^2.
\]

With polynomial bounds, this gives

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q}.
\]

If additionally

\[
|u'|\le M_u,\qquad M_uh\le c\delta,
\]

then

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\delta.
\]

So D4 applies at \(m_1\) if Gate 2 mass remains live.

This gives a second theorem:

## Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

If

\[
q_0\approx0,\qquad u\not\approx0
\]

at a Gate 2-live point, then there exists a nearby point where

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C},\qquad |u|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and row conversion can be performed through D4.

This is valid if the downstream contradiction needs a row lower bound **somewhere in the packet**, not exactly at the original point.

---

# 5. New attack: combine saturation and escape

There is a useful hybrid.

Even if saturated rows are not globally legitimate, they may be legitimate **as limits of non-wall rows**.

If \(q_0(m_1)\ne0\), then

\[
\frac{A_7(m_1)}{q_0(m_1)}
\]

is just a ratio of ordinary quantities. D4 at \(m_1\) gives

\[
A_7(m_1)
\sim
q_0(m_1)u(m_1)^3\Gamma_G(m_1).
\]

The wall-escape lemma gives

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge c|u(m_0)|h^2.
\]

Thus the original rows themselves become nonzero at \(m_1\), with size

\[
|A_7(m_1)|
\gtrsim
|u(m_0)|h^2
\cdot
|u(m_1)|^3
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|.
\]

If

\[
|u(m_0)|,\ |u(m_1)|,\ |\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\]

are polynomially bounded below and

\[
h=Q^{-C_h},
\]

then

\[
|A_7(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So even if the quotient is not an admissible row, it predicts the magnitude of the original row after an admissible displacement.

This makes wall escape the safer route.

---

# 6. Exact theorem to add to D3

D3 should be split into two alternatives.

## D3a — Saturated Row Theorem

The saturated row vector

\[
(A_7/q_0,\ A_9/q_0)
\]

or the wall-normal derivative vector is proof-relevant and satisfies

\[
\left|
(A_7/q_0,\ A_9/q_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

under wall Gate 2 mass.

## D3b — Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

If saturated rows are not proof-relevant, then any wall point with

\[
|q_0|\le Q^{-C_0},
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and Gate 2 pointwise mass yields a nearby point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u'},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)\ge Q^{-A'},
\]

so D4 applies.

If either D3a or D3b is proved, the \(q_0\)-wall is resolved.

---

# 7. Remaining technical blockers

For D3a:

1. prove divisibility

\[
A_7,A_9\in(q_0)
\]

as exact algebraic row expressions;

2. prove the quotients are canonical downstream invariants;

3. prove correction bounds for the quotient rows.

For D3b:

1. prove a sampling lemma allowing the row-conversion point to move within \(I_\rho\);

2. prove local derivative bounds

\[
|q_0'''|,\ |u'|,\ |\Gamma_G'|,\ |\Gamma_{G,2}'|
\le Q^C;
\]

3. preserve Gate 2 signal under displacement;

4. handle packet boundary cases.

---

# 8. Verdict

The attack has improved D3:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 no longer needs only an unknown source-robust row.}
}
\]

It can be attacked by either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{saturated/blow-up rows}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall-escape sampling + D4}.
}
\]

The wall-escape route is currently the most proof-like, because it uses original rows at a nearby non-wall point rather than changing the row algebra.

The next best target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that downstream row conversion is existential on }I_\rho
\text{ and allows nearby sampling.}
}
\]

If yes, D3 reduces to a local Taylor lemma plus D4 correction control.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:18:39)

I’ll sharpen the wall-escape route into an integral-to-pointwise argument: split Gate 2 mass into non-wall and wall strips, then show wall-strip mass can be transported to nearby non-wall samples unless the packet is too short or derivatives are uncontrolled.

_Thought for 42s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continued attack: wall escape as a replacement for D3

The \(q_0\)-wall can likely be bypassed if downstream row conversion is **existential on the packet interval** rather than tied to one fixed point. The key is:

\[
q_0\approx0,\qquad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q_0\text{ becomes polynomially nonzero nearby.}
\]

Then the already-structured nondegenerate row-conversion theorem D4 applies at the nearby point. This is now more concrete than searching indefinitely for a row that survives exactly at \(q_0=0\). The current downstream framework identifies D3/D4 as the wall and nondegenerate row-conversion inputs. 

---

# 1. Packet-level split

Let

\[
u=q_0''=q''_{\can},
\]

and define a nondegeneracy threshold

\[
\varepsilon_q=Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Split the packet interval \(I\) into:

\[
I_{\rm nd}:=\{m\in I: |q_0(m)|\ge \varepsilon_q\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}:=\{m\in I: |q_0(m)|< \varepsilon_q\}.
\]

On \(I_{\rm nd}\), D4 applies, provided Gate 2 pointwise mass and correction control hold.

So the only issue is:

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall},
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\not\ll1.
\]

---

# 2. Quantitative wall-escape lemma

Let

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le \eta,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|=|q_0''(m_0)|\ge \delta.
\]

Assume derivative bounds on \([m_0-h,m_0+h]\):

\[
|q_0'(m)|\le M_1,
\]

\[
|q_0'''(m)|\le M_3,
\]

\[
|u'(m)|\le M_u.
\]

Choose \(h\) such that

\[
M_3h\le c\delta,
\]

\[
M_uh\le c\delta,
\]

\[
M_1h\le c\delta
\]

if we want to control the upper size of \(q_0\) as well.

Then the second-difference identity gives

\[
q_0(m_0+h)+q_0(m_0-h)-2q_0(m_0)
=
u(m_0)h^2+O(M_3h^3).
\]

Therefore, if

\[
\eta\le c\delta h^2,
\]

then there exists

\[
m_1\in\{m_0-h,m_0,m_0+h\}
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge c\delta h^2.
\]

Also, by the \(u'\)-bound,

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\delta.
\]

Set

\[
\varepsilon_q:=c\delta h^2.
\]

Then

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge \varepsilon_q,
\]

so \(m_1\in I_{\rm nd}\).

With polynomial bounds

\[
\delta\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
M_1,M_3,M_u\le Q^C,
\]

choose

\[
h=Q^{-C_h}
\]

with \(C_h\) large enough. Then

\[
\varepsilon_q=Q^{-C_q}
\]

for some polynomial exponent \(C_q\). This is sufficient for D4.

---

# 3. Preserve Gate 2 pointwise mass

At the wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

If \(q_0\) is very small relative to \(u\), then

\[
\Gamma_G\approx u.
\]

After displacement, if we keep

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\le c|u(m_1)|
\]

by choosing \(h\) sufficiently small and controlling \(q_0'\), then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c|u(m_1)|.
\]

Hence

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2)
\ge c|u(m_1)|^4
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So D4 pointwise Gate 2 mass holds at \(m_1\).

If the upper control

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ll |u(m_1)|
\]

is not available, Gate 2 mass can still remain live, but proving it requires a Lipschitz bound for the full anisotropy vector:

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|\le Q^C.
\]

Then choose \(h\) so small that the Gate 2 integrand cannot drop below every polynomial threshold between \(m_0\) and \(m_1\).

The cleaner theorem uses the upper control route.

---

# 4. Boundary handling

If \(m_0\) is near the endpoint of \(I\), use a one-sided second difference.

If

\[
[m_0,m_0+2h]\subset I,
\]

then

\[
q_0(m_0+2h)-2q_0(m_0+h)+q_0(m_0)
=
u(m_0)h^2+O(M_3h^3).
\]

Thus one of

\[
m_0,\quad m_0+h,\quad m_0+2h
\]

has

\[
|q_0|\ge c\delta h^2-\eta.
\]

Similarly on the left side.

If no one-sided segment of length \(2h\) exists, then \(I\) is shorter than \(2h\). Choose \(h\ll |I|\) at the start, or trim a boundary layer of size \(2h\). Since \(h\) is polynomially small, the boundary layer is negligible for an interval-level Gate 2 sampling argument.

---

# 5. Wall-escape sampling theorem

A usable D3 replacement is:

## D3a — \(q_0\)-Wall Escape Sampling Theorem

Assume \(m_0\in I\) satisfies

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le Q^{-C_0},
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_0)|^2(\Gamma_G(m_0)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_0)^2)\ge Q^{-A_G}.
\]

Assume local derivative bounds on a neighborhood of radius \(Q^{-C_h}\):

\[
|q_0'|\le Q^{C_1},
\]

\[
|q_0'''|\le Q^{C_3},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_u'},
\]

and, if using anisotropy-stability rather than \(\Gamma_G\)-dominance,

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_1\in I,\qquad |m_1-m_0|\le Q^{-C_h},
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u''},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2)\ge Q^{-A_G'}.
\]

Therefore D4 applies at \(m_1\), assuming D4 correction control.

---

# 6. D4 after wall escape

At \(m_1\), D4 says:

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

The wall-escape theorem gives

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and Gate 2 pointwise mass.

Thus

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

With

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}(m_1)|\le\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|,
\]

we get

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|
\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

So the wall is resolved **if row conversion may sample at \(m_1\)**.

---

# 7. Sampling admissibility is now the key issue

This attack reduces the \(q_0\)-wall to one precise question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the downstream contradiction require a row lower bound at a preassigned point,}
}
\]

or only

\[
\boxed{
\text{somewhere in the packet interval }I?
}
\]

If the row lower bound is existential on \(I\), the wall-escape theorem solves D3 modulo derivative bounds and D4 correction control.

If the row lower bound must occur at exactly the original \(m_0\), then wall escape is not enough and one needs a genuine source-robust row:

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

In most energy-to-row arguments, an existential sample point is enough. If that is true here, D3 is much closer than previously thought.

---

# 8. Relation to saturated / blow-up rows

The wall-blow-up row

\[
A_7/q_0
\]

has wall residue

\[
(A_7/q_0)|_{q_0=0}\sim u^4,
\]

and

\[
(A_9/q_0)|_{q_0=0}\sim u^3\eta,
\qquad
\eta=u-\frac16u''.
\]

This proves that the row architecture contains wall information after saturation by \(q_0\).

The wall-escape theorem is the geometric version of that saturation: instead of dividing by \(q_0\), move to a nearby point where \(q_0\) is small but nonzero, so the original rows reveal the saturated information with a polynomial loss.

Thus D3 can be attacked by either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{saturated / blow-up row admissibility}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall-escape sampling admissibility}.
}
\]

The second is more likely compatible with the original row architecture.

---

# 9. Final attack status

The \(q_0\)-wall is no longer just an unknown source-robust row problem.

A concrete path is:

\[
\boxed{
q_0\approx0,\quad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
q_0\text{ nonzero nearby}
\Rightarrow
\text{D4 applies nearby}.
}
\]

So the next exact theorem should be:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wall-Escape Sampling + D4}
\Rightarrow
\textbf{\(q_0\)-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

The remaining tasks are:

1. prove the wall-escape Taylor lemma with packet-boundary handling;
2. prove local derivative bounds for \(q_0',q_0''',u'\) and anisotropy stability;
3. confirm row conversion only requires an existential point in \(I\);
4. apply D4 correction control at the displaced point.

If these hold, D3 can be replaced by a local analytic theorem rather than a new row/invariant.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:20:25)

I’ll push the wall-escape argument from pointwise Taylor to an interval/sublevel-set theorem. The goal is to convert wall-branch Gate 2 mass into nearby non-wall samples systematically, not just at one hand-picked point.

_Thought for 16s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continued attack: wall escape via sublevel geometry

The previous attack showed a pointwise Taylor escape:

\[
q_0\approx0,\qquad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
q_0\text{ becomes polynomially nonzero nearby}.
\]

Now I’ll sharpen that into a **sublevel-set / interval theorem**. This is better because Gate 2 gives mass on sets, not necessarily one preselected point.

---

# 1. Replace pointwise escape by wall-strip escape

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''.
\]

Fix thresholds

\[
\varepsilon_q=Q^{-C_q},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_u}.
\]

Define the wall strip

\[
W_{\varepsilon_q}
=
\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon_q\}.
\]

Define the live-source wall region

\[
W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}
=
\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon_q,\ |u(m)|\ge \tau\}.
\]

The wall problem is serious only on \(W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}\). If \(|u|\) is small, Gate 1/Gate 2 source mass is not concentrated there.

The target is:

\[
\boxed{
W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}
\text{ lies within a small neighborhood of the non-wall set }
\{|q|\ge\varepsilon_q'\},
}
\]

where \(\varepsilon_q'\) is still polynomially small and where \(u\) remains live.

---

# 2. Local convexity from \(u=q''\)

Assume on a short interval \(J\)

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau
\]

and

\[
|u'(m)|\le M_u
\]

for

\[
|m-m_0|\le h.
\]

If

\[
M_u h\le \frac14\tau,
\]

then on that neighborhood

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau.
\]

Also \(u\) has fixed sign there.

Thus \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave on

\[
[m_0-h,m_0+h].
\]

This is stronger than the earlier second-difference argument: it gives sublevel-set geometry.

---

# 3. Sublevel width bound

Suppose on an interval \(J\),

\[
|q''|\ge \tau
\]

with fixed sign. Then for any \(\varepsilon>0\), every connected component of

\[
\{m\in J: |q(m)|\le \varepsilon\}
\]

has length

\[
\boxed{
\ll \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
}
\]

up to boundary effects.

Reason: if \(q''\ge\tau\), then \(q\) is \(\tau\)-convex. A convex function with second derivative at least \(\tau\) cannot remain inside a vertical strip of height \(2\varepsilon\) over a horizontal interval longer than \(O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})\). The same holds for \(q''\le-\tau\) by replacing \(q\) by \(-q\).

Thus, on live-source regions where \(u\) is stable, the wall strip is thin:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{width}\{|q|\le \varepsilon_q\}
\ll
\sqrt{\varepsilon_q/\tau}.
}
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon_q=Q^{-C_q},\qquad \tau=Q^{-C_u},
\]

this width is

\[
Q^{-(C_q-C_u)/2}.
\]

Choose \(C_q\gg C_u\), and the wall strip is polynomially thin.

---

# 4. Escape point at controlled distance and controlled \(q\)

For any

\[
m_0\in W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau},
\]

under the local stability condition for \(u\), there is a point \(m_1\) with

\[
|m_1-m_0|
\ll
\sqrt{\varepsilon_q/\tau}
\]

such that

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon_q
\]

unless the entire relevant interval is trapped at the boundary.

Moreover, since \(m_1\) is close and

\[
|u'|\le M_u,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau
\]

provided

\[
M_u\sqrt{\varepsilon_q/\tau}\le \frac12\tau.
\]

That is,

\[
\varepsilon_q\le c\frac{\tau^3}{M_u^2}.
\]

With polynomial thresholds, this is achievable by choosing \(C_q\) sufficiently large relative to \(C_u\) and the derivative exponent for \(M_u\).

So the wall escape theorem can be strengthened to:

\[
\boxed{
|q|\le\varepsilon_q,\ |u|\ge\tau
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\text{ nearby}:
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon_q,\ |u(m_1)|\ge\tau/2.
}
\]

This avoids the earlier issue of \(q\) becoming too large: we sample at the **first exit** from the wall strip.

---

# 5. Preserve \(\Gamma_G\)

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

If

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon_q
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon_q\ll \tau,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6\varepsilon_q-2\varepsilon_q^3
\ge
c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

So Gate 2 pointwise mass remains live at the escaped point, independently of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\).

This is important. We do **not** need to preserve the full anisotropy vector by Lipschitz control. The identity

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

itself gives the lower bound if we exit the wall strip at a level still much smaller than \(|u|\).

---

# 6. D3 via first-exit sampling

This gives a clean replacement for the source-robust row theorem.

## D3a — First-Exit Wall-Escape Theorem

Let

\[
W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}
=
\{|q_0|<\varepsilon_q,\ |u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

Assume local derivative control

\[
|u'|\le M_u
\]

and choose

\[
\varepsilon_q\le c\frac{\tau^3}{M_u^2},
\qquad
\varepsilon_q\ll\tau.
\]

Then for every \(m_0\in W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}\), away from packet-boundary exceptions, there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|
\ll
\sqrt{\varepsilon_q/\tau},
\]

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon_q,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Consequently,

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) satisfies the nondegenerate branch hypotheses for D4:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge \varepsilon_q=Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then D4 row conversion applies at \(m_1\), assuming correction control.

---

# 7. Boundary cases

If \(m_0\) lies near the packet boundary, first exit may occur outside \(I\). There are three remedies.

## Remedy A — interior mass selection

If Gate 2 wall mass is not confined to a boundary layer of thickness

\[
\rho:=\sqrt{\varepsilon_q/\tau},
\]

then choose \(m_0\) from the interior

\[
I_{\rm int}
=
\{m:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\ge \rho\}.
\]

Then the first-exit point lies inside \(I\).

## Remedy B — one-sided exit

If \(m_0\) is near one boundary but the interval extends in the other direction, use the one-sided sublevel exit.

Uniform convexity still implies a first exit within

\[
O(\sqrt{\varepsilon_q/\tau})
\]

unless the function remains in the wall strip all the way to the boundary.

## Remedy C — boundary row conversion

If wall mass is genuinely concentrated in a boundary layer of thickness \(\rho\), then either:

\[
\rho |I|^{-1}
\]

is not negligible, in which case the packet can be shrunk/recentered, or the boundary layer carries too little mass to be relevant if

\[
\rho\ll Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

So choose

\[
C_q
\]

large enough that

\[
\rho\le Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

Then boundary wall mass is negligible relative to polynomial Gate 2 mass.

---

# 8. Integral version

Suppose the wall branch carries Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_{W_{\varepsilon_q}}
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Split

\[
W_{\varepsilon_q}
=
W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}
\cup
\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

If \(\tau\) is chosen small enough, the \(|u|<\tau\) part cannot carry much Gate 2 mass unless anisotropy is enormous. With a polynomial anisotropy upper bound

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we have

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\le
\tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}
\]

on \(|u|<\tau\). Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

so this is negligible. Then \(W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}\) carries polynomial mass.

Pick a point

\[
m_0\in W_{\varepsilon_q,\tau}
\]

away from the boundary and apply first-exit escape to get \(m_1\in I_{\rm nd}\). D4 applies there.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\text{non-wall D4 sample nearby}.
}
\]

---

# 9. What remains to verify

The wall-escape route now needs only local analytic and sampling assumptions:

1. polynomial upper bound for

\[
|u'|
\]

on the packet;

2. polynomial upper bound for anisotropy to discard \(|u|<\tau\) regions;

3. boundary-layer negligibility or packet recentering;

4. confirmation that downstream row conversion only needs an existential point in \(I\);

5. D4 correction control at the escaped point.

No new source-robust row is needed if these hold.

---

# 10. Updated D3 theorem

## D3 — \(q_0\)-Wall Escape Resolution

Assume Gate 2 pointwise or integral mass on the wall branch

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon_q.
\]

Assume polynomial derivative and anisotropy upper bounds. Then either the wall branch contributes negligible mass, or there exists a point

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Therefore D4 applies and yields

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

under correction control.

---

# 11. Verdict

This is a significant improvement over the original D3 formulation.

Instead of needing a new row with

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

we can likely resolve the wall by **first-exit sampling**:

\[
q_0=0,\ u=q_0''\ne0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
q_0\ne0\text{ nearby}.
\]

The only serious architectural check left is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{row conversion must be existential somewhere in the packet interval.}
}
\]

If true, then D3 reduces to the First-Exit Wall-Escape Theorem plus D4.

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: make wall escape an interval-level theorem

The wall-escape route can be made sharper. The goal is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass on the }q_0\text{-wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{a nearby non-wall D4 sample exists.}
}
\]

This would replace the difficult “find a source-robust row at \(q_0=0\)” problem with a local Taylor/sublevel theorem plus ordinary nondegenerate row conversion.

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''=q''_{\can}.
\]

Fix thresholds

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Define the wall strip

\[
W_\varepsilon=\{m\in I: |q(m)|\le \varepsilon\},
\]

and the live wall strip

\[
W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
=
\{m\in I: |q(m)|\le\varepsilon,\ |u(m)|\ge \tau\}.
\]

The problematic branch is when Gate 2 mass is carried by \(W_{\varepsilon,\tau}\).

At \(q=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3=u.
\]

So if \(|u|\ge\tau\) and \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\), then throughout the wall strip

\[
|\Gamma_G|
\ge
|u|-6|q|-2|q|^3
\ge
\frac12\tau.
\]

Thus Gate 2 is live on \(W_{\varepsilon,\tau}\). The issue is only that known rows are multiplied by \(q\).

---

# 2. Uniform convexity lemma

Assume on an interval \(J\)

\[
|u|=|q''|\ge \tau
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le M.
\]

If

\[
|J|\le \frac{\tau}{2M},
\]

then \(u\) has constant sign on \(J\), and

\[
|q''|\ge \frac12\tau
\]

throughout \(J\).

Therefore \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave on \(J\).

For such \(J\), every connected component of

\[
\{|q|\le \varepsilon\}\cap J
\]

has length

\[
\boxed{
\ll \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
}
\]

Proof: if \(q''\ge \tau/2\), subtract the tangent at the minimum point of \(q\) on the component. The quadratic lower bound gives

\[
|q(x)-q(x_*)|\ge c\tau |x-x_*|^2.
\]

Since \(|q|\le\varepsilon\), the component width is at most \(C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\). The concave case is identical after replacing \(q\) by \(-q\).

---

# 3. First-exit wall escape

Let

\[
m_0\in W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
\]

and suppose

\[
\operatorname{dist}(m_0,\partial I)\ge \rho,
\]

where

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Assume

\[
|u'|\le M
\]

and

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Then \(u\) remains live on \([m_0-\rho,m_0+\rho]\), and the sublevel width lemma implies there exists

\[
m_1,\qquad |m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

such that

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

Moreover, if

\[
\varepsilon\le c\tau,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
=
|u(m_1)-6q(m_1)+2q(m_1)^3|
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
|u(m_1)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2\right)
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

So \(m_1\) satisfies both:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

and a polynomial Gate 2 pointwise lower bound.

This is exactly the D4 nondegenerate branch.

---

# 4. Choosing exponents

Let

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_M}.
\]

Choose

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

with

\[
C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_M+10.
\]

Then

\[
\rho=\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

The stability condition

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau
\]

becomes

\[
Q^{C_M}Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\le
Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

i.e.

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
3C_\tau+2C_M+O(1).
\]

So all losses remain polynomial.

At the escaped point,

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}/2,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}/C.
\]

Then D4 gives

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|
\ge Q^{-C}
\]

assuming correction control.

---

# 5. Integral wall-mass version

Suppose Gate 2 wall mass is nontrivial:

\[
\int_{W_\varepsilon}
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Split

\[
W_\varepsilon
=
W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
\cup
\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

Assume an anisotropy upper bound

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}
\]

on \(I\). Then on \(\{|u|<\tau\}\),

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\le
\tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

with \(C_\tau\) large enough that this part contributes negligibly. Then \(W_{\varepsilon,\tau}\) carries polynomial Gate 2 mass.

If \(W_{\varepsilon,\tau}\) is not concentrated in the boundary layer

\[
\{m:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\},
\]

choose

\[
m_0\in W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
\]

in the interior and apply first-exit wall escape.

If it is concentrated in the boundary layer, then since

\[
|\text{boundary layer}|\le 2\rho,
\]

its contribution is negligible provided

\[
\rho\ll Q^{-A'}|I|
\]

for the relevant polynomial exponent. This is ensured by choosing \(C_\varepsilon\) large enough.

Thus the integral version gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nontrivial wall Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists\text{ nearby non-wall D4 sample}.
}
\]

---

# 6. D3 becomes a sampling theorem, not a row theorem

The original D3 was:

\[
\boxed{
\text{find }R_{\rm rob}\text{ with }R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
}
\]

The wall-escape route replaces it by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{show row conversion may sample nearby in }I.
}
\]

More precisely:

## D3a — Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

Assume Gate 2 pointwise or integral mass occurs in

\[
|q_0|\le \varepsilon.
\]

Assume polynomial bounds for

\[
u',
\qquad
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

or just anisotropy upper bounds.

Then either wall mass is negligible, or there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|^2
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Therefore D4 applies at \(m_1\).

This is a much more concrete path than the source-robust row search.

---

# 7. Remaining architectural check

The only serious remaining question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the downstream contradiction require the row lower bound at a fixed point,}
}
\]

or is it enough to have

\[
\boxed{
\exists m\in I\text{ with row lower bound?}
}
\]

If the downstream row conversion is existential, the wall is essentially handled by wall escape plus D4.

If it is point-locked, then wall escape is insufficient and one still needs the source-robust row or saturated-row theorem.

Given Gate 1 and Gate 2 are interval/energy statements, the row lower bound should normally be existential. But this must be verified against the final contradiction layer.

---

# 8. Relation to \(q_0\)-adic saturation

Wall escape is the analytic realization of the algebraic saturation

\[
(A_7,A_9):q_0.
\]

Algebraically,

\[
A_7/q_0\sim u^3\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9/q_0\sim u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
A_7/q_0\sim u^4,
\qquad
A_9/q_0\sim u^3\eta.
\]

Analytically, instead of dividing by \(q_0\), we move to a nearby point where

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C}
\]

and use the original rows. The polynomial loss from \(q_0\) is exactly the cost of escaping the wall.

Thus the \(q_0\)-wall is not fatal if sampling can move.

---

# 9. Final attack theorem

## Wall-Escape + D4 Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass holds on \(I\);

2. D4 correction control holds at all non-wall samples;

3. derivative bounds

\[
|u'|\le Q^C
\]

and anisotropy upper bounds hold on \(I\);

4. row conversion only requires an existential point in \(I\).

Then

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Proof split:

- if significant Gate 2 mass occurs where \(|q_0|\ge\varepsilon\), apply D4 directly;
- if significant Gate 2 mass occurs where \(|q_0|<\varepsilon\), use first-exit wall escape to find a nearby point with \(|q_0|=\varepsilon\), \(|u|\) live, and \(\Gamma_G\) live; then apply D4.

---

# 10. Verdict

The \(q_0\)-wall can plausibly be resolved without a new source-robust row by proving:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem}
}
\]

plus confirming existential sampling in the downstream contradiction.

This is now the best D3 attack. It is local, analytic, and uses the already-structured D4 theorem rather than requiring new row algebra.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:23:10)

_Thought for 7s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: convert Gate 2 wall mass into non-wall D4 samples

I’ll now make the wall-escape argument into a full **packet-level sampling theorem**.

The goal is:

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C},
\quad
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then the nondegenerate D4 row conversion applies at \(m_\ast\). This would remove the need for a row that survives exactly at \(q_0=0\). This is still within the current downstream attack: Gate 2 propagation and \(q_0\)-wall resolution are the active blockers. 

---

# 1. Start from Gate 2 mass

Assume Gate 2 has been proved:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
G(m):=
|u(m)|^2(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2).
\]

Assume a polynomial upper bound

\[
G(m)\le Q^{C_G}
\]

on \(I\). This follows from the usual derivative/amplitude complexity package if available.

Then by Chebyshev there exists a set

\[
S_G=\{m\in I:G(m)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-2}\}
\]

with

\[
|S_G|\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

So we have many points where Gate 2 is pointwise live.

Now split this set by the wall threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Define

\[
S_{\rm nd}:=S_G\cap\{|q_0|\ge\varepsilon\},
\]

\[
S_{\rm wall}:=S_G\cap\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
S_{\rm nd}\ne\varnothing,
\]

then D4 applies directly at some point of \(S_{\rm nd}\), assuming correction control.

So the only difficult case is:

\[
S_G\subseteq S_{\rm wall}.
\]

That means Gate 2 pointwise mass is occurring inside the \(q_0\)-wall strip.

---

# 2. Inside the wall strip, \(u\) must be live

Inside

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

If

\[
\varepsilon\ll |u|,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge \frac12 |u|.
\]

Thus on wall points where \(u\) is not too small,

\[
G(m)\ge |u|^2\Gamma_G^2\gtrsim |u|^4.
\]

Conversely, if \(G(m)\ge Q^{-C_G'}\) and \(|q_0|<\varepsilon\), then either

\[
|u(m)|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-channel is extremely large. Under a polynomial anisotropy upper bound

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|u(m)|^2
\ge
Q^{-C_G'}Q^{-2C_\Gamma}.
\]

So on \(S_{\rm wall}\), after adjusting exponents,

\[
\boxed{
|u(m)|\ge \tau:=Q^{-C_\tau}.
}
\]

Thus the live wall region satisfies

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|=|q_0''|\ge \tau.
\]

---

# 3. Wall-strip width theorem

Assume on a neighborhood \(J\)

\[
|q_0''|=|u|\ge \tau
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le M.
\]

On any subinterval of length

\[
\le c\tau/M,
\]

the sign of \(u\) is fixed and

\[
|u|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

Hence \(q_0\) is uniformly convex or concave there.

Then every connected component of

\[
\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\}
\]

inside that neighborhood has length

\[
\boxed{
\le C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
}
\]

Proof: if \(q_0''\ge\tau/2\), subtract the tangent at the minimum point; the quadratic lower bound forces exit from \(|q_0|<\varepsilon\) within distance \(O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})\). The concave case is identical after changing sign.

So the live wall strip is thin at scale

\[
\rho:=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

---

# 4. First-exit sample

Take

\[
m_0\in S_{\rm wall}
\]

with distance at least \(\rho\) from \(\partial I\).

By the wall-strip width theorem, there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

and

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon.
\]

Also, since

\[
|u'|\le M
\]

and

\[
M\rho\le \frac12\tau,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

Choose

\[
\varepsilon\ll \tau.
\]

Then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
=
|u(m_1)-6q_0(m_1)+2q_0(m_1)^3|
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
=
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a **non-wall Gate 2 sample**:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

D4 applies at \(m_1\).

---

# 5. Exponent choices

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
M=Q^{C_M}.
\]

Choose

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

with

\[
C_\varepsilon>3C_\tau+2C_M+10.
\]

Then

\[
\rho=\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

The stability condition

\[
M\rho\le \frac12\tau
\]

becomes

\[
Q^{C_M}Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\le
Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

which is exactly

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_M+O(1).
\]

So all losses are polynomial.

---

# 6. Boundary-layer handling

The first-exit argument fails only if all live wall mass lies within the boundary layer

\[
I_{\rm bd}:=\{m:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\}.
\]

But

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho.
\]

If

\[
\rho\le Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

then this boundary layer is too small to carry polynomial Gate 2 mass unless the integrand is too large. Under the polynomial upper bound

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

its contribution is at most

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) large enough that

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho\ll Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then live Gate 2 wall mass cannot be confined to the boundary.

If boundary concentration still matters, shrink the packet to an interior subpacket. Since Gate 1/Gate 2 are interval-energy statements, an interior selection lemma should recover a smaller interval carrying comparable mass.

---

# 7. D3 resolved by wall escape, conditional on existential sampling

We can now state a clean theorem.

## Wall-Escape Row-Conversion Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 pointwise or integral mass holds on \(I\);

2. polynomial upper bounds hold for

\[
G,\quad u',\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2};
\]

3. D4 correction control holds at non-wall points;

4. downstream row conversion only needs a row lower bound at **some** point of \(I\).

Then either:

- Gate 2 mass occurs at a non-wall point and D4 applies directly; or
- Gate 2 mass occurs in the wall strip, and first-exit wall escape produces a nearby non-wall point where D4 applies.

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This replaces D3 by a local analytic sampling theorem.

---

# 8. The remaining architectural question

The decisive issue is now precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is row conversion existential on }I?
}
\]

If yes, the \(q_0\)-wall is essentially solved by wall escape plus D4.

If no, and the row lower bound must occur at an exact preassigned point, then wall escape does not suffice and we must return to either:

\[
\text{source-robust rows}
\]

or

\[
q_0\text{-adic saturated rows }A/q_0.
\]

But downstream energy-to-row arguments are normally existential. They seek a point where the row is large. If this architecture follows that pattern, then wall escape is admissible.

---

# 9. Updated downstream dependency

The downstream branch becomes:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{D1}
+
\text{D2}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

Then:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{wall-escape sampling}
+
\text{D4 correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

So D3 can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling Admissibility}
}
\]

rather than a new source-robust row theorem.

---

# 10. Final verdict of this attack

The \(q_0\)-wall no longer looks like the hardest downstream blocker **if** nearby sampling is allowed.

The true remaining blockers become:

1. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation;
2. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation;
3. D4: Correction control;
4. Sampling admissibility for moving from wall point \(m_0\) to nearby non-wall point \(m_1\).

The source-robust row search is still useful as a backup, but wall escape is the cleaner path.

## Agent 4 / D — Continuing attack: sampling admissibility and wall-escape closure

The wall-escape route now reduces D3 to one architectural question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does downstream row conversion require a large row at a fixed point, or merely somewhere in }I?
}
\]

If the row lower bound is existential on the packet, then the \(q_0\)-wall can be bypassed by first-exit sampling and D4. This is stronger than the previous “find a source-robust row” approach.

---

# 1. The row-conversion target should be existential

Gate 2 is an interval statement:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

D4 converts pointwise nondegenerate Gate 2 mass into rows:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}(m_\ast)|\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_\ast)|
\]

imply

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is naturally existential:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If the downstream contradiction only needs such an \(m_\ast\), then the exact original Gate 2 sample point is irrelevant. We may move within \(I\).

So the required sampling principle is:

## Row Sampling Admissibility

If there exists \(m_1\in I\) satisfying the D4 hypotheses, then the downstream row-conversion layer is valid. It does not require \(m_1\) to be the same point initially selected from Gate 2 mass.

This should be treated as a local theorem in the downstream architecture.

---

# 2. Integral-to-nonwall sampling theorem

Define

\[
G(m)=|u(m)|^2(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2).
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G(m)\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'(m)|\le Q^{C_u},
\]

and the D4 correction-control bound at non-wall samples.

Fix a wall threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Split

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q_0|\ge \varepsilon\},
\qquad
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G(m)\,dm\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-1}.
\]

D4 applies at \(m_\ast\).

So assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G(m)\,dm\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

We now escape the wall.

---

# 3. Remove low-\(u\) wall mass

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

On

\[
\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

if

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

then

\[
G(m)\le \tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so large that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|\ll Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore the wall Gate 2 mass must occur on

\[
W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
=
\{|q_0|<\varepsilon,\ |u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

So there exists

\[
m_0\in W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
\]

with non-negligible Gate 2 mass, away from a negligible boundary layer.

---

# 4. First-exit wall escape

Assume

\[
|u'(m)|\le M=Q^{C_M}
\]

near \(m_0\).

Set

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Choose

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_M+O(1)
\]

so that

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Then on the local interval around \(m_0\),

\[
|u|\ge \frac34\tau,
\]

and \(u=q_0''\) has fixed sign. Therefore \(q_0\) is uniformly convex or concave.

A uniformly convex/concave function with

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<\varepsilon
\]

must exit the wall strip within distance

\[
O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})=\rho.
\]

Thus there exists

\[
m_1\in I,
\qquad
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon.
\]

Moreover,

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

So \(m_1\) satisfies the D4 hypotheses:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

with \(C\) polynomial.

---

# 5. Boundary-layer issue

The first-exit point may leave \(I\) only if \(m_0\) is within distance \(\rho\) of \(\partial I\).

The boundary layer has measure

\[
O(\rho).
\]

Since

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2},
\]

we choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho\ll Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then the boundary layer cannot carry all Gate 2 mass. Hence an interior wall point exists.

If needed, shrink \(I\) to an interior subpacket and repeat the Gate 2 sampling there.

---

# 6. D3 is reduced to D4 plus sampling admissibility

We can now state the improved D3.

## D3a — Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass holds on \(I\):

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. polynomial upper bounds hold for

\[
G,\quad |u'|,\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2};
\]

3. D4 correction control holds at all non-wall samples;

4. row conversion is existential on \(I\).

Then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and hence

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

Proof:

- If non-wall mass exists, sample there and apply D4.
- If wall mass dominates, remove low-\(u\) mass, escape by first exit, and apply D4 at the escaped point.

Thus the \(q_0\)-wall no longer requires a source-robust row, provided sampling can move.

---

# 7. What remains to prove for this route

The D3a route has four local assumptions.

## A. Existential row sampling

Need:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I\text{ with row lower bound}
\]

is sufficient for the downstream contradiction.

If row conversion is point-locked, this route fails.

## B. Polynomial upper bounds

Need

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_M},
\]

and preferably polynomial bounds for the anisotropy factors.

These are standard complexity-style bounds, likely easier than the earlier actual-zeta nonrecurrence inputs.

## C. Boundary layer control

Need

\[
\rho\ll Q^{-C}|I|
\]

after exponent choices. This is achieved by taking \(C_\varepsilon\) sufficiently large, unless \(I\) is too short.

## D. D4 correction control

Need

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\]

at the escaped point.

This is the same D4 local correction theorem.

---

# 8. Resulting downstream chain

With this attack, downstream becomes:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{D1}
+
\text{D2}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

Then:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{D3a wall escape}
+
\text{D4 correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

The old D3 source-robust row theorem becomes a backup:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-robust row needed only if existential sampling fails.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Final attack conclusion

The \(q_0\)-wall can plausibly be resolved without new row algebra.

The key replacement theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling Admissibility}.
}
\]

If downstream row conversion is existential over the packet, then:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\]

forces nearby non-wall samples, and D4 handles them.

So the highest-priority downstream checks are now:

1. verify existential row sampling is admissible;
2. prove the wall-escape lemma with boundary handling;
3. prove polynomial upper bounds for \(G\) and \(u'\);
4. finish D4 correction control.

This is a materially better path than searching indefinitely for a row surviving exactly at \(q_0=0\).

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: formal D3a theorem and proof skeleton

I’ll now turn the wall-escape idea into a self-contained theorem. The aim is to replace the source-robust-row requirement with:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass}+\text{local derivative bounds}
\Rightarrow
\exists \text{ non-wall point where D4 applies.}
}
\]

This would solve the \(q_0\)-wall without finding a row that survives exactly at \(q_0=0\).

---

# 1. Define the Gate 2 density

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q''.
\]

Define

\[
G(m)
=
|u(m)|^2\bigl(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\bigr).
\]

Gate 2 gives

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume the standard local upper bounds

\[
G(m)\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'(m)|\le Q^{C_u'},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G(m)|+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}
\]

on \(I\).

The nondegenerate row-conversion theorem D4 applies at any point satisfying

\[
|q(m)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and

\[
G(m)\ge Q^{-C_G'}
\]

plus correction control.

So we only need to show that Gate 2 mass produces such a point.

---

# 2. Split by the \(q_0\)-wall

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q|\ge \varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then since \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-1}.
\]

At that point,

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge \varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

D4 applies.

Thus assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

We must escape the wall.

---

# 3. Remove low-source wall points

Fix

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Let

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

On this set,

\[
G
=
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\le
\tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) large enough that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|
\le
\frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge \tau\}
\]

still carries polynomial Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G
\ge
\frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

In particular, \(I_{\rm wall,live}\) is nonempty and not confined to a negligible set unless the integrand is too large.

---

# 4. Local wall-strip escape

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

So

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Let

\[
M=Q^{C_u'}
\]

be an upper bound for \(|u'|\). Define

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
Q^{C_u'}Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\le Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

so it suffices that

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_u'+O(1).
\]

Then throughout

\[
[m_0-\rho,m_0+\rho]\cap I
\]

we have

\[
|u|\ge \frac34\tau
\]

as long as the interval remains inside \(I\). Hence \(q''=u\) has constant sign there, and \(q\) is uniformly convex or concave.

A uniformly convex or concave function with

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon
\]

must exit the strip \(|q|<\varepsilon\) within distance

\[
O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})=\rho,
\]

unless blocked by the boundary of \(I\).

Thus for an interior point \(m_0\), there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

---

# 5. Gate 2 remains live at the escaped point

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6\varepsilon-2\varepsilon^3
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4
=
Q^{-C}.
\]

So \(m_1\) satisfies

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is exactly the D4 nondegenerate branch.

---

# 6. Boundary layer control

The only failure mode is that all of \(I_{\rm wall,live}\) lies within distance \(\rho\) of \(\partial I\).

Let

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

the total Gate 2 mass in the boundary layer is at most

\[
2Q^{C_G}\rho.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
2Q^{C_G}\rho
\le
\frac18 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then the boundary layer cannot contain all wall-live Gate 2 mass. Hence an interior \(m_0\) exists and the escape applies.

This introduces the condition

\[
\rho
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\ll Q^{-A-C_G}|I|.
\]

As long as \(|I|\) is not super-polynomially small, this is achievable by increasing \(C_\varepsilon\).

---

# 7. D3a theorem

## Wall-Escape Sampling Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

2. Polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_u'},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

3. The packet length \(|I|\) is at least polynomially large relative to the escape radius.

Then for a suitable polynomial threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

either there exists \(m_\ast\in I\) with

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon,
\]

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

or the Gate 2 mass assumption is contradicted.

Hence there always exists a non-wall point where D4 applies.

---

# 8. Consequence for D3

The original D3 wall input was:

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C}
+
G\text{ live}
\Rightarrow
\exists R_{\rm rob}: |R_{\rm rob}|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The wall-escape theorem replaces this by:

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C}
+
G\text{ live}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\text{ nearby with }|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}
\text{ and }G(m_1)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then D4 handles \(m_1\).

So D3 becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 = Wall-Escape Sampling Admissibility + D4.}
}
\]

No source-robust row is needed unless the proof requires row conversion at an exact predetermined point.

---

# 9. Check row-conversion admissibility

The downstream row-conversion theorem should be stated existentially:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If this is the required output, wall escape is admissible.

If instead the proof demands the row lower bound at a point already fixed by an external construction, then wall escape is not enough.

But because Gate 1 and Gate 2 are interval-energy statements, the natural downstream target is existential. Thus the wall-escape route is likely compatible with the architecture.

---

# 10. Updated downstream dependency

The downstream chain becomes:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{D1}
+
\text{D2}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

Then:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

So D3 can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling}
}
\]

instead of:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row Theorem}.
}
\]

---

# 11. Final verdict

The \(q_0\)-wall is no longer the main structural blocker if existential row sampling is allowed.

The active downstream blockers become:

1. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation;
2. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation;
3. D4: Correction control;
4. verifying existential sampling and polynomial upper bounds for the wall-escape theorem.

The source-robust row search remains a backup, not the primary path.
