_Thought for 16s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: close the \(q_0\)-wall modulo existential row sampling

The wall-escape route can now be stated as a precise replacement for the old D3 source-robust-row input. The key idea is:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
q_0\text{ exits the wall strip nearby.}
\]

At the exit point, \(|q_0|\) is polynomially nonzero, \(u\) is still live, and \(\Gamma_G\) is still live. Then the D4 nondegenerate row-conversion theorem applies. This converts the \(q_0\)-wall from a row-algebra problem into a local sampling theorem. The current downstream framework identifies D1/D2 as Gate 2 propagation inputs and D3/D4 as wall/non-wall row-conversion inputs. 

---

# 1. Define the usable non-wall threshold

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''=q''_{\can}.
\]

Let

\[
G(m):=|u(m)|^2\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right).
\]

Fix a source threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

and choose the non-wall threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

so that

\[
\varepsilon\ll \tau.
\]

Eventually we will require

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1),
\]

where

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}
\]

on the packet.

The wall strip is

\[
W_\varepsilon=\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

The live wall strip is

\[
W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
=
\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon,\ |u(m)|\ge \tau\}.
\]

The whole point is to prove:

\[
W_{\varepsilon,\tau}
\quad\text{escapes to}\quad
\{|q|=\varepsilon,\ |u|\gtrsim\tau,\ |\Gamma_G|\gtrsim\tau\}
\]

within polynomial distance.

---

# 2. First-exit lemma

Assume

\[
m_0\in W_{\varepsilon,\tau}.
\]

Let

\[
M:=\sup_{I}|u'|.
\]

Set

\[
\rho:=C\sqrt{\frac{\varepsilon}{\tau}}.
\]

Assume

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Then for all \(m\) with

\[
|m-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau.
\]

In particular, \(u=q''\) has constant sign on that neighborhood, and \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave there.

A uniformly convex or concave function with

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon
\]

cannot remain in the strip

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for distance larger than \(O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})\). Therefore, unless blocked by the boundary of \(I\), there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

This is the first-exit sample.

---

# 3. Gate 2 signal survives at the exit

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6\varepsilon-2\varepsilon^3
\ge
c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
=
|u(m_1)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2\right)
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

So \(m_1\) satisfies the D4 nondegenerate branch hypotheses:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

This is enough for row conversion, modulo D4 correction control.

---

# 4. Exponent bookkeeping

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
M=Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

Then

\[
\rho=CQ^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

The stability condition

\[
M\rho\le\frac14\tau
\]

becomes

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\le
Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Thus by choosing \(C_\varepsilon\) large enough, the escape threshold remains polynomial and all losses are polynomial.

At the exit point, D4 yields a leading vector of size

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|
\asymp
|q_0(m_1)|\,|u(m_1)|^3
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

Using

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

we get

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|
\ge
c\,\varepsilon\,\tau^4
=
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

So D4 row conversion gives

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\]

provided

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}(m_1)|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}(m_1)|.
\]

---

# 5. Packet-boundary handling

If \(m_0\) lies within distance \(\rho\) of \(\partial I\), the first-exit point might exit the packet.

There are two options.

## Option A: boundary layer is negligible

Let

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho.
\]

If

\[
G\le Q^{C_G}
\]

on \(I\), then the Gate 2 contribution from the boundary layer is at most

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}.
\]

Choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\]

large enough that

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}\ll Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then significant Gate 2 mass cannot be supported entirely near the boundary.

## Option B: one-sided escape

If one side is available, use a one-sided convexity argument. On an interval

\[
[m_0,m_0+2\rho]\subset I,
\]

uniform convexity still forces either exit from the strip or monotone quadratic growth. The same \(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\) scale applies.

Thus boundary issues are not structural.

---

# 6. Integral Gate 2 to escaped non-wall sample

Assume Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume upper bounds

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

Split into non-wall and wall:

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q|\ge \varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then there is a point in \(I_{\rm nd}\) with

\[
G\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

D4 applies directly.

Otherwise wall mass dominates:

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Remove low-source points

\[
\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

On that set,

\[
G\le \tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(\tau\) such that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Then live wall points with

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\]

carry polynomial Gate 2 mass.

Pick a live wall point outside the boundary layer and apply first-exit escape. This gives a non-wall D4 sample.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 integral mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C},
\quad
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 7. D3 is now a sampling theorem

The old D3 was:

\[
\text{find a source-robust row at }q_0=0.
\]

The improved D3 is:

## D3a — Wall-Escape Sampling

Assume Gate 2 mass, polynomial upper bounds, and \(u'\)-control. Then either the non-wall branch already contains a Gate 2 sample, or the wall branch first-exits to a nearby non-wall Gate 2 sample.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a + D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row conversion across the }q_0\text{-wall}.
}
\]

This is cleaner than a raw row search because it uses the known rows \(A_7,A_9\) at a nearby non-wall point.

---

# 8. Remaining check: existential row conversion

The entire attack depends on row conversion being existential:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If the downstream contradiction accepts this, then wall escape solves D3.

If the proof requires the row lower bound at a preassigned point, wall escape is insufficient.

Given Gate 1 and Gate 2 are interval-energy inputs, the natural row-conversion output should be existential. So this assumption is plausible and should be formalized.

---

# 9. New downstream replacement

Replace

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3: Source-Robust Row / }q_0\text{-Wall Resolution}
}
\]

by the more concrete pair:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4: Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control}.
}
\]

Source-robust rows remain only a fallback if existential sampling fails.

---

# 10. Final attack result

The \(q_0\)-wall is no longer the main structural blocker under existential sampling.

The downstream blockers become:

1. D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation;
2. D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation;
3. D4: correction control;
4. a small architectural lemma: row conversion is existential over \(I\).

If those hold, wall escape handles the \(q_0\)-wall.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:27:40)

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: prove the wall-escape branch as a standalone downstream theorem

The \(q_0\)-wall can be handled if row conversion is existential on the packet. I’ll now isolate the exact theorem and the remaining dependencies.

---

# 1. Desired downstream output

The downstream layer should not need a row lower bound at a preassigned point. It should need:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If this is the required output, the wall can be bypassed.

The reason is:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\]

forces \(q_0\) to leave the wall strip nearby. Then the ordinary nondegenerate row theorem applies at the exit point.

---

# 2. The theorem to prove

## Wall-Escape Row-Conversion Theorem

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q''.
\]

Let

\[
G(m)=|u(m)|^2\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right).
\]

Assume on an interval \(I\):

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

2. Polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G(m)\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'(m)|\le Q^{C_{u'}},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m)|+|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

3. D4 correction control at all non-wall points.

4. Row conversion is existential on \(I\).

Then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C_G'},
\]

and hence

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This theorem replaces the source-robust-row wall input.

---

# 3. Proof

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Split

\[
I=I_{\rm nd}\cup I_{\rm wall},
\]

where

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q|\ge\varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then by

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

there is

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

Since

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon,
\]

D4 applies.

So assume wall mass dominates:

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 4. Remove low-\(u\) wall mass

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Let

\[
I_{\rm low}=\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

On \(I_{\rm low}\),

\[
G=|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\le \tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so large that

\[
\tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|
\le \frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then the live wall set

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
\{|q|<\varepsilon,\ |u|\ge\tau\}
\]

carries nontrivial mass:

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G
\ge \frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

So \(I_{\rm wall,live}\) is nonempty and, modulo boundary-layer handling, has an interior point.

---

# 5. First-exit argument

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Let

\[
M=Q^{C_{u'}}
\]

with

\[
|u'|\le M.
\]

Define

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Then on the local interval

\[
[m_0-\rho,m_0+\rho],
\]

provided it is inside \(I\), one has

\[
|u|\ge\frac34\tau.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

the function \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave there.

A uniformly convex or concave function satisfying

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon
\]

cannot remain inside the strip

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for distance more than

\[
O\left(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\right)=O(\rho).
\]

Hence there is a first-exit point

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge\frac12\tau.
\]

---

# 6. Gate 2 signal survives at first exit

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Because

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we have

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4
=
Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

Also,

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 7. Boundary layer

The previous step assumes \(m_0\) is at distance at least \(\rho\) from \(\partial I\).

Let

\[
I_{\rm bd}:=\{m:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

Gate 2 mass in the boundary layer is bounded by

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}
\le
\frac18Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then not all wall-live mass can lie in the boundary layer. So an interior \(m_0\) exists.

This requires

\[
\rho\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}|I|.
\]

If \(I\) has polynomial length, this is achievable by increasing \(C_\varepsilon\).

---

# 8. Exponent choices

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

We need

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
\le Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

We also need

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

which is weaker:

\[
C_\varepsilon>C_\tau.
\]

Boundary negligibility adds

\[
\frac{C_\varepsilon-C_\tau}{2}
\]

large enough relative to \(A+C_G+\log_Q(1/|I|)\).

All are polynomial exponent choices.

---

# 9. Apply D4

At the first-exit point \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

D4 says, under correction control,

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is the downstream row lower bound.

---

# 10. Consequence

The \(q_0\)-wall is resolved if the following are accepted:

1. row conversion is existential on \(I\);

2. local upper bounds for \(G\), \(u'\), and anisotropy hold polynomially;

3. \(I\) has enough interior length for \(\rho\)-scale escape;

4. D4 correction control is proved.

Then D3 no longer needs a source-robust row. It can be replaced by:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling}.
}
\]

---

# 11. Remaining risk

The only serious risk is architectural:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the downstream contradiction allow us to move from }m_0\text{ to }m_1?
}
\]

If the proof demands row conversion at the exact point where Gate 2 mass was first detected, wall escape fails.

But Gate 2 is an integral statement and D4 is pointwise. The natural row-conversion conclusion is existential. Therefore movement inside \(I\) should be admissible.

This is now the key lemma to check in the global proof architecture.

## Agent 4 / D — Wall-Escape Sampling theorem

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: formalize the new D3a theorem

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 wall mass}
\Rightarrow
\text{nearby non-wall D4 sample}.
}
\]

The current downstream update identifies this as the strongest \(q_0\)-wall route: replace the old need for a source-robust row at \(q_0=0\) by first-exit sampling plus D4, provided row conversion is existential on the packet interval. 

---

# 1. Definitions

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q''.
\]

Define the Gate 2 density

\[
G(m)
=
|u(m)|^2\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right).
\]

Gate 2 gives

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

be the non-wall threshold and split

\[
I_{\rm nd}
=
\{m\in I: |q(m)|\ge\varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}
=
\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

D4 applies on \(I_{\rm nd}\), provided \(G\) is pointwise polynomially non-small and correction control holds.

---

# 2. Non-wall mass case

Assume

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

If

\[
G(m)\le Q^{C_G}
\]

on \(I\), then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

such that

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

At that point,

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

So \(m_\ast\) satisfies the non-wall branch input for D4:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Therefore D4 gives

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

assuming correction control.

So the only remaining case is wall-dominated Gate 2 mass.

---

# 3. Wall mass case and low-source removal

Assume

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Split

\[
I_{\rm wall}
=
I_{\rm wall,live}\cup I_{\rm wall,low},
\]

where

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
\{|q|<\varepsilon,\ |u|\ge\tau\},
\]

and

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}
=
\{|q|<\varepsilon,\ |u|<\tau\}.
\]

Assume the anisotropy upper bound

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then on \(I_{\rm wall,low}\),

\[
G
\le
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) large enough that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|
\le
\frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Thus \(I_{\rm wall,live}\) is nonempty and carries polynomial Gate 2 mass.

---

# 4. First-exit escape from the wall strip

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Thus

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Assume

\[
|u'(m)|\le Q^{C_{u'}}
\]

on \(I\).

Set

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so that

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Equivalently, since

\[
\rho=CQ^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2},
\]

it suffices that

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Then on

\[
[m_0-\rho,m_0+\rho]\cap I
\]

we have

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau
\]

as long as this local interval stays inside \(I\). Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

the function \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave there.

A uniformly convex or concave function with

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon
\]

cannot remain inside

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for distance \(\gg\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\). Hence, for an interior point \(m_0\), there exists a first-exit point

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

---

# 5. Gate 2 signal at the exit point

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we have

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q(m_1)|-2|q(m_1)|^3
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

D4 applies at \(m_1\), assuming correction control.

---

# 6. Boundary-layer handling

The first-exit argument requires \(m_0\) to be at least \(\rho\) away from \(\partial I\).

Define the boundary layer

\[
I_{\rm bd}
=
\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le2\rho.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

the boundary contribution satisfies

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G(m)\,dm
\le
2\rho Q^{C_G}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}
\le
\frac18Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then \(I_{\rm bd}\) cannot contain all wall-live Gate 2 mass. Hence an interior wall-live point exists.

This requires

\[
\rho\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}|I|.
\]

If the packet interval \(I\) has polynomial length, this is achieved by increasing \(C_\varepsilon\). If \(I\) is too short, one must either use one-sided escape or include a packet-shrinking/recentering lemma.

---

# 7. Wall-Escape Sampling theorem

## Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

2. Polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}},
\]

\[
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

3. The packet has enough interior length relative to

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Then for suitable polynomial thresholds

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Consequently, if D4 correction control holds at non-wall points, then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

---

# 8. What this proves about D3

The old D3 was:

\[
\text{Find a source-robust row surviving at }q_0=0.
\]

The wall-escape theorem replaces it by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling + D4}.
}
\]

Thus source-robust row search becomes a fallback only if the downstream proof requires row conversion at an exact preassigned point.

If row conversion is existential on \(I\), then the \(q_0\)-wall is resolved by first-exit sampling.

---

# 9. Remaining assumptions to verify

The theorem still requires four items.

## A. Existential row conversion

The downstream contradiction must accept:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is natural because Gate 1 and Gate 2 are interval-energy statements.

## B. Polynomial upper bounds

Need

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

These are local analytic complexity bounds.

## C. Boundary control

Need

\[
\rho\ll Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

This follows by exponent choice if \(I\) is not too short.

## D. D4 correction control

Need

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|
\]

at the escaped point.

---

# 10. Final conclusion

The \(q_0\)-wall is no longer a fundamental row-algebra blocker under existential sampling.

The downstream chain can be revised to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

This is a significant simplification: D3 can be replaced by a local analytic sampling theorem rather than an unknown source-robust row, provided the final contradiction layer only needs a row lower bound somewhere inside the packet interval.

## Agent 4 / D — Wall-Escape Sampling as D3a

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: formalize

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 wall mass}
\Rightarrow
\text{nearby non-wall D4 sample}.
}
\]

The latest downstream update identifies this as the most concrete replacement for the old D3 \(q_0\)-wall row search, provided row conversion is existential on the packet interval. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q''.
\]

Define

\[
G(m)
=
|u(m)|^2\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right).
\]

Assume Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Let

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\qquad
|\Gamma|=(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

Assume polynomial upper bounds

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}
\]

or equivalently after normalizing \(I\) to unit scale,

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

---

# 2. Split into non-wall and wall regions

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{m\in I:|q(m)|\ge \varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{m\in I:|q(m)|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac12 Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then since \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

such that

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

At this point,

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon.
\]

So \(m_\ast\) is already a non-wall D4 sample.

Thus the only hard case is

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 3. Remove low-source wall points

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

On \(I_{\rm wall,low}\),

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2
\le
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so large that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|
\le
\frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

In particular, \(I_{\rm wall,live}\) is nonempty after boundary-layer removal.

---

# 4. First-exit lemma

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Then

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau.
\]

Let

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Assume

\[
|u'|\le M,
\qquad
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Then on the local interval

\[
[m_0-\rho,m_0+\rho]
\]

inside \(I\),

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

the function \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave on this local interval.

A uniformly convex or uniformly concave function cannot remain inside

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for distance \(\gg\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\). More explicitly, every connected component of

\[
\{|q|<\varepsilon\}
\]

inside a region where \(|q''|\ge 3\tau/4\) has length

\[
\le C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Therefore, provided \(m_0\) is not trapped at the boundary, there exists a first-exit point

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

---

# 5. Exponent condition for first exit

Write

\[
M=Q^{C_{u'}}
\]

on normalized scale.

Since

\[
\rho=CQ^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2},
\]

the stability condition

\[
M\rho\le\frac14\tau
\]

is

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\le
Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Also require

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

which is weaker:

\[
C_\varepsilon>C_\tau+O(1).
\]

So the first-exit scale can be chosen with only polynomial losses.

---

# 6. Gate 2 signal at the exit point

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Using

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q(m_1)|-2|q(m_1)|^3
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
=
|u(m_1)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_1)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_1)^2\right)
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2\Gamma_G(m_1)^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall point satisfying

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

This is a D4 sample.

---

# 7. Boundary-layer handling

The first-exit argument can fail only if \(m_0\) lies within \(\rho\) of the boundary of \(I\).

Define

\[
I_{\rm bd}
=
\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G(m)\,dm
\le
2\rho Q^{C_G}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so large that

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}
\le
\frac18Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\rho\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}|I|.
\]

Then boundary layers cannot carry all wall-live Gate 2 mass, so an interior \(m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}\) exists.

If \(I\) is too short for this, use one-sided escape or shrink/recenter the packet. The theorem should include a mild interval-length hypothesis:

\[
|I|\ge Q^{-C_I}\rho
\]

for an appropriate polynomial exponent.

---

# 8. Conclusion: Wall-Escape Sampling theorem

## D3a — Wall-Escape Sampling

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}};
\]

3. packet interior size is large enough relative to

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau};
\]

4. thresholds satisfy

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m_\ast)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)^2\right)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Consequently, D4 applies at \(m_\ast\), assuming correction control.

---

# 9. D4 application

At \(m_\ast\),

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

D4 uses the matrix normal form

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and correction control

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 10. Final conditional statement

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 matrix row conversion}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

This means the original D3 source-robust row theorem is no longer necessary if:

\[
\boxed{
\text{row conversion is existential somewhere in }I.
}
\]

If the downstream proof demands row lower bound at a fixed preassigned point, then wall escape is insufficient and one must return to the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil / source-robust row route.

But for an interval-energy downstream contradiction, existential row sampling is the natural formulation. So this is now the preferred D3 resolution.

## Agent 4 / D — Existential row-sampling admissibility

Executing Agent 4’s assigned task: determine whether Wall-Escape Sampling is admissible in the downstream contradiction layer. The latest downstream architecture is:

\[
\text{Gate 1}+\text{G2-A}+\text{G2-B}\Rightarrow \text{Gate 2},
\]

then

\[
\text{Gate 2}+\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}+\text{D4 matrix row conversion}\Rightarrow \text{row lower bound},
\]

provided row conversion may sample somewhere in the packet interval. 

---

# 1. The row-output should be existential or energetic

The natural downstream output after Gate 2 is not:

\[
\text{a row lower bound at a preassigned point }m_0.
\]

Gate 2 itself is an interval-energy statement:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

D4 is pointwise:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\quad
|u(m_\ast)|^2|\Gamma(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus the natural bridge is existential:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

or, even better, energetic:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I |\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Therefore Wall-Escape Sampling is admissible if the final downstream contradiction accepts either an existential row sample or row-energy lower bound on the packet.

This is the expected architecture: interval source mass \(\to\) interval anisotropy mass \(\to\) existence of a row-large sample \(\to\) row-energy thickening.

---

# 2. Wall escape is compatible with existential sampling

Wall escape produces a point

\[
m_1\in I
\]

near a wall-live point \(m_0\) such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This exactly satisfies the D4 pointwise hypotheses at \(m_1\). D4 then gives

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

So if the downstream layer only needs

\[
\exists m\in I
\]

with row lower bound, wall escape is fully admissible.

---

# 3. Row mobility upgrades existential pointwise to energy

If the final contradiction requires row energy rather than a single point, we need a mobility lemma.

Let

\[
\mathbf A(m)=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Assume

\[
|\mathbf A(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Assume a derivative bound

\[
|\mathbf A'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}
\]

on \(I\).

Then for

\[
|m-m_\ast|
\le
cQ^{-C_A-C_D}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|\mathbf A(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Thus there exists a subinterval

\[
J_\ast\subset I
\]

with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]

such that

\[
|\mathbf A(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\quad\text{on }J_\ast.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
\int_{J_\ast}|\mathbf A(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

So existential row lower bound implies row-energy lower bound under polynomial derivative control.

This makes wall escape admissible even if the final contradiction uses row-energy.

---

# 4. Weighted packet norms

If the row norm is weighted by a smooth packet weight \(w_I(m)\), we require \(m_\ast\) not to lie in a negligible boundary region where \(w_I\) is too small.

Wall escape already needs boundary-layer removal. We can choose \(m_\ast\) in the interior support where

\[
w_I(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If \(w_I\) is Lipschitz or smooth at packet scale, then on the thickened interval \(J_\ast\),

\[
w_I(m)\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

after possibly shrinking \(J_\ast\). Hence

\[
\int_I w_I(m)|\mathbf A(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C''}|I|.
\]

So weighted packet norms do not obstruct row mobility, assuming the Gate 2 mass selection avoids the negligible weight boundary.

---

# 5. Exact-point-only architecture would break wall escape

If the final contradiction somehow requires

\[
|\mathbf A(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

at the exact same point \(m_0\) selected before wall escape, then the wall-escape route fails.

At \(m_0\), one may have

\[
q_0(m_0)=0,
\]

so

\[
H(m_0)=0
\]

and the known rows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

may vanish. In that exact-point architecture, one would need one of:

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

or the saturated/blow-up rows

\[
A_7/q_0,\quad A_9/q_0,
\]

or a \(q_0\)-wall exclusion theorem.

But this exact-point requirement is unnatural for an energy-based proof. Since Gate 1 and Gate 2 are interval statements, the downstream row output should be existential or energetic.

---

# 6. Final admissibility theorem

## Row-Sampling Admissibility Theorem

Assume the downstream contradiction layer accepts either:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

or

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

Assume polynomial derivative control

\[
|\mathbf A'_{\rm row}(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then Wall-Escape Sampling is admissible: if Gate 2 mass produces a wall-live point, the first-exit non-wall point \(m_1\) may be used for D4, and the resulting row lower bound is valid for the downstream contradiction layer.

If an energy output is needed, row mobility thickens the pointwise row lower bound into a polynomial row-energy lower bound.

---

# 7. Remaining requirements

Wall escape plus D4 now requires only:

1. Gate 2 mass;

2. polynomial upper bounds for

\[
G,\quad |u'|,\quad |\Gamma|;
\]

3. boundary-layer control / interior selection;

4. D4 matrix normal form and correction control;

5. row mobility derivative bound

\[
|\mathbf A'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1};
\]

6. the architecture accepts existential or energetic row output.

These are local analytic/canonical estimates, not new actual-zeta arithmetic inputs.

---

# 8. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling is admissible if downstream row conversion is existential or energetic.}
}
\]

Under that formulation, the \(q_0\)-wall is no longer a fundamental structural blocker. It reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling + D4 matrix row conversion + row mobility.}
}
\]

The \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil / source-robust row route remains only a fallback if the final architecture is exact-point locked.

## Attack on the remaining wall-escape + D4 requirements

I will target the six residual requirements from the wall-escape route: polynomial upper bounds, boundary-layer control, D4 matrix/correction control, row mobility, and existential/energy admissibility. The current framework is the downstream package where Gate 2 plus Wall-Escape Sampling plus D4 should imply the row lower bound. 

---

# 0. Notation

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

and

\[
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

The D4 row vector is

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The desired matrix form is

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q\,u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R.
\]

The wall-escape route needs:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{local complexity}
+
\text{Wall Escape}
+
\text{D4}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast\in I:\ |\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 1. Requirement: polynomial upper bounds for \(G,u',\Gamma\)

This can be reduced to a canonical finite-derivative package.

Assume on a slightly thickened packet \(I^\ast\),

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le j\le 5} |\partial_m^j q(m)|\le Q^{C_{\rm der}}|I|^{-j}.
}
\]

Equivalently, in normalized packet coordinate \(t=(m-m_c)/|I|\),

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le j\le 5} |\partial_t^j q|\le Q^{C_{\rm der}}.
}
\]

Then:

\[
u=q'',
\qquad
u'=q''',
\]

so

\[
|u|\le Q^{C_{\rm der}}|I|^{-2},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{\rm der}}|I|^{-3}.
\]

In normalized coordinates this is simply

\[
|u|\le Q^{C_{\rm der}},
\qquad
|\dot u|\le Q^{C_{\rm der}}.
\]

Next,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Thus

\[
|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{C}.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Since \(\Gamma_G''\) uses \(q\) through \(q^{(4)}\), the \(j\le 4\) package already controls \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). To control \(\Gamma_{G,2}'\), one needs \(q^{(5)}\).

Hence \(j\le5\) suffices for:

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
\]

in physical coordinates.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{j\le5}|\partial_t^j q|\le Q^C
\Rightarrow
G\le Q^C,\quad |u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},\quad |\Gamma|\le Q^C.
}
\]

This handles the polynomial upper bounds required for wall escape.

---

# 2. Requirement: boundary-layer control

Wall escape used the radius

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Let

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Then

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

The boundary layer is

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho |I|\}
\]

in normalized units, or length

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho |I|.
\]

If

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G
\le
2Q^{C_G}\rho |I|.
\]

To make this negligible compared with Gate 2 mass

\[
Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

it suffices to impose

\[
2Q^{C_G}\rho\le \frac18Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\rho\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

That is,

\[
\frac{C_\varepsilon-C_\tau}{2}
\ge
A+C_G+O(1).
\]

So choose

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
}
\]

This is compatible with the wall-escape stability condition

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Thus set

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
}
\]

Then boundary layers cannot carry all Gate 2 mass.

---

# 3. Requirement: D4 matrix normal form and correction control

The known row expansions are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

with

\[
H=-\frac{q\,u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Substitute \(H\):

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q\,u^3\Gamma_G
+
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G
+
\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q\,u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
+
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\mathcal R_9.
\]

So

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q\,u^3L_0\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

where

\[
L_0
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf R
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7\\
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

A clean sufficient condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|c_7|,|c_9|\ge Q^{-C_c}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_0)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Correction control is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_0)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

It is enough to prove the two bounds

\[
|\mathcal R_H|
\le
\frac{1}{8\max(|c_7|,|c_9|)}
|q|\,|u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_0),
\]

and

\[
\left(|\mathcal R_7|^2+|\mathcal R_9|^2\right)^{1/2}
\le
\frac14 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_0)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf R|\le \frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_0)|\Gamma|.
\]

Under these assumptions,

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_0)|\Gamma|.
\]

If D4 pointwise mass gives

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

then

\[
|u|\,|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Thus

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_0)|q||u|^2
\cdot
\left(|u||\Gamma|\right).
\]

If additionally

\[
|q|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-2C_u-A_2/2-C_L-O(1)}.
\]

So D4 is reduced to finite row-expansion verification:

\[
\boxed{
c_7,c_9\ne0,\quad
\mathcal R_H,\mathcal R_7,\mathcal R_9
\text{ are half-leading.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Requirement: row mobility derivative bound

We need to turn an existential sample

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]

into row energy if required.

Assume

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then for

\[
|m-m_\ast|
\le
\frac12 Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m)|
\ge
\frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Thus there is a subinterval \(J_\ast\) with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m)|\ge\frac12Q^{-C_A}
\quad (m\in J_\ast).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|^2
\ge
Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

So existential pointwise lower bound implies row-energy lower bound.

Now verify the derivative bound.

From

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q\,u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

differentiate:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}'
=
q'u^3L\Gamma
+
3qu^2u'L\Gamma
+
qu^3L'\Gamma
+
qu^3L\Gamma'
+
\mathbf R'.
\]

So it suffices to assume polynomial bounds for

\[
q,\ q',\ u,\ u',\ \Gamma,\ \Gamma',\ L,\ L',\ \mathbf R'.
\]

These follow from the canonical derivative package if the row coefficients and projections are canonical with polynomial complexity.

Thus row mobility is a local analytic estimate, not a new arithmetic input.

---

# 5. Requirement: existential sampling admissibility

The final downstream theorem should be stated in row-energy form:

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Then existential sampling is automatically admissible via row mobility.

The wall-escape route produces

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Row mobility upgrades it to row energy.

Therefore the downstream contradiction should avoid exact-point formulations and use interval row energy.

This resolves the architectural concern.

---

# 6. Requirement: wall escape plus D4 as a complete theorem

We can now state the complete theorem.

## Wall-Escape + D4 Row Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

2. Polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

3. D4 matrix normal form:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q\,u^3L_0\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_0)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R|\le\frac12|q||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_0)|\Gamma|.
\]

4. Row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Proof:

- If Gate 2 mass occurs off wall, D4 gives a pointwise row lower bound.
- If Gate 2 mass occurs on wall, first-exit sampling produces a nearby off-wall point with \(G\ge Q^{-C}\).
- D4 gives a pointwise row lower bound there.
- Row mobility thickens to row energy.

This closes the \(q_0\)-wall under local correction/complexity estimates.

---

# 7. Updated status

The \(q_0\)-wall no longer needs a source-robust row **if** the following are proved:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 matrix normal form + half-leading correction control;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{polynomial upper bounds for }G,\Gamma,u',\mathbf A_{\rm row}';
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{downstream row output formulated as row energy or existential sampling.}
}
\]

These are local/canonical verification tasks. They are much more concrete than the previous D3 black-box.

So the main remaining downstream hard proof is now Gate 2 integral rigidity, plus finite row-expansion bookkeeping for D4.

_Thought for 14s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: make D4 correction control finite and checkable

The wall-escape route reduces the \(q_0\)-wall to the non-wall row-conversion theorem D4. So the next useful attack is to make D4 a **finite verification problem** with explicit inequalities.

We want to prove:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

where

\[
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and then show

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

If this holds, then D4 is closed.

---

# 1. Start from the known expansions

We have

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

and

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Substitute \(H\):

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G
+
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G
+
\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
+
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\mathcal R_9.
\]

Thus

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L_0\Gamma+\mathbf R_0,
\]

where

\[
L_0
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf R_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7\\
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If

\[
|c_7|,\ |c_9|\ge Q^{-C_c},
\]

then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_0)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

So the entire D4 theorem reduces to controlling \(\mathbf R_0\).

---

# 2. Split correction terms into absorbable and dangerous pieces

Write

\[
\mathcal R_H=q_0u^3\rho_H+\mathcal E_H,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_7=q_0u^3(a_{77}\Gamma_G+a_{79}\Gamma_{G,2})+\mathcal E_7,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_9=q_0u^3(a_{97}\Gamma_G+a_{99}\Gamma_{G,2})+\mathcal E_9.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

where

\[
L
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}
+
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\rho_H+a_{77}&a_{79}\\
a_{97}&c_9\rho_H+a_{99}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf E=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\mathcal E_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal E_7\\
c_9\mathcal E_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal E_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

This is the cleanest finite form.

The D4 proof requires two checks:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

---

# 3. Matrix nondegeneracy condition

Let

\[
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Let

\[
\Delta L=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\rho_H+a_{77}&a_{79}\\
a_{97}&c_9\rho_H+a_{99}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

A sufficient condition is

\[
\|\Delta L\|
\le
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead}).
\]

Then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)
\ge
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead})
\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

So a finite D4 audit only needs to verify:

\[
|c_7|,\ |c_9|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
|\rho_H|+|a_{77}|+|a_{79}|+|a_{97}|+|a_{99}|
\le Q^{-C'}
\]

with \(C'\) large enough relative to the leading constants.

If \(\Delta L\) is not perturbative, D4 can still hold if

\[
\det L\neq0
\]

and

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

but then this becomes a finite matrix nonvanishing theorem rather than a perturbation estimate.

---

# 4. Error-control condition

The error vector is

\[
\mathbf E=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\mathcal E_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal E_7\\
c_9\mathcal E_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal E_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

A sufficient scalar condition is

\[
|\mathcal E_H|
\le
\frac{1}{8\max(|c_7|,|c_9|)}
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L),
\]

and

\[
\left(|\mathcal E_7|^2+|\mathcal E_9|^2\right)^{1/2}
\le
\frac14
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

So D4 correction control is finite:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E_H,\mathcal E_7,\mathcal E_9
\text{ must be half-leading relative to }
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|.
}
\]

---

# 5. D4 row lower bound

Assume

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

From

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|,
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
\frac12 Q^{-C_q}Q^{-C_L}|u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

Since

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A_2/2},
\]

this becomes

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-A_2/2}|u|^2.
\]

If

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-A_2/2-2C_u}.
\]

Alternatively, if

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

then

\[
|u|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}Q^{-2C_\Gamma},
\]

so

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-3A_2/2-2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Thus D4 proves a polynomial row lower bound.

---

# 6. Finite D4 verification checklist

D4 is proved once the following finite items are checked.

## D4.1 Leading constants

\[
c_7\neq0,\qquad c_9\neq0,
\]

quantitatively:

\[
|c_7|,\ |c_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

## D4.2 \(H\)-expansion

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+q_0u^3\rho_H+\mathcal E_H.
\]

Check either:

\[
|\rho_H|\le Q^{-C}
\]

or absorb \(\rho_H\) into the matrix \(L\) and prove \(\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}\).

Check:

\[
|\mathcal E_H|
\le
c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L).
\]

## D4.3 Row correction expansions

\[
\mathcal R_7=q_0u^3(a_{77}\Gamma_G+a_{79}\Gamma_{G,2})+\mathcal E_7,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_9=q_0u^3(a_{97}\Gamma_G+a_{99}\Gamma_{G,2})+\mathcal E_9.
\]

Either absorb \(a_{ij}\) into \(L\) and prove

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

or prove \(a_{ij}\) are perturbative.

Then check

\[
\sqrt{|\mathcal E_7|^2+|\mathcal E_9|^2}
\le
c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

## D4.4 Canonical errors

All \(E_2\), tail, projection, gauge, row-normalization, and lower-order errors must be included in

\[
\mathcal E_H,\mathcal E_7,\mathcal E_9.
\]

The audit should verify these errors are half-leading at the D4 sample.

---

# 7. Interaction with wall escape

Wall escape gives the D4 sample \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2=Q^{-C_\tau}/2,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

so

\[
|\Gamma(m_1)|\ge cQ^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Therefore the leading row size at the escaped point is at least

\[
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|
\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

So the correction terms only need to be controlled relative to this polynomial quantity. That is feasible if all canonical errors are sufficiently high-order.

---

# 8. Row mobility requirement

After D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

row-energy follows if

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Differentiate

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R.
\]

A polynomial derivative bound follows from bounds on:

\[
q_0,\ q_0',\ u,\ u',\ L,\ L',\ \Gamma,\ \Gamma',\ \mathbf R'.
\]

All are local canonical derivative/projection bounds. This is another finite verification.

Then

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|^2
\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

---

# 9. Attack conclusion

The wall branch is reduced to a concrete finite/local package:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall Escape gives a non-wall D4 sample.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 proves row lower bound at that sample if }L\text{ is nondegenerate and errors are half-leading.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Row mobility thickens pointwise row lower bound to row energy.}
}
\]

So the remaining proof work is not conceptual; it is finite bookkeeping:

1. compute \(c_7,c_9\);

2. compute or bound \(\rho_H,a_{ij}\);

3. show \(L\) has polynomial singular value lower bound;

4. bound \(\mathcal E_H,\mathcal E_7,\mathcal E_9\);

5. prove derivative bounds for row mobility.

This is now the cleanest D4 attack surface.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:56:47)

_Thought for 15s_

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: eliminate D4 correction control as a black box

The next weak link is D4 correction control. The current downstream path is:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 matrix row conversion}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

The remaining D4 task is to show the row vector has the stable form

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

I will now attack this by turning D4 into a **finite coefficient-normal-form check**, rather than leaving it as a vague correction-control input. The current downstream update already identifies D4 matrix row conversion and correction control as one of the remaining local tasks. 

---

# 1. Normalize the row expansion

Start with

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\mathcal R_H.
\]

Write

\[
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathbf A=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf A
=
q_0u^3L_0\Gamma+\mathbf R_0,
\]

where

\[
L_0
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf R_0
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\mathcal R_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7\\
c_9\mathcal R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The D4 problem is now finite:

\[
\boxed{
\text{separate the part of }\mathbf R_0\text{ linear in }\Gamma
\text{ from the truly smaller remainder.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Absorb same-scale corrections into \(L\)

Do **not** try to prove every correction is tiny. Some corrections may be same-scale but structurally linear in \(\Gamma\). Those should be absorbed into the matrix \(L\).

Write

\[
\mathcal R_H
=
q_0u^3\rho_H+\mathcal E_H,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_7
=
q_0u^3(a_{77}\Gamma_G+a_{79}\Gamma_{G,2})+\mathcal E_7,
\]

\[
\mathcal R_9
=
q_0u^3(a_{97}\Gamma_G+a_{99}\Gamma_{G,2})+\mathcal E_9.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf A
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

where

\[
L=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}
+
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\rho_H+a_{77}&a_{79}\\
a_{97}&c_9\rho_H+a_{99}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

and

\[
\mathbf E
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\mathcal E_H\Gamma_G+\mathcal E_7\\
c_9\mathcal E_H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal E_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Now the correction-control theorem is clean:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

This avoids over-demanding that all lower terms be small; only the non-linear or non-absorbed remainder must be small.

---

# 3. Matrix nondegeneracy has two possible proofs

## Route A — perturbative matrix proof

If

\[
|c_7|,\ |c_9|\ge Q^{-C_c}
\]

and

\[
\left\|
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\rho_H+a_{77}&a_{79}\\
a_{97}&c_9\rho_H+a_{99}
\end{pmatrix}
\right\|
\le
\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_0),
\]

then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge\frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_0)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is the easiest proof if the corrections are genuinely lower order.

## Route B — finite determinant proof

If the correction matrix is not perturbative, prove directly that

\[
\det L\ne0
\]

with a polynomial lower bound:

\[
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\|L\|\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)
\ge
\frac{|\det L|}{\|L\|}
\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

This is important: D4 does **not** require the leading diagonal matrix alone to dominate. It only requires the total \(2\times2\) matrix \(L\) to be nondegenerate.

Thus the D4 matrix audit should not stop if \(a_{ij}\) are not tiny. It should compute \(L\) and check \(\det L\).

---

# 4. Error terms must be measured relative to the escaped sample

At the wall-escape sample \(m_1\), we have

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|
\ge
C^{-1}\varepsilon\tau^4.
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

the leading scale is

\[
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

So the true error requirement at escaped samples is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf E(m_1)|
\le
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1)}.
}
\]

This is a concrete target. It may be easier than a uniform symbolic inequality everywhere.

Thus D4 can be localized:

## Escaped-sample D4 correction theorem

At every wall-escape sample \(m_1\),

\[
|\mathbf E(m_1)|
\le
\frac12|q_0(m_1)||u(m_1)|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma(m_1)|.
\]

This theorem only needs to hold on the D4 sampling set, not globally.

---

# 5. Canonical errors can be sorted by homogeneity

The finite audit should classify every term in \(\mathbf E\) by its homogeneity in

\[
q_0,\quad u,\quad \Gamma.
\]

Terms of the form

\[
q_0u^3(\text{linear in }\Gamma)
\]

belong in \(L\), not in \(\mathbf E\).

Terms of the form

\[
q_0u^3(\text{quadratic or higher in small variables})
\]

may be perturbative.

Terms missing a factor \(q_0u^3\) are dangerous unless they are canceled or belong to a wall-live source-robust row.

Therefore the audit table should be:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{term} & \text{homogeneity} & \text{action}\\
\hline
q_0u^3\Gamma_G & \text{leading linear} & \text{put in }L\\
q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2} & \text{leading linear} & \text{put in }L\\
q_0u^3\cdot Q^{-C}\Gamma & \text{small linear} & \text{put in }L\text{ or }\mathbf E\\
q_0u^3\Gamma^2 & \text{higher anisotropy} & \text{error if }\Gamma\text{ bounded}\\
q_0^2u^a\Gamma & \text{extra wall factor} & \text{error at escaped sample if }q_0\ll1\\
E_2\text{ / tail} & \text{canonical error} & \text{must be }<\text{ half-leading}\\
\text{term without }q_0 & \text{wall-live correction} & \text{D3 source-robust candidate}
\end{array}
\]

This gives a mechanical way to finish D4.

---

# 6. A potential hidden danger: corrections without \(q_0\)

If \(\mathcal R_7\) or \(\mathcal R_9\) contains a term not divisible by \(q_0\), then it is **not** a D4 error. It is either:

1. a wall-live correction row that solves D3 directly; or

2. a dangerous term that may cancel the leading row off-wall.

So all terms not divisible by \(q_0\) should be separated:

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm wall}
=
\mathbf R\bmod(q_0).
\]

If

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm wall}\ne0,
\]

then the row architecture contains source-robust wall information.

If

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm wall}=0,
\]

then all corrections are at least \(q_0\)-divisible and can potentially be absorbed into the D4 matrix/error package.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{First check }\mathbf R\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

This either improves D3 or simplifies D4.

---

# 7. Row mobility derivative bound

We also need

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
\]

for existential-to-energy thickening.

Using

\[
\mathbf A=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

differentiate:

\[
\mathbf A'
=
q_0'u^3L\Gamma
+
3q_0u^2u'L\Gamma
+
q_0u^3L'\Gamma
+
q_0u^3L\Gamma'
+
\mathbf E'.
\]

Thus it suffices to have polynomial bounds for

\[
q_0',\ u,\ u',\ L,\ L',\ \Gamma,\ \Gamma',\ \mathbf E'.
\]

All are finite local derivative/projection estimates.

So row mobility is not conceptually hard; it is part of the same finite canonical derivative package used for Gate 2 extraction and wall escape.

---

# 8. Current best finite theorem

## D4 Matrix-Correction Theorem

Assume on the D4 sampling set:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf E|\le\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|,
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then any point satisfying

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}
\]

yields

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

This theorem combines D4 pointwise row conversion and row mobility.

---

# 9. What remains genuinely open in D4

D4 is no longer conceptually vague. It has four finite checks:

1. compute the \(2\times2\) matrix \(L\);

2. prove

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C};
\]

3. prove

\[
|\mathbf E|\le \frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|;
\]

4. prove

\[
|\mathbf A'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Everything else follows.

---

# 10. Attack conclusion

The downstream wall/row conversion problem has been reduced to two local proof packages:

## Package 1 — Gate 2

\[
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

## Package 2 — Row conversion

\[
\text{Wall escape}
+
\text{D4 matrix-correction theorem}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

The remaining D4 work is finite row algebra and canonical error bookkeeping.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 10:59:06)

_Thought for 15s_

## Continuing attack — D4 as a finite weighted-normal-form theorem

The next useful move is to make D4 checkable by a **weighted row-expansion audit**. The point is to stop treating “correction control” as qualitative, and instead classify every row term by whether it is:

1. part of the leading matrix \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\);
2. absorbable into \(L\);
3. perturbative at the wall-escape / non-wall D4 sample;
4. wall-live, hence a D3 bonus;
5. genuinely dangerous.

The current downstream route is already narrowed to: Gate 2, Wall-Escape Sampling, D4 matrix row conversion, and row mobility. 

---

# 1. D4 sample scale

At a D4 sample \(m_\ast\), either obtained directly from non-wall Gate 2 mass or by wall escape, we have

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge \varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge \tau,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma(m_\ast)|\ge \tau_\Gamma,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

For wall escape, one can take

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
\tau_\Gamma\asymp \tau,
\]

because at the first-exit point

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c\tau.
\]

The D4 leading row scale is

\[
S_{\rm lead}
:=
|q_0|\,|u|^3\,|\Gamma|.
\]

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
S_{\rm lead}
\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

So every correction term only needs to be smaller than this polynomial scale.

---

# 2. Weighted normal form for row terms

Let a row term have schematic form

\[
T
=
q_0^{a}u^{b}\,\Gamma^\ell\,D,
\]

where \(\Gamma^\ell\) means a term linear, quadratic, etc. in \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\), and \(D\) denotes bounded derivative/gauge/canonical factors.

Assume

\[
|D|\le Q^{C_D}.
\]

Compare \(T\) to the leading scale

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma.
\]

The ratio is

\[
\frac{|T|}{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
\le
Q^{C_D}
|q_0|^{a-1}|u|^{b-3}|\Gamma|^{\ell-1}.
\]

This gives a mechanical classification.

---

# 3. Terms that belong in \(L\)

Terms of exact leading type

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\qquad
q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

belong in the matrix \(L\), not in the error.

More generally, any term of form

\[
q_0u^3
\begin{pmatrix}
a_{77}\Gamma_G+a_{79}\Gamma_{G,2}\\
a_{97}\Gamma_G+a_{99}\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
\]

should be absorbed into \(L\).

So the row vector should be normalized as

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

not as

\[
q_0u^3L_{\rm lead}\Gamma+\text{all lower terms}.
\]

This matters: same-scale off-diagonal terms \(a_{79}\Gamma_{G,2}\) and \(a_{97}\Gamma_G\) are not errors. They only threaten D4 if they make \(L\) singular.

Thus the first D4 audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{extract every term linear in }\Gamma\text{ and exactly divisible by }q_0u^3.
}
\]

Then prove

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Terms that are automatically perturbative

At the D4 sample, a term is automatically perturbative if it has an **extra small factor** compared with \(q_0u^3\Gamma\).

Examples:

## Extra \(q_0\)

\[
T=q_0^2u^3\Gamma.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{|T|}{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
\le
Q^C|q_0|
\le
Q^{C-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) large enough, and this is \(<1/100\).

## Extra anisotropy

\[
T=q_0u^3\Gamma^2.
\]

Then

\[
\frac{|T|}{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
\le
Q^C|\Gamma|.
\]

This is perturbative only if \(|\Gamma|\) is small. At a wall-escape sample \(|\Gamma|\ge\tau\), but it may also be polynomially large. So quadratic anisotropy terms are not automatically small unless there is an anisotropy upper bound sharper than \(Q^C\). Such terms should either be absorbed into a nonlinear row theorem or explicitly bounded.

## Extra positive power of \(u\)

\[
T=q_0u^4\Gamma.
\]

The ratio is

\[
Q^C|u|.
\]

This is not automatically small unless \(|u|\ll1\). If \(u\) is merely polynomially bounded, \(q_0u^4\Gamma\) is same-order or larger. Such terms should not be thrown into the error. They must be included in the leading coefficient matrix if they are linear in \(\Gamma\), with \(u\)-dependent entries:

\[
L=L(q,u,q',\ldots).
\]

Then the condition is still

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Therefore \(L\) should be allowed to depend polynomially on controlled local variables, not just constants.

---

# 5. Better D4 normal form: variable matrix \(L(Y)\)

Let

\[
Y=(q_0,u,q_0',u',\ldots)
\]

denote bounded local variables.

The correct normal form is

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E.
}
\]

Here \(L(Y)\) contains every term that is:

- divisible by \(q_0u^3\);
- linear in \(\Gamma\);
- not demonstrably perturbative.

Then D4 requires

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L(Y))\ge Q^{-C_L}
}
\]

on the D4 sampling set.

This is more flexible and safer than trying to prove all corrections are lower-order.

The dangerous set is now finite-dimensional:

\[
\mathcal Z_L
=
\{Y:\det L(Y)=0\}.
\]

So D4 reduces to showing the D4 sampling set avoids \(\mathcal Z_L\), or that \(\det L(Y)\) is structurally nonzero.

This is a finite local algebra problem, not an analytic propagation problem.

---

# 6. Error terms after extracting \(L(Y)\)

After forming \(L(Y)\), the residual error \(\mathbf E\) should contain only terms satisfying at least one of:

1. extra \(q_0\) factor;
2. extra tail/error factor \(E_2\);
3. higher-order small gauge factor;
4. canonical truncation remainder;
5. terms supported outside the local row model.

The target is

\[
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L(Y))|\Gamma|.
\]

It is enough to prove each residual term \(T\) obeys

\[
|T|
\le
Q^{-K}
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|
\]

with

\[
K>C_L+O(1).
\]

This is now a term-by-term finite estimate.

---

# 7. Wall-live terms as a bonus

If a residual term is **not divisible by \(q_0\)**, it should not be treated as an error. It is a wall-live row contribution.

Modulo \(q_0\), such a term gives

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\bmod(q_0)\ne0.
\]

Then the wall can be solved directly by a source-robust row, without wall escape.

So the D4 audit should first split

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\mathbf A_{\rm wall}
+
q_0\mathbf A_{\rm div},
\]

where

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm wall}
=
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\bmod(q_0).
\]

If

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm wall}\ne0
\]

and it is controlled by Gate 2 wall mass, then D3 is solved.

If

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm wall}=0,
\]

then all rows are \(q_0\)-divisible and wall escape plus D4 is the correct route.

---

# 8. Finite D4 audit algorithm

The D4 row-expansion audit should be executed as follows.

## Step 1: compute wall residue

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm wall}
=
\mathbf A_{\rm row}\bmod(q_0).
\]

If nonzero, test whether

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm wall}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

under wall Gate 2 mass. If yes, D3 is solved directly.

## Step 2: divide by \(q_0\)

If

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm wall}=0,
\]

write

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0\mathbf B.
\]

## Step 3: extract \(u^3\Gamma\)-linear part

Write

\[
\mathbf B=u^3L(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E_1.
\]

## Step 4: test matrix nondegeneracy

Prove

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L(Y))\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on the D4 sampling set.

If \(L(Y)\) is constant plus small perturbation, use the perturbation test.

If not, compute

\[
\det L(Y)
\]

and prove a polynomial lower bound or identify a secondary degeneracy wall.

## Step 5: bound residual error

Show

\[
|\mathbf E_1|
\le
\frac12u^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|\mathbf E|
=
|q_0\mathbf E_1|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

---

# 9. Possible new secondary wall

If

\[
\det L(Y)=0
\]

on a nontrivial set, there is a secondary row-conversion wall.

Then D4 splits:

1. off \(\det L=0\), row conversion works;
2. near \(\det L=0\), need either:
   - another row \(A_{11},A_{13}\);
   - a row-pencil argument;
   - an escape lemma analogous to \(q_0\)-wall escape.

So the D4 audit should include \(A_{11},A_{13}\) as backup rows.

The row vector should perhaps be enlarged:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L_{4\times2}(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E.
\]

The correct nondegeneracy condition is

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(L_{4\times2})\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is stronger and more robust than relying only on \(A_7,A_9\).

---

# 10. Improved D4 theorem

## Extended Matrix Row Conversion Theorem

Let

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Assume

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

where

\[
L(Y)\in \mathbb C^{4\times2}.
\]

Assume

\[
\sigma_2(L(Y))\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L(Y))|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at any D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) or \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\), one has

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This version avoids accidental degeneracy in the \(2\times2\) \(A_7,A_9\) subsystem.

---

# 11. Attack conclusion

D4 can be made finite and robust by using an **extended row matrix** and extracting all \(q_0u^3\Gamma\)-linear terms into a variable coefficient matrix \(L(Y)\).

The proof target becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\qquad
\sigma_2(L(Y))\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\mathbf E|\le\frac12\text{leading}.
}
\]

This is a finite row algebra / correction bookkeeping problem.

If \(A_7,A_9\) alone are degenerate, enlarge to \(A_{11},A_{13}\).

This gives a concrete way to eliminate D4 as a black box.
## User (2026-04-27 11:00:50)

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:00:52)

## Continuing attack — remove the “secondary wall” in D4 by enlarging the row system

The previous step improved D4 from a two-row statement

\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})
\]

to an extended matrix-row statement

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T
=
q_0u^3L(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

with

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

The new possible obstruction is a **secondary row wall**:

\[
\sigma_2(L(Y))\approx0.
\]

I’ll now attack that.

---

# 1. The correct D4 object is a row pencil, not a fixed two-row matrix

The two-row system

\[
(A_7,A_9)
\]

has leading model

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7\\
A_9
\end{pmatrix}
=
q_0u^3
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_{71}(Y)&\ell_{72}(Y)\\
\ell_{91}(Y)&\ell_{92}(Y)
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
+\mathbf E.
\]

If the \(2\times2\) matrix is nondegenerate, D4 closes.

If not, this may be an artifact of using too few rows. The natural object is the row pencil

\[
\mathcal L_N(Y)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_{7,1}(Y)&\ell_{7,2}(Y)\\
\ell_{9,1}(Y)&\ell_{9,2}(Y)\\
\ell_{11,1}(Y)&\ell_{11,2}(Y)\\
\vdots\\
\ell_{2N+1,1}(Y)&\ell_{2N+1,2}(Y)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The desired condition is not

\[
\det L_{7,9}\ne0,
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the D4 sampling set.

Equivalently, the two columns of \(\mathcal L_N\) should be quantitatively independent.

---

# 2. Interpret the row pencil as anisotropy observables

The rows have leading shape

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
q_0u^3
\left(
\ell_{k,1}(Y)\Gamma_G+\ell_{k,2}(Y)\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

So each row measures one scalar projection of the anisotropy vector

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

The secondary wall occurs if all available row projections nearly annihilate the same anisotropy direction:

\[
\mathcal L_N(Y)\Gamma\approx0
\]

for some nonzero \(\Gamma\).

Thus the secondary wall is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists \Gamma\ne0:\quad
\ell_{k,1}(Y)\Gamma_G+\ell_{k,2}(Y)\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\quad
\forall k.
}
\]

This is a finite-dimensional observability problem.

---

# 3. Minimal observability theorem

The correct theorem is:

## Anisotropy Row Observability Theorem

There exists a finite \(N=O(1)\) or \(N\le R^{O(1)}\) such that the leading row coefficient matrix

\[
\mathcal L_N(Y)
\]

satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the D4 admissible set

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

with the canonical local boundedness assumptions.

If true, D4 becomes:

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|
\ge
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|-|\mathbf E|.
\]

With half-leading error,

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This would close row conversion uniformly, including any secondary degeneracy of \(A_7,A_9\).

---

# 4. How to prove observability: two independent rows suffice generically

If the leading matrix for \(A_7,A_9\) is

\[
L_{7,9}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}
+
\Delta L,
\]

then if \(\|\Delta L\|\le \frac12\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm diag})\), observability is immediate.

But if correction terms produce off-diagonal or same-scale changes, we can still prove observability by checking any \(2\times2\) minor:

\[
\Delta_{ij}(Y)
=
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_{i,1}(Y)&\ell_{i,2}(Y)\\
\ell_{j,1}(Y)&\ell_{j,2}(Y)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If for some \(i,j\),

\[
|\Delta_{ij}(Y)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and row norms are bounded above by \(Q^C\), then

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

So the finite audit becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute minors }\Delta_{ij}(Y)\text{ for }i,j\in\{7,9,11,13,\ldots\}.
}
\]

If one minor is polynomially nonzero on the admissible set, D4 closes.

---

# 5. If all minors vanish: hidden scalar row architecture

If every \(2\times2\) minor vanishes identically, then every row is proportional to a single coefficient vector:

\[
(\ell_{k,1},\ell_{k,2})
=
\alpha_k(Y)(a(Y),b(Y)).
\]

Then the row system only measures

\[
a(Y)\Gamma_G+b(Y)\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

It cannot control the orthogonal anisotropy direction.

In that case, D4 cannot prove row conversion from Gate 2, because Gate 2 controls

\[
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2,
\]

while the rows see only one projection.

Then one needs either:

1. another row family outside \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\);
2. a structural relation forcing \(\Gamma\) to lie in the measured direction;
3. a different anisotropy factor for Gate 2;
4. a row-pencil higher-order term nonlinear in \(\Gamma\).

Thus the minor audit is decisive.

---

# 6. Higher-order row-pencil fallback

Suppose the linear coefficient matrix \(\mathcal L_N\) loses rank on a secondary variety

\[
\mathcal Z_{\rm sec}=\{\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)=0\}.
\]

Near \(\mathcal Z_{\rm sec}\), the leading linear-in-\(\Gamma\) terms may not suffice. But higher-order terms in the row expansion may contain quadratic anisotropy:

\[
q_0u^3 Q_2(Y;\Gamma,\Gamma),
\]

or derivative anisotropy terms. These could still give a row lower bound when \(\mathcal L_N\Gamma\) is small.

This leads to a row-pencil stratification:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3
\left[
\mathcal L_N(Y)\Gamma
+
\mathcal Q_N(Y;\Gamma,\Gamma)
+
\cdots
\right]
+
\mathbf E.
\]

If

\[
|\mathcal L_N\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}|\Gamma|,
\]

linear D4 works.

If not, impose

\[
\Gamma\in\ker \mathcal L_N+O(Q^{-C})
\]

and test whether

\[
|\mathcal Q_N(Y;\Gamma,\Gamma)|\ge Q^{-C}|\Gamma|^2.
\]

This is a finite jet observability hierarchy.

But ideally the linear row pencil already has rank two.

---

# 7. Relation to Gate 2 anisotropy choice

Gate 2 currently uses

\[
|\Gamma|^2=\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2.
\]

If the row pencil only observes a different pair of anisotropy combinations, then Gate 2 should be adjusted.

For example, if rows naturally observe

\[
\Lambda_1=a_1\Gamma_G+b_1\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
\Lambda_2=a_2\Gamma_G+b_2\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

then Gate 2 should use

\[
|\Lambda_1|^2+|\Lambda_2|^2
\]

instead of

\[
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2,
\]

provided the two are equivalent:

\[
|\Lambda_1|^2+|\Lambda_2|^2
\asymp_Q
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2.
\]

This is exactly the same as

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So D4 observability is also a consistency check that Gate 2 is measuring the anisotropy directions actually used by the rows.

---

# 8. Finite audit protocol for D4 observability

The next concrete audit is:

1. Collect rows:

\[
A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}
\]

or more if needed.

2. Normalize each row by extracting the common factor:

\[
q_0u^3.
\]

3. Extract the part linear in

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

4. Build

\[
\mathcal L_N(Y).
\]

5. Compute all \(2\times2\) minors.

6. Prove either:

\[
\max_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}(Y)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on the D4 sampling set, or identify a secondary degeneracy variety.

7. If secondary degeneracy appears, include the next row pair or next-order anisotropy terms.

This is finite and executable.

---

# 9. Updated D4 theorem

## Extended D4 Row Observability Theorem

Let

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,\ldots,A_{2N+1})^T.
\]

Assume

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_N(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E_N.
\]

Assume

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C_L}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf E_N|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at any D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

plus a pointwise lower bound for \(u\) or upper bound for \(\Gamma\), implies

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

With row mobility,

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

This is the robust form of D4.

---

# 10. Attack conclusion

D4 is no longer “correction control” in vague form. It is now a finite observability problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do the leading row coefficients observe both anisotropy directions?}
}
\]

Mathematically:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If yes, D4 closes.

If no, either enlarge the row system or modify Gate 2 to match the row-observed anisotropy.

This is the next most concrete finite audit after the Gate 2 integral rigidity lemma.
