## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:02:58)

## Continuing attack — turn D4 observability into an explicit finite-minor theorem

The D4 row-conversion problem is now reduced to this:

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_N(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E_N,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

If

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf E_N|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|,
\]

then D4 closes.

The remaining question is how to prove

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

without treating it as another black box.

---

# 1. Reduce \(\sigma_2\) to minors

Let

\[
\mathcal L_N
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_{7,1} & \ell_{7,2}\\
\ell_{9,1} & \ell_{9,2}\\
\ell_{11,1} & \ell_{11,2}\\
\vdots
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

For any two rows \(i,j\), define the \(2\times2\) minor

\[
\Delta_{ij}
=
\ell_{i,1}\ell_{j,2}-\ell_{i,2}\ell_{j,1}.
\]

If

\[
\max_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|\ge Q^{-C_\Delta},
\]

and

\[
\|\mathcal L_N\|\le Q^{C_L},
\]

then

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)\ge Q^{-C_\Delta-C_L}.
\]

Reason:

\[
\det(\mathcal L_N^*\mathcal L_N)
=
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2
\]

by Cauchy–Binet. Also,

\[
\det(\mathcal L_N^*\mathcal L_N)
=
\sigma_1^2\sigma_2^2
\le
\|\mathcal L_N\|^2\sigma_2^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\sigma_2
\ge
\frac{\left(\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2\right)^{1/2}}
{\|\mathcal L_N\|}
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the finite audit target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find one polynomially nonzero minor }\Delta_{ij}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Why \(A_7,A_9\) probably already suffice

From the known leading structure,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

and

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

After extracting \(q_0u^3\), the leading coefficient matrix for rows \(7,9\) is

\[
L_{7,9}^{(0)}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Thus

\[
\Delta_{7,9}^{(0)}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}.
\]

If

\[
|c_7c_9|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and same-scale corrections do not cancel this determinant, then \(A_7,A_9\) alone give observability.

So the most efficient D4 audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
+
\text{correction determinant}
}
\]

and prove

\[
|\Delta_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This may be a finite constant calculation.

---

# 3. Correction determinant expansion

Let

\[
L_{7,9}
=
L_{7,9}^{(0)}+\Delta L.
\]

Write

\[
\Delta L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha&\beta\\
\gamma&\delta
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then

\[
\det L_{7,9}
=
\left(-\frac{c_7}{288}+\alpha\right)
\left(-\frac{c_9}{288}+\delta\right)
-\beta\gamma.
\]

Expanding,

\[
\det L_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
-\frac{c_7}{288}\delta
-\frac{c_9}{288}\alpha
+\alpha\delta
-\beta\gamma.
\]

So a sufficient perturbative condition is

\[
\left|
-\frac{c_7}{288}\delta
-\frac{c_9}{288}\alpha
+\alpha\delta
-\beta\gamma
\right|
\le
\frac12\left|\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}\right|.
\]

This is stronger than needed but easy.

If perturbation fails, compute the exact determinant. It may still be nonzero.

---

# 4. If \(A_7,A_9\) determinant cancels

If

\[
\Delta_{7,9}\approx0,
\]

add \(A_{11}\).

Now inspect

\[
\Delta_{7,11}
\]

and

\[
\Delta_{9,11}.
\]

If either is polynomially nonzero, D4 closes.

If all minors among \(7,9,11,13\) vanish, then all rows are collinear in anisotropy space:

\[
(\ell_{k,1},\ell_{k,2})
=
\alpha_k(Y)(a(Y),b(Y)).
\]

Then the row system observes only

\[
a(Y)\Gamma_G+b(Y)\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

and misses the orthogonal direction.

This would be a real secondary wall.

But it is highly structured. It would mean the entire projected row tower is rank-one as a map from the anisotropy vector to rows.

That is a finite algebraic claim and should be testable.

---

# 5. Secondary wall escape

Suppose the row pencil loses rank on

\[
\mathcal Z_{\rm sec}
=
\{\Delta_{ij}=0\ \forall i,j\}.
\]

Can we escape it like the \(q_0\)-wall?

Maybe. If the rank-loss condition is defined by some scalar determinant

\[
D(Y)=\Delta_{ij}(Y),
\]

and if along the packet

\[
D(m_0)\approx0
\]

but

\[
D'(m_0)\not\approx0
\]

or

\[
D''(m_0)\not\approx0,
\]

then one can move slightly to a point where

\[
|D|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is exactly the same sublevel escape logic.

So if \(A_7,A_9\) have a secondary degeneracy, one can either:

1. add more rows; or
2. prove determinant escape for \(\Delta_{ij}(m)\); or
3. show the degenerate anisotropy direction is incompatible with Gate 2 dynamics.

This gives a hierarchy:

\[
q_0\text{-wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{wall escape};
\]

\[
\det L\text{-wall}
\Rightarrow
\text{minor escape or add rows}.
\]

---

# 6. Finite D4 theorem with row enlargement

The robust statement is:

## D4 Row Observability Theorem

There exists a finite row set

\[
\mathcal R=\{A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}:1\le k\le K\}
\]

with \(K=O(1)\) or \(K\le Q^C\), such that after extracting \(q_0u^3\Gamma\)-linear terms,

\[
\mathbf A_{\mathcal R}
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_{\mathcal R}(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\]

and:

\[
\max_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}(Y)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on the D4 admissible set.

Equivalently,

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_{\mathcal R}(Y))\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

With half-leading error,

\[
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_{\mathcal R})|\Gamma|,
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_{\mathcal R}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This proves D4.

---

# 7. What exactly to compute next

The next symbolic audit should compute:

\[
\ell_{7,1},\ell_{7,2},
\]

\[
\ell_{9,1},\ell_{9,2},
\]

\[
\ell_{11,1},\ell_{11,2},
\]

\[
\ell_{13,1},\ell_{13,2}.
\]

Then compute minors:

\[
\Delta_{7,9},\quad
\Delta_{7,11},\quad
\Delta_{9,11},\quad
\Delta_{7,13},\quad
\Delta_{9,13},\quad
\Delta_{11,13}.
\]

The first expected result is:

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
+
\text{controlled terms}.
\]

If \(c_7,c_9\) are known nonzero constants and corrections are lower order, D4 closes immediately.

---

# 8. D4 and Gate 2 compatibility

Gate 2 gives

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

D4 leading rows give

\[
|\mathbf A_{\mathcal R}|
\gtrsim
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2|\Gamma|.
\]

At non-wall or escaped-wall samples,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Need \(|u|\) lower bound. Since

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A/2},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_{\mathcal R}|
\gtrsim
Q^{-C_q}\sigma_2 |u|^2 Q^{-A/2}.
\]

If wall escape gives

\[
|u|\ge\tau,
\]

done.

If non-wall sample came from Gate 2 mass but \(|u|\) is not explicitly lower-bounded, use an anisotropy upper bound

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}
\]

to infer

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-A/2-C_\Gamma}.
\]

So D4 must always include either:

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

This was already in the D4 theorem; it is essential.

---

# 9. Attack conclusion

D4 is now reduced to a finite row-minor audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute }\mathcal L_{\mathcal R}
\text{ and prove one }2\times2\text{ minor is polynomially nonzero.}
}
\]

The likely first check is

\[
\Delta_{7,9}\approx \frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}.
\]

If that holds, D4 closes with \(A_7,A_9\) alone.

If not, add \(A_{11},A_{13}\).

If all minors vanish, that reveals a genuine secondary wall and requires either more rows or a different anisotropy observable.

This is finite, concrete, and likely tractable compared with the original global arithmetic inputs.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:10:03)

_Thought for 16s_

## Continuing attack — use filtration/parity to kill the D4 secondary wall

The D4 row-conversion problem is now concentrated in one finite question:

\[
\mathbf A_{\mathcal R}
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_{\mathcal R}(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
\]

and we need

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_{\mathcal R})\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The most likely obstruction is that \(A_7,A_9\) might not give two independent anisotropy directions after correction terms are included. I’ll attack that by introducing a **filtration** under which the two diagonal terms are the unique lowest-order contributions to their respective rows.

If that filtration is valid, then the \(A_7,A_9\) determinant cannot vanish by correction cancellation.

---

# 1. The expected leading structure

The known row structure is

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

with

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Thus

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G+\cdots,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}+\cdots.
\]

So the leading matrix should be

\[
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If \(c_7c_9\ne0\), this is full rank.

The only way D4 fails is if correction terms produce an opposite same-order determinant cancellation.

---

# 2. Introduce an anisotropy filtration

Define a filtration by assigning weights:

\[
\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_G)=1,
\]

\[
\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_{G,2})=2,
\]

and count additional derivatives, gauge corrections, or transport corrections as increasing weight.

The intended structure is:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ first sees } \Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ first sees } \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

More precisely:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G
+
\text{terms of filtration }>\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_G)
\right),
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\text{terms of filtration }>\operatorname{wt}(\Gamma_{G,2})
\right),
\]

where

\[
\alpha_7=-\frac{c_7}{288},
\qquad
\alpha_9=-\frac{c_9}{288}.
\]

If this is true, then the determinant has leading filtration term

\[
\alpha_7\alpha_9.
\]

Corrections cannot cancel it because they live in higher filtration.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 closes if the row expansion is triangular in this anisotropy filtration.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Triangular D4 theorem

## Triangular Row-Conversion Theorem

Assume

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G
+
b_7\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
b_9\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)
+
E_9.
\]

Suppose the off-diagonal terms satisfy one of:

### Perturbative case

\[
|b_7|+|b_9|
\le
\frac14\min(|\alpha_7|,|\alpha_9|).
\]

Then

\[
\sigma_{\min}
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha_7&b_7\\
b_9&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}
\ge
c\min(|\alpha_7|,|\alpha_9|).
\]

### Filtration case

The terms \(b_7\Gamma_{G,2}\) and \(b_9\Gamma_G\) have strictly higher filtration or extra small packet factor, so they cannot cancel the lowest-filtration determinant term

\[
\alpha_7\alpha_9.
\]

Then again

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

provided

\[
|\alpha_7|,|\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Finally, if

\[
|(E_7,E_9)|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|,
\]

then

\[
|(A_7,A_9)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

at every D4 sample.

---

# 4. How to prove triangularity

The row indices suggest a graded hierarchy:

\[
A_7
\leftrightarrow
\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9
\leftrightarrow
\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

This is likely not accidental. The indices \(7,9\) differ by two, matching the first and second anisotropy channels.

To prove it, one should show:

\[
A_{2k+5}^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,k}
+
\text{higher transport/correction}.
\]

For \(k=1\),

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_G+\cdots.
\]

For \(k=2\),

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
H\Gamma_{G,2}+\cdots.
\]

The fact that \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) first appears in \(A_9\), not \(A_7\), is the triangularity.

Similarly, \(\Gamma_G\) appearing in \(A_9\) should be a lower-channel correction. If it appears, it should be removable by replacing

\[
A_9
\]

with a row-combination

\[
\widetilde A_9=A_9-\beta A_7.
\]

This gives another route.

---

# 5. Row elimination: remove lower-channel contamination

Suppose

\[
A_7=q_0u^3(\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\beta_7\Gamma_{G,2})+E_7,
\]

\[
A_9=q_0u^3(\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2})+E_9.
\]

If \(\alpha_7\) is nonzero, define

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
A_9-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}A_7.
\]

Then the \(\Gamma_G\) coefficient in \(\widetilde A_9\) is removed.

The \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) coefficient becomes

\[
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}.
\]

This is exactly

\[
\frac{\det L}{\alpha_7}.
\]

So D4 reduces to proving

\[
\alpha_7\ne0
\]

and

\[
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}\ne0.
\]

If triangularity gives \(\beta_7,\beta_9\) lower order, then done.

If not, this produces a scalar finite nonvanishing condition.

This row elimination is useful because it shows D4 is stable under row operations. The downstream row norm can use row combinations as long as the transformation matrix has polynomial condition number.

---

# 6. Use row operations as part of D4

Define a row-operation matrix

\[
T(Y)
\]

with polynomial condition number, and set

\[
\widetilde{\mathbf A}=T(Y)\mathbf A.
\]

If

\[
T
\]

is uniformly invertible with

\[
\|T\|+\|T^{-1}\|\le Q^C,
\]

then

\[
|\widetilde{\mathbf A}|\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
|\mathbf A|\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

So we can triangularize \(L\):

\[
T L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\tilde\alpha_7&0\\
0&\tilde\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}
\]

or at least row-echelon it.

D4 then becomes:

\[
\widetilde A_7
=
q_0u^3\tilde\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\widetilde E_7,
\]

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
q_0u^3\tilde\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}+\widetilde E_9.
\]

This is the cleanest finite-algebra formulation.

---

# 7. Secondary wall becomes a determinant condition

After row operations, the only remaining secondary wall is:

\[
\det L=0.
\]

If

\[
\det L
\]

is a nonzero polynomial/rational expression in local variables, then its zeros are a lower-dimensional set.

There are two options:

## Option A — prove uniform nonvanishing

\[
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

on the D4 sampling set.

This closes D4.

## Option B — determinant escape

If

\[
\det L\approx0
\]

but its derivative is live, one can use an escape theorem analogous to wall escape.

This would be a **secondary wall escape**.

Let

\[
D(m)=\det L(Y(m)).
\]

If

\[
D(m_0)\approx0
\]

and

\[
|D'(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then nearby

\[
|D|\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

while Gate 2 signal remains live.

Then D4 applies at the nearby point.

This suggests a robust hierarchy:

\[
q_0\text{-wall}
\to
\text{wall escape};
\]

\[
\det L\text{-wall}
\to
\text{minor/determinant escape};
\]

if row conversion is existential.

---

# 8. Extended rows likely avoid determinant escape

Instead of escaping \(\det L=0\), one can add more rows.

Let

\[
\mathcal L_{4\times2}
\]

come from

\[
A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}.
\]

Then the secondary wall is not one determinant but the simultaneous vanishing of all \(2\times2\) minors.

This is much harder for the bad set to satisfy.

The row observability theorem becomes:

\[
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is more robust and avoids having to choose one determinant.

So the preferred D4 audit is:

1. try \(A_7,A_9\);
2. if determinant uncertain, use \(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}\);
3. prove the Cauchy–Binet minor sum is nonzero:

\[
\det(\mathcal L^*\mathcal L)
=
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 9. Attack plan for D4 finite audit

The finite audit should now proceed in this exact order.

## Step 1: Extract row-leading coefficients

For each row \(A_{2k+1}\), compute

\[
A_{2k+1}
=
q_0u^3
(\ell_{k,1}\Gamma_G+\ell_{k,2}\Gamma_{G,2})
+
E_{2k+1}.
\]

## Step 2: Form \(\mathcal L\)

\[
\mathcal L
=
(\ell_{k,j})_{k,j}.
\]

## Step 3: Compute minor sum

\[
\mathcal D_{\rm obs}
:=
\sum_{i<j}
|\ell_{i,1}\ell_{j,2}-\ell_{i,2}\ell_{j,1}|^2.
\]

## Step 4: Prove

\[
\mathcal D_{\rm obs}\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

## Step 5: Bound errors

\[
\sum_k|E_{2k+1}|^2
\le
\frac14
|q_0|^2|u|^6
\sigma_2(\mathcal L)^2
|\Gamma|^2.
\]

Then D4 closes.

---

# 10. Conclusion

The D4 secondary wall can be attacked by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{row operations and finite minor observability.}
}
\]

The likely outcome is:

- \(A_7,A_9\) already form a triangular system and suffice;
- if not, \(A_{11},A_{13}\) supply missing anisotropy directions;
- if all rows remain rank-one, that reveals a genuine row-architecture defect.

This is now a finite symbolic problem, not a conceptual blocker.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:11:26)

## Continuing attack — collapse D4 to a triangular normal form

I’ll push D4 one step further. The current finite problem is:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\ell_{k,1}\Gamma_G+\ell_{k,2}\Gamma_{G,2}
\right)
+
E_{2k+1}.
\]

We need the row coefficient matrix

\[
\mathcal L=(\ell_{k,j})
\]

to observe both anisotropy directions. I will now show that, under the expected triangular row hierarchy, \(A_7,A_9\) should already suffice, and formulate the exact triangular normal-form theorem.

---

# 1. Expected hierarchy

The row labels suggest:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{detects}\quad
\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{detects}\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

More generally,

\[
A_{2k+5}^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{detects}\quad
\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Thus the expected leading hierarchy is

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G
+
\text{higher / later anisotropy channels}
\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\text{lower-channel correction removable by }A_7
+
\text{higher terms}
\right)
+
E_9.
\]

The constants should be

\[
\alpha_7=-\frac{c_7}{288},
\qquad
\alpha_9=-\frac{c_9}{288}.
\]

If

\[
\alpha_7\alpha_9\ne0,
\]

then the two rows are already the right anisotropy coordinates after triangularization.

---

# 2. Triangular normal form

Allow row operations with polynomially bounded coefficients. Define

\[
\widetilde A_7=A_7,
\]

and choose \(\beta\) so that

\[
\widetilde A_9=A_9-\beta A_7
\]

removes the \(\Gamma_G\) coefficient from \(A_9\).

Suppose

\[
A_7
=
q_0u^3
(\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\beta_7\Gamma_{G,2})
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9
=
q_0u^3
(\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2})
+
E_9.
\]

If

\[
|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

take

\[
\beta=\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}.
\]

Then

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right)
\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\widetilde E_9.
\]

So the triangular determinant is

\[
\alpha_7
\left(
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right)
=
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_9\beta_7
=
\det L_{7,9}.
\]

Thus D4 reduces to:

\[
|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

\[
\left|
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right|
\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and controlled errors.

Equivalently,

\[
|\det L_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 3. Filtration should force \(\beta_7,\beta_9\) small or removable

The row hierarchy suggests a filtration:

\[
\operatorname{fil}(\Gamma_G)=1,
\qquad
\operatorname{fil}(\Gamma_{G,2})=2.
\]

Then

\[
A_7
\]

has first nonzero anisotropy term in filtration \(1\), namely \(\Gamma_G\).

Similarly,

\[
A_9
\]

has first genuinely new anisotropy term in filtration \(2\), namely \(\Gamma_{G,2}\).

Under this filtration:

- a \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) term in \(A_7\) is higher filtration;
- a \(\Gamma_G\) term in \(A_9\) is a lower-channel contamination and should be removable by subtracting a multiple of \(A_7\);
- the new coefficient of \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) in \(\widetilde A_9\) cannot cancel with a lower-filtration term.

Therefore the triangular determinant should be protected.

This gives the theorem:

## Filtered Triangular Row Theorem

Assume rows admit expansions

\[
A_7
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G
+
O_{\mathrm{fil}>1}
\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\beta_9\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
+
O_{\mathrm{fil}>2}
\right)
+
E_9.
\]

Assume

\[
|\alpha_7|,|\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and row operations removing lower filtration terms have condition number \(\le Q^C\). Then

\[
\sigma_2(L_{7,9})\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

modulo higher-filtration perturbations.

If higher-filtration perturbations are half-leading on the D4 sampling set, D4 closes.

---

# 4. Why this matters

This avoids needing to compute every row minor. We only need to prove the **filtration statement**:

\[
A_7 \text{ first detects } \Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9 \text{ first detects } \Gamma_{G,2}
\]

with nonzero coefficients.

That is likely much easier than a brute-force \(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}\) minor audit.

---

# 5. What must be checked from actual formulas

The actual row formulas need to verify:

## Check 1 — \(A_7\) leading coefficient

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G
+
\text{terms of higher filtration}
+
E_7,
\]

with

\[
c_7\ne0.
\]

## Check 2 — \(A_9\) new-channel coefficient

After subtracting the lower-channel contamination,

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
A_9-\beta A_7,
\]

one has

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
-\frac{\widetilde c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\text{higher filtration}
+
\widetilde E_9,
\]

with

\[
\widetilde c_9\ne0.
\]

## Check 3 — bounded row operation

\[
|\beta|\le Q^C.
\]

## Check 4 — error control

\[
|(E_7,\widetilde E_9)|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3
Q^{-C}
|\Gamma|.
\]

These four checks close D4.

---

# 6. Handling higher-filtration terms

Suppose higher-filtration terms include powers like

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

inside \(A_7\). This is not necessarily small if \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) dominates. But it does not break observability; it just gives an off-diagonal entry \(\beta_7\).

The determinant becomes

\[
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9.
\]

If \(\beta_9=0\) after row elimination, \(\beta_7\) is harmless.

So the safer procedure is:

1. Use \(A_7\) to define the first coordinate.
2. Project \(A_9\) orthogonally to \(A_7\)’s leading direction.
3. Check that the remaining component in the \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) direction is nonzero.

This is Gram–Schmidt at the row-symbol level.

---

# 7. Symbolic Gram–Schmidt theorem

Let

\[
v_7=(\ell_{7,1},\ell_{7,2}),
\]

\[
v_9=(\ell_{9,1},\ell_{9,2}).
\]

Assume

\[
|v_7|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Define

\[
v_9^\perp
=
v_9-
\frac{\langle v_9,v_7\rangle}{|v_7|^2}v_7.
\]

If

\[
|v_9^\perp|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then

\[
\sigma_2(L_{7,9})\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

The row operation

\[
\widetilde A_9=A_9-\frac{\langle v_9,v_7\rangle}{|v_7|^2}A_7
\]

has polynomial condition number.

So D4 closes if:

\[
v_7\not\approx0,
\qquad
v_9\not\parallel v_7.
\]

This gives a coordinate-free test.

---

# 8. If \(A_7,A_9\) fail

If

\[
v_9^\perp\approx0,
\]

use \(A_{11}\).

Let

\[
v_{11}=(\ell_{11,1},\ell_{11,2}).
\]

Check

\[
\operatorname{dist}(v_{11},\operatorname{span}(v_7))\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Since the target anisotropy space is only two-dimensional, a single row outside the span suffices.

Thus the row audit is simple:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find two row coefficient vectors }v_i,v_j\text{ not polynomially parallel.}
}
\]

This is the finite row observability problem.

---

# 9. Why a full tower should succeed

If every row coefficient vector is parallel,

\[
v_k=\alpha_k v_0,
\]

then all rows measure the same anisotropy combination

\[
v_0\cdot\Gamma.
\]

But the row hierarchy was built to produce successive Gram anisotropies:

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\Gamma_{G,3},\ldots.
\]

It would be surprising if all projected rows measured only one combination of the first two channels. If that happened, Gate 2 was incorrectly chosen or the row projection loses anisotropy information.

Thus either:

- \(A_7,A_9\) already work;
- \(A_{11}\) or \(A_{13}\) supplies the missing direction;
- or the current row architecture has a genuine design flaw.

This is exactly the finite audit needed.

---

# 10. Updated D4 close theorem

## Filtered Row Observability D4

Let

\[
v_k=(\ell_{k,1},\ell_{k,2})
\]

be the coefficient vector of \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) in

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}/(q_0u^3).
\]

Assume for some \(i,j\)

\[
|v_i|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

\[
\operatorname{dist}(v_j,\operatorname{span}v_i)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L)\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

for the row matrix containing \(i,j\).

If also

\[
|\mathbf E|\le \frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L)|\Gamma|,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

at any D4 sample.

This closes D4 after a finite coefficient-vector nonparallelism check.

---

# 11. Attack result

The D4 “secondary wall” is now reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find two row-symbol vectors }v_i,v_j
\text{ not parallel.}
}
\]

Expected first pair:

\[
v_7\sim(1,0),
\qquad
v_9\sim(0,1).
\]

If confirmed, D4 is solved with \(A_7,A_9\).

If not, add \(A_{11},A_{13}\).

This is a finite local row-symbol computation, not a global analytic obstacle.

_Thought for 13s_

## Continuing attack — close D4 if the displayed row asymptotics are literal leading expansions

The D4 row-conversion layer now hinges on whether the known schematic rows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are merely heuristic labels, or actual leading-term expansions with nonzero coefficients and controlled remainders. If they are actual leading expansions, then the D4 secondary wall is essentially gone. 

---

# 1. Convert “\(\sim\)” into a quantitative leading statement

The needed proof-level statement is:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+R_9,
\]

with

\[
|c_7|,|c_9|\ge Q^{-C_c}.
\]

Also

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+R_H.
\]

Substitution gives

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G
+
c_7R_H\Gamma_G
+
R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
+
c_9R_H\Gamma_{G,2}
+
R_9.
\]

So the leading coefficient matrix is

\[
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead})
\ge
\frac1{288}\min(|c_7|,|c_9|)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus, if \(R_H,R_7,R_9\) are half-leading, \(A_7,A_9\) alone close D4.

---

# 2. The exact D4 closure condition

At a D4 sample, assume

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|=(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Define

\[
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathbf A=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If

\[
\left|
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7R_H\Gamma_G+R_7\\
c_9R_H\Gamma_{G,2}+R_9
\end{pmatrix}
\right|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3
\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead})
|\Gamma|,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf A|
\ge
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3
\sigma_{\min}(L_{\rm lead})
|\Gamma|.
\]

Using

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A_2/2},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-A_2/2}|u|^2.
\]

If \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\), then

\[
|\mathbf A|\ge Q^{-C_q-C_L-A_2/2-2C_u}.
\]

If instead \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\), then

\[
|u|^2\ge Q^{-A_2-2C_\Gamma},
\]

so

\[
|\mathbf A|\ge Q^{-C_q-C_L-3A_2/2-2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Either way,

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf A|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

So D4 is closed once the row expansions and half-leading correction bound are established.

---

# 3. What if \(R_7,R_9\) contain same-order cross terms?

Suppose the true expansion is

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3(\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\beta_7\Gamma_{G,2})+E_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3(\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2})+E_9.
\]

Then

\[
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha_7&\beta_7\\
\beta_9&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

D4 needs

\[
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
\|L\|\le Q^C.
\]

The determinant is

\[
\det L
=
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9.
\]

Using the expected leading constants,

\[
\alpha_7=-\frac{c_7}{288}+\text{correction},
\]

\[
\alpha_9=-\frac{c_9}{288}+\text{correction}.
\]

So the finite test is:

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9
\right|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If cross terms are lower filtration or perturbative, this is immediate.

If not, compute this scalar determinant exactly.

---

# 4. Row-operation closure

Even if \(A_9\) contains a \(\Gamma_G\)-term, we can remove it.

Let

\[
A_7=q_0u^3(\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\beta_7\Gamma_{G,2})+E_7,
\]

with

\[
|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Set

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
A_9-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}A_7.
\]

Then

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right)
\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\widetilde E_9.
\]

So after row elimination, the only nonvanishing condition is

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The row operation is allowed if

\[
\left|\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}\right|\le Q^C.
\]

This is automatic if coefficients are polynomially bounded and \(|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C}\).

Thus D4 is stable under finite row operations.

---

# 5. If \(A_7,A_9\) fail, use \(A_{11},A_{13}\)

If

\[
\det L_{7,9}\approx0,
\]

extend the row vector:

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Extract

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_N\Gamma+\mathbf E_N,
\]

where

\[
\mathcal L_N\in\mathbb C^{4\times2}.
\]

Then D4 needs

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

By Cauchy–Binet,

\[
\det(\mathcal L_N^\ast \mathcal L_N)
=
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2,
\]

where

\[
\Delta_{ij}
=
\ell_{i,1}\ell_{j,2}-\ell_{i,2}\ell_{j,1}.
\]

So it suffices to prove

\[
\boxed{
\max_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is a finite row-symbol audit.

---

# 6. D4 proof package

D4 is now the following finite theorem.

## D4 Row Observability + Correction Theorem

Let

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,\ldots,A_{2N+1})^T.
\]

Assume

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_N(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E_N.
\]

Assume

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf E_N|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)
|\Gamma|.
\]

Then every D4 sample satisfies

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

With row mobility,

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

This proves row conversion.

---

# 7. The most likely shortcut

Because the given structure already says

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

the likely finite proof is simply:

\[
\boxed{
A_7,A_9\text{ are triangular at leading order.}
}
\]

Namely:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G
+
\text{half-leading error},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\text{half-leading error}.
\]

If this is the actual row expansion, D4 is done.

---

# 8. Remaining concrete tasks

The next exact calculations are:

1. verify \(c_7,c_9\neq0\);

2. write \(R_H,R_7,R_9\) explicitly enough to decide whether they are:
   - half-leading errors;
   - same-order linear terms absorbed into \(L\);
   - wall-live terms;
   - genuinely dangerous;

3. if same-order terms exist, compute

\[
\det L_{7,9};
\]

4. if \(\det L_{7,9}\) is not uniformly nonzero, compute row-symbol vectors for \(A_{11},A_{13}\) and check a \(2\times2\) minor.

That is finite and proof-level.

---

# 9. Attack conclusion

D4 no longer needs to be treated as a named open input in broad form.

It reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite row-symbol observability}
+
\text{half-leading correction control}.
}
\]

Given the displayed leading rows, the first-pass expectation is that \(A_7,A_9\) already close it.

The next proof action is to compute the \(A_7,A_9\) row-symbol matrix and verify its determinant is polynomially nonzero.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:14:09)

_Thought for 5s_

## Continuing attack — reduce D4 to two explicit coefficient tests

The D4 row-conversion problem is now finite. We no longer need broad strategy. We need to verify two concrete algebraic facts:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Coefficient Test 1: } c_7c_9\neq0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Coefficient Test 2: row corrections do not cancel the }A_7/A_9\text{ leading determinant.}
}
\]

If both hold, then the row-conversion layer closes modulo standard canonical error control. The latest downstream architecture already isolates D4 as the local matrix row-conversion problem after Wall-Escape Sampling. 

---

# 1. The D4 determinant

Start with

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+R_7,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+R_9,
\]

and

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+R_H.
\]

Substitution gives the principal row-symbols

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G+\cdots,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}+\cdots.
\]

Thus the principal \(2\times2\) matrix is

\[
L_0=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Its determinant is

\[
\det L_0=\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
c_7c_9\neq0
\Longrightarrow
L_0\text{ observes both anisotropy channels.}
}
\]

If \(c_7,c_9\) are absolute nonzero constants, then

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_0)\asymp 1.
\]

This is the desired leading behavior.

---

# 2. Corrections as a perturbation matrix

Write the full anisotropy-linear part as

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf E,
\qquad
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Let

\[
L=L_0+\Delta L,
\]

where

\[
\Delta L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha&\beta\\
\gamma&\delta
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then

\[
\det L
=
\det L_0
-\frac{c_7}{288}\delta
-\frac{c_9}{288}\alpha
+
\alpha\delta-\beta\gamma.
\]

A sufficient perturbative condition is

\[
\left|
-\frac{c_7}{288}\delta
-\frac{c_9}{288}\alpha
+
\alpha\delta-\beta\gamma
\right|
\le
\frac12
\left|
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
\right|.
\]

Then

\[
|\det L|\ge \frac12|\det L_0|,
\]

and with \(\|L\|\le Q^C\),

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the correction audit becomes a finite determinant estimate.

---

# 3. If corrections are not perturbative

If \(\Delta L\) is same-scale, do **not** classify it as error. Absorb it into \(L\) and prove directly:

\[
\boxed{
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is still finite.

There are only three outcomes:

## Outcome A — determinant nonzero

\[
|\det L|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then \(A_7,A_9\) close D4.

## Outcome B — determinant zero due to exact cancellation

\[
\det L\equiv0.
\]

Then \(A_7,A_9\) observe only one anisotropy direction. Need add \(A_{11}\) or \(A_{13}\).

## Outcome C — determinant small only on a secondary variety

\[
\det L(Y)\approx0
\]

on a lower-dimensional set. Then either prove a secondary escape lemma, or add rows to avoid the bad set.

The simplest robust solution is to enlarge the row vector.

---

# 4. Extended row observability

Let

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Extract

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^3\mathcal L_N(Y)\Gamma+\mathbf E_N,
\]

where

\[
\mathcal L_N(Y)\in \mathbb C^{4\times2}.
\]

Then D4 needs

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N(Y))\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

By Cauchy–Binet,

\[
\det(\mathcal L_N^\ast\mathcal L_N)
=
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2,
\]

where

\[
\Delta_{ij}
=
\ell_{i,1}\ell_{j,2}
-
\ell_{i,2}\ell_{j,1}.
\]

So it suffices to show

\[
\boxed{
\max_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is the precise finite minor audit.

If

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
\]

works, stop.

If not, test

\[
\Delta_{7,11},\quad
\Delta_{9,11},\quad
\Delta_{7,13},\quad
\Delta_{9,13},\quad
\Delta_{11,13}.
\]

If all vanish, the row architecture is rank-one in anisotropy space.

---

# 5. Use triangularity to avoid full minor computation

The displayed structure strongly suggests triangularity:

\[
A_7\leadsto \Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9\leadsto \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Formalize this as a filtered statement:

\[
A_7
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G
+
\text{higher filtration}
\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\beta_9\Gamma_G
+
\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\text{higher filtration}
\right)
+
E_9.
\]

Subtract lower-channel contamination:

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
A_9-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}A_7.
\]

Then

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_9+O(\text{higher filtration})
\right)
\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\widetilde E_9.
\]

Thus, if

\[
|\alpha_7|,|\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and higher-filtration terms are controlled, the rows are anisotropy-observing.

The key finite check is:

\[
\boxed{
A_7\text{ first detects }\Gamma_G,\quad
A_9\text{ first detects the new channel }\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

---

# 6. D4 theorem after determinant/filtration check

Assume

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^3\mathcal L_N\Gamma+\mathbf E_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf E_N|\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

At a D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Also either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf A_N|
\ge
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Since

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A_2/2},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_N|
\ge
Q^{-C_q-C_L-A_2/2}|u|^2.
\]

If \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\),

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C_q-C_L-A_2/2-2C_u}.
\]

If \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\), then

\[
|u|^2\ge Q^{-A_2-2C_\Gamma},
\]

hence

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C_q-C_L-3A_2/2-2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Thus D4 closes.

---

# 7. What remains to calculate

The actual finite audit now has exactly four pieces.

## 7.1 Coefficients

Compute

\[
c_7,\qquad c_9.
\]

Need

\[
c_7c_9\ne0.
\]

## 7.2 Anisotropy-linear corrections

Compute all terms of form

\[
q_0u^3(a\Gamma_G+b\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

inside \(A_7,A_9\), and if needed \(A_{11},A_{13}\). These define \(L\).

## 7.3 Minor determinant

Check

\[
|\det L_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If false, check extended minors.

## 7.4 Residual error

Everything not included in \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\) must satisfy

\[
|\mathbf E_N|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

This includes:

\[
E_2,
\]

tail/truncation,

projection/gauge,

row normalization,

higher-order transport,

and non-linear anisotropy terms.

---

# 8. Attack conclusion

D4 has been reduced to a finite row-symbol determinant calculation.

Expected close:

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
+
\text{controlled correction},
\]

with \(c_7c_9\ne0\).

If this is confirmed, D4 closes using only \(A_7,A_9\).

If not, add \(A_{11},A_{13}\) and use the Cauchy–Binet minor sum.

This is now finite algebra and correction bookkeeping, not a conceptual obstruction.

## Continuing attack — finite D4 audit, now focused on the determinant obstruction

The next thing to attack is the only remaining local algebra obstruction in D4:

\[
\det L_{7,9}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

The downstream package now uses Gate 2 integral rigidity and Wall-Escape Sampling to produce a non-wall D4 sample; D4 itself is the matrix row-conversion step

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

So D4 closes once \(L\) has polynomially bounded rank \(2\) and \(\mathbf R\) is half-leading. 

---

# 1. The determinant to isolate

For the first two rows,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Write the anisotropy-linear part as

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}
=
q_0u^3
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha_7&\beta_7\\
\beta_9&\alpha_9
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
+
\mathbf E.
\]

The leading expectation is

\[
\alpha_7=-\frac{c_7}{288}+(\text{same-scale correction}),
\]

\[
\alpha_9=-\frac{c_9}{288}+(\text{same-scale correction}),
\]

and

\[
\beta_7,\beta_9
\]

are off-diagonal correction coefficients.

The determinant is

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9.
\]

D4 for \(A_7,A_9\) is equivalent to proving

\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If \(\beta_7,\beta_9\) are lower filtration or perturbative, this reduces to

\[
\boxed{
|c_7c_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Attack by row-symbol triangularity

The displayed row architecture strongly suggests the triangular normal form:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\text{higher channel}\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}+\text{higher channel}\right)
+
E_9.
\]

Then eliminate the lower channel from \(A_9\):

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
A_9-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}A_7.
\]

This gives

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right)
\Gamma_{G,2}
+
\widetilde E_9.
\]

Thus the triangular coefficient is

\[
\widetilde\alpha_9
=
\frac{\Delta_{7,9}}{\alpha_7}.
\]

So D4 closes if

\[
|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|\widetilde\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is the cleanest symbolic test:

\[
\boxed{
A_7\text{ detects }\Gamma_G,\quad
A_9\text{ detects a genuinely new }\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ direction after removing }A_7.
}
\]

---

# 3. How to certify triangularity without full formulas

Use filtration.

Assign

\[
\operatorname{fil}(\Gamma_G)=1,
\]

\[
\operatorname{fil}(\Gamma_{G,2})=2.
\]

The target statements are:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G+O_{\mathrm{fil}>1}
\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}+O_{\mathrm{fil}>2}
\right)
+
E_9.
\]

Here \(O_{\mathrm{fil}>k}\) means either a later anisotropy channel, extra small local factor, or a term that can be absorbed into a higher row.

If this filtration is valid, then the determinant’s lowest nonzero filtered part is

\[
\alpha_7\alpha_9.
\]

No higher-filtration term can cancel it.

So a proof can avoid computing all corrections if it proves:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{in}(A_7/q_0u^3)=\alpha_7\Gamma_G,\qquad
\operatorname{in}(A_9/q_0u^3)\notin \operatorname{span}\{\Gamma_G\}
}
\]

in the associated graded algebra.

That is likely the most efficient D4 proof.

---

# 4. If triangularity fails, enlarge rows

If

\[
\Delta_{7,9}=0
\]

or cannot be bounded, define

\[
\mathbf A_4=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Extract

\[
\mathbf A_4=q_0u^3\mathcal L_4\Gamma+\mathbf E_4,
\]

with

\[
\mathcal L_4\in \mathbb C^{4\times2}.
\]

Then the correct rank condition is

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_4)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

By Cauchy–Binet,

\[
\sigma_1^2\sigma_2^2
=
\det(\mathcal L_4^\ast\mathcal L_4)
=
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2.
\]

Thus, assuming \(\|\mathcal L_4\|\le Q^C\), it suffices to prove

\[
\max_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The row audit is finite:

\[
\Delta_{7,9},\quad
\Delta_{7,11},\quad
\Delta_{9,11},\quad
\Delta_{7,13},\quad
\Delta_{9,13},\quad
\Delta_{11,13}.
\]

If any minor is polynomially nonzero, D4 closes.

If all vanish, then the available row family is rank-one in the \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\)-plane. That would reveal a genuine row-architecture defect.

---

# 5. Error classification: what can remain in \(\mathbf E\)

After extracting \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\), the residual \(\mathbf E\) must be half-leading.

At a non-wall D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

And after wall escape, more specifically,

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

So the leading scale is

\[
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-O(1)}
\]

at wall-escape samples.

Therefore every residual term must be bounded by

\[
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1)}.
\]

Classification:

### Absorb into \(L\)

Any term of the form

\[
q_0u^3(a\Gamma_G+b\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

belongs in \(L\), not \(\mathbf E\).

### Perturbative

Terms with an extra wall factor:

\[
q_0^2u^3\Gamma
\]

are smaller by \(|q_0|\), hence perturbative at wall-escape samples if \(C_\varepsilon\) is large.

Terms with canonical tail factor \(E_2\) are perturbative if the \(E_2\)-derivative/tail budget beats the leading scale.

### Dangerous

Terms not divisible by \(q_0\) are not D4 errors. They are wall-live rows and should be moved to the D3 source-robust side.

Terms like

\[
q_0u^2\Gamma
\]

or

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma^2
\]

are not automatically perturbative and must be absorbed, controlled by extra assumptions, or shown absent by filtration.

---

# 6. A sharper D4 theorem

## Filtered Matrix D4 Theorem

Assume rows \(A_7,A_9,\ldots,A_{2N+1}\) admit a decomposition

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3\mathcal L_N\Gamma+\mathbf E_N.
\]

Assume:

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf E_N|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(\mathcal L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at every D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) or \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\), one has

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If additionally

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

then

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

This is the row-conversion theorem needed downstream.

---

# 7. How to finish D4 in practice

The fastest proof path is:

1. Verify

\[
A_7/(q_0u^3)
=
\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\text{higher},
\qquad
\alpha_7\neq0.
\]

2. Verify

\[
A_9/(q_0u^3)
=
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}+\text{higher},
\qquad
\alpha_9\neq0.
\]

3. Eliminate \(\Gamma_G\) from \(A_9\) using \(A_7\).

4. Prove higher terms are half-leading or higher filtration.

Then D4 closes with \(A_7,A_9\).

If step 2 fails, add \(A_{11}\), then \(A_{13}\).

---

# 8. Current attack conclusion

D4 is now a **finite filtered row-symbol problem**.

The likely theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
A_7,A_9\text{ form a triangular anisotropy coordinate system.}
}
\]

If true, D4 is no longer a named open input; it becomes a local expansion lemma plus canonical error bounds.

The only way D4 stays open is if the actual formulas show \(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots\) all measure only one anisotropy direction or if uncontrolled residual terms remain same-scale and non-absorbed.

## Continuing attack — prove D4 by associated-graded row symbols

The next attack is to stop thinking about \(A_7,A_9\) as analytic functions first, and instead pass to their **principal row symbols** in the associated graded algebra.

If the principal symbols are

\[
\sigma(A_7)=\alpha_7\,q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\qquad
\sigma(A_9)=\alpha_9\,q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
\alpha_7\alpha_9\ne0,
\]

then D4 is done modulo lower-order estimates. The current downstream state already identifies the D4 row normal form as the finite local step after Gate 2 and Wall-Escape Sampling. 

---

# 1. Define the row-symbol projection

Let

\[
\Gamma=
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

Define the principal row-symbol projection

\[
\Pi_{\rm lin}
\]

to extract exactly the part of a row that is:

1. divisible by \(q_0u^3\);
2. linear in \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\);
3. lowest order in the downstream filtration.

Thus for any row \(A\),

\[
\Pi_{\rm lin}(A)
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\ell_1(A)\Gamma_G+\ell_2(A)\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

The row-symbol vector is

\[
v(A):=(\ell_1(A),\ell_2(A)).
\]

Then for

\[
\mathbf A=(A_7,A_9)^T,
\]

the symbol matrix is

\[
L_{7,9}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
v(A_7)\\
v(A_9)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

D4 reduces to

\[
\det L_{7,9}\ne0
\]

with polynomial lower bound.

---

# 2. Principal-symbol target

The desired symbolic calculation is:

\[
v(A_7)=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288},0
\right),
\]

\[
v(A_9)=
\left(
0,-\frac{c_9}{288}
\right),
\]

or after lower-channel row elimination,

\[
v(A_7)=
(\alpha_7,\beta_7),
\]

\[
v(\widetilde A_9)=
(0,\widetilde \alpha_9),
\]

with

\[
|\alpha_7|,\ |\widetilde\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\det L_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
\]

in the clean diagonal case, and D4 closes.

So the concrete target is:

\[
\boxed{
\Pi_{\rm lin}(A_7)=
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\quad
\Pi_{\rm lin}(A_9)=
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Why off-diagonal terms should be lower order

A same-order term

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

inside \(A_7\) would mean the \(A_7\) row already sees the second anisotropy channel. That contradicts the apparent tower order:

\[
A_7\sim H\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
A_9\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Similarly, a same-order \(\Gamma_G\)-term inside \(A_9\) is a lower-channel contamination. It can be removed by a row operation using \(A_7\).

So the row hierarchy suggests:

\[
A_7:\quad \Gamma_G\text{ first channel},
\]

\[
A_9:\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\text{ first new channel}.
\]

This is a triangular associated-graded structure.

The proof-level statement should be:

\[
\operatorname{gr}(A_7)=\alpha_7 q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
\operatorname{gr}(A_9)\notin \operatorname{span}\{\operatorname{gr}(A_7)\},
\]

and specifically its new component is

\[
\alpha_9 q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If this associated-graded statement is true, no lower-order correction can cancel the determinant.

---

# 4. Associated-graded D4 theorem

## Theorem

Assume rows \(A_7,A_9\) admit expansions

\[
A_7
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\alpha_7\Gamma_G
+
B_7
\right)
+
E_7,
\]

\[
A_9
=
q_0u^3
\left(
\beta_9\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
+
B_9
\right)
+
E_9,
\]

where \(B_7,B_9\) are strictly higher in the row filtration or perturbative on the D4 sample set.

Assume

\[
|\alpha_7|,\ |\alpha_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then after the row operation

\[
\widetilde A_9=A_9-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}A_7,
\]

one has

\[
A_7=
q_0u^3\alpha_7\Gamma_G+\widetilde E_7,
\]

\[
\widetilde A_9=
q_0u^3\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}+\widetilde E_9,
\]

with polynomially controlled row-operation constants.

If

\[
|(\widetilde E_7,\widetilde E_9)|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3
\min(|\alpha_7|,|\alpha_9|)
|\Gamma|,
\]

then

\[
|(A_7,A_9)|\ge Q^{-C'}
\]

at every D4 sample.

This proves D4.

---

# 5. The exact finite computation needed

To make this theorem usable, compute only the following associated-graded coefficients:

\[
\alpha_7
=
[q_0u^3\Gamma_G]A_7,
\]

\[
\beta_7
=
[q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}]A_7,
\]

\[
\beta_9
=
[q_0u^3\Gamma_G]A_9,
\]

\[
\alpha_9
=
[q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}]A_9.
\]

Then compute

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9.
\]

D4 closes if

\[
|\Delta_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Expected values:

\[
\alpha_7=-\frac{c_7}{288},
\]

\[
\alpha_9=-\frac{c_9}{288},
\]

\[
\beta_7,\beta_9
\text{ perturbative or removable}.
\]

So expected determinant:

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}
+
\text{higher filtration}.
\]

---

# 6. Attack on possible determinant cancellation

Suppose the finite calculation gives

\[
\Delta_{7,9}=0.
\]

Then there are only three explanations.

## Case 1 — bad row pair

\(A_7,A_9\) are not enough. Add \(A_{11}\) and test

\[
\Delta_{7,11},
\qquad
\Delta_{9,11}.
\]

## Case 2 — hidden row dependence

All projected rows are measuring one scalar anisotropy combination:

\[
a(Y)\Gamma_G+b(Y)\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then Gate 2 is measuring more anisotropy than the row tower can see. This is a genuine row-architecture defect.

## Case 3 — wrong anisotropy basis

The rows observe a different pair

\[
\Lambda_1,\Lambda_2
\]

rather than

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Then redefine Gate 2 anisotropy to the row-observed pair, provided it is equivalent:

\[
|\Lambda_1|^2+|\Lambda_2|^2
\asymp_Q
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2.
\]

This is again a finite matrix equivalence problem.

---

# 7. D4 row-mobility after associated-graded closure

Once

\[
|(A_7,A_9)(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]

is proved at a D4 sample, row-energy follows from

\[
|(A_7,A_9)'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

The derivative bound follows from the same finite derivative package needed for Gate 2:

\[
q,q',q'',q''',q^{(4)},q^{(5)}
\]

plus row projection/gauge derivative bounds.

Then

\[
\int_I(|A_7|^2+|A_9|^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

So the row output is energy-level and compatible with downstream existential sampling.

---

# 8. Remaining proof obligations

D4 now has exactly four proof obligations:

1. **Associated-graded coefficient computation**

   \[
   \alpha_7,\beta_7,\beta_9,\alpha_9.
   \]

2. **Nonzero determinant**

   \[
   \alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9\ne0
   \]

   or extended minor nonvanishing with \(A_{11},A_{13}\).

3. **Residual half-leading estimate**

   \[
   |\mathbf E|\le\frac12\text{leading}.
   \]

4. **Row-mobility derivative bound**

   \[
   |\mathbf A'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
   \]

All four are local finite computations.

---

# 9. Attack conclusion

The D4 correction-control theorem is no longer a broad black box. It is equivalent to an associated-graded determinant calculation:

\[
\boxed{
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
[q_0u^3\Gamma_G]A_7 & [q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}]A_7\\
[q_0u^3\Gamma_G]A_9 & [q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}]A_9
\end{pmatrix}
\ne0.
}
\]

Expected answer:

\[
\boxed{
\det=\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}\ne0.
}
\]

If that expected determinant is confirmed, then D4 closes with \(A_7,A_9\) alone.

## Continuing attack — certify the D4 determinant by principal-symbol tests

The current D4 bottleneck is finite:

\[
\det L_{7,9}\neq0,
\]

where \(L_{7,9}\) is the coefficient matrix of \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\) in

\[
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f})/(q_0u^3).
\]

The expected leading rows are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

So the expected determinant is

\[
\det L_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}.
\]

The attack now is to turn that expectation into a checkable principal-symbol theorem. The downstream architecture currently treats this D4 row-conversion step as the local finite piece after Gate 2 and wall-escape sampling. 

---

# 1. Define the principal-symbol quotient

Work in the local row algebra and quotient by terms that are higher order relative to the D4 leading scale.

Let the D4 leading scale be

\[
\mathfrak m_{\rm D4}:=q_0u^3\cdot \operatorname{span}\{\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\}.
\]

Define

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A)
\]

to be the projection of a row \(A\) onto the coefficient of

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma_G
\quad\text{and}\quad
q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

modulo:

\[
\text{higher filtration terms},
\]

\[
\text{extra }q_0\text{-factors},
\]

\[
\text{canonical }E_2\text{/tail errors},
\]

\[
\text{quadratic or higher anisotropy terms}.
\]

Thus

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A)
=
(\ell_1(A),\ell_2(A))
\]

if

\[
A
=
q_0u^3
\bigl(\ell_1(A)\Gamma_G+\ell_2(A)\Gamma_{G,2}\bigr)
+
\text{higher}.
\]

Then

\[
L_{7,9}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_7)\\
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_9)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

D4 closes if

\[
\boxed{
\det L_{7,9}\neq0
}
\]

with polynomial margin.

---

# 2. Principal-symbol theorem sufficient for D4

The clean theorem is:

## Principal Row-Symbol Theorem

Assume

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_7)
=
\left(-\frac{c_7}{288},0\right),
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_9)
=
\left(0,-\frac{c_9}{288}\right),
\]

with

\[
|c_7c_9|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
\det L_{7,9}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2},
\]

and hence

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L_{7,9})\ge Q^{-C'}.
\]

If the residual satisfies

\[
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L_{7,9})|\Gamma|,
\]

then

\[
|(A_7,A_9)|\ge Q^{-C''}
\]

at every D4 sample.

So the entire D4 row-conversion problem is reduced to proving the two principal-symbol identities and the half-leading residual bound.

---

# 3. Calibration tests for the coefficients

Without full formulas, the most direct way to certify the principal symbols is to test the rows on two formal anisotropy calibrations.

## Calibration 1 — pure \(\Gamma_G\)

Set formally

\[
\Gamma_G=1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

and normalize

\[
q_0u^3=1.
\]

Then the principal symbols should give

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_7}{288}
+
\text{higher},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
0
+
\text{higher}.
\]

This certifies the first column:

\[
(\ell_{7,1},\ell_{9,1})
=
\left(-\frac{c_7}{288},0\right).
\]

## Calibration 2 — pure \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)

Set formally

\[
\Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=1,
\]

and again normalize

\[
q_0u^3=1.
\]

Then

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
0
+
\text{higher},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
-\frac{c_9}{288}
+
\text{higher}.
\]

This certifies the second column:

\[
(\ell_{7,2},\ell_{9,2})
=
\left(0,-\frac{c_9}{288}\right).
\]

These two calibration computations are enough. They avoid needing to understand every lower-order term.

---

# 4. What can still go wrong?

There are exactly four possible failures.

## Failure 1 — \(c_7=0\) or \(c_9=0\)

Then the displayed leading row is not genuinely leading. One must move to higher rows, likely \(A_{11}\) or \(A_{13}\).

## Failure 2 — same-filtration off-diagonal terms

The true principal symbols may be

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_7)=(\alpha_7,\beta_7),
\]

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_9)=(\beta_9,\alpha_9).
\]

Then D4 requires

\[
\Delta_{7,9}:=\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9
\]

to be polynomially nonzero.

This is still finite. If

\[
|\Delta_{7,9}|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

D4 closes.

## Failure 3 — determinant cancellation

If

\[
\Delta_{7,9}=0,
\]

then \(A_7,A_9\) observe only one anisotropy direction. Add rows and test minors:

\[
\Delta_{7,11},\quad \Delta_{9,11},\quad \Delta_{7,13},\quad\ldots
\]

D4 closes once any minor is nonzero.

## Failure 4 — residual not half-leading

Then the leading matrix is fine, but canonical/tail/projection corrections are too large. This is not an observability failure; it is an error-budget failure. It should be attacked by improving the canonical \(E_2\)/tail estimates or by absorbing more terms into \(L\).

---

# 5. Associated-graded row operations

If there is a lower-channel contamination in \(A_9\), i.e.

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_9)
=
(\beta_9,\alpha_9),
\]

but

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_7)
=
(\alpha_7,\beta_7),
\qquad
|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

perform the row operation

\[
\widetilde A_9
=
A_9-\frac{\beta_9}{\alpha_7}A_7.
\]

Then

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(\widetilde A_9)
=
\left(
0,
\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}
\right).
\]

The new coefficient is

\[
\frac{\det L_{7,9}}{\alpha_7}.
\]

So after row operations, the D4 test is:

\[
|\alpha_7|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

\[
\left|\alpha_9-\frac{\beta_9\beta_7}{\alpha_7}\right|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This row operation has polynomial condition number if

\[
|\beta_9/\alpha_7|\le Q^C.
\]

Thus same-filtration contamination is harmless unless it forces determinant cancellation.

---

# 6. Extend to a row family if needed

If \(A_7,A_9\) fail, define

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Let

\[
L_N
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_7)\\
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_9)\\
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_{11})\\
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_{13})
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

By Cauchy–Binet,

\[
\det(L_N^\ast L_N)
=
\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2.
\]

So if any

\[
\Delta_{ij}
\]

is polynomially nonzero, then

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Thus the extended-row proof target is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists i<j\in\{7,9,11,13\}:
|\Delta_{ij}|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Again finite.

---

# 7. D4 after principal-symbol certification

Assume the principal-symbol matrix \(L_N\) satisfies

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Then for D4 sample

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get:

\[
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If residuals are half-leading, then

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

With row mobility, this yields row energy:

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

So principal symbols plus half-leading residuals complete row conversion.

---

# 8. Immediate attack checklist

To finish D4, do the following in order:

1. Compute

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_7)
\]

and verify it has a nonzero \(\Gamma_G\) coefficient.

2. Compute

\[
\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_9)
\]

and verify it has a new nonzero \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) coefficient modulo \(A_7\).

3. If needed, compute \(\operatorname{psym}_{\rm D4}(A_{11})\), then \(A_{13}\).

4. Compute the first nonzero \(2\times2\) minor.

5. Prove the residual half-leading estimate.

This is now the exact finite row-audit required.

---

# 9. Conclusion

D4 is reduced to an associated-graded determinant calculation:

\[
\boxed{
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
[q_0u^3\Gamma_G]A_7 & [q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}]A_7\\
[q_0u^3\Gamma_G]A_9 & [q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}]A_9
\end{pmatrix}
\neq0.
}
\]

The expected determinant is

\[
\boxed{
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}.
}
\]

If confirmed, D4 closes with \(A_7,A_9\) alone.

If not, the fallback is the finite Cauchy–Binet minor audit over \(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13}\).

## Continuing attack — make the D4 proof a finite associated-graded certificate

The row-conversion layer is now concentrated in a finite symbolic question: do the principal row symbols of \(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) observe both anisotropy directions \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\)? The current downstream route is Gate 2, Wall-Escape Sampling, then D4 matrix row conversion. 

---

# 1. Build the associated-graded ring

Let the relevant local variables be

\[
q_0,\quad u=q''_{\can},\quad \Gamma_1=\Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

plus derivative/gauge/tail variables.

For D4, assign leading monomial

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma_i
\]

degree \(0\), and declare higher-order terms to be those with at least one extra small factor, for example:

\[
q_0^2u^3\Gamma_i,\qquad
q_0u^3\Gamma_i\Gamma_j,\qquad
q_0u^3E_2,\qquad
\text{tail/gauge remainders}.
\]

Define

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A)
\]

as the coefficient pair \((\ell_1,\ell_2)\) in

\[
A
=
q_0u^3(\ell_1\Gamma_G+\ell_2\Gamma_{G,2})
+
\text{higher}.
\]

Then D4 is exactly the statement that, for a finite row set,

\[
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_7)\\
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_9)\\
\vdots
\end{pmatrix}
\]

has rank \(2\) with polynomial margin.

---

# 2. Principal-symbol certificate

The expected leading identities are

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\text{higher},
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\text{higher},
\]

\[
H=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{higher}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_7)
=
\left(-\frac{c_7}{288},0\right),
\]

\[
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_9)
=
\left(0,-\frac{c_9}{288}\right).
\]

The associated-graded determinant is

\[
\Delta_{7,9}^{\rm gr}
=
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
-\frac{c_7}{288} & 0\\
0 & -\frac{c_9}{288}
\end{pmatrix}
=
\frac{c_7c_9}{288^2}.
\]

So the finite certificate is:

\[
\boxed{
c_7c_9\ne0.
}
\]

If this holds and the omitted terms are genuinely higher in the D4 filtration, then no correction can cancel the leading determinant.

---

# 3. Coefficient extraction by formal calibration

If the row formulas are available but complicated, \(c_7,c_9\) can be extracted by two formal calibrations.

## Calibration 1 — \(\Gamma_G\)-only

Set

\[
q_0u^3=1,\qquad \Gamma_G=1,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=0,
\]

and kill all higher-filtration variables.

Then

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=-\frac{c_7}{288},
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

This extracts the first column of \(L\).

## Calibration 2 — \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-only

Set

\[
q_0u^3=1,\qquad \Gamma_G=0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}=1.
\]

Then

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=-\frac{c_9}{288}.
\]

This extracts the second column.

If either off-diagonal coefficient appears in these calibrations, record it and compute the determinant

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
=
\alpha_7\alpha_9-\beta_7\beta_9.
\]

---

# 4. Residual half-leading estimate by filtration gap

Suppose a residual term \(T\) has one extra filtration factor. At a D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\Gamma^-},
\]

and the leading scale is

\[
S_{\rm lead}=|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

A residual term is harmless if

\[
|T|\le Q^{-K}S_{\rm lead}
\]

with

\[
K>C_L+O(1),
\]

where \(Q^{-C_L}\) is the lower bound for \(\sigma_{\min}(L)\).

Examples:

\[
T=q_0^2u^3\Gamma
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}\le |q_0|\le Q^{-C_q}.
\]

\[
T=q_0u^3E_2
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}\le \frac{|E_2|}{|\Gamma|}.
\]

So this is harmless if

\[
|E_2|\le Q^{-K}|\Gamma|.
\]

\[
T=q_0u^3\Gamma^2
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}\le |\Gamma|.
\]

This is harmless only if \(|\Gamma|\) is small. If \(|\Gamma|\) is merely polynomially bounded, such a term must not be treated as an error; it must either be absent, absorbed into a nonlinear row analysis, or controlled by a sharper local bound.

Thus the audit must separate:

\[
\boxed{
\text{extra }q_0\text{ or tail factors: perturbative;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale linear }\Gamma\text{ terms: absorb into }L;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{quadratic anisotropy terms: dangerous unless bounded or absent.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Robust D4 theorem

Let

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13})^T.
\]

Assume the associated-graded decomposition

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf E_N,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf E_N|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at every D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) or \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\), one gets

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This is now a finite symbolic/canonical verification problem.

---

# 6. If \(A_7,A_9\) fail

If the determinant

\[
\Delta_{7,9}
\]

vanishes, add rows. The rank condition is

\[
\det(L_N^\ast L_N)=\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

So the fallback finite tests are:

\[
\Delta_{7,11},\quad
\Delta_{9,11},\quad
\Delta_{7,13},\quad
\Delta_{9,13},\quad
\Delta_{11,13}.
\]

If all vanish, then the known rows observe only one anisotropy direction. That is a genuine row-architecture defect and would require either a different row family or a different Gate 2 anisotropy.

---

# 7. Final attack state

D4 is reduced to the following finite certificate:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{rank}
\begin{pmatrix}
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_7)\\
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_9)\\
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_{11})\\
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_{13})
\end{pmatrix}
=2
}
\]

with polynomial quantitative margin, plus half-leading residual control.

The most likely immediate close is:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_7)=(-c_7/288,0),\quad
\operatorname{gr}_{D4}(A_9)=(0,-c_9/288),\quad
c_7c_9\ne0.
}
\]

If confirmed, D4 closes with \(A_7,A_9\) alone.

## Continuing attack — remove dangerous D4 residuals by sampling into the small-anisotropy regime

The remaining D4 issue is not the leading determinant anymore. It is the possibility that residual terms such as

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma^2
\]

are same-scale or larger than the linear row term

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma.
\]

If such terms exist, they cannot simply be called “error” unless \(|\Gamma|\ll1\). I will now attack that by modifying the sampling: choose the D4 sample from a controlled-anisotropy layer, so nonlinear anisotropy terms become perturbative.

---

# 1. D4 row expansion with nonlinear anisotropy

Write the row vector as

\[
\mathbf A
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma
+
q_0u^3\mathcal Q_2(\Gamma,\Gamma)
+
q_0u^3\mathcal Q_{\ge3}(\Gamma)
+
\mathbf E_{\rm tail},
\]

where

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]

Here

\[
L
\]

is the linear anisotropy matrix, and the \(\mathcal Q_j\) terms are nonlinear in \(\Gamma\).

The old D4 half-leading condition was

\[
|\mathbf E|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

But if

\[
|\mathcal Q_2(\Gamma,\Gamma)|\sim |\Gamma|^2,
\]

then

\[
\frac{|q_0u^3\mathcal Q_2|}{|q_0u^3L\Gamma|}
\sim
\frac{|\Gamma|}{\sigma_{\min}(L)}.
\]

So nonlinear anisotropy terms are perturbative whenever

\[
|\Gamma|\le c\,\sigma_{\min}(L).
\]

Thus the row proof becomes clean if the D4 sample is chosen in a small-anisotropy layer:

\[
Q^{-C}\le |\Gamma|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma^-}
\]

with the upper threshold small enough.

---

# 2. Can Gate 2 provide a small-anisotropy D4 sample?

Gate 2 mass is

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

It does not by itself force \(|\Gamma|\) to be small. But if \(|\Gamma|\) is large, there are two possibilities.

## Case A — \(|\Gamma|\) is controlled above by a small polynomial threshold

If we can choose or prove

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma^-}
\]

on the sampling region, then nonlinear anisotropy is perturbative and D4 closes through the linear matrix \(L\).

## Case B — \(|\Gamma|\) is not small

If

\[
|\Gamma|\ge \gamma_0
\]

for some polynomial threshold, then Gate 2 mass plus \(|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A}\) may still be enough, but the row expansion must treat

\[
L\Gamma+\mathcal Q_2(\Gamma,\Gamma)+\cdots
\]

as a nonlinear polynomial in \(\Gamma\), not as a linear map.

That becomes a row-polynomial nonvanishing problem. It is finite, but more complex.

Therefore the best near-term attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{choose D4 samples where }\Gamma\text{ is polynomially small but nonzero.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Two-sided anisotropy sampling

Introduce thresholds

\[
\gamma_- = Q^{-C_-},
\qquad
\gamma_+ = Q^{-C_+},
\]

with

\[
\gamma_-\ll \gamma_+\ll1.
\]

Define the moderate anisotropy region

\[
I_{\Gamma,\mathrm{mod}}
=
\{m\in I:\gamma_-\le|\Gamma(m)|\le\gamma_+\}.
\]

If Gate 2 mass has nontrivial contribution there, then at a sample point

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-C},
\]

we have

\[
|\Gamma|\le\gamma_+,
\]

so nonlinear anisotropy terms are small, and

\[
|\Gamma|\ge\gamma_-
\]

so the linear leading term is not vanishing.

Then D4 closes through the principal linear matrix.

---

# 4. What if Gate 2 mass lies at large anisotropy?

Suppose instead Gate 2 mass is concentrated where

\[
|\Gamma|>\gamma_+.
\]

If \(\gamma_+\) is still polynomially small but not tiny, then this region may produce an even stronger downstream signal, but not necessarily through the linearized D4 theorem.

There are two options.

## Option 1 — nonlinear row conversion

Use the full polynomial row map

\[
\mathcal P(\Gamma)
=
L\Gamma+\mathcal Q_2(\Gamma,\Gamma)+\cdots.
\]

Prove

\[
|\mathcal P(\Gamma)|\ge Q^{-C}|\Gamma|
\]

on the large-anisotropy region.

This is finite algebra: prove no nonzero \(\Gamma\) in the relevant range is a common approximate root of the row polynomial.

## Option 2 — move to a first-entry point

If \(|\Gamma|\) becomes large somewhere, then moving from a small-\(\Gamma\) region to a large-\(\Gamma\) region gives a first-entry point where

\[
|\Gamma|=\gamma_+.
\]

At that first-entry point, \(|\Gamma|\) is exactly controlled:

\[
|\Gamma|=\gamma_+.
\]

If \(u\) and \(q_0\) remain live, D4 linearization applies.

This is analogous to wall escape.

Thus we can add an **anisotropy first-entry sampling theorem**.

---

# 5. Anisotropy first-entry theorem

Let

\[
m_0
\]

be a point with Gate 2 mass:

\[
|u(m_0)|^2|\Gamma(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Assume \(|\Gamma(m_0)|>\gamma_+\).

If there is a nearby point in the same component where \(|\Gamma|<\gamma_+\), then by continuity there is

\[
m_1
\]

with

\[
|\Gamma(m_1)|=\gamma_+.
\]

If \(u,q_0\) do not vary too much between \(m_0\) and \(m_1\), then \(m_1\) is a controlled D4 sample.

If no such point exists, then

\[
|\Gamma|\ge\gamma_+
\]

throughout a component. In that case the row-polynomial map must be controlled in the large-anisotropy regime, or Gate 2 itself is very strong on that component.

So the remaining large-anisotropy branch is either controlled by first-entry sampling or by nonlinear row observability.

---

# 6. D4 linearization theorem with anisotropy control

We can now state a sharper D4 theorem.

## Controlled-Anisotropy D4 Theorem

Assume

\[
\mathbf A
=
q_0u^3
\left(
L\Gamma+\mathcal Q_{\ge2}(\Gamma)
\right)
+
\mathbf E_{\rm tail}.
\]

Assume

\[
\sigma_2(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Assume for \(|\Gamma|\le\gamma_+\),

\[
|\mathcal Q_{\ge2}(\Gamma)|
\le
\frac14\sigma_2(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

This holds, for example, if

\[
|\Gamma|\le cQ^{-C_L}
\]

and the nonlinear coefficients are polynomially bounded.

Assume

\[
|\mathbf E_{\rm tail}|
\le
\frac14|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf A|
\ge
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Thus at a sample with

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma|\le\gamma_+,
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This version absorbs nonlinear anisotropy safely.

---

# 7. How to guarantee controlled anisotropy at wall-escape samples

At the wall-escape point \(m_1\), we already know

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

But we also need an upper bound

\[
|\Gamma(m_1)|\le\gamma_+.
\]

We can ensure this by choosing \(m_0\) from a moderate-anisotropy Gate 2 layer, or by a global upper bound if \(\gamma_+\) is allowed polynomially large.

For nonlinear perturbation, however, \(\gamma_+\) must be small enough.

So split the wall-live region further:

\[
W_{\rm mod}
=
\{|q|<\varepsilon,\ |u|\ge\tau,\ |\Gamma|\le\gamma_+\},
\]

\[
W_{\rm large}
=
\{|q|<\varepsilon,\ |u|\ge\tau,\ |\Gamma|>\gamma_+\}.
\]

If \(W_{\rm mod}\) carries Gate 2 mass, wall escape gives a controlled D4 sample.

If \(W_{\rm large}\) carries Gate 2 mass, use anisotropy first-entry or nonlinear row observability.

This is the clean split.

---

# 8. Is nonlinear anisotropy actually present?

It may be absent from the row expansion at the relevant order. If the rows are genuinely linear in \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), then the whole moderate/large split is unnecessary.

The original displayed structure

\[
A_7\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

suggests the row architecture is linear in anisotropy at leading order.

So the finite audit should answer:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do terms }q_0u^3\Gamma^2\text{ appear at the same row order?}
}
\]

If no, D4 is simpler.

If yes, use the controlled-anisotropy split above.

---

# 9. Revised D4 audit checklist

Add one new classification to the D4 audit.

For every row term after extracting \(q_0u^3\), classify it as:

1. **linear anisotropy**: goes into \(L\Gamma\);

2. **quadratic/higher anisotropy**: goes into \(\mathcal Q_{\ge2}\);

3. **tail/gauge/canonical error**: goes into \(\mathbf E_{\rm tail}\);

4. **wall-live term not divisible by \(q_0\)**: goes to D3 direct row;

5. **extra \(q_0\)-small term**: perturbative.

Then prove either:

\[
\mathcal Q_{\ge2}=0
\]

at the D4 row order, or

\[
|\mathcal Q_{\ge2}(\Gamma)|\le\frac14\sigma_2(L)|\Gamma|
\]

on the sampling region.

---

# 10. Attack conclusion

The D4 correction problem has one hidden subtlety: nonlinear anisotropy terms.

We can handle it by either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{show nonlinear anisotropy is absent/lower order;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{sample in a controlled-anisotropy layer;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove nonlinear row-polynomial observability.}
}
\]

The simplest expected path remains:

\[
A_7,A_9
\]

are linear triangular rows at leading order, with no same-order nonlinear anisotropy.

If confirmed, D4 closes.
