_Thought for 13s_

## Continuing attack — quantitative nonzero root-trap rigidity

I’ll now attack the remaining D4 nonlinear-root branch quantitatively.

The problematic branch after triangularization is:

\[
X:=\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
Y:=\Gamma_{G,2}\approx \zeta\ne0.
\]

The exact equations are

\[
X=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
Y=2q(q')^2-\frac16X''.
\]

The goal is to show that \(X\approx0\) and \(Y\approx\zeta\ne0\) cannot persist on a polynomial-length interval. If this is true, then any nonzero row-polynomial root of the triangularized \(A_9\) row cannot create a genuine D4 obstruction under existential row sampling. This is directly aligned with the current downstream plan: Gate 2 plus Wall-Escape Sampling plus D4 row conversion. 

---

# 1. Exact rigidity, sharpened

Assume first

\[
X\equiv0,
\qquad
Y\equiv\zeta\ne0
\]

on an interval.

Then

\[
q''=6q-2q^3,
\]

and since \(X''=0\),

\[
Y=2q(q')^2=\zeta.
\]

Differentiate:

\[
(2q(q')^2)'=0.
\]

So

\[
2q'(q')^2+4qq'q''=0,
\]

hence

\[
2q'\bigl((q')^2+2qq''\bigr)=0.
\]

If \(q'\equiv0\), then

\[
Y=0,
\]

contradiction. So on a subinterval with \(q'\ne0\),

\[
(q')^2+2qq''=0.
\]

Substitute

\[
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
(q')^2+12q^2-4q^4=0,
\]

so

\[
(q')^2=4q^2(q^2-3).
\]

Differentiate:

\[
2q'q''=(16q^3-24q)q'.
\]

Since \(q'\ne0\),

\[
q''=8q^3-12q.
\]

Compare with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3.
\]

Therefore

\[
6q-2q^3=8q^3-12q,
\]

so

\[
18q-10q^3=0,
\]

hence

\[
q^2=\frac95
\]

because \(q\ne0\). But then

\[
(q')^2=4q^2(q^2-3)
=
4\cdot\frac95\left(\frac95-3\right)<0,
\]

impossible for real \(q\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
X\equiv0,\quad Y\equiv\zeta\ne0
\quad\text{on an interval is impossible.}
}
\]

This exact rigidity is strong enough to attack the root-trap branch.

---

# 2. Quantitative version to prove

The desired quantitative theorem is:

## Nonzero Root-Trap Rigidity

Let

\[
|\zeta|\ge Q^{-C_\zeta}.
\]

Assume on an interval \(J\),

\[
|X|\le \varepsilon,
\qquad
|Y-\zeta|\le \varepsilon,
\]

with polynomial derivative bounds

\[
\max_{0\le k\le 4}|q^{(k)}|\le Q^C.
\]

Then either

\[
|J|\le Q^C\varepsilon^c,
\]

or one obtains a contradiction once \(\varepsilon\) is chosen sufficiently small relative to \(Q^{-C_\zeta}\).

Equivalently, on any polynomial-length interval,

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J |X|+\sup_J|Y-\zeta|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This says nonzero row-root traps cannot occupy the intervals produced by Gate 2 extraction.

---

# 3. Avoiding pointwise \(X''\): integrate the \(Y\)-equation

The identity

\[
Y=2q(q')^2-\frac16X''
\]

contains \(X''\), so pointwise smallness of \(X\) does not immediately control \(Y\). The fix is to integrate against cutoffs, exactly like the Gate 2 integral-rigidity strategy.

Let \(\phi\in C_c^\infty(J)\), \(\phi\equiv1\) on \(J'\Subset J\), with

\[
|\phi^{(j)}|\le C_j |J|^{-j}.
\]

From

\[
Y-\zeta
=
2q(q')^2-\zeta-\frac16X'',
\]

multiply by \(\phi\) and integrate:

\[
\int \phi(2q(q')^2-\zeta)
=
\int \phi(Y-\zeta)+\frac16\int \phi X''.
\]

Integrating by parts,

\[
\int \phi X''
=
\int \phi'' X.
\]

Thus

\[
\left|
\int \phi(2q(q')^2-\zeta)
\right|
\le
\varepsilon\int|\phi|
+
\frac16\varepsilon\int|\phi''|.
\]

With packet-normalized coordinates and polynomial cutoff losses, this gives

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\int_{J'}(2q(q')^2-\zeta)
\right|
\le Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
}
\]

So in averaged form,

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

must be close to the nonzero constant \(\zeta\).

In particular, on a large subinterval, \(q\) cannot be too small:

\[
|q|\gtrsim Q^{-C_\zeta-C}
\]

unless \((q')^2\) is enormous, which is excluded by derivative bounds.

---

# 4. Derive approximate algebraic contradiction

From

\[
X=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

small \(X\) gives

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon).
\]

In averaged or pointwise form, this is a perturbed autonomous ODE.

The root-trap condition also says, averaged,

\[
2q(q')^2=\zeta+O(Q^C\varepsilon).
\]

Differentiate the latter formally:

\[
2q'\bigl((q')^2+2qq''\bigr)=O(Q^C\varepsilon)
\]

in distribution / averaged sense.

The exact contradiction came from the pair:

\[
q''=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
(q')^2+2qq''=0.
\]

In the approximate case, we get

\[
(q')^2+2q(6q-2q^3)=O(Q^C\varepsilon/|q'|)
\]

where \(q'\) is not too small.

But if \(q'\) is too small, then

\[
2q(q')^2
\]

cannot approximate \(\zeta\ne0\). Hence \(q'\) is also polynomially non-small on a large set.

Thus, on a large set,

\[
(q')^2=4q^2(q^2-3)+O(Q^C\varepsilon).
\]

Differentiating this relation gives

\[
q''=8q^3-12q+O(Q^C\varepsilon).
\]

Compare with

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon).
\]

Then

\[
10q^3-18q=O(Q^C\varepsilon),
\]

so

\[
q^2=\frac95+O(Q^C\varepsilon),
\]

because \(q\ne0\).

Plugging into

\[
(q')^2=4q^2(q^2-3)+O(Q^C\varepsilon)
\]

gives

\[
(q')^2
=
4\cdot\frac95\left(\frac95-3\right)+O(Q^C\varepsilon)
=
-\frac{216}{25}+O(Q^C\varepsilon).
\]

For

\[
\varepsilon\ll Q^{-C},
\]

this is impossible over the reals.

This is the quantitative skeleton.

---

# 5. A cleaner proof route: finite algebraic resultant

The exact contradiction can be encoded algebraically.

The exact root-trap equations imply the polynomial system

\[
q''=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
2q(q')^2=\zeta,
\]

and, after differentiating the second equation,

\[
(q')^2+2qq''=0.
\]

Eliminate \(q''\) using the first equation:

\[
(q')^2+12q^2-4q^4=0.
\]

Now combine this with

\[
2q(q')^2=\zeta.
\]

Eliminate \((q')^2\):

\[
2q(4q^4-12q^2)=\zeta,
\]

so

\[
8q^5-24q^3-\zeta=0.
\]

The differentiated compatibility also forced

\[
q^2=\frac95.
\]

Substitute into

\[
8q^5-24q^3-\zeta=0.
\]

This gives a finite set of possible \(\zeta\)-values. But the earlier sign contradiction shows no real solution because \((q')^2<0\).

For complex-valued \(q\), the contradiction may fail. Then the theorem must use real-valuedness of \(q_0\) on the real line. If \(q\) is complex, one must work with real and imaginary parts and the positivity of \((q')^2\) is lost. In the current real row-conversion geometry, \(q_0\) appears to be real; this should be explicitly assumed.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Nonzero root-trap rigidity is a real-trajectory theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Consequence for D4 row roots

Suppose the triangularized D4 rows have a nonzero common root

\[
Y=\zeta\ne0.
\]

A persistent D4 failure would require

\[
X=\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
Y=\Gamma_{G,2}\approx \zeta
\]

on a polynomial interval, because isolated failures can be avoided by row mobility/existential sampling.

But Nonzero Root-Trap Rigidity says this is impossible on a polynomial interval.

Thus the common root does not obstruct energetic row conversion.

At worst, it creates isolated or very short bad subintervals. Their contribution can be discarded if row energy is the target.

---

# 7. Row-energy version

Let the bad root set be

\[
\mathcal B_\zeta
=
\{m\in I: |X(m)|\le\varepsilon,\ |Y(m)-\zeta|\le\varepsilon\}.
\]

Nonzero Root-Trap Rigidity should imply

\[
|\mathcal B_\zeta|
\le Q^C\varepsilon^c |I|
\]

or a comparable smallness bound.

If the row polynomial is non-small outside the union of finitely many such \(\mathcal B_\zeta\), then

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A|^2
\]

is controlled from below outside small bad sets.

This turns root traps into negligible exceptional sets.

Thus D4 can be closed in row-energy form even if pointwise roots exist.

---

# 8. Updated D4 theorem with root traps

## D4 with Root-Trap Rigidity

Assume after triangularization,

\[
B_7=X+E_7,
\]

\[
B_9=YR_Y(Y)+X(\cdots)+E_9,
\]

and \(R_Y\) has finitely many nonzero roots

\[
\zeta_1,\ldots,\zeta_s.
\]

Assume:

1. \(Y=0\) is excluded by Gate 2 mass when \(X\) is small;

2. each nonzero root trap

\[
X\approx0,\quad Y\approx\zeta_j
\]

has measure at most \(Q^C\varepsilon^c|I|\);

3. row mobility/energy formulation allows discarding these small exceptional sets;

4. errors are half-leading outside the exceptional sets.

Then

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

This closes D4 even when \(R_Y\) has nonzero roots.

---

# 9. What remains to prove

The main remaining lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Quantitative Nonzero Root-Trap Rigidity.}
}
\]

This is a local real-variable theorem using

\[
X=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
Y=2q(q')^2-\frac16X''.
\]

It is very similar in spirit to the Gate 2 integral-rigidity lemma, but centered at

\[
Y=\zeta\ne0
\]

rather than

\[
Y=0.
\]

The proof likely uses the same integration-by-parts machinery, with the extra nonzero constant \(\zeta\) creating an algebraic impossibility.

---

# 10. Attack conclusion

The D4 nonlinear-root obstruction is not fatal.

A nonzero row root would force the trajectory into

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\approx\zeta\ne0.
\]

But the defining ODE identities make such a state impossible on an interval for real \(q\).

Thus D4 can likely be closed by:

\[
\boxed{
\text{triangular row structure}
+
\text{root-trap rigidity}
+
\text{row-energy/existential sampling}.
}
\]

This is now a local real-variable problem, not a global row-algebra mystery.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 11:41:41)

_Thought for 14s_

## Continuing attack — prove nonzero root-trap rigidity by an energy identity

The remaining nonlinear D4 obstruction is now very specific:

\[
X:=\Gamma_G\approx0,\qquad
Y:=\Gamma_{G,2}\approx\zeta\ne0.
\]

If this trap cannot persist on a polynomial-size interval, then nonzero roots of the triangularized D4 row polynomial are harmless under existential / energetic row sampling. I will now attack this by deriving a quantitative energy contradiction from the exact identities

\[
X=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
Y=2q(q')^2-\frac16X''.
\]

This is a local real-variable attack on the residual D4 root branch. The downstream context is still Gate 2 plus Wall-Escape Sampling plus D4 matrix / row conversion. 

---

# 1. Use the autonomous energy for \(X=0\)

Define

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
X=q''-F(q).
\]

For the exact equation

\[
q''=F(q),
\]

there is a conserved energy. Multiply by \(q'\):

\[
q'q''=q'(6q-2q^3).
\]

Thus

\[
\frac{d}{dm}\left(
\frac12(q')^2-3q^2+\frac12q^4
\right)=0.
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal E(q,q')
=
\frac12(q')^2-3q^2+\frac12q^4.
\]

When \(X\neq0\),

\[
q''=F(q)+X,
\]

so

\[
\mathcal E'
=
q'X.
\]

Therefore if \(X\) is small on an interval and \(q'\) is polynomially bounded, \(\mathcal E\) is almost conserved:

\[
|\mathcal E(m)-\mathcal E(m_0)|
\le Q^C\|X\|_{L^\infty(J)}|J|.
\]

This gives a stable replacement for exact ODE conservation.

---

# 2. Express the root trap as a second constraint

The root trap says

\[
Y\approx\zeta,
\qquad
|\zeta|\ge Q^{-C_\zeta}.
\]

Since

\[
Y=2q(q')^2-\frac16X'',
\]

the difficult term is \(X''\). But distributionally, on an interval with cutoff \(\phi\),

\[
\int \phi \left(2q(q')^2-\zeta\right)
=
\int \phi(Y-\zeta)+\frac16\int \phi X''.
\]

Integrating by parts twice,

\[
\int \phi X''=\int \phi''X.
\]

Hence if

\[
|X|\le\varepsilon,
\qquad
|Y-\zeta|\le\varepsilon
\]

on \(J\), then

\[
\left|
\int \phi \left(2q(q')^2-\zeta\right)
\right|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon |J|
\]

for standard packet-scale cutoffs.

So the trap implies, in an averaged sense,

\[
2q(q')^2\approx \zeta.
\]

This already forces \(q\) and \(q'\) not to vanish on most of \(J\), because \(\zeta\neq0\).

---

# 3. Convert averaged nonzero \(Y\) into lower bounds for \(q\) and \(q'\)

Assume polynomial upper bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|\le Q^C.
\]

If

\[
|2q(q')^2-\zeta|\le \varepsilon
\]

on a large subset and

\[
|\zeta|\ge Q^{-C_\zeta},
\]

then on that subset,

\[
|q|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|q'|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
|2q(q')^2|
\ge \frac12|\zeta|
\]

for \(\varepsilon\ll|\zeta|\). Since \(|q|,|q'|\le Q^C\), neither factor can be super-polynomially small.

Thus on most of the root-trap interval we may divide by \(q\) and \(q'\) with only polynomial losses.

This is important because the exact contradiction used divisions by \(q\) and \(q'\).

---

# 4. Derive approximate algebraic incompatibility

The exact trap produced two equations:

\[
q''=6q-2q^3,
\]

\[
2q(q')^2=\zeta.
\]

Differentiate the second:

\[
2q'\left((q')^2+2qq''\right)=0.
\]

Since \(q'\neq0\), this gives

\[
(q')^2+2qq''=0.
\]

In the approximate setting, if \(2q(q')^2-\zeta\) is nearly constant on a thick interval, then its derivative is small in a weak or averaged sense. On the region where \(q'\) is polynomially non-small, this gives

\[
(q')^2+2qq''
=
O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

Substitute

\[
q''=6q-2q^3+X.
\]

Then

\[
(q')^2+12q^2-4q^4
=
O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

So

\[
(q')^2
=
4q^4-12q^2+O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

Now differentiate this approximate identity on a slightly smaller interval. Using \(q'\) polynomially non-small,

\[
q''
=
8q^3-12q+O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

But from \(X\approx0\),

\[
q''
=
6q-2q^3+O(\varepsilon).
\]

Compare:

\[
6q-2q^3
=
8q^3-12q+O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

Thus

\[
18q-10q^3=O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

Since \(q\) is polynomially nonzero,

\[
q^2=\frac95+O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

Substitute into

\[
(q')^2
=
4q^2(q^2-3)+O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

Then

\[
(q')^2
=
4\cdot\frac95\left(\frac95-3\right)
+
O(Q^C\varepsilon^c)
=
-\frac{216}{25}
+
O(Q^C\varepsilon^c).
\]

For \(\varepsilon\le Q^{-C'}\) sufficiently small, this is impossible for real \(q'\).

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
X\approx0,\quad Y\approx\zeta\ne0
\text{ cannot persist on a polynomial interval.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Avoid differentiating noisy quantities: use finite differences

The preceding derivation differentiates the approximate equation

\[
2q(q')^2\approx\zeta.
\]

A rigorous proof can avoid pointwise differentiation by using finite differences.

Let \(s\) be a small step with

\[
Q^{-C}|J|\le s\le |J|.
\]

If

\[
2q(q')^2\approx \zeta
\]

at \(m\) and \(m+s\), then

\[
\frac{2q(q')^2(m+s)-2q(q')^2(m)}{s}\approx0.
\]

By Taylor expansion,

\[
\frac{d}{dm}\left(2q(q')^2\right)
=
2q'\left((q')^2+2qq''\right)
\]

up to controlled \(O(s)\) errors.

Since \(q'\) is polynomially non-small on a large set, this yields

\[
(q')^2+2qq''\approx0
\]

on a large subset.

This finite-difference version only needs derivative bounds through \(q^{(3)}\) or \(q^{(4)}\), which are already part of the Gate 2 integral-rigidity package.

---

# 6. Root-trap measure bound

The desired rigorous output is a measure estimate.

Let

\[
\mathcal B_{\zeta,\varepsilon}
=
\{m\in J: |X(m)|\le\varepsilon,\ |Y(m)-\zeta|\le\varepsilon\}.
\]

For

\[
|\zeta|\ge Q^{-C_\zeta},
\]

prove

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal B_{\zeta,\varepsilon}|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^c |J|
}
\]

or at least that \(\mathcal B_{\zeta,\varepsilon}\) contains no subinterval of length \(Q^{-C}|J|\).

This is sufficient for row-energy D4 because bad root-trap neighborhoods cannot carry polynomial row-energy obstruction.

The proof uses:

1. \(X\approx0\Rightarrow q''\approx6q-2q^3\);
2. \(Y-\zeta\approx0\Rightarrow 2q(q')^2\approx\zeta\) weakly;
3. finite differences imply the differentiated compatibility relation;
4. algebraic sign contradiction.

---

# 7. Consequence for triangular D4 roots

Suppose the triangularized D4 row polynomial has roots

\[
\zeta_1,\ldots,\zeta_s\neq0
\]

in the \(Y\)-coordinate.

The bad row set is contained in

\[
\bigcup_j
\{|\Gamma_G|\le\varepsilon,\ |\Gamma_{G,2}-\zeta_j|\le\varepsilon\}
\]

plus the harmless \(Y=0\) branch.

By the root-trap measure estimate, each nonzero root neighborhood has small measure. Thus these bad sets can be removed without losing row-energy mass.

Outside them, the triangular row system gives

\[
|\mathbf A|\ge Q^{-C}|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

Therefore D4 row-energy lower bound survives.

This means even if \(P_9(Y)\) has nonzero roots, they are dynamically negligible.

---

# 8. Stronger conclusion: no need for higher rows if root traps are unstable

Previously we needed \(A_{11},A_{13}\) to kill nonzero roots of \(P_9\). But the ODE rigidity shows a persistent nonzero root trap is impossible.

Therefore \(A_7,A_9\) may suffice even if \(P_9\) has nonzero roots, provided:

1. the only zeros are isolated nonzero \(Y\)-values;
2. row conversion is energetic/existential;
3. root-trap neighborhoods are small by the rigidity estimate.

This is stronger than the Euclidean gcd route.

The gcd route remains useful for exact pointwise row lower bounds, but for row energy, root-trap rigidity is enough.

---

# 9. Updated D4 closure theorem

## D4 with Nonzero Root-Trap Rigidity

Assume after triangularization,

\[
B_7=c_7X+E_7,
\]

\[
B_9=Y R_Y(Y)+X S(X,Y)+E_9,
\]

with

\[
c_7\ne0
\]

and \(R_Y\) a finite polynomial.

Assume:

1. \(Y=0\) is excluded by Gate 2 mass when \(X\approx0\);

2. for every nonzero root \(\zeta\) of \(R_Y\), the root-trap set

\[
|X|\le\varepsilon,\quad |Y-\zeta|\le\varepsilon
\]

has measure at most \(Q^C\varepsilon^c|I|\);

3. errors are half-leading outside these small exceptional sets;

4. row output is energetic.

Then

\[
\int_I(|A_7|^2+|A_9|^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

Thus D4 closes with \(A_7,A_9\) alone under root-trap rigidity.

---

# 10. Remaining technical theorem

The only serious new lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Quantitative Nonzero Root-Trap Rigidity}
}
\]

for the pair

\[
X=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
Y=2q(q')^2-\frac16X''.
\]

This lemma is local, real-variable, and likely provable with the same cutoff / integration-by-parts methods as the Gate 2 integral-rigidity lemma.

If proved, D4 is robust even under nonlinear triangular row corrections.

---

# 11. Attack conclusion

The D4 nonlinear root issue is not fatal.

A nonzero row-polynomial root forces the trajectory into

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx\zeta\ne0.
\]

The real ODE identities make such a trap impossible on intervals.

Therefore, under energetic/existential row sampling, nonzero roots are negligible, and \(A_7,A_9\) likely still suffice.

## Agent 4 / D — Wall escape, wall-to-annulus, and row-energy admissibility

Executing Agent 4’s lane: prove the strongest admissible wall-resolution statement

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + wall escape + D4 + row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

The current downstream architecture replaces the old \(D1/D2/D3\) stack with \(G2\)-A, \(G2\)-B, \(D3a\) wall escape, and \(D4\) matrix row conversion. 

---

# 1. Wall split

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

and

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\qquad
G(m)=|u(m)|^2|\Gamma(m)|^2.
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Split

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{m\in I: |q(m)|\ge \varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

---

# 2. Non-wall branch

Assume

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G(m)\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume a polynomial upper bound

\[
G(m)\le Q^{C_G}.
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

such that

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

At \(m_\ast\),

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge \varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Thus \(m_\ast\) is a non-wall D4 sample:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2|\Gamma(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If D4 matrix row conversion and correction control hold at non-wall samples, then

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C'},
\]

where

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix}
\]

or the enlarged row vector used in D4.

---

# 3. Wall branch: remove low-source points

Assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G(m)\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Fix

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

Assume the anisotropy upper bound

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Then on \(I_{\rm wall,low}\),

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le \tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|
\le
\frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

So the live wall strip is nonempty and carries polynomial Gate 2 mass.

---

# 4. First-exit wall escape

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Then

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Assume

\[
|u'(m)|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

In normalized coordinates on \(I\), this is

\[
|\dot u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

Define the escape radius

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\frac{\varepsilon}{\tau}}
=
C Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

Require

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

This is equivalent to

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Then on the local interval

\[
[m_0-\rho|I|,\,m_0+\rho|I|]\cap I,
\]

one has

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

the function \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave there.

A uniformly convex/concave function with

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon
\]

cannot remain in the strip

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for distance larger than

\[
O\!\left(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\right)=O(\rho).
\]

Thus, provided \(m_0\) is not trapped at the packet boundary, there exists a first-exit point

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho |I|,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

---

# 5. Signal survival at first exit

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Since

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau,
\]

and \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\), we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q(m_1)|-2|q(m_1)|^3
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)
=
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

So

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

Also

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 6. Boundary-layer handling

The first-exit argument requires an interior point. Define the boundary layer

\[
I_{\rm bd}
=
\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho |I|.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

we have

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G(m)\,dm
\le
2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so that

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|
\le
\frac18Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\rho\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)},
\]

i.e.

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

Together with the convexity-stability condition, it suffices to take

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
}
\]

Then the boundary layer cannot carry all wall-live Gate 2 mass, so an interior \(m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}\setminus I_{\rm bd}\) exists and first-exit escape applies.

---

# 7. D3a theorem: wall escape gives a D4 sample

## Theorem: Wall-Escape Sampling

Assume:

\[
\int_I G\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Choose \(\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}\) and \(\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}\) with

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1),
\]

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
\]

Then there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2|\Gamma(m_\ast)|^2
\ge Q^{-C},
\]

where \(C\) is polynomial in the displayed exponents.

Thus \(m_\ast\) is a valid non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 8. D4 input at the escaped sample

At \(m_\ast\), D4 requires the row normal form

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R
\]

or the enlarged-row version

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N.
\]

If

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|,
\]

then

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\ge
\frac12|q_0(m_\ast)|\,|u(m_\ast)|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma(m_\ast)|.
\]

Since

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma(m_\ast)|\ge |\Gamma_G(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1)}.
\]

So

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

---

# 9. Row mobility: pointwise sample to row energy

Assume the row derivative bound

\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

then for

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le c Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|,
\]

one has

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Thus there is an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]

such that

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\quad(m\in J_\ast).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

So existential row sampling implies row energy.

For weighted packet norms, the same proof works after selecting \(m_\ast\) in the interior region where the packet weight is \(\ge Q^{-C}\), which is compatible with the boundary-layer exclusion above.

---

# 10. Exact-point failure mode

If the downstream contradiction requires a row lower bound at a preassigned point \(m_0\), then wall escape is insufficient.

In that exact-point architecture, one must use the fallback:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil / ideal-generation audit}
\]

or find a source-robust row

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

But if the downstream output is existential or energetic, Wall-Escape Sampling is admissible.

Given Gate 2 is an interval-energy statement, the row-energy formulation is the natural one.

---

# 11. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall escape is admissible for row energy / existential downstream output.}
}
\]

The wall-resolution module becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 row conversion}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

The only remaining conditions are local and finite:

1. polynomial bounds for \(G,\Gamma,u'\);
2. D4 principal-symbol rank and projected-residual correction control;
3. row derivative bound for mobility;
4. packet interior / weight control.

No exact source-robust row at \(q_0=0\) is needed unless the final architecture is exact-point locked.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:17:46)

## Continuing attack — close D3a as a row-energy theorem, with all losses explicit

I’ll now consolidate the wall-escape branch into a final row-energy theorem. The aim is to show that the \(q_0\)-wall no longer needs a source-robust row if the downstream contradiction accepts an interval row-energy lower bound. This matches the current downstream architecture:

\[
\text{Gate 2}+\text{D3a Wall-Escape Sampling}+\text{D4}+\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound / row energy}.
\]

---

# 1. Inputs

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\qquad
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I G\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Assume D4 row conversion has the form

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12|q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Assume row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

---

# 2. Choose wall and source thresholds

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so that low-source points cannot carry Gate 2 mass:

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so that wall escape is stable and boundary layers are negligible:

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\rho:=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2+O(1)}
\]

satisfies both

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le \frac14\tau
\]

and

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho\le Q^{-A-O(1)}.
\]

---

# 3. Non-wall mass gives D4 directly

Split

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q|\ge\varepsilon\},
\qquad
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then since \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), there exists \(m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}\) with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

At this point,

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge \varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Using D4,

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\ge
\frac12|q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Since

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2,
\]

we have

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-(A+C_G+O(1))/2}.
\]

To use D4 directly, we need either an explicit lower bound for \(|u|\), or an anisotropy upper bound. Since

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-(A+C_G)/2-C_\Gamma-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]

for some polynomial exponent \(C_A\).

Then row mobility gives row energy:

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

So the non-wall branch closes.

---

# 4. Wall mass also gives a non-wall sample

Assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Remove low-source points:

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\}.
\]

On this set,

\[
G\le \tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

By the choice of \(C_\tau\),

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,low}}G\le \frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Therefore the live wall region

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
\{|q|<\varepsilon,\ |u|\ge\tau\}
\]

carries mass:

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G\ge \frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Boundary layer:

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho|I|\}
\]

has contribution at most

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G\le 2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|
\le \frac18Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Hence there exists

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}\setminus I_{\rm bd}.
\]

At \(m_0\),

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Because

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}
\]

and

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le \frac14\tau,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau
\]

for

\[
|m-m_0|\le \rho|I|.
\]

Since \(u=q''\), \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave there. Thus \(q\) exits the wall strip within distance \(O(\rho|I|)\). There exists \(m_1\in I\) such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho|I|,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

At \(m_1\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Because \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\),

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)=|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge |u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

So

\[
|q(m_1)|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

This is a non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 5. D4 at the escaped point

At \(m_1\),

\[
|q|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Thus

\[
|q|\,|u|^3|\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|
\ge
\frac12
|q|\,|u|^3
\sigma_2(L_N)
|\Gamma|
\ge
Q^{-C_A},
\]

where

\[
C_A=C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

---

# 6. Row mobility gives row energy

Assume

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

From

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\]

whenever

\[
|m-m_1|\le cQ^{-C_A-C_D}|I|.
\]

So there exists an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\]

on \(J_\ast\). Therefore

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

This is the desired row-energy output.

---

# 7. Final theorem

## Wall-Escape + D4 Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le\frac12|q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|,
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|
}
\]

for some polynomial exponent \(C\).

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + Wall-Escape Sampling + D4 + row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

---

# 8. What remains after this theorem

The wall branch is now closed **modulo finite local estimates**:

1. upper bounds for \(G,\Gamma,u'\);
2. D4 row normal form and principal-symbol rank;
3. D4 projected residual half-leading bound;
4. row derivative bound.

The source-robust wall row and \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil become fallback tools only if row-energy / existential sampling is not accepted downstream.

Thus the downstream chain is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + D4 finite row audit + wall escape}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

The main remaining proof work is no longer conceptual; it is finite verification of the local derivative and row-symbol/correction bounds.

## Agent 4 / D — D3a wall escape and row-energy admissibility

Executing Agent 4’s lane: prove the downstream implication

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall Escape}
+
\text{D4}
+
\text{Row Mobility}
\Rightarrow
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

The latest update replaces the older \(D1/D2/D3\) structure with source-large interval extraction, \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity, D3a wall escape, D4 row-span conversion, and row mobility. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and

\[
G(m)=|u(m)|^2|\Gamma(m)|^2.
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I G(m)\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume polynomial upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Let the D4 row vector be

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},\ldots,A_{2N+1})^T.
\]

Assume D4 gives, at every non-wall sample,

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Assume row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

---

# 2. Non-wall branch

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{m\in I: |q(m)|\ge \varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{m\in I: |q(m)|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G(m)\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then, since \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

such that

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

and

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2|\Gamma(m_\ast)|^2\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

Using \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\),

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A-C_G-2C_\Gamma-O(1)}.
\]

Therefore D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\ge
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Since

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-(A+C_G+O(1))/2},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|
\ge
Q^{-C_A}
\]

for

\[
C_A
=
C_\varepsilon+C_L+\frac{3}{2}(A+C_G)+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

So the non-wall branch gives a pointwise row lower bound.

---

# 3. Wall branch and low-source removal

Assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G(m)\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}
=
I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

On \(I_{\rm wall,low}\),

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le \tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so that

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}|I|
\le
\frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G(m)\,dm
\ge
\frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 4. First-exit wall escape

Let

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Then

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau.
\]

Set

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\frac{\varepsilon}{\tau}}
=
C Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

Assume

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Then for

\[
|m-m_0|\le \rho |I|
\]

one has

\[
|u(m)|\ge \frac34\tau.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

the function \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave on this local interval.

Thus \(q\) cannot remain in the strip

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

over a distance larger than

\[
O\!\left(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\right).
\]

So, unless obstructed by the boundary of \(I\), there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho |I|,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

---

# 5. Boundary-layer control

Define

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho |I|.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G(m)\,dm\le 2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so that

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|
\le
\frac18Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

Thus if

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1),
\]

the boundary layer cannot carry all wall-live Gate 2 mass. Hence an interior \(m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}\setminus I_{\rm bd}\) exists, and the first-exit point \(m_1\in I\) exists.

---

# 6. Signal survival at first exit

At \(m_1\),

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \frac12\tau.
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and choosing \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\), i.e.

\[
C_\varepsilon>C_\tau+O(1),
\]

we obtain

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q(m_1)|-2|q(m_1)|^3
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)=|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

So

\[
G(m_1)\ge Q^{-4C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

Also

\[
|q(m_1)|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a valid non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 7. D4 at the escaped point

At \(m_1\),

\[
|q|\ge Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge |\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|
\ge
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Thus

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|
\ge
Q^{-C_A},
\]

where

\[
C_A=C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

---

# 8. Row mobility: pointwise lower bound to row energy

Assume

\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

then for all

\[
|m-m_\ast|\le cQ^{-C_A-C_D}|I|,
\]

we have

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Therefore there exists an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]

such that

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\quad (m\in J_\ast).
\]

Hence

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

For weighted packet norms \(w_I\,dm\), the same proof works after selecting \(m_\ast\) outside a negligible boundary region where \(w_I<Q^{-C}\). The boundary-layer exclusion above can be combined with the weight-interior selection.

---

# 9. Final theorem

## D3a Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1},
\]

and D4 row conversion:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Assume row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + D3a + D4 + row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

---

# 10. Exact-point fallback

If the downstream contradiction requires a row lower bound at a fixed preassigned point, then wall escape is not admissible. In that case one must use the fallback:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil / source-robust wall row}.
\]

But for an interval-energy architecture, the row-energy theorem above is the natural output.

---

# 11. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall escape is near-Green for row-energy / existential downstream output.}
}
\]

It reduces D3 to local bounds and D4. The remaining work is:

1. verify polynomial upper bounds for \(G,\Gamma,u'\);

2. verify D4 principal-symbol rank and residual control;

3. verify row derivative bounds for mobility;

4. confirm the final downstream contradiction accepts row energy rather than exact-point rows.

## Agent 4 / D — Continue attack: reduce D3a to three finite local estimates

The wall-escape branch is now close enough that the remaining work should be stated as explicit lemmas. We already have:

\[
\text{Gate 2}+\text{Wall Escape}+\text{D4}+\text{Row Mobility}
\Rightarrow
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

The latest downstream update also confirms the preferred architecture is now source-large interval extraction plus \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity for Gate 2, followed by wall escape and D4 row conversion. 

The wall escape theorem still depends on three local estimates:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},\qquad |\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},\qquad |u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

I will now attack those dependencies.

---

# 1. Reduce upper bounds to canonical derivative bounds

Recall:

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Assume the normalized packet coordinate

\[
t=\frac{m-m_I}{|I|},
\qquad
\partial_t=|I|\partial_m.
\]

A sufficient canonical local complexity package is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_t^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 5.
}
\]

Then:

\[
u=q'' \quad\Rightarrow\quad |u|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
\partial_t u=q''' \quad\Rightarrow\quad |\partial_t u|\le Q^C,
\]

so in physical coordinates,

\[
|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Next,

\[
|\Gamma_G|
=
|u-6q+2q^3|
\le Q^C.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_G''
=
u''-6q''+2(q^3)'',
\]

and

\[
(q^3)''=6q(q')^2+3q^2q''.
\]

So

\[
|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^C
\]

under \(k\le4\). Hence

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|
=
\left|2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right|
\le Q^C.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Finally,

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le Q^{2C_u+2C_\Gamma}=Q^{C_G}.
\]

So the wall-escape upper-bound package follows from:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_t^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 4,
}
\]

and the row mobility package needs one more derivative, as below.

---

# 2. Row mobility derivative bound

D3a row energy needs:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Use the D4 normal form

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N.
\]

Differentiate in normalized coordinate \(t\):

\[
\partial_t\mathbf A_N
=
(\partial_t q)u^3L_N\Gamma
+
3qu^2(\partial_t u)L_N\Gamma
+
qu^3(\partial_t L_N)\Gamma
+
qu^3L_N(\partial_t\Gamma)
+
\partial_t\mathbf R_N.
\]

Therefore it is enough to prove polynomial bounds for:

\[
q,\quad \partial_t q,\quad u,\quad \partial_t u,\quad \Gamma,\quad \partial_t\Gamma,\quad L_N,\quad \partial_tL_N,\quad \partial_t\mathbf R_N.
\]

For \(\partial_t\Gamma\), compute:

\[
\partial_t\Gamma_G
=
\partial_t u-6\partial_tq+6q^2\partial_tq,
\]

so \(k\le3\) controls this.

For \(\Gamma_{G,2}\),

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

so

\[
\partial_t\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q'(q')^2+4qq'q''
-\frac16\Gamma_G'''.
\]

This requires control up to \(q^{(5)}\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_t^kq|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 5
}
\]

suffices for

\[
|\partial_t u|,\quad |\partial_t\Gamma| \le Q^C.
\]

For \(L_N\) and \(\mathbf R_N\), the finite row audit must verify:

\[
|L_N|+|\partial_tL_N|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|+|\partial_t\mathbf R_N|\le Q^C.
\]

Those are row-formula/projection/gauge checks, but not new dynamics.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Row mobility follows from }k\le5\text{ canonical }q\text{-bounds plus row coefficient complexity.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Boundary layer with packet weights

If the downstream row norm is weighted,

\[
\int_I w_I(m)|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm,
\]

we need the sampled point \(m_\ast\) to lie where \(w_I\) is not tiny.

Assume \(w_I\) is a standard packet cutoff satisfying:

\[
0\le w_I\le1,
\]

\[
w_I\ge c
\quad\text{on}\quad
I_{\rm core},
\]

and

\[
|I\setminus I_{\rm core}|\le Q^{-C_{\rm edge}}|I|.
\]

The wall-escape boundary argument already removes a layer of relative width

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

So choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\]

large enough that

\[
\rho+Q^{-C_{\rm edge}}
\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

Then neither the packet edge nor the wall-escape boundary layer can carry all Gate 2 mass. Hence the D4 sample can be chosen in the core:

\[
w_I(m_\ast)\ge c.
\]

Row mobility then yields:

\[
\int_I w_I|\mathbf A_N|^2
\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

So weighted norms are compatible with wall escape if the packet cutoff has a polynomial-thick core.

---

# 4. D3a theorem with all local dependencies exposed

We can now state the refined theorem.

## D3a Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem

Assume on \(I^\ast\):

\[
\sup_{0\le k\le5}|\partial_t^kq|\le Q^C.
\]

Assume row coefficient complexity:

\[
|L_N|+|\partial_tL_N|+|\mathbf R_N|+|\partial_t\mathbf R_N|\le Q^C.
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume D4 row conversion:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12|q||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|
\]

at non-wall samples.

Then, after choosing thresholds

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

with

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1),
\]

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1),
\]

there exists \(m_\ast\in I\) such that

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Furthermore, since

\[
|\partial_t\mathbf A_N|\le Q^{C_D},
\]

there is a subinterval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\text{on }J_\ast.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Weighted version holds if the packet cutoff has a polynomial-thick core.

---

# 5. What remains after this reduction

D3a is now near-Green. The only nontrivial remaining checks are not conceptual:

## Local complexity

Need:

\[
\sup_{0\le k\le5}|\partial_t^kq|\le Q^C.
\]

This belongs to Agent 1’s ordinary zero-separated transfer.

## D4 rank

Need:

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

This belongs to Agent 5’s row-symbol / projection-coercivity audit.

## D4 residual

Need:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12|q||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Again finite row audit.

## Row derivative

Need:

\[
|\partial_t\mathbf A_N|\le Q^C.
\]

This follows from local complexity plus row coefficient complexity.

Thus the \(q_0\)-wall itself is no longer a named conceptual blocker.

---

# 6. Fallback if exact-point locking appears

If the final contradiction layer demands:

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

at a fixed preassigned \(m_0\), then D3a fails. In that case, one must return to:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil / source-robust wall row}.
\]

But under row-energy or existential row architecture, D3a is sufficient.

---

# 7. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The remaining D3a requirements reduce to local derivative bounds and finite D4 row audits.}
}
\]

The wall escape step itself is now proof-level:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass cannot be trapped at }q_0=0
\text{ when }u=q_0''\text{ is live.}
}
\]

The downstream row-energy theorem follows once D4 rank/residual and row derivative bounds are verified.

## Continuing attack — collapse D3a into a corollary of local complexity + D4

At this point the \(q_0\)-wall route has become a local theorem with explicit hypotheses. The aim now is to remove D3a as a separate named input by proving:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local complexity}+\text{Gate 2}+\text{D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy},
}
\]

where wall escape is just the proof of the implication.

---

# 1. Current D3a dependencies

D3a currently requires:

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2,
\]

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1},
\]

and D4:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

I will now show all the analytic upper bounds are consequences of one canonical local package.

---

# 2. One canonical local package

Work in normalized coordinate

\[
t=\frac{m-m_I}{|I|}.
\]

Assume

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_t^k q|\le Q^{C_q},
\qquad 0\le k\le 5.
}
\]

Then:

\[
u=q'',
\]

\[
\partial_t u=q'''.
\]

Hence

\[
|u|\le Q^{C_q},
\qquad
|\partial_t u|\le Q^{C_q}.
\]

So

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_q}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Next,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3.
\]

Thus

\[
|\Gamma_G|\le Q^C.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G''=q^{(4)}-6q''+2(q^3)'',
\]

and

\[
(q^3)''=6q(q')^2+3q^2q'',
\]

the bound \(k\le4\) controls \(\Gamma_{G,2}\). Therefore

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^C.
\]

Thus

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^C,
\]

and

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le Q^C.
\]

For row mobility, need \(\partial_t\Gamma\). We have:

\[
\partial_t\Gamma_G=q'''-6q'+6q^2q',
\]

controlled by \(k\le3\).

For \(\Gamma_{G,2}\),

\[
\partial_t\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q'(q')^2+4qq'q''
-\frac16\Gamma_G''',
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_G'''
\]

uses \(q^{(5)}\). So \(k\le5\) suffices.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{k\le5}|\partial_t^kq|\le Q^C
\Rightarrow
G\le Q^C,\ |\Gamma|\le Q^C,\ |u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Row mobility from row coefficient complexity

Assume in addition row coefficient complexity:

\[
|L_N|+|\partial_t L_N|\le Q^C,
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|+|\partial_t\mathbf R_N|\le Q^C.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N.
\]

Differentiate:

\[
\partial_t\mathbf A_N
=
q'u^3L_N\Gamma
+
3qu^2u'L_N\Gamma
+
qu^3(\partial_tL_N)\Gamma
+
qu^3L_N(\partial_t\Gamma)
+
\partial_t\mathbf R_N.
\]

Each term is bounded by \(Q^C\). Hence

\[
|\partial_t\mathbf A_N|\le Q^C,
\]

equivalently

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Thus row mobility also follows from:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical local complexity}
+
\text{row coefficient complexity}.
}
\]

---

# 4. D3a becomes a theorem

Now state the theorem with no separate upper-bound hypotheses.

## Local Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

1. canonical local complexity:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\partial_t^k q|\le Q^C,
\qquad 0\le k\le5;
\]

2. row coefficient complexity:

\[
|L_N|+|\partial_tL_N|+|\mathbf R_N|+|\partial_t\mathbf R_N|\le Q^C;
\]

3. Gate 2:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

4. D4 rank and residual control:

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12|q||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|
\]

at non-wall samples.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
}
\]

This theorem includes both non-wall sampling and wall escape.

Therefore D3a is not an independent input; it is a corollary of local complexity and D4.

---

# 5. Proof compression

The proof is now a short split.

## Non-wall mass

If

\[
\int_{\{|q|\ge\varepsilon\}}G\ge\frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then by \(G\le Q^C\), choose \(m_\ast\) with

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon,
\qquad
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Row mobility gives row energy.

## Wall mass

If wall mass dominates, remove \(|u|<\tau\) using \(|\Gamma|\le Q^C\). Pick \(m_0\) with

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau,
\]

away from the boundary. By \(|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}\), \(u=q''\) has fixed sign nearby and \(q\) exits the strip \(|q|<\varepsilon\) within

\[
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

At first exit \(m_1\):

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge\tau/2,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
G(m_1)\ge c\tau^4.
\]

D4 gives row lower bound at \(m_1\). Row mobility gives row energy.

Boundary layers are removed by choosing \(\varepsilon\) sufficiently small polynomially.

---

# 6. Final dependency reduction

The downstream package is now:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{source-large interval extraction}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

Then:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{canonical local complexity}
+
\text{D4 row rank/residual}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
\]

So the separate label

\[
D3a=\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
\]

can be demoted from “input” to “lemma inside row-energy conversion.”

The only remaining row-side hard work is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 principal-symbol rank + residual/projection control.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Remaining attack surface

The actual remaining tasks are:

## A. Local complexity

Prove

\[
\sup_{k\le5}|\partial_t^k q|\le Q^C
\]

on ordinary zero-separated packets, including primitive/basepoint control for \(q,q'\).

## B. Gate 2 integral rigidity

Finalize the \(L^2\)-input lemma.

## C. D4 row audit

Prove

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and projected residual half-leading.

Everything else in the wall branch follows.

---

# 8. Verdict

The \(q_0\)-wall is no longer a separate conceptual blocker under row-energy architecture.

It is a corollary of local convexity:

\[
u=q_0''
\]

and existential/energetic row sampling.

The next proof-critical modules are now only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 }L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 principal-symbol / residual finite audit}.
}

## Agent 4 / D — D3a wall escape as corollary of local complexity + D4

Executing Agent 4’s lane: wall escape / row-energy conversion. The current downstream route is

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{local wall escape}
+
\text{D4 row-span conversion}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
\]

The latest update also demotes the old \(D1/D2/D3\) labels to fallback status and replaces them with the sharper source-thickening + \(L^2\)-input rigidity Gate 2 route. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
q=q_0,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I G\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local complexity:

\[
\sup_{0\le k\le5}|\partial_t^kq|\le Q^C,
\]

where \(t\) is normalized packet coordinate.

Then:

\[
u=q'',
\qquad
\partial_t u=q''',
\]

so

\[
|u|\le Q^C,
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

so

\[
|\Gamma_G|\le Q^C.
\]

And

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

where \(\Gamma_G''\) uses derivatives of \(q\) up to order \(4\). Hence

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^C.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^C,
\qquad
G\le Q^C.
\]

These are exactly the upper bounds needed by wall escape.

---

# 2. D4 as black box at non-wall samples

Assume D4 gives a finite row vector

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,\ldots,A_{2N+1})^T
\]

with normal form

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

and

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 |q|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at any point satisfying

\[
|q|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

plus either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

one obtains

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

The local complexity already provides \(|\Gamma|\le Q^C\), so the upper-bound alternative is available.

---

# 3. Split into non-wall and wall regions

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q|\ge\varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then since \(G\le Q^C\), there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

At \(m_\ast\),

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

so D4 applies and gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

This handles the non-wall branch.

---

# 4. Wall branch: remove low-source points

Assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\ge \frac12Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Let

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

On the low-source set,

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le \tau^2 Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

Choose \(C_\tau\) so that

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,low}}G\le \frac14Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

hence

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G\ge \frac14Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

So live wall mass is nontrivial.

---

# 5. First-exit wall escape

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Then

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Let

\[
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

The local complexity gives

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Choose \(C_\varepsilon\) so that

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Then on the packet-normalized interval

\[
|m-m_0|\le \rho |I|,
\]

one has

\[
|u(m)|\ge\frac34\tau.
\]

Since

\[
u=q'',
\]

the function \(q\) is uniformly convex or uniformly concave there. Therefore \(q\) cannot stay inside

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for distance \(\gg \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\). Hence, barring packet boundary issues, there exists a first-exit point \(m_1\in I\) such that

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge\tau/2.
\]

---

# 6. Boundary layer

The possible failure is that \(m_0\) is too close to \(\partial I\).

Let

\[
I_{\rm bd}
=
\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho |I|.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G\le 2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|.
\]

Choose

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|\le \frac18 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

So the boundary layer cannot carry all live wall mass. An interior \(m_0\) exists, and the first-exit construction applies.

Thus choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
\]

---

# 7. Signal survival at exit

At the first-exit point \(m_1\),

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge\tau/2.
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)=|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

Also

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

D4 yields

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

---

# 8. Row mobility to row energy

Assume row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then from

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

we obtain an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with

\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\quad(m\in J_\ast).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

For weighted packet norms, the same holds if the Gate 2 mass selection avoids a negligible cutoff boundary; this is handled by the same boundary-layer exclusion.

---

# 9. Final D3a theorem

## D3a Wall Escape as Local-Complexity Corollary

Assume:

1. Gate 2:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. local complexity:

\[
\sup_{0\le k\le5}|\partial_t^kq|\le Q^C;
\]

3. D4 row conversion at non-wall samples:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le
\frac12 |q||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|;
\]

4. row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a is not an independent conceptual input under row-energy architecture.}
}
\]

It follows from local complexity plus D4.

---

# 10. Exact-point caveat

If the final contradiction requires the row lower bound at a fixed preassigned point, wall escape is insufficient.

Then one must use the fallback:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil / source-robust wall row}.
\]

But for the current interval/energy downstream architecture, D3a is admissible and near-Green.

---

# 11. Verdict

The \(q_0\)-wall no longer remains as a separate blocker.

The row side now reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 principal-symbol rank + projected residual control + row derivative bounds.}
}
\]

The Gate 2 side reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
|u'|\text{-source thickening}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}.
}
\]

This is the current sharp downstream architecture.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:03:08)

_Thought for 15s_

## Continuing attack — remove the hidden real-valuedness assumption in wall escape

The wall-escape proof used convexity:

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]

and argued that if

\[
|q|<\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\ge\tau,
\]

then \(q\) exits the strip \(|q|<\varepsilon\) within distance

\[
\rho\asymp \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

That argument is immediate if \(q\) is real-valued. But if \(q\) is complex-valued, ordinary convexity of \(q\) is not defined. This is a potential hidden assumption. I’ll now remove it.

The current downstream architecture uses wall escape as the D3a replacement: Gate 2 plus local wall escape plus D4 plus row mobility gives row energy. 

---

# 1. Problem

For real \(q\), if

\[
q''=u,\qquad |u|\ge\tau,
\]

then \(q\) is locally convex or concave, so it cannot remain in

\[
|q|<\varepsilon
\]

for more than \(O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})\).

For complex \(q\), the statement

\[
|q''|\ge\tau
\]

does not imply convexity of \(|q|\). The vector \(q''\) could rotate, and the complex trajectory could in principle curve inside a small disk longer than a real convex function could remain inside a strip.

So D3a needs either:

1. an explicit real-valuedness hypothesis for \(q_0\); or  
2. a complex-valued wall-escape lemma.

The second is available.

---

# 2. Complex wall escape by projecting onto \(u(m_0)\)

Let

\[
q:I\to\mathbb C,
\qquad
u=q''.
\]

Assume at \(m_0\):

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Let

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(m_0)}}{|u(m_0)|}.
\]

Define the real scalar projection

\[
Q(m):=\Re(e\,q(m)).
\]

Then

\[
Q''(m_0)=\Re(e\,q''(m_0))
=
\Re(e\,u(m_0))
=
|u(m_0)|
\ge\tau.
\]

If

\[
|u'(m)|\le M
\]

for

\[
|m-m_0|\le \rho,
\]

then

\[
|u(m)-u(m_0)|\le M\rho.
\]

Hence

\[
Q''(m)=\Re(eu(m))
\ge |u(m_0)|-|u(m)-u(m_0)|
\ge \tau-M\rho.
\]

If

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau,
\]

then

\[
Q''(m)\ge \frac34\tau
\]

on the local interval.

So \(Q\) is genuinely real-convex even when \(q\) is complex-valued.

---

# 3. Complex first-exit lemma

Assume

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau,
\qquad
|u'|\le M.
\]

Let

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
\]

and assume

\[
M\rho\le \frac14\tau.
\]

Using \(Q=\Re(e q)\), we have

\[
Q''\ge \frac34\tau
\]

on the local interval.

Since

\[
|Q(m_0)|\le |q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\]

real convexity implies that within distance

\[
O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau})
\]

one has

\[
|Q(m_1)|\ge 2\varepsilon
\]

for some \(m_1\), unless blocked by the packet boundary.

Then

\[
|q(m_1)|\ge |Q(m_1)|\ge 2\varepsilon.
\]

By continuity, there is a first point between \(m_0\) and \(m_1\) such that

\[
|q(m_\ast)|=\varepsilon.
\]

Moreover, because

\[
|u'|\rho\le \frac14\tau,
\]

we have

\[
|u(m_\ast)|\ge \frac34\tau.
\]

Thus the wall escape works for complex \(q\):

\[
\boxed{
|q|<\varepsilon,\ |q''|\ge\tau
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast:\ |q(m_\ast)|=\varepsilon,\ |q''(m_\ast)|\ge c\tau.
}
\]

No real-valuedness of \(q\) is required.

---

# 4. Signal survival for complex \(q\)

Previously we used

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

and

\[
|q|=\varepsilon\ll |u|
\]

to conclude

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c|u|.
\]

This remains valid for complex \(q,u\) by the triangle inequality:

\[
|\Gamma_G|
=
|u-6q+2q^3|
\ge
|u|-6|q|-2|q|^3.
\]

At first exit,

\[
|q|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge c\tau.
\]

If

\[
\varepsilon\le c'\tau,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c''\tau.
\]

So

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2
\ge
|u|^2|\Gamma_G|^2
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

Thus complex-valued wall escape still produces a valid non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 5. Updated wall-escape theorem without real assumption

## Complex Wall-Escape Sampling Lemma

Let \(q:I\to\mathbb C\), \(u=q''\). Assume

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau,
\]

and

\[
|u'(m)|\le M|I|^{-1}
\]

near \(m_0\). Let

\[
\rho=C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

If

\[
M\rho\le c\tau,
\]

and \(m_0\) is at least \(\rho|I|\) from the boundary, then there exists

\[
m_1\in I
\]

such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho |I|,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau
\]

provided

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)=|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2\ge c\tau^4.
\]

This proves D3a wall escape without assuming \(q\) is real-valued.

---

# 6. Consequence for D3a

The previous D3a theorem is now stronger.

It only needs:

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

and local complexity ensuring these bounds.

It does **not** need \(q_0\) to be real-valued.

The wall branch proof becomes:

1. Gate 2 mass on \(|q|<\varepsilon\);
2. discard \(|u|<\tau\);
3. pick live wall point;
4. project \(q\) onto the direction of \(u(m_0)\);
5. convexity of the projected scalar function gives first exit;
6. triangle inequality gives \(|\Gamma_G|\gtrsim\tau\);
7. D4 applies.

---

# 7. Boundary layer is unchanged

The boundary layer estimate is identical.

With

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2},
\]

and

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

the boundary contribution is at most

\[
2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|.
\]

Choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1)
\]

to make it negligible.

The stability condition is still

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

Thus choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
\]

Same exponents as before.

---

# 8. Row-energy conclusion remains unchanged

At the first-exit point \(m_1\):

\[
|q(m_1)|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

D4 gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Row mobility gives

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

So the final wall escape + row mobility theorem survives unchanged.

---

# 9. Updated dependency

D3a no longer depends on real-valuedness of \(q\). Its dependencies are:

1. Gate 2 mass;
2. local complexity for \(u'\);
3. polynomial upper bounds for \(G,\Gamma\);
4. D4 rank/residual at non-wall samples;
5. row mobility.

This makes D3a very robust.

---

# 10. Verdict

The hidden real-valuedness problem in wall escape is removed.

The \(q_0\)-wall can be escaped for real or complex \(q_0\) by projecting onto the direction of \(q_0''(m_0)\).

Thus D3a remains near-Green under the row-energy architecture.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:07:38)

I’ll check for hidden assumptions in the wall-escape step itself. The main one is whether \(u=q_0''\) is exact canonical identity or only a model identity with residual; that matters.

_Thought for 15s_

## One step further — make wall escape robust to \(q_0''\neq u\) residuals

The last attack removed a hidden real-valuedness assumption: even for complex \(q_0\), wall escape works by projecting \(q_0\) onto the direction of \(q_0''\). There is one more hidden assumption worth isolating:

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=q_0''
}
\]

must be exact, or at least true up to a small residual. The wall-escape proof uses this identity directly. If \(q_0\) is only a model primitive or a gauge-normalized coordinate, then we need a robust version. The current downstream framework treats wall escape as the D3a replacement after Gate 2 and before D4 row conversion, so this compatibility matters. 

---

# 1. Introduce curvature mismatch

Let

\[
r_{\rm curv}:=q_0''-u.
\]

Then

\[
q_0''=u+r_{\rm curv}.
\]

The wall escape needs local curvature of \(q_0\), not merely largeness of \(u\). Previously, at a live wall point,

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge\tau,
\]

we concluded \(q_0\) has curvature \(\gtrsim\tau\). With residual, this becomes valid if

\[
|r_{\rm curv}|\le \frac14|u|
\]

near the wall sample.

So the correct robust hypothesis is:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0''-u|\le Q^{-C_{\rm gap}}|u|
}
\]

or at least

\[
\boxed{
|q_0''-u|\le \tau/4
}
\]

on the escape neighborhood.

---

# 2. Robust complex wall escape

Assume at \(m_0\):

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau,
\]

and

\[
|r_{\rm curv}(m)|\le \tau/8
\]

near \(m_0\).

Let

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(m_0)}}{|u(m_0)|},
\]

and define

\[
Q(m)=\Re(e q_0(m)).
\]

Then

\[
Q''(m)
=
\Re(e q_0''(m))
=
\Re(eu(m))+\Re(e r_{\rm curv}(m)).
\]

If also

\[
|u(m)-u(m_0)|\le \tau/8
\]

on the local escape interval, then

\[
\Re(eu(m))\ge |u(m_0)|-\tau/8\ge 7\tau/8.
\]

Hence

\[
Q''(m)\ge 7\tau/8-\tau/8=\frac34\tau.
\]

Thus the same convexity / first-exit proof works. We get a point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

provided \(|u'|\rho\ll\tau\), and

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau
\]

provided \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\).

So D3a survives curvature mismatch if:

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=u+O(\tau)
}
\]

on the wall-escape neighborhood.

---

# 3. If the residual is not small, it may itself be useful

If

\[
|r_{\rm curv}|=|q_0''-u|\gtrsim |u|
\]

on a live wall region, then \(q_0''\) is not controlled by \(u\). This does not automatically kill wall escape; instead, one should redo the argument using \(q_0''\) directly.

There are two branches.

## Branch A — \(q_0''\) is live

If

\[
|q_0''|\ge c\tau,
\]

then use \(q_0''\) as the curvature in the wall escape proof. The first-exit point still exists.

At the exit point, we need Gate 2 signal:

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

This depends on \(u\), not \(q_0''\). So we still need \(u\) live at the exit. If \(u\) is live and \(q_0''\) is live, wall escape works even if they differ.

## Branch B — \(q_0''\) cancels while \(u\) is live

If

\[
|u|\ge\tau,
\qquad
|q_0''|\ll\tau,
\]

then

\[
r_{\rm curv}=q_0''-u\approx -u
\]

is live. This indicates a mismatch between the wall coordinate \(q_0\) and the canonical source curvature \(u\). That mismatch must be accounted for elsewhere.

In proof architecture terms, this would mean:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall escape is not valid unless }q_0\text{ is the primitive whose curvature is }u.
}
\]

So one must either:

1. redefine \(q_0\) so that \(q_0''=u\) canonically;
2. add curvature-transfer control \(q_0''-u\) as a local error term;
3. abandon wall escape and return to \(q_0\)-adic row algebra.

This is a real guardrail.

---

# 4. Correct D3a statement with curvature compatibility

The final robust wall-escape theorem should include:

## Curvature-Compatible Wall Escape

Assume:

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge\tau,
\]

\[
|q_0''-u|\le \tau/8,
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C}|I|^{-1},
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau.
\]

Then there exists \(m_1\in I\) within

\[
O\!\left(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}\,|I|\right)
\]

such that

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Hence

\[
G(m_1)=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2(m_1)\ge c\tau^4.
\]

D4 applies at \(m_1\).

---

# 5. Where this residual belongs in the dependency graph

This is not a new arithmetic input. It is a **canonical consistency check**:

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=q''_{\can}
\quad\text{or}\quad
q_0''-q''_{\can}\text{ is perturbative.}
}
\]

It should be listed alongside:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

the local derivative bounds, and D4 row normal form.

If \(q_0\) is simply the primitive \(q\) whose second derivative is \(q''_{\can}\), then this check is automatic. If \(q_0\) is a normalized coordinate after gauge/projection, it must be verified.

---

# 6. Extra improvement: use second differences to reduce derivative needs

The wall-escape proof used \(|u'|\) to keep curvature stable. A slightly weaker version uses a second-difference identity:

\[
q_0(m+h)+q_0(m-h)-2q_0(m)
=
h^2q_0''(m)+O(h^3\sup |q_0'''|).
\]

If

\[
q_0''=u+r_{\rm curv},
\]

and

\[
|u|\ge\tau,
\qquad
|r_{\rm curv}|\le\tau/8,
\qquad
\sup|q_0'''|\le M_3,
\]

choose

\[
h\le c\tau/M_3.
\]

Then the second difference is \(\gtrsim \tau h^2\), forcing at least one of

\[
m-h,\ m,\ m+h
\]

to have

\[
|q_0|\gtrsim \tau h^2-\varepsilon.
\]

This avoids needing pointwise convexity over the whole interval. It only needs a local third-derivative bound. It gives a slightly weaker but simpler escape point.

So D3a can be proved by either:

1. convex first-exit with \(u'\)-control; or
2. second-difference escape with \(q_0'''\)-control.

Both are local complexity consequences.

---

# 7. Final extra finding

The extra hidden requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall escape needs curvature compatibility }q_0''\approx u.
}
\]

Once included, the D3a theorem is robust for both real and complex \(q_0\).

The revised wall-side dependency is:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{local complexity}
+
(q_0''=u+O_{\rm small})
+
\text{D4}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
\]

If \(q_0''=u\) is definitional, no new work is needed. If not, this is the next finite local audit.

## One step further — the hidden threshold-corridor condition

The next hidden issue is not geometric. It is **exponent feasibility**.

Wall escape requires choosing the wall threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

very small, so the wall strip is thin and boundary layers are negligible. But D4 row conversion requires the leading row size

\[
|q_0|\,|u|^3|\Gamma|
\]

to remain larger than the residual/canonical error floor. If \(\varepsilon\) is chosen too small, the escaped non-wall sample has

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon
\]

and the leading row becomes too small to dominate D4 errors.

So D3a is valid only if there is a **threshold corridor**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(\varepsilon\) must be small enough for wall escape, but large enough for D4 correction control.}
}
\]

This is the next finite audit.

---

# 1. Lower bounds forcing \(\varepsilon\) small

Write

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

The wall-escape proof needs:

## Low-source removal

To ensure \(|u|<\tau\) cannot carry Gate 2 mass, using

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we need

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
}
\]

## Curvature stability / first exit

With

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1},
\]

and

\[
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau},
\]

we need

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le c\tau.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
}
\]

## Boundary-layer negligibility

Since boundary contribution is bounded by

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho |I|,
\]

we require

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
}
\]

So wall escape imposes the lower bound

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
:=
\max
\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}
+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 2. Upper bounds forcing \(\varepsilon\) not too small

At the first-exit sample \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
|\Gamma(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

The D4 leading scale is

\[
S_{\rm lead}
=
|q_0|\,|u|^3\,\sigma_2(L_N)\,|\Gamma|.
\]

Assuming

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

we get

\[
S_{\rm lead}
\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon}\,
Q^{-3C_\tau}\,
Q^{-C_L}\,
Q^{-C_\tau}
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

D4 correction control requires

\[
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 S_{\rm lead}.
\]

Suppose the residual floor is

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}}.
\]

Then we need

\[
Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L
\le
C_R^{\rm row}-O(1).
}
\]

So D4 imposes the upper bound

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon
\le
C_{\varepsilon,\max}
:=
C_R^{\rm row}-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1).
}
\]

---

# 3. The threshold corridor

Wall escape plus D4 requires

\[
\boxed{
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
\le
C_\varepsilon
\le
C_{\varepsilon,\max}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
C_{\varepsilon,\min}+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

Substitute

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
=
\max
\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}
+O(1).
\]

Then the row residual exponent must satisfy

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
\max
\{7C_\tau+2C_{u'}+C_L,\ 5C_\tau+2A+2C_G+C_L\}
+O(1).
}
\]

This is the precise “room in the exponents” condition for D3a.

---

# 4. Why this matters

If row residuals are only bounded by some fixed polynomial exponent but not large enough, then wall escape can force us to choose

\[
\varepsilon
\]

so small that

\[
|q_0|\,|u|^3|\Gamma|
\]

falls below the D4 error floor.

Then D3a does not close, even though the geometric escape is valid.

So the true row-side requirement is not merely:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C}
\]

for some unspecified \(C\). It must beat the specific escaped-leading scale:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf R_N|
\le
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
}
\]

This should be built into the D4 residual audit.

---

# 5. Two possible fixes if the corridor is empty

If

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}>C_{\varepsilon,\max},
\]

there are two ways to repair the route.

## Fix A — strengthen D4 residual estimates

Improve the canonical/tail/projection residual exponent:

\[
C_R^{\rm row}
\]

until the corridor opens.

This is the cleanest solution if residuals are artificial truncation errors.

## Fix B — use saturated/blow-up rows near the wall

Instead of using original rows

\[
A_N\sim q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\]

use the saturated rows

\[
\widehat A_N=A_N/q_0,
\]

if admissible.

Then the leading scale at the escaped/wall sample becomes

\[
|u|^3|\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-4C_\tau},
\]

with no \(C_\varepsilon\) loss. The D4 correction requirement becomes

\[
C_R^{\rm sat}
\ge
4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

This is much easier.

Thus if the \(\varepsilon\)-corridor is too narrow, the \(q_0\)-adic saturated row route becomes valuable again.

---

# 6. Third possible fix: choose a larger source threshold \(\tau\)

The lower-source threshold was chosen to discard low-source wall mass. We required

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

Taking \(C_\tau\) larger makes \(\tau\) smaller, which weakens leading scale. So we want \(C_\tau\) as small as permitted:

\[
\boxed{
C_\tau=\frac{A+2C_\Gamma}{2}+O(1).
}
\]

This minimizes the D4 leading-loss term \(4C_\tau\).

So exponent optimization should set \(C_\tau\) at its lower feasible value, not arbitrarily large.

---

# 7. Revised D3a theorem with threshold corridor

## Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem with Residual Corridor

Assume Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local complexity gives

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Assume D4 rank:

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Assume row residual bound:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}}.
\]

Choose

\[
C_\tau=\frac{A+2C_\Gamma}{2}+O(1),
\]

and require the threshold-corridor inequality

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
\max
\{7C_\tau+2C_{u'}+C_L,\ 5C_\tau+2A+2C_G+C_L\}
+O(1).
}
\]

Then there exists a threshold \(C_\varepsilon\) for which wall escape and D4 both hold, and therefore

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

---

# 8. Extra hidden assumption found

The new hidden requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 residual estimates must be strong enough relative to the wall-escape threshold.}
}
\]

This is not automatic. It must be included in the D4 projected-residual audit.

So the remaining row-side checklist becomes:

1. principal-symbol rank:

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L};
\]

2. projected residual bound with explicit exponent:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}};
\]

3. threshold-corridor inequality:

\[
C_R^{\rm row}>C_{\varepsilon,\min}+4C_\tau+C_L.
\]

If this holds, wall escape closes.

---

# 9. Verdict

The wall-escape theorem is geometrically sound, but its compatibility with D4 depends on an exponent corridor.

This is the final extra audit needed for D3a:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the row residual floor beat the escaped leading scale }|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|?
}
\]

If yes, D3a is closed.

If no, use saturated \(q_0\)-adic rows or improve residual estimates.
