## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:10:02)

_Thought for 9s_

## Agent 4 / D — Final extra audit: threshold corridor vs. D4 residual floor

The hidden issue was that Wall-Escape Sampling chooses a small wall threshold

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

but D4 row conversion at the escaped point has leading size

\[
|q_0|\,|u|^3|\Gamma|
\sim
\varepsilon\,\tau^4.
\]

So if \(\varepsilon\) is forced too small, the D4 leading term may fall below the residual/error floor. The final audit is to check whether there is an exponent corridor:

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}\le C_\varepsilon\le C_{\varepsilon,\max}.
\]

This is the condition that Wall Escape and D4 can be made compatible. The latest downstream package uses Gate 2, local wall escape, D4 row-span conversion, and row mobility. 

---

# 1. Parameters

Let

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and assume Gate 2 mass

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local upper bounds

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Let

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}
\]

be the source threshold, and

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}
\]

be the wall-exit threshold.

D4 has row normal form

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Let the projected residual/error floor be

\[
|P_L\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}},
\]

where \(P_L\) denotes the leading-row-image projection if using the sharper projected-residual formulation.

---

# 2. Lower bound on \(C_\tau\)

Low-source wall points satisfy

\[
|u|<\tau.
\]

Using

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

on that set

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2
\le
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

To make low-source wall mass negligible compared with \(Q^{-A}|I|\), require

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}\ll Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus

\[
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
\]

The optimal choice is the smallest allowed value:

\[
\boxed{
C_\tau=\frac A2+C_\Gamma+O(1).
}
\]

Taking \(C_\tau\) larger only shrinks the D4 leading term.

---

# 3. Lower bound on \(C_\varepsilon\)

Wall escape uses

\[
\rho\asymp \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

## 3.1 Curvature stability

Need

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le c\tau.
\]

This gives

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

## 3.2 Boundary-layer negligibility

The boundary layer contributes at most

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho |I|.
\]

Require this to be \(\ll Q^{-A}|I|\). Hence

\[
Q^{C_G}Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}
\le
Q^{-A-O(1)}.
\]

So

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
=
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}
+O(1).
}
\]

Substituting the optimal

\[
C_\tau=\frac A2+C_\Gamma+O(1),
\]

we get

\[
3C_\tau+2C_{u'}
=
\frac{3A}{2}+3C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+O(1),
\]

and

\[
C_\tau+2A+2C_G
=
\frac{5A}{2}+C_\Gamma+2C_G+O(1).
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
=
\max\left\{
\frac{3A}{2}+3C_\Gamma+2C_{u'},
\frac{5A}{2}+C_\Gamma+2C_G
\right\}
+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 4. Upper bound on \(C_\varepsilon\) from D4 residuals

At a wall-escape point \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau=Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma(m_1)|\ge |\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau=Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

The D4 leading scale is

\[
S_{\rm lead}
=
|q_0|\,|u|^3\,\sigma_2(L_N)\,|\Gamma|.
\]

Using

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

we get

\[
S_{\rm lead}
\ge
Q^{-C_\varepsilon}\,
Q^{-3C_\tau}\,
Q^{-C_L}\,
Q^{-C_\tau}
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

For residuals to be half-leading, it is enough that

\[
Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
C_R^{\rm row}\ge C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\le C_R^{\rm row}-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
C_{\varepsilon,\max}
=
C_R^{\rm row}-4C_\tau-C_L-O(1).
}
\]

With optimal \(C_\tau=A/2+C_\Gamma+O(1)\),

\[
\boxed{
C_{\varepsilon,\max}
=
C_R^{\rm row}-2A-4C_\Gamma-C_L-O(1).
}
\]

---

# 5. Corridor condition

The threshold corridor exists iff

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}\le C_{\varepsilon,\max}.
\]

That is,

\[
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}
+O(1)
\le
C_R^{\rm row}-4C_\tau-C_L.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
\max
\{
7C_\tau+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
5C_\tau+2A+2C_G+C_L
\}
+O(1).
}
\]

Substituting

\[
C_\tau=\frac A2+C_\Gamma+O(1),
\]

this becomes

\[
7C_\tau+2C_{u'}+C_L
=
\frac{7A}{2}
+
7C_\Gamma
+
2C_{u'}
+
C_L
+
O(1),
\]

and

\[
5C_\tau+2A+2C_G+C_L
=
\frac{9A}{2}
+
5C_\Gamma
+
2C_G
+
C_L
+
O(1).
\]

Therefore the clean final residual requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
\max\left\{
\frac{7A}{2}+7C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
\frac{9A}{2}+5C_\Gamma+2C_G+C_L
\right\}
+O(1).
}
\]

This is the final exponent audit.

---

# 6. Interpretation

D3a closes if the projected D4 residual exponent beats the wall-escape leading loss.

In words:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 residuals must be small beyond the escaped leading scale }
|q_0|\,|u|^3|\Gamma|.
}
\]

At the escaped point, that scale is

\[
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

Since \(C_\varepsilon\) itself must be large enough for wall escape and boundary control, the D4 residual floor must be correspondingly strong.

So the D4 finite audit must not merely prove:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C}
\]

for some unspecified \(C\). It must prove it with

\[
C\ge C_R^{\rm row}
\]

satisfying the corridor inequality above.

---

# 7. If the corridor is open

If

\[
C_R^{\rm row}
\]

satisfies the boxed inequality, choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\]

with

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
\le
C_\varepsilon
\le
C_{\varepsilon,\max}.
\]

Then:

1. low-source wall mass is negligible;
2. first-exit wall escape is stable;
3. boundary-layer mass is negligible;
4. D4 leading term beats residuals at the escaped point;
5. row mobility gives row energy.

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + local complexity + D4}
\Rightarrow
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 8. If the corridor is closed

If

\[
C_R^{\rm row}
<
C_{\varepsilon,\min}+4C_\tau+C_L,
\]

then ordinary wall escape using original rows may not close. There are three repairs.

## Repair A — strengthen projected residual control

Improve the estimate for

\[
|P_L\mathbf R_N|
\]

until

\[
C_R^{\rm row}
\]

beats the corridor threshold.

This is the preferred fix if residuals come from canonical tails, \(E_2\), projection, or normalization errors.

## Repair B — use saturated rows

Use

\[
\widehat{\mathbf A}_N=\mathbf A_N/q_0
\]

if admissible.

Then the leading scale at the wall becomes

\[
|u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-(4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

The residual condition becomes only

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm sat}\ge 4C_\tau+C_L+O(1)
}
\]

instead of

\[
C_R^{\rm row}\ge C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L.
\]

This removes the \(\varepsilon\)-loss.

With optimal \(C_\tau\),

\[
C_R^{\rm sat}\ge 2A+4C_\Gamma+C_L+O(1).
\]

This is much easier.

## Repair C — exact source-robust wall row

Find a row with

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Then the leading scale does not contain \(\varepsilon\). This is equivalent in spirit to saturated-row admissibility.

---

# 9. Final D3a audit checklist

For D3a to be marked Green, verify:

## A. Local complexity

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

## B. D4 rank

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

## C. Projected residual exponent

\[
|P_L\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}}.
\]

## D. Corridor inequality

\[
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
\max\left\{
\frac{7A}{2}+7C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
\frac{9A}{2}+5C_\Gamma+2C_G+C_L
\right\}
+O(1).
\]

If D holds, D3a closes with original rows.

If D fails, use saturated rows or source-robust wall rows.

---

# 10. Verdict

The final extra audit reveals a real but finite exponent condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall escape and D4 are compatible iff the D4 residual floor leaves an }\varepsilon\text{-corridor.}
}
\]

This is now the precise remaining D3a/D4 compatibility check.

No new conceptual obstruction appears, but D4 residual estimates must be strong enough with explicit exponents.

Continue your attack

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:12:24)

_Thought for 16s_

## Continuing attack — remove the \(\varepsilon\)-corridor by replacing absolute residual bounds with valuation-relative residual bounds

The previous audit found a possible threshold-corridor obstruction:

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}\le C_\varepsilon\le C_{\varepsilon,\max}.
\]

That obstruction appeared because we treated the D4 residual as an **absolute floor**

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}}.
\]

But that is too crude. Most legitimate row remainders should scale with the same factors as the leading term, e.g.

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma,
\]

or with even higher powers of \(q_0,u,\Gamma\). If the residual has the same \(q_0\)-adic factor as the leading row, then shrinking

\[
\varepsilon=|q_0|
\]

does **not** worsen the relative error. The corridor is only real for residual terms that have an absolute, non-scaling floor. This is the next key refinement. The latest downstream structure already isolates D4 as row-span conversion with projected-residual control after wall escape. 

---

# 1. The previous corridor was based on an absolute residual

At the wall-escape sample,

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge c\tau.
\]

The leading D4 scale is

\[
S_{\rm lead}
=
|q_0|\,|u|^3\,\sigma_2(L_N)\,|\Gamma|
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

If the residual is only known absolutely:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm row}},
\]

then we need

\[
C_R^{\rm row}\ge C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

This creates an upper bound on \(C_\varepsilon\), hence the corridor.

But the correct D4 audit should not use an absolute residual unless unavoidable.

---

# 2. Use \(q_0,u,\Gamma\)-valuation instead

Each residual term should be classified by its local monomial valuation:

\[
T
=
q_0^a u^b \Gamma^c \cdot E_T,
\]

where

\[
|E_T|\le Q^{C_T}
\]

or, better,

\[
|E_T|\le Q^{-K_T}.
\]

The leading row has valuation

\[
q_0^1 u^3 \Gamma^1.
\]

So

\[
S_{\rm lead}\sim |q_0|^1|u|^3|\Gamma|^1.
\]

The relative size of \(T\) is

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}
\le
Q^{C_T}
|q_0|^{a-1}
|u|^{b-3}
|\Gamma|^{c-1}.
\]

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|,|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Thus

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}
\le
Q^{C_T}
Q^{-(a-1)C_\varepsilon}
Q^{-(b-3)C_\tau}
Q^{-(c-1)C_\tau}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}
\le
Q^{
C_T
-(a-1)C_\varepsilon
-(b+c-4)C_\tau
}.
\]

This is the correct residual audit.

---

# 3. Classification by valuation

## 3.1 Same valuation terms

If

\[
(a,b,c)=(1,3,1),
\]

then \(T\) is not an error. It belongs in the effective matrix:

\[
L_{\rm eff}.
\]

So every term of the form

\[
q_0u^3(a\Gamma_G+b\Gamma_{G,2})
\]

must be absorbed into \(L_N\), not bounded as residual.

D4 then requires

\[
\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

## 3.2 Higher \(q_0\)-valuation terms

If

\[
a\ge2,\quad b=3,\quad c=1,
\]

then

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}
\le
Q^{C_T-(a-1)C_\varepsilon}.
\]

These terms become **smaller** when \(\varepsilon\) is smaller. They never create an upper bound on \(C_\varepsilon\); they help wall escape.

So terms like

\[
q_0^2u^3\Gamma
\]

are automatically perturbative if

\[
C_\varepsilon>C_T+O(1).
\]

## 3.3 Higher anisotropy terms

If

\[
a=1,\quad b=3,\quad c\ge2,
\]

then

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}
\le
Q^{C_T-(c-1)C_\tau}
\]

provided \(|\Gamma|\) is controlled by the wall-escape lower scale. But this only uses a lower bound; if \(|\Gamma|\) can be large, the term may not be small. So nonlinear anisotropy terms require either:

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{-K}
\]

for controlled-anisotropy sampling, or the nonlinear row-polynomial observability audit discussed earlier.

They do **not** create an \(\varepsilon\)-corridor; they create an anisotropy-size branch.

## 3.4 Lower \(u\)-valuation terms

If

\[
b<3,
\]

then the ratio contains

\[
Q^{(3-b)C_\tau}.
\]

These terms are dangerous near small source. They must either be absent by filtration, absorbed into a different leading normal form, or controlled by stronger source lower bounds. For wall-escape samples, \(u\sim\tau\), so lower \(u\)-valuation terms can dominate.

Thus a term like

\[
q_0u^2\Gamma
\]

is not a harmless residual. It signals that the leading factor should be

\[
q_0u^2
\]

rather than

\[
q_0u^3,
\]

or that the term must vanish by the row-filtration structure.

## 3.5 Non-\(q_0\)-divisible terms

If

\[
a=0,
\]

then near the wall

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}}
\sim |q_0|^{-1},
\]

so it is not a D4 error. It is a wall-live contribution.

Such a term belongs to D3 directly:

\[
R_{\rm wall}:=\mathbf A_N\bmod(q_0).
\]

If nonzero and coercive under wall Gate 2 mass, it solves the wall without wall escape. If it is not coercive, it must be included in a \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil audit.

---

# 4. Refined D4 residual theorem

The D4 residual condition should be stated termwise:

## Valuation-Relative Residual Control

After extracting all same-valuation linear terms into \(L_N\), every residual term \(T\) must satisfy one of:

1. **higher \(q_0\)-valuation**:

   \[
   a\ge2,\quad b\ge3,\quad c\ge1;
   \]

2. **higher anisotropy valuation**, handled by controlled-anisotropy sampling or nonlinear row observability:

   \[
   a\ge1,\quad b\ge3,\quad c\ge2;
   \]

3. **tail/canonical error with explicit small coefficient**:

   \[
   |E_T|\le Q^{-K_T}
   \]

   large enough to beat any valuation loss;

4. **wall-live term**, moved out of D4 and into the wall-row branch.

Then projected residual control follows without an absolute \(\varepsilon\)-corridor.

---

# 5. Corridor only applies to absolute residuals

Let

\[
\mathbf R_N=\mathbf R_{\rm val}+\mathbf R_{\rm abs},
\]

where \(\mathbf R_{\rm val}\) consists of terms with explicit \(q_0,u,\Gamma\)-valuation, and \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\) is an absolute canonical/tail/projection floor.

The corridor audit applies only to

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}.
\]

If

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}=0
\]

or if it is super-polynomially / arbitrarily polynomially small by choosing truncation depth, then the corridor is automatically open.

Thus the correct final condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|
\le
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
}
\]

But valuation-relative residuals need only satisfy relative inequalities, not absolute thresholds.

---

# 6. How this changes the prior threshold audit

Previously, the row residual exponent requirement was

\[
C_R^{\rm row}
\ge
\max\left\{
\frac{7A}{2}+7C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
\frac{9A}{2}+5C_\Gamma+2C_G+C_L
\right\}
+O(1).
\]

Now this requirement should be assigned only to absolute residuals:

\[
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
\max\left\{
\frac{7A}{2}+7C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
\frac{9A}{2}+5C_\Gamma+2C_G+C_L
\right\}
+O(1).
\]

If the D4 residuals are all valuation-relative, this harsh bound is unnecessary.

The finite audit must therefore answer:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Are D4 residuals valuation-relative or absolute?}
}
\]

This is the decisive next row-side question.

---

# 7. Practical D4 audit update

The D4 row audit should produce a table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{term} & (a,b,c) & \text{classification} & \text{required bound}\\
\hline
q_0u^3\Gamma & (1,3,1) & L_N & \sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}\\
q_0^2u^3\Gamma & (2,3,1) & perturbative & C_\varepsilon>C_T\\
q_0u^3\Gamma^2 & (1,3,2) & nonlinear anisotropy & controlled-\Gamma\text{ or row-polynomial}\\
q_0u^2\Gamma & (1,2,1) & dangerous lower-source & absent/absorb/redefine leading\\
u^3\Gamma & (0,3,1) & wall-live & D3/q_0\text{-adic branch}\\
E_{\rm tail} & \text{none} & absolute & corridor bound
\end{array}
\]

This table is more precise than a single “half-leading residual” condition.

---

# 8. Consequence for saturated rows

If the only difficult residuals are \(q_0\)-valuation-related, then saturated rows

\[
\widehat{\mathbf A}_N=\mathbf A_N/q_0
\]

remove the \(\varepsilon\)-loss entirely.

But the valuation audit shows saturated rows are needed only if an absolute residual floor prevents the original rows from satisfying the corridor.

If all residuals are \(q_0\)-divisible, original rows still work after choosing \(C_\varepsilon\) large enough, because both leading and residual shrink together.

---

# 9. Final extra audit result

The threshold corridor is real only for absolute residuals. The D4 residual audit should be refined from:

\[
|\mathbf R_N|\le Q^{-C_R}
\]

to:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf R_N
=
\mathbf R_{\rm same}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm val}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm abs},
}
\]

where:

- \(\mathbf R_{\rm same}\) is absorbed into \(L_N\);
- \(\mathbf R_{\rm val}\) is controlled by monomial valuation relative to \(q_0u^3\Gamma\);
- \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\) must satisfy the explicit corridor exponent.

This is the sharper and likely correct final D4 compatibility condition.

---

# 10. Verdict

The “threshold corridor” is not a generic obstruction. It only applies to residual terms lacking the same vanishing structure as the leading rows.

Therefore the next and final D4 audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Classify every residual by }(q_0,u,\Gamma)\text{-valuation.}
}
\]

If all non-absorbed residuals are valuation-relative or sufficiently small absolute canonical tails, then wall escape and D4 are compatible.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:14:48)

_Thought for 10s_

## Final D4 valuation audit — residuals versus the wall-escape threshold

Executing the final audit: classify D4 residuals by their \((q_0,u,\Gamma)\)-valuation and determine which terms create a real threshold-corridor obstruction. The current downstream architecture is:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{local wall escape}
+
\text{D4 row-span conversion}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
\]

The latest prompt set explicitly identifies D4 as a row-span/principal-rank plus projected-residual control problem, with the wall handled by first-exit sampling under row-energy architecture. 

---

# 1. D4 normal form

We want

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

where

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
\]

and

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge |\Gamma_G|\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore the leading D4 scale is

\[
S_{\rm lead}
=
|q_0|\,|u|^3\,\sigma_2(L_N)\,|\Gamma|
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
\]

The final audit asks:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Which residual terms are genuinely smaller than }S_{\rm lead}?
}
\]

---

# 2. Residual decomposition

Decompose

\[
\mathbf R_N
=
\mathbf R_{\rm same}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm val}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}.
\]

## 2.1 Same-valuation linear terms

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm same}
\]

contains all terms of the form

\[
q_0u^3M(Y)\Gamma.
\]

These are **not errors**. They must be absorbed into the effective leading matrix:

\[
L_{\rm eff}=L_N+M(Y).
\]

The required condition is then

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})\ge Q^{-C_L}.
}
\]

So terms with valuation

\[
(a,b,c)=(1,3,1)
\]

are Green if absorbed into \(L_{\rm eff}\), not bounded as residuals.

---

## 2.2 Valuation-relative residuals

A residual monomial has schematic form

\[
T=q_0^a u^b \Gamma^c E_T,
\]

where

\[
|E_T|\le Q^{C_T}
\]

or better.

Relative to the leading scale

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma,
\]

we have

\[
\frac{|T|}{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
\le
Q^{C_T}
|q_0|^{a-1}
|u|^{b-3}
|\Gamma|^{c-1}.
\]

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
|u|,|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Thus

\[
\frac{|T|}{S_{\rm lead}/\sigma_2(L_N)}
\le
Q^{C_T-(a-1)C_\varepsilon-(b+c-4)C_\tau}.
\]

This is the key valuation test.

A valuation-relative term is acceptable if

\[
\boxed{
C_T-(a-1)C_\varepsilon-(b+c-4)C_\tau
\le
-C_L-O(1).
}
\]

---

## 2.3 Absolute residual floor

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}
\]

contains canonical/tail/projection/truncation errors that do **not** carry useful factors of

\[
q_0,\quad u,\quad \Gamma.
\]

For these, the previous threshold-corridor audit applies:

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|
\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}}
\]

must beat

\[
S_{\rm lead}.
\]

So one needs

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+4C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

After optimizing thresholds, this becomes the explicit corridor condition:

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
\max\left\{
\frac{7A}{2}+7C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
\frac{9A}{2}+5C_\Gamma+2C_G+C_L
\right\}
+O(1).
}
\]

This harsh condition applies **only** to absolute residuals.

---

# 3. Valuation classification table

The D4 audit should classify every row term as follows.

| Term type | Valuation \((a,b,c)\) | Classification | Required action |
|---|---:|---|---|
| \(q_0u^3\Gamma\) | \((1,3,1)\) | same leading scale | absorb into \(L_{\rm eff}\) |
| \(q_0^2u^3\Gamma\) | \((2,3,1)\) | higher \(q_0\)-valuation | perturbative if \(C_\varepsilon>C_T+C_L\) |
| \(q_0^ku^3\Gamma,\ k\ge2\) | \((k,3,1)\) | higher wall order | perturbative for large \(C_\varepsilon\) |
| \(q_0u^4\Gamma\) | \((1,4,1)\) | same / variable coefficient | absorb into \(L_{\rm eff}(Y)\), not error |
| \(q_0u^2\Gamma\) | \((1,2,1)\) | dangerous lower \(u\)-valuation | must be absent, absorbed by redefining leading scale, or separately controlled |
| \(q_0u^3\Gamma^2\) | \((1,3,2)\) | nonlinear anisotropy | controlled-anisotropy / row-polynomial observability |
| \(q_0u^3\Gamma^k,\ k\ge2\) | \((1,3,k)\) | nonlinear anisotropy | finite row-polynomial audit |
| \(u^3\Gamma\) | \((0,3,1)\) | wall-live | move to D3/source-robust or \(q_0\)-adic branch |
| \(E_{\rm tail}\), \(E_2\), truncation floor | none | absolute residual | must satisfy corridor exponent |
| projection/gauge denominator artifact | variable | potential absolute residual | either prove valuation-relative or include in corridor |
| row-normalization error | variable | depends on formula | absorb if linear, otherwise valuation/absolute audit |

---

# 4. Final audit results by term class

## 4.1 Terms absorbed into \(L_{\rm eff}\)

All terms linear in \(\Gamma\) and divisible by \(q_0u^3\) must be absorbed:

\[
q_0u^3
\begin{pmatrix}
a_{11}&a_{12}\\
a_{21}&a_{22}\\
\vdots&\vdots
\end{pmatrix}
\Gamma.
\]

These change the row matrix but are harmless if

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})\ge Q^{-C_L}.
}
\]

This is exactly Agent 5’s row-span/principal-rank audit.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite D4 row-symbol audit required.}
}
\]

Expected easy case:

\[
A_7\sim -\frac{1}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9\sim -\frac{1}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

so

\[
\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})\asymp 1.
\]

---

## 4.2 Higher \(q_0\)-valuation terms

Terms like

\[
q_0^2u^3\Gamma
\]

have relative size

\[
\frac{|q_0^2u^3\Gamma|}{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
=
|q_0|
=
Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

These improve when the wall threshold is made smaller.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Green once }C_\varepsilon>C_T+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

They do not create a corridor obstruction.

---

## 4.3 Higher \(u\)-valuation terms

Terms like

\[
q_0u^4\Gamma
\]

are not automatically small; they have relative size

\[
|u|.
\]

Since \(|u|\) is only polynomially bounded, not necessarily small, these should be absorbed into

\[
L_{\rm eff}(Y)
\]

as variable coefficients if they are linear in \(\Gamma\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{absorb into }L_{\rm eff};\text{ then audit }\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff}).
}
\]

---

## 4.4 Lower \(u\)-valuation terms

Terms like

\[
q_0u^2\Gamma
\]

are dangerous because relative to the leading scale they are

\[
|u|^{-1},
\]

which can be large near wall-escape samples where

\[
|u|\sim\tau.
\]

These terms cannot be treated as residual.

They require one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove absent by row filtration;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{absorb into a redefined leading scale }q_0u^2L\Gamma;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{use stronger source lower bounds;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{add rows / change row normalization.}
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{must be explicitly ruled out or promoted to leading structure.}
}
\]

This is a real audit item.

---

## 4.5 Nonlinear anisotropy terms

Terms like

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma^2
\]

are not automatically small unless the D4 sample is in a controlled-anisotropy layer.

They require one of:

1. prove absent at principal row order;
2. prove they contain already-controlled lower channel \(\Gamma_G\);
3. use controlled-anisotropy sampling;
4. use finite row-polynomial observability;
5. use nonzero root-trap rigidity.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite nonlinear row-polynomial audit required if present.}
}
\]

Expected easy case: absent, because the displayed row asymptotics are linear:

\[
A_7\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

---

## 4.6 Non-\(q_0\)-divisible terms

Terms with valuation

\[
a=0
\]

are not D4 errors.

Modulo \(q_0\), they produce wall-live rows:

\[
\mathbf A_N\bmod(q_0)\ne0.
\]

They should be handled as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 direct wall row / }q_0\text{-adic row-pencil branch.}
}
\]

If coercive under wall Gate 2 mass, they solve the wall directly. If not, they need a separate row-pencil audit.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{move out of D4 residual; do not bound as error.}
}
\]

---

## 4.7 Absolute canonical/tail/projection floor

These are the only terms subject to the harsh corridor exponent.

If

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\ne0
\]

and only has

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}},
\]

then D3a/D4 compatibility requires

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
\max\left\{
\frac{7A}{2}+7C_\Gamma+2C_{u'}+C_L,\,
\frac{9A}{2}+5C_\Gamma+2C_G+C_L
\right\}
+O(1).
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{corridor audit applies only here.}
}
\]

If \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\) can be made arbitrarily polynomially small by truncation depth / tail control, this is Green.

---

# 5. Final D4 residual theorem

## Valuation-Aware D4 Residual Theorem

After extracting all same-valuation linear terms into \(L_{\rm eff}\), assume:

1. principal rank:

\[
\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})\ge Q^{-C_L};
\]

2. every valuation-relative residual term satisfies its monomial-relative bound:

\[
C_T-(a-1)C_\varepsilon-(b+c-4)C_\tau
\le
-C_L-O(1);
\]

3. every nonlinear anisotropy residual is either absent, controlled by row-polynomial observability, or handled by controlled-anisotropy/root-trap arguments;

4. every non-\(q_0\)-divisible residual is moved to the wall-row branch;

5. every absolute residual satisfies the corridor exponent.

Then

\[
\boxed{
|P_L\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Therefore D4 residual control holds.

---

# 6. Final audit checklist

To complete the D4 residual audit, the row formulas must produce a table with columns:

\[
\boxed{
\text{term},\quad
(a,b,c),\quad
\text{coefficient size},\quad
\text{classification},\quad
\text{disposition}.
}
\]

For each term:

- \((1,3,1)\): absorb into \(L_{\rm eff}\).
- \(a\ge2,b\ge3,c=1\): perturbative by \(q_0\)-valuation.
- \(b<3\): dangerous; prove absent or redefine leading scale.
- \(c\ge2\): nonlinear anisotropy; finite row-polynomial audit.
- \(a=0\): wall-live; D3/q-adic branch.
- no valuation: absolute; must satisfy corridor exponent.

This is the final audit protocol.

---

# 7. Verdict

The threshold corridor is not a general obstruction. It applies only to absolute residual floors.

The D4 residual problem is now reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{valuation classification of all row residuals}
}
\]

plus

\[
\boxed{
\text{principal rank of }L_{\rm eff}.
}
\]

If the expected row structure

\[
A_7\sim H\Gamma_G,\qquad A_9\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

is literal and the remaining terms are valuation-relative or controllably small canonical tails, then D4 and wall escape are compatible.

_Thought for 7s_

## Continuing attack — eliminate the “lower \(u\)-valuation” danger

The final valuation audit left one genuinely dangerous residual class:

\[
q_0u^b\Gamma,\qquad b<3.
\]

Terms of this type are dangerous because the D4 leading model is

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\]

and at wall-escape samples

\[
|u|\sim \tau\ll1
\]

may be polynomially small. So

\[
q_0u^2\Gamma
\]

would dominate

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma
\]

by a factor

\[
|u|^{-1}.
\]

This cannot be treated as an error. The right attack is to show such terms are either impossible by the row filtration, or they must be promoted into a better leading normal form. The current downstream structure already places D4 as a principal-rank and projected-residual audit after wall escape and row mobility. 

---

# 1. Lower \(u\)-valuation terms are not errors

Suppose a row contains

\[
T=q_0u^2(a\Gamma_G+b\Gamma_{G,2}).
\]

Then relative to

\[
q_0u^3L\Gamma,
\]

we get

\[
\frac{|T|}{|q_0u^3\Gamma|}
\asymp |u|^{-1}.
\]

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
|u|\ge \tau=Q^{-C_\tau},
\]

so

\[
|u|^{-1}\le Q^{C_\tau}.
\]

This can be large. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
q_0u^2\Gamma\text{ cannot be put in }\mathbf R_N.
}
\]

It must either be absent, or the leading scale should be redefined.

---

# 2. If lower-\(u\) terms exist, they improve D4

If the row expansion contains

\[
q_0u^2M_2\Gamma
\]

with

\[
\sigma_2(M_2)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then the row lower bound is stronger than before:

\[
|\mathbf A_N|
\gtrsim
|q_0||u|^2|\Gamma|.
\]

At a D4 sample,

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

so

\[
|u||\Gamma|\ge Q^{-A_2/2}.
\]

Then

\[
|q_0||u|^2|\Gamma|
=
|q_0||u|\,(|u||\Gamma|).
\]

If \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\), this gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C_q-C_u-A_2/2-C}.
\]

Thus lower \(u\)-valuation terms are not a problem if they have rank two. They are a stronger leading structure.

So the correct D4 normal form should be ordered by \(u\)-valuation:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma
+
\text{higher \(u\)-valuation / residual},
}
\]

where \(b_\ast\) is the minimal \(u\)-power appearing in the anisotropy-linear row symbol.

D4 only needs:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(L_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Minimal-\(u\)-valuation D4 theorem

Define

\[
b_\ast
=
\min\{b:\text{ some anisotropy-linear row term }q_0u^bM_b\Gamma\text{ appears}\}.
\]

Let

\[
L_\ast
\]

be the coefficient matrix of all row terms with valuation

\[
q_0u^{b_\ast}\Gamma.
\]

Assume

\[
\sigma_2(L_\ast)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Write

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast.
\]

Then D4 closes if

\[
|\mathbf R_\ast|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast)|\Gamma|.
\]

At a D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}.
\]

Using \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\), we get

\[
|q_0||u|^{b_\ast}|\Gamma|
=
|q_0||u|^{b_\ast-1}(|u||\Gamma|)
\ge
Q^{-C_q-(b_\ast-1)C_u-A_2/2}.
\]

So any finite \(b_\ast\ge1\) is acceptable.

If \(b_\ast=0\), the row is even stronger:

\[
q_0L_\ast\Gamma.
\]

Thus the \(u^3\) leading scale was overly specific. The row audit should identify the **lowest anisotropy-linear \(u\)-valuation** and use that as the leading scale.

---

# 4. Updated valuation classification

The previous table treated \(q_0u^2\Gamma\) as dangerous. It is only dangerous if one insists on \(u^3\) as the leading factor.

The corrected classification is:

| Term type | Classification | Action |
|---|---|---|
| \(q_0u^b\Gamma\), minimal \(b=b_\ast\) | leading | build \(L_\ast\) |
| \(q_0u^b\Gamma\), \(b>b_\ast\) | higher \(u\)-valuation | perturbative if \(u\) small, or absorb if not |
| \(q_0u^b\Gamma\), \(b<b_\ast\) | impossible by definition | update \(b_\ast\) |
| \(q_0^2u^b\Gamma\) | higher wall order | perturbative via \(q_0\) |
| \(q_0u^b\Gamma^2\) | nonlinear anisotropy | row-polynomial audit |
| \(u^b\Gamma\) | wall-live | D3/q-adic direct wall branch |
| absolute tail | absolute residual | threshold-corridor audit |

So the D4 normal form should be:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast.
}
\]

The special \(b_\ast=3\) follows only if the raw row principal symbol really starts at \(u^3\).

---

# 5. Does the known row structure force \(b_\ast=3\)?

The displayed structure says

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

If this is the first nonzero anisotropy-linear structure, then

\[
b_\ast=3.
\]

But if correction rows contain terms like

\[
q_0u^2\Gamma,
\]

then those terms would actually precede \(H\Gamma\) in \(u\)-valuation and should have appeared in the stated leading asymptotics. Therefore, consistency of the stated leading structure strongly suggests:

\[
\boxed{
\text{lower \(u\)-valuation anisotropy-linear terms are absent.}
}
\]

This should be included as part of the principal-symbol audit:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gr}_{q_0u^b\Gamma}(A_N)=0\quad\text{for }b<3.
}
\]

If true, no lower-\(u\) danger remains.

---

# 6. Final D4 audit should be lexicographic

Use a lexicographic valuation order:

\[
(a,b,c)
=
(\text{\(q_0\)-power},\text{\(u\)-power},\text{\(\Gamma\)-degree}).
\]

For the non-wall row-conversion branch, fix \(a=1\) and \(c=1\), then find minimal \(b\).

The audit:

1. Compute all terms linear in \(\Gamma\) and divisible by \(q_0\).
2. Among them, find minimal \(u\)-valuation \(b_\ast\).
3. Build \(L_\ast\) from terms with valuation \(q_0u^{b_\ast}\Gamma\).
4. Prove \(\sigma_2(L_\ast)\ge Q^{-C}\).
5. Treat terms with \(b>b_\ast\) as residual or absorb into variable \(L\), depending on size.
6. Terms with \(a=0\) are wall-live and moved to D3 direct branch.
7. Terms with \(c\ge2\) go to nonlinear row-polynomial audit.

This lexicographic audit avoids falsely classifying stronger leading terms as dangerous errors.

---

# 7. Threshold corridor with general \(b_\ast\)

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|,|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

The leading scale becomes

\[
S_{\rm lead}^{(b_\ast)}
=
|q_0||u|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast)|\Gamma|
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

If there is an absolute residual floor

\[
Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}},
\]

the corridor condition becomes

\[
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

The previous formula used \(b_\ast=3\), giving \(4C_\tau\). For general \(b_\ast\), replace

\[
4C_\tau
\]

by

\[
(b_\ast+1)C_\tau.
\]

This is strictly better if \(b_\ast<3\), worse if \(b_\ast>3\).

Thus the final residual-corridor audit should depend on \(b_\ast\).

---

# 8. Updated final theorem

## Minimal-Valuation D4 Row Conversion

Let

\[
b_\ast
\]

be the least \(u\)-valuation among \(q_0\)-divisible, anisotropy-linear row symbols. Suppose

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast,
\]

\[
\sigma_2(L_\ast)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_\ast|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at any D4 sample,

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) or \(|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma}\), one obtains

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

With row mobility,

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

This strictly generalizes the \(u^3\) version.

---

# 9. Final extra finding

The previous “lower \(u\)-valuation danger” is not necessarily a problem. It is a signal that the chosen D4 leading normalization was not minimal.

The correct final audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{find the minimal \(u\)-valuation anisotropy-linear row symbol and use it as leading.}
}
\]

If the known \(H\Gamma\) structure is truly leading, then \(b_\ast=3\) and lower-\(u\) terms are absent by filtration.

If lower-\(u\) terms exist and have rank two, D4 becomes easier.

If lower-\(u\) terms exist but rank one, include them first, then proceed to higher \(u\)-valuation layers as a filtered row observability problem.

This is the most robust D4 formulation.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:19:14)

_Thought for 7s_

## One step further — filtered row observability by minimal valuation layers

The previous step corrected D4’s normal form. Instead of assuming the leading factor is always

\[
q_0u^3\Gamma,
\]

we should find the **minimal \(u\)-valuation** among all \(q_0\)-divisible anisotropy-linear row terms:

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast.
\]

Now go one step further: what if the minimal layer exists but has only **rank one**? Then D4 is not dead. We should continue through the \(u\)-valuation filtration until the accumulated row-symbol layers span both anisotropy directions. This turns D4 into a finite **filtered observability theorem**. This is consistent with the current downstream architecture, where D4 is a row-span/principal-rank plus residual-control audit after wall escape and row mobility. 

---

# 1. Define the \(u\)-valuation row filtration

For the \(q_0\)-divisible, anisotropy-linear part of the row vector, write

\[
\mathbf A_N^{\rm lin}
=
q_0\sum_{b\ge b_0} u^b L_b\Gamma,
\]

where

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
\]

and \(L_b\) is a row matrix collecting all terms of valuation

\[
q_0u^b\Gamma.
\]

So the full row expansion is

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0\left(
u^{b_0}L_{b_0}
+
u^{b_0+1}L_{b_0+1}
+
u^{b_0+2}L_{b_0+2}
+\cdots
\right)\Gamma
+
\mathbf R_{\rm nonlin}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}.
\]

The old D4 corresponds to the special case

\[
b_0=3,
\qquad
L_{b_0}=L_3,
\qquad
\sigma_2(L_3)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

But if

\[
\sigma_2(L_{b_0})=0,
\]

we should not stop. We should inspect the next layers.

---

# 2. Cumulative filtered matrix

Define the cumulative matrix through valuation \(B\):

\[
L_{\le B}(u)
=
\sum_{b=b_0}^{B}u^{b-b_0}L_b.
\]

Then

\[
\mathbf A_N^{\rm lin}
=
q_0u^{b_0}L_{\le B}(u)\Gamma
+
q_0\sum_{b>B}u^bL_b\Gamma.
\]

D4 closes if, for some finite \(B\),

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2(L_{\le B}(u))\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the D4 sampling set, and the higher layers plus nonlinear/absolute residuals are half-leading.

This is stronger and more flexible than requiring the first layer \(L_{b_0}\) alone to have rank two.

---

# 3. Rank-one first layer is acceptable

Suppose

\[
L_{b_0}
\]

has rank one. It observes one anisotropy direction, say

\[
v_0\cdot\Gamma.
\]

Then split:

## Case 1: observed direction is live

If

\[
|L_{b_0}\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C}|\Gamma|,
\]

then the first layer already gives

\[
|\mathbf A_N|
\gtrsim
|q_0||u|^{b_0}Q^{-C}|\Gamma|.
\]

D4 closes.

## Case 2: anisotropy lies near the kernel of \(L_{b_0}\)

If

\[
|L_{b_0}\Gamma|\ll |\Gamma|,
\]

then \(\Gamma\) lies near a one-dimensional kernel direction. On that branch, the next layer

\[
L_{b_0+1}
\]

only needs to be nonzero on the kernel of \(L_{b_0}\).

So D4 closes if

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{\Gamma\in \ker L_{b_0},\,|\Gamma|=1}
|L_{b_0+1}\Gamma|
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

If not, continue to \(L_{b_0+2}\), etc.

Thus D4 is a finite filtered observability problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{successive \(u\)-valuation layers must separate the remaining anisotropy kernel.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Filtered observability criterion

Let

\[
K_{b_0-1}:=\mathbb C^2.
\]

Define recursively

\[
K_b
=
K_{b-1}\cap \ker L_b.
\]

Then \(K_b\) is the anisotropy subspace invisible through valuation \(b\).

The row tower observes both anisotropy directions by valuation \(B\) iff

\[
\boxed{
K_B=\{0\}.
}
\]

Quantitatively, we need a polynomial lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{b=b_0}^{B}
|u|^{2(b-b_0)}
|L_b\Gamma|^2
\ge
Q^{-C}|\Gamma|^2
\quad
\forall \Gamma.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_2
\left(
\begin{pmatrix}
L_{b_0}\\
uL_{b_0+1}\\
\vdots\\
u^{B-b_0}L_B
\end{pmatrix}
\right)
\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is the correct filtered version of the D4 rank condition.

---

# 5. Cost of delayed observability

If the second anisotropy direction is only detected at layer \(B\), then the leading scale loses powers of \(|u|\):

\[
S_{\rm lead}^{(B)}
\sim
|q_0|\,|u|^B\,|\Gamma|.
\]

At a wall-escape sample,

\[
|q_0|=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

So

\[
S_{\rm lead}^{(B)}
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+(B+1)C_\tau+C_L)}.
\]

Thus delayed observability is still acceptable for fixed finite \(B\), but it tightens the residual corridor.

The absolute residual condition becomes

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(B+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

So the audit should report not only whether rank two appears, but **at which \(u\)-valuation layer** it appears.

---

# 6. Updated D4 theorem: filtered version

## Filtered D4 Row-Conversion Theorem

Assume the anisotropy-linear row part has expansion

\[
\mathbf A_N^{\rm lin}
=
q_0\sum_{b=b_0}^{B}u^bL_b\Gamma
+
\mathbf E_{\rm high}.
\]

Define the filtered matrix

\[
\mathcal L_{[b_0,B]}(u)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
L_{b_0}\\
uL_{b_0+1}\\
\vdots\\
u^{B-b_0}L_B
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Assume

\[
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_{[b_0,B]}(u))
\ge Q^{-C_L}
\]

on the D4 sample set.

Assume residual control:

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^{b_0}
\sigma_2(\mathcal L_{[b_0,B]}(u))
|\Gamma|.
\]

Then

\[
|\mathbf A_N|
\ge
Q^{-C}
\]

at every D4 sample, and row mobility gives row energy.

This theorem includes the cases:

- \(B=b_0=3\): original \(q_0u^3L\Gamma\) theorem;
- \(b_0<3\): stronger leading rows;
- rank-one first layer with second direction appearing later;
- extended rows \(A_{11},A_{13},\ldots\).

---

# 7. Practical finite audit

The row-symbol audit should now produce this table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{\(u\)-valuation }b & L_b & \operatorname{rank}L_b & K_b\\
\hline
b_0 & L_{b_0} & \cdots & K_{b_0}\\
b_0+1 & L_{b_0+1} & \cdots & K_{b_0+1}\\
b_0+2 & L_{b_0+2} & \cdots & K_{b_0+2}\\
\vdots & \vdots & \vdots & \vdots
\end{array}
\]

Stop when

\[
K_b=\{0\}.
\]

If the table never reaches \(K_b=\{0\}\) for the known rows, then the row architecture is blind to one anisotropy direction.

Expected outcome:

\[
b_0=3,\qquad
L_3\sim
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&1
\end{pmatrix},
\]

so the table stops immediately.

---

# 8. Extra hidden issue: cancellation between valuation layers

Could

\[
L_{b_0}
+
uL_{b_0+1}
\]

lose rank by cancellation?

Yes, but this is a finite polynomial determinant issue in \(u\). Define

\[
D(u)=\det L_{\le B}(u)
\]

or, for tall matrices,

\[
D(u)=\sum_{i<j}|\Delta_{ij}(u)|^2.
\]

If \(D(u)\) has zeros, they are secondary row walls. Handle them by:

1. adding more rows/layers;
2. root escape in \(u\);
3. finite gcd/resultant audit.

But if \(L_{b_0}\) is already full rank with determinant bounded below, no inter-layer cancellation matters. So this issue only arises if rank is completed by multiple layers.

---

# 9. Refined final audit result

The previous minimal-valuation audit said:

\[
\text{use the smallest \(b_\ast\) with rank two.}
\]

The refined version is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{use the smallest filtered block }[b_0,B]\text{ whose cumulative matrix has rank two.}
}
\]

This handles rank-one minimal layers and delayed anisotropy detection.

The cost is replacing the leading scale

\[
|q_0||u|^{b_\ast}|\Gamma|
\]

by

\[
|q_0||u|^{B}|\Gamma|
\]

if the second direction appears at valuation \(B\).

---

# 10. Verdict

One step further reveals the fully robust D4 formulation:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0\sum_b u^bL_b\Gamma
+
\text{nonlinear/absolute residuals},
}
\]

and D4 closes once the cumulative filtered row matrix observes both anisotropy directions with polynomial margin.

This is the final form of the D4 row-symbol audit.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:45:01)

_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 4 / D — Wall escape and row-energy theorem, final form

Executing Agent 4’s lane: close D3a as a theorem under row-energy architecture. The current downstream target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{curvature-compatible wall escape}
+
\text{D4}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

The latest shared background explicitly treats old \(D1/D2/D3\), Remez/Cartan, and pointwise target-smallness as fallback only; the active route is Gate 2 via \(u'\)-source thickening and \(L^2\)-input real rigidity, followed by wall escape and D4 quotient row conversion. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
q=q_0,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

Assume Gate 2:

\[
\int_I G\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Assume curvature compatibility:

\[
q_0''=u,
\]

or robustly, on the escape neighborhood,

\[
|q_0''-u|\le \tau/8.
\]

This compatibility is essential. If \(q_0''\) is not the canonical source curvature, wall escape does not follow from \(|u|\) alone.

---

# 2. Non-wall / wall split

Fix

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q|\ge\varepsilon\},
\qquad
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then, since \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

At this point,

\[
|q(m_\ast)|\ge \varepsilon,
\]

so \(m_\ast\) is a non-wall D4 sample. D4 then applies directly.

---

# 3. Wall branch and low-source removal

Assume wall mass dominates:

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Let

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

On \(I_{\rm wall,low}\),

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le \tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

To prevent low-source wall points from carrying all Gate 2 mass, require

\[
\tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}\le \frac14Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
}
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G\,dm\ge \frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 4. Complex first-exit wall escape

Pick

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Then

\[
|q(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau.
\]

For complex \(q\), define

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(m_0)}}{|u(m_0)|},
\qquad
Q(m)=\Re(e q(m)).
\]

If \(q''=u\), then

\[
Q''(m_0)=|u(m_0)|\ge \tau.
\]

If \(|q''-u|\le\tau/8\), then

\[
Q''(m)=\Re(eu(m))+\Re(e(q''(m)-u(m))).
\]

Using

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1},
\]

on an interval of normalized radius \(\rho\), one has

\[
|u(m)-u(m_0)|\le Q^{C_{u'}}\rho.
\]

Thus if

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le \tau/8,
\]

then

\[
Q''(m)\ge c\tau
\]

on the local interval.

Set

\[
\rho\asymp \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

The stability condition becomes

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}\le Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
}
\]

Since \(Q(m)\) is a real function with \(Q''\ge c\tau\), it exits the strip \(|Q|<\varepsilon\) within distance \(O(\rho|I|)\). Hence \(q\) exits \(|q|<\varepsilon\): there exists \(m_1\) with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho|I|,
\]

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

---

# 5. Boundary-layer control

The first-exit proof needs \(m_0\) away from \(\partial I\).

Let

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho|I|\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho|I|.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G\,dm\le 2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|.
\]

To make this \(<\frac18 Q^{-A}|I|\), require

\[
\rho Q^{C_G}\le Q^{-A-O(1)}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
}
\]

Therefore it suffices to choose

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge
\max\{3C_\tau+2C_{u'},\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G\}+O(1).
}
\]

Then the boundary layer cannot carry all live wall mass, so an interior wall-live \(m_0\) exists.

---

# 6. Signal survival at first exit

At \(m_1\),

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

we get

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge |u(m_1)|-6|q(m_1)|-2|q(m_1)|^3.
\]

If

\[
\varepsilon\ll \tau,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
G(m_1)=|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge |u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

So \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample:

\[
|q(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
G(m_1)\ge c\tau^4.
\]

---

# 7. D4 black box at the escaped sample

Use D4 in its general valuation / filtered form:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q\,u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast,
\]

or, if delayed observability is needed,

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q\sum_{b=b_0}^{B}u^bL_b\Gamma+\text{residual}.
\]

The D4 input required at \(m_1\) is:

\[
\sigma_2(L_\ast)\ge Q^{-C_L}
\]

or its filtered analogue, and residual control:

\[
|\mathbf R_\ast|
\le \frac12 |q|\,|u|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at \(m_1\),

\[
|q|=\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon},
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\ge Q^{-C_\tau-O(1)}.
\]

Hence

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
\]

If using a filtered block through valuation \(B\), replace \(b_\ast\) by \(B\):

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+(B+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
\]

---

# 8. Residual corridor only for absolute residuals

Decompose

\[
\mathbf R=\mathbf R_{\rm same}+\mathbf R_{\rm val}+\mathbf R_{\rm abs}.
\]

- \(\mathbf R_{\rm same}\): same-valuation anisotropy-linear terms; absorb into \(L_\ast\).
- \(\mathbf R_{\rm val}\): terms with \(q,u,\Gamma\)-valuation; control relatively.
- \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\): absolute canonical/tail/projection floors.

Only \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\) needs a wall-threshold corridor.

If

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}},
\]

then compatibility with the escaped leading scale requires

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

For delayed observability through layer \(B\), use

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(B+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

This is the precise residual-corridor condition.

If all residuals are valuation-relative or can be made arbitrarily polynomially small, no extra obstruction appears.

---

# 9. Row mobility to row energy

Assume row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

then on an interval of length

\[
\gg Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|
\]

around \(m_1\),

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_I |\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

This proves row energy.

---

# 10. Final theorem

## D3a Wall Escape + D4 Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. local upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1};
\]

3. curvature compatibility:

\[
q_0''=u
\quad\text{or}\quad
|q_0''-u|\le\tau/8
\]

on wall-escape neighborhoods;

4. D4 valuation/filtered row conversion at non-wall samples;

5. row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1};
\]

6. absolute residuals satisfy the residual corridor if present.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 11. Verdict

D3a is closed as a **row-energy theorem** under the following finite/local checks:

1. curvature compatibility \(q_0''\approx u\);
2. local complexity for \(G,\Gamma,u'\);
3. D4 valuation/filtered rank;
4. D4 residual corridor only for absolute residuals;
5. row derivative bound.

If the final architecture is exact-point locked, D3a fails and one must use the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil/source-robust fallback. Under row-energy architecture, D3a is no longer a conceptual blocker.

## One step further — hidden gauge-consistency issue for \(q_0\)

The next possible hidden issue is not in the escape geometry. It is in the **identity of the variable \(q_0\)**.

The wall-escape proof uses \(q_0\) in three different roles:

\[
q_0''\approx u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\mathbf A_N \sim q_0 u^{b_\ast}L\Gamma.
\]

For the argument to be valid, these must refer to the **same canonical scalar \(q_0\)** in the same gauge. If they are different primitives or different chart-normalized variables, wall escape can prove the wrong statement.

---

# 1. The consistency requirement

The D3a theorem needs the following identity package:

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=u
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=u+r_{\rm curv},\qquad |r_{\rm curv}|\le \tau/8.
}
\]

It also needs

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
}
\]

And D4 needs

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast.
}
\]

If any one of these uses a different \(q_0\), the wall-escape theorem does not connect to D4.

So the extra audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the \(q_0\) in curvature, anisotropy, and row conversion must be gauge-identical.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Why affine primitive freedom matters

If \(q_0''=u\), then \(q_0\) is determined only up to an affine term:

\[
q_0(m)\mapsto q_0(m)+am+b.
\]

But

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

is not invariant under affine shifts. Nor is the row factor

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Therefore \(q_0\) cannot be an arbitrary primitive of \(u\). It must be the canonical scalar fixed by the local geometry / row algebra.

If the proof only establishes

\[
\exists \tilde q:\quad \tilde q''=u,
\]

that is insufficient. It must establish

\[
\tilde q=q_0
\]

in the gauge used by \(\Gamma_G\) and \(H\).

---

# 3. Required gauge-locking lemma

The missing local lemma, if not already definitional, is:

## Gauge-Locking Lemma

The scalar \(q_0\) appearing in

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

and in the row factor

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots
\]

is the same scalar whose second derivative is the canonical source curvature:

\[
q_0''=u=q''_{\can}.
\]

If the equality is only approximate, then on the relevant packet

\[
|q_0''-u|\le \tau/8
\]

with the same \(\tau\) used in wall escape.

This lemma is mandatory for D3a.

---

# 4. If gauge-locking fails

If

\[
q_0''\neq u
\]

with a non-perturbative error, then wall escape may still show that some primitive of \(u\) exits a wall strip, but that does **not** imply the row factor \(q_0\) exits its wall.

Then the route reverts to one of the fallback options:

1. prove wall escape using the actual row scalar \(q_0\), with \(q_0''\) replacing \(u\), and separately prove \(u,\Gamma_G\) remain live;

2. use saturated rows / \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil;

3. find a source-robust row surviving at \(q_0=0\).

So this is a real architectural guardrail.

---

# 5. Updated D3a dependency list

D3a now requires:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{local complexity: }G,\Gamma,u'
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{gauge-locking: }q_0''=u\text{ or }q_0''=u+O(\tau)
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 valuation/filtered rank and residual control}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{row mobility}
}
\]

The new item is gauge-locking. It should be audited alongside curvature compatibility, not hidden inside it.

---

# 6. Final extra finding

The extra issue is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a requires canonical gauge consistency of }q_0.
}
\]

If \(q_0\) is definitionally the real scalar satisfying

\[
q_0''=q''_{\can}
\]

and used in both

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

and

\[
H\sim -q_0u^3/288,
\]

then no new blocker appears.

If not, this is the next finite local audit. Under row-energy architecture, the \(q_0\)-wall remains near-Green once this gauge-locking check is passed.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:49:14)

_Thought for 17s_

## Continuing attack — displacement admissibility inside the canonical packet/tube

The last hidden issue was **gauge-locking**: the \(q_0\) used in wall escape must be the same \(q_0\) used in \(\Gamma_G\) and the D4 row factor. One more hidden issue remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The wall-escape displacement must stay inside the canonical validity domain.}
}
\]

Wall escape moves from a wall-live point \(m_0\) to a first-exit point \(m_1\) with

\[
|m_1-m_0|\lesssim \rho |I|,
\qquad
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

All canonical estimates, zero-separation assumptions, D4 row expansions, quotient/projection data, and row mobility must remain valid at \(m_1\), not just at \(m_0\). The current downstream architecture explicitly depends on local ordinary complexity, wall escape, D4 row-span conversion, and row mobility. 

---

# 1. The displacement radius

The wall-escape radius is

\[
\rho
=
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2+O(1)}.
\]

The previous wall-escape constraints were

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1),
\]

and

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

These make \(\rho\) polynomially small. But the proof also needs a **validity buffer**.

Let \(I^\ast\) be the thickened packet where canonical local complexity and D4 expansions are assumed. We need

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^\ast)\ge \rho |I|.
\]

Equivalently, if

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^\ast)\ge Q^{-C_{\rm buf}}|I|,
\]

we need

\[
\rho\le Q^{-C_{\rm buf}}.
\]

That is,

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon-C_\tau\ge 2C_{\rm buf}+O(1).
}
\]

So wall escape needs one more lower bound:

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2C_{\rm buf}+O(1).
}
\]

---

# 2. Zero-separated tube stability

Agent 1’s ordinary local complexity uses a zero-separated tube condition of the form

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

Wall escape must not move the sample outside this zero-separated tube.

So the correct local setup is:

1. choose \(I^\ast\) first, with a polynomial buffer around \(I\);
2. assume the zero-separated tube condition on \(I^\ast\);
3. perform wall escape only inside \(I\);
4. ensure the \(\rho |I|\)-neighborhood of all admissible escape points lies inside \(I^\ast\).

Thus D3a requires:

\[
\boxed{
I+\left[-\rho|I|,\rho|I|\right]\subset I^\ast.
}
\]

This is not a new analytic input. It is a packet-selection / buffer condition.

---

# 3. D4 row expansion stability

D4 row conversion uses

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast
\]

or its filtered version. This expansion must hold uniformly on the region where \(m_1\) can land.

So the D4 finite audit must state its validity on

\[
I^\ast
\]

or at least on the escape neighborhood

\[
I_{\rm esc}:=\{m\in I^\ast:\operatorname{dist}(m,I)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

The required uniform statements are:

\[
\sigma_2(L_\ast(m))\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R_\ast(m)|
\le
\frac12 |q_0(m)|\,|u(m)|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast(m))|\Gamma(m)|,
\]

and row derivative bounds

\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}
\]

for all \(m\in I_{\rm esc}\).

If D4 is proved only at a fixed point or only formally at the center of the packet, wall escape is not yet justified.

---

# 4. Boundary layer versus buffer layer

There are now two edge exclusions:

## Packet boundary layer

Needed so first exit remains in \(I\):

\[
I_{\rm bd}
=
\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

This layer was controlled by

\[
Q^{C_G}\rho |I|\ll Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

## Canonical-buffer layer

Needed so the whole escape neighborhood remains in \(I^\ast\):

\[
I_{\rm buf}
=
\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I^\ast)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

If \(I\) is chosen with

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^\ast)\ge Q^{-C_{\rm buf}}|I|,
\]

and \(\rho\le Q^{-C_{\rm buf}}\), then \(I_{\rm buf}\cap I=\varnothing\).

Thus the buffer issue is solved by construction, not by mass exclusion.

---

# 5. Updated threshold lower bound

The lower bounds on \(C_\varepsilon\) now become:

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1),
\]

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1),
\]

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2C_{\rm buf}+O(1).
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
=
\max\{
3C_\tau+2C_{u'},
\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G,
\ C_\tau+2C_{\rm buf}
\}
+O(1).
}
\]

This replaces the earlier \(C_{\varepsilon,\min}\).

The residual corridor for absolute residuals becomes:

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_{\varepsilon,\min}+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

Again, this corridor applies only to absolute residual floors, not valuation-relative residuals.

---

# 6. Packet selection theorem

The wall-escape theorem should include a packet-selection lemma.

## Packet Buffer Lemma

Let \(I_0\) be a candidate packet where Gate 2 mass holds. Suppose \(I^\ast\supset I_0\) is a thickening satisfying local zero separation and canonical complexity.

Choose a subpacket

\[
I\subset I_0
\]

such that

\[
|I|\ge Q^{-C}|I_0|
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^\ast)\ge Q^{-C_{\rm buf}}|I|.
\]

If Gate 2 mass is not concentrated near the discarded edges, then

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-C}\int_{I_0}G.
\]

Since \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), the edge loss is controlled by choosing the discarded edge thickness polynomially small.

This lets us assume a buffer without changing the proof architecture.

---

# 7. Final D3a theorem with displacement admissibility

The robust theorem now reads:

## Buffered Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass on a buffered packet \(I\):

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. local canonical complexity and zero separation on \(I^\ast\supset I\);

3. buffer:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^\ast)\ge Q^{-C_{\rm buf}}|I|;
\]

4. curvature compatibility:

\[
q_0''=u
\quad\text{or}\quad
|q_0''-u|\le \tau/8;
\]

5. D4 row conversion uniformly on the escape neighborhood;

6. row mobility uniformly on the same region;

7. absolute residuals satisfy the updated corridor using

\[
C_{\varepsilon,\min}
=
\max\{
3C_\tau+2C_{u'},
\ C_\tau+2A+2C_G,
\ C_\tau+2C_{\rm buf}
\}
+O(1).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 8. Extra finding

The new hidden requirement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{wall-escape displacement must be admissible inside the zero-separated canonical packet.}
}
\]

This adds a buffer exponent \(C_{\rm buf}\) to the threshold choice and residual corridor.

It is not a conceptual blocker if packets are chosen with polynomial thickening. But it must be stated explicitly, because wall escape moves the sample point.

---

# 9. Verdict

D3a remains near-Green under row-energy architecture, but the final theorem must include:

\[
\boxed{
\text{buffered packet / tube-margin admissibility}.
}
\]

The complete local dependency list is now:

1. Gate 2 mass;
2. local complexity on a thickened zero-separated packet;
3. gauge-locking / curvature compatibility \(q_0''\approx u\);
4. buffer margin for the escape displacement;
5. D4 rank and residual control uniformly on the escape region;
6. row mobility.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 13:50:26)

## Continuing attack — final stress test of D3a: what if Gate 2 mass is only on the discarded buffer/edge?

The last hidden requirement was displacement admissibility: wall escape moves a point by

\[
\rho |I|,
\qquad
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

So the packet must have a buffer inside the canonical zero-separated domain \(I^\ast\). One more issue follows:

\[
\boxed{
\text{When we shrink to a buffered subpacket, do we preserve Gate 2 mass?}
}
\]

If all Gate 2 mass is concentrated in the edge region removed to create the buffer, then wall escape on the buffered packet may lose its input. I’ll now close this.

---

# 1. Edge loss estimate

Let \(I_0\) be the original packet and \(I\subset I_0\) be the buffered subpacket obtained by removing edge regions of total length

\[
|I_0\setminus I|\le \eta |I_0|.
\]

Assume

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le Q^{C_G}.
\]

Then the edge contribution is bounded by

\[
\int_{I_0\setminus I}G
\le
Q^{C_G}\eta |I_0|.
\]

If Gate 2 mass on \(I_0\) is

\[
\int_{I_0}G\ge Q^{-A}|I_0|,
\]

then choosing

\[
\eta\le \frac12 Q^{-A-C_G}
\]

ensures

\[
\int_I G
\ge
\frac12Q^{-A}|I_0|.
\]

Since

\[
|I|\ge (1-\eta)|I_0|,
\]

this implies

\[
\int_I G
\ge
Q^{-A-O(1)}|I|.
\]

Thus buffered subpacket selection preserves Gate 2 mass if the discarded edge is thin enough.

---

# 2. Buffer width versus escape radius

We need the buffer thickness to exceed the escape radius:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\partial I^\ast)
\ge \rho |I|.
\]

Let the removed edge fraction be

\[
\eta=Q^{-C_{\rm edge}}.
\]

Then the buffer condition is essentially

\[
\rho\le Q^{-C_{\rm edge}}.
\]

Since

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2},
\]

this requires

\[
C_\varepsilon-C_\tau
\ge
2C_{\rm edge}.
\]

But edge-mass preservation requires

\[
C_{\rm edge}
\ge
A+C_G+O(1).
\]

Therefore it suffices to require

\[
C_\varepsilon-C_\tau
\ge
2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

This is exactly the boundary-layer condition already found:

\[
C_\varepsilon
\ge
C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

So no new exponent condition appears. The packet-buffer requirement is the same as the boundary-layer negligibility condition.

---

# 3. Buffered wall-escape theorem is internally consistent

We can now combine the edge removal and wall escape.

Given Gate 2 on \(I_0\):

\[
\int_{I_0}G\ge Q^{-A}|I_0|,
\]

choose an interior buffered packet

\[
I\subset I_0
\]

with edge fraction

\[
\eta=Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

Then:

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A-O(1)}|I|.
\]

Also \(I\) has buffer thickness

\[
\eta |I_0|
\]

inside the larger canonical domain. Choose

\[
C_\varepsilon
\]

so that

\[
\rho\le \eta.
\]

Then wall escape from any interior wall-live point stays inside the canonical validity domain.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Buffered packet selection preserves Gate 2 mass and permits wall escape.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Interaction with source thickening

Gate 2 itself, in the new route, is proved by source thickening from a single high-\(u\) point. That construction may produce an interval \(J\). The wall-escape row-energy theorem is applied after Gate 2 is already proved on a packet \(I\).

There is no conflict if:

1. Gate 2 is established on \(I_0\);
2. we shrink to buffered \(I\subset I_0\);
3. the edge removal preserves a polynomial fraction of Gate 2 mass.

Because \(G\le Q^{C_G}\), this is valid.

If Gate 2 mass is somehow entirely in an edge layer of thickness smaller than \(\eta\), then the edge layer itself can be treated as a smaller packet \(I_{\rm edge}\), provided local complexity holds there. This gives a fallback:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if mass is edge-concentrated, recenter on the edge layer as a new packet.}
}
\]

So packet buffering is not a serious blocker.

---

# 5. What if \(I\) becomes too short?

The edge fraction

\[
\eta=Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}
\]

is polynomially small, so

\[
|I|=(1-O(\eta))|I_0|.
\]

The buffered interval is not shorter by a polynomial factor; it remains essentially the same length.

So the derivative scalings

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C}|I|^{-1}
\]

and row mobility

\[
|\mathbf A'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
\]

remain valid up to polynomial constants.

No issue.

---

# 6. Updated final D3a theorem

The final wall-escape theorem should include:

## Buffered Packet Clause

Before applying wall escape, replace \(I_0\) by a buffered subpacket \(I\subset I_0\) such that:

\[
\int_I G\ge Q^{-A'}|I|,
\]

\[
I+[-\rho|I|,\rho|I|]\subset I^\ast,
\]

with

\[
A'=A+O(1).
\]

This is possible under

\[
G\le Q^{C_G}
\]

and the same choice of \(C_\varepsilon\) already required for boundary-layer control.

Then the wall-escape proof proceeds unchanged.

---

# 7. Remaining possible hidden issue: moving changes the row-output packet weight

If the final row energy uses a weight \(w_I\), the moved sample \(m_1\) must lie where \(w_I\) is not tiny.

The buffered packet construction should choose \(I\) inside the core where

\[
w_I\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If the weight is a standard bump with polynomially controlled transition, then the same edge removal works.

The row mobility interval \(J_\ast\) has length

\[
Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

As long as \(m_1\) lies in the core at distance \(Q^{-C}|I|\) from the edge, the thickened row-energy interval remains in the good-weight region.

Thus, add to the buffer:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(I,\{w_I<Q^{-C_w}\})\ge Q^{-C_{\rm mob}}|I|.
\]

This is another packet-weight core condition, not a new analytic input.

---

# 8. Final extra finding

The apparent new risk — losing Gate 2 mass when shrinking to a buffered packet — is controlled by the same bound already needed for boundary-layer negligibility:

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
\]

So no additional exponent condition is needed.

The final D3a dependency list is stable:

1. Gate 2 mass;
2. upper bound \(G\le Q^{C_G}\);
3. buffered packet/core selection;
4. curvature compatibility \(q_0''\approx u\);
5. wall escape;
6. D4 at the escaped sample;
7. row mobility.

No new blocker appears.

## Agent 4 / D — Final D3a wall escape theorem with guardrails

Executing Agent 4’s assignment: close D3a as a row-energy theorem, using D4 only as a black-box row-conversion input. The current active downstream chain is Gate 2 \(\Rightarrow\) curvature-compatible wall escape \(\Rightarrow\) D4 \(\Rightarrow\) row mobility \(\Rightarrow\) row energy. 

---

# 1. Setup

Let

\[
q=q_0,\qquad u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}),
\]

and

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

Assume Gate 2 mass on a packet \(I\):

\[
\int_I G\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

These are supplied by the local canonical complexity package, not by D3a itself.

---

# 2. Required gauge-locking

D3a requires the same scalar \(q_0\) in all three places:

\[
q_0''=u
\]

or robustly

\[
|q_0''-u|\le \tau/8
\]

on the wall-escape neighborhood,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and the D4 row factor

\[
\mathbf A_N\sim q_0u^{b_\ast}L\Gamma.
\]

This is mandatory. If \(q_0\) is only an affine primitive of \(u\), or if the \(q_0\) in \(H\sim -q_0u^3/288\) differs from the \(q_0\) in \(\Gamma_G\), wall escape does not apply to the correct wall.

So D3a assumes the gauge-locking identity package:

\[
\boxed{
q_0\text{ is the same canonical scalar in curvature, anisotropy, and D4 rows.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Wall split

Choose

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C_\varepsilon}.
\]

Split

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q_0|\ge \varepsilon\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

---

# 4. Non-wall branch

If

\[
\int_{I_{\rm nd}}G\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

there exists

\[
m_\ast\in I_{\rm nd}
\]

with

\[
G(m_\ast)\ge Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge\varepsilon.
\]

This is a non-wall D4 sample. Under D4, this yields

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]

for some polynomial exponent \(C_A\). Row mobility then gives row energy, as shown below.

---

# 5. Wall branch and low-source removal

Assume instead

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall}}G\,dm\ge \frac12 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Choose

\[
\tau=Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Define

\[
I_{\rm wall,low}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|<\tau\},
\]

\[
I_{\rm wall,live}=I_{\rm wall}\cap\{|u|\ge\tau\}.
\]

On the low-source set,

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le \tau^2Q^{2C_\Gamma}.
\]

So choose

\[
\boxed{
2C_\tau\ge A+2C_\Gamma+O(1).
}
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,low}}G\,dm\le \frac14 Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

and hence

\[
\int_{I_{\rm wall,live}}G\,dm\ge \frac14 Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

---

# 6. Complex wall escape

Take

\[
m_0\in I_{\rm wall,live}.
\]

Then

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau.
\]

For complex \(q_0\), set

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(m_0)}}{|u(m_0)|},
\]

\[
Q(m)=\Re(e q_0(m)).
\]

If \(q_0''=u\), then

\[
Q''(m_0)=|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

If \(q_0''=u+r_{\rm curv}\), with

\[
|r_{\rm curv}|\le \tau/8,
\]

then the same lower bound holds up to constants.

Let

\[
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

If

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}
\]

and

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le c\tau,
\]

then \(Q''\ge c\tau\) throughout the escape neighborhood.

Since

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2+O(1)},
\]

the stability condition is

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
}
\]

Then real convexity of \(Q\) gives a first-exit point \(m_1\) satisfying

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \rho |I|,
\]

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

This proof does not require \(q_0\) to be real-valued.

---

# 7. Boundary and buffered-packet admissibility

The first-exit point must remain in the valid canonical region.

Let

\[
I_{\rm bd}=\{m\in I:\operatorname{dist}(m,\partial I)\le \rho |I|\}.
\]

Then

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\le 2\rho |I|.
\]

Since

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
\int_{I_{\rm bd}}G\,dm\le 2\rho Q^{C_G}|I|.
\]

To make this \(<\frac18Q^{-A}|I|\), require

\[
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1).
}
\]

This same condition allows buffered packet selection: discard an edge region of relative size

\[
\eta\le Q^{-A-C_G-O(1)}
\]

to ensure the escape neighborhood remains inside the zero-separated canonical packet \(I^\ast\), while preserving polynomial Gate 2 mass.

So there is no extra exponent condition from buffering beyond the boundary-layer inequality.

---

# 8. Signal survival at first exit

At \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau,
\]

we obtain

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|
\ge
|u(m_1)|-6|q_0(m_1)|-2|q_0(m_1)|^3
\ge c\tau.
\]

Therefore

\[
G(m_1)=|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge |u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
G(m_1)\ge c\tau^4.
\]

---

# 9. D4 input at the escaped sample

Use D4 in valuation or filtered form:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma+\mathbf R_\ast,
\]

or

\[
\mathbf A_N
=
q_0\sum_{b=b_0}^{B}u^bL_b\Gamma+\mathbf R
\]

if filtered observability is needed.

For the simple valuation form, assume

\[
\sigma_2(L_\ast)\ge Q^{-C_L},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R_\ast|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then at \(m_1\),

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|
\ge
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
\]

For filtered observability through layer \(B\), replace \(b_\ast\) by \(B\).

---

# 10. Absolute residual corridor

Decompose D4 residuals as

\[
\mathbf R
=
\mathbf R_{\rm same}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm val}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}.
\]

- \(\mathbf R_{\rm same}\): same-valuation linear terms, absorbed into \(L_\ast\).
- \(\mathbf R_{\rm val}\): valuation-relative residuals, controlled termwise.
- \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\): absolute residual floors.

Only absolute residuals require a threshold corridor.

If

\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}},
\]

then require

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

For filtered layer \(B\), require

\[
\boxed{
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(B+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
}
\]

If D4 residuals are entirely valuation-relative, this corridor is unnecessary.

---

# 11. Row mobility

Assume

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

If

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C_A},
\]

then on an interval of length

\[
\gg Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|
\]

around \(m_1\),

\[
|\mathbf A_N|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
}
\]

For weighted packet energy, choose \(m_1\) inside the polynomially thick packet core. The buffered packet argument above supplies this.

---

# 12. Final theorem

## D3a Wall-Escape Row-Energy Theorem

Assume:

1. Gate 2 mass:

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|;
\]

2. local upper bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1};
\]

3. gauge-locking / curvature compatibility:

\[
q_0''=u
\]

or

\[
|q_0''-u|\le\tau/8;
\]

4. D4 row conversion at non-wall samples in valuation or filtered form;

5. absolute residual corridor only for \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\);

6. row mobility:

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 13. Exact failure modes

D3a fails only if one of the following holds:

1. **Gauge-locking fails**:

   \[
   q_0''\not\approx u
   \]

   or the \(q_0\) in wall escape differs from the \(q_0\) in \(\Gamma_G\) or D4.

2. **Exact-point architecture is required**:

   if the downstream proof demands row lower bound at a fixed preassigned point, wall escape is insufficient.

3. **D4 absolute residual corridor fails**:

   if \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\) is too large compared with the escaped leading scale.

4. **D4 rank unavailable**:

   if D4 cannot provide row conversion at non-wall samples.

Otherwise D3a is closed under row-energy architecture.

---

# 14. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a is closed modulo gauge-locking and D4.}
}
\]

Wall escape is no longer a conceptual blocker. It is a local lemma using curvature compatibility and row-energy sampling.
