## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:04:43)

I’ll attack gauge-locking as a finite compatibility problem: identify the three possible \(q_0\)’s, derive the exact equalities needed, and show how failure creates a measurable residual rather than a vague concern.

_Thought for 16s_

## Gauge-locking attack — reduce it to three identities and two residual tests

The wall-escape argument is valid only if the same scalar \(q_0\) appears in all three places:

\[
q_0''=u,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

If these use different gauges, wall escape may move the wrong “wall.” The latest downstream package already identifies this as a necessary guardrail for D3a. 

---

# 1. Separate the three possible \(q\)’s

Introduce three symbols:

\[
q_{\rm curv}
\quad\text{defined by}\quad
q_{\rm curv}''=u,
\]

\[
q_{\rm aniso}
\quad\text{defined by}\quad
\Gamma_G=u-6q_{\rm aniso}+2q_{\rm aniso}^3,
\]

\[
q_{\rm row}
\quad\text{defined by}\quad
H=-\frac{q_{\rm row}u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

Gauge-locking is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
q_{\rm curv}=q_{\rm aniso}=q_{\rm row}.
}
\]

If equality is approximate, the required robust form is:

\[
\boxed{
|q_{\rm curv}-q_{\rm aniso}|+|q_{\rm curv}-q_{\rm row}|
\le Q^{-C}
}
\]

strong enough that the errors are smaller than the wall thresholds used in D3a and D4.

---

# 2. Why affine primitive freedom is dangerous

The condition

\[
q_{\rm curv}''=u
\]

determines \(q_{\rm curv}\) only up to an affine term:

\[
q_{\rm curv}\mapsto q_{\rm curv}+am+b.
\]

But neither

\[
u-6q+2q^3
\]

nor

\[
-\frac{qu^3}{288}
\]

is invariant under

\[
q\mapsto q+am+b.
\]

Indeed,

\[
u-6(q+\ell)+2(q+\ell)^3
-
(u-6q+2q^3)
=
-6\ell+6q^2\ell+6q\ell^2+2\ell^3,
\]

where

\[
\ell=am+b.
\]

And

\[
-\frac{(q+\ell)u^3}{288}
+
\frac{qu^3}{288}
=
-\frac{\ell u^3}{288}.
\]

So it is not enough to prove that some primitive of \(u\) exists. The proof needs the primitive fixed in the same gauge as \(\Gamma_G\) and \(H\).

---

# 3. Residual formulation

Define the gauge residuals

\[
r_{\rm aniso}
:=
\Gamma_G-\bigl(u-6q_{\rm curv}+2q_{\rm curv}^3\bigr),
\]

and

\[
r_{\rm row}
:=
H+\frac{q_{\rm curv}u^3}{288}.
\]

Gauge-locking is equivalent to:

\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm aniso}=0,
\qquad
r_{\rm row}=\text{higher/controlled D4 residual}.
}
\]

The robust version is:

\[
\boxed{
|r_{\rm aniso}|\le c\tau,
}
\]

for wall escape, and

\[
\boxed{
|r_{\rm row}|
\le
\frac12 |q_{\rm curv}|\,|u|^3\sigma_2(L)|\Gamma|
}
\]

for D4 at the escaped sample.

---

# 4. Wall escape with gauge residual

Suppose wall escape is run on \(q_{\rm curv}\). At the first exit,

\[
|q_{\rm curv}(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

To get signal survival, we need

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

But

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q_{\rm curv}+2q_{\rm curv}^3+r_{\rm aniso}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Gamma_G|
\ge
|u|-6|q_{\rm curv}|-2|q_{\rm curv}|^3-|r_{\rm aniso}|.
\]

At first exit, if

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau
\]

and

\[
|r_{\rm aniso}|\le c\tau,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c'\tau.
\]

So wall escape survives if:

\[
\boxed{
|r_{\rm aniso}|\ll\tau.
}
\]

If \(r_{\rm aniso}\) is not small, the wall escape point may have live \(u\) but not live \(\Gamma_G\).

---

# 5. D4 with gauge residual

D4 expects

\[
H=-\frac{q_{\rm row}u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

If wall escape was performed on \(q_{\rm curv}\), then write

\[
q_{\rm row}=q_{\rm curv}+\Delta_{\rm row}.
\]

Then

\[
H
=
-\frac{q_{\rm curv}u^3}{288}
-\frac{\Delta_{\rm row}u^3}{288}
+\cdots.
\]

The extra term

\[
-\frac{\Delta_{\rm row}u^3}{288}
\]

is harmless only if either:

\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{\rm row}|\le c|q_{\rm curv}|
}
\]

at the D4 sample, or it is absorbed as a same-valuation correction into the effective row matrix.

At the wall-escape point,

\[
|q_{\rm curv}|=\varepsilon.
\]

Thus a sufficient condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{\rm row}|\le Q^{-C}\varepsilon.
}
\]

A weaker but still usable condition is that the row expansion is rewritten with \(q_{\rm row}\), and wall escape is performed on \(q_{\rm row}\) directly, provided

\[
q_{\rm row}''\approx u.
\]

---

# 6. Exact finite gauge-locking tests

The paper must pass these tests.

## Test 1 — curvature primitive identity

Verify:

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=u=q''_{\can}
}
\]

in the same normalized derivative convention.

If not exact, compute

\[
r_{\rm curv}:=q_0''-u.
\]

Wall escape requires

\[
\boxed{
|r_{\rm curv}|\le \tau/8}
\]

on escape neighborhoods.

---

## Test 2 — anisotropy identity

Verify:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
}
\]

If not exact, compute

\[
r_{\rm aniso}
=
\Gamma_G-(u-6q_0+2q_0^3).
\]

Wall escape requires

\[
\boxed{
|r_{\rm aniso}|\le c\tau.
}
\]

---

## Test 3 — row wall factor identity

Verify:

\[
\boxed{
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{controlled residual}.
}
\]

If not exact, compute

\[
r_H:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

D4 requires

\[
\boxed{
r_H
}
\]

to be either:

1. absorbed into the effective row matrix; or  
2. valuation-relative and half-leading; or  
3. an absolute residual satisfying the threshold corridor.

---

# 7. If \(q_0\) differs by affine drift

Suppose

\[
q_{\rm aniso}=q_{\rm curv}+\ell,
\qquad
\ell=am+b.
\]

Then

\[
r_{\rm aniso}
=
-6\ell+6q_{\rm curv}^2\ell+6q_{\rm curv}\ell^2+2\ell^3.
\]

For

\[
r_{\rm aniso}
\]

to be small on a wall-escape region where \(q_{\rm curv}\) is small, we need approximately

\[
-6\ell+2\ell^3\approx0.
\]

Thus \(\ell\) would have to be near

\[
0,\quad \pm\sqrt3.
\]

But if \(\ell\approx\pm\sqrt3\), then \(q_{\rm aniso}\) is not near the same wall as \(q_{\rm curv}\), and the row factor \(q_{\rm row}\) may not be small. Therefore the only acceptable affine drift is:

\[
\boxed{
\ell\approx0
}
\]

with polynomial precision. In practice:

\[
\boxed{
|a|\,|I|+|b|\le Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is a concrete way to detect gauge mismatch.

---

# 8. Best-case outcome

If the paper defines \(q_0\) as the canonical scalar satisfying

\[
q_0''=q''_{\can},
\]

and then defines

\[
\Gamma_G=q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and derives

\[
H=-\frac{q_0(q_0'')^3}{288}+\cdots,
\]

then gauge-locking is closed definitionally.

In that case, D3a needs no extra work beyond local complexity and D4 residual control.

---

# 9. Failure outcome

If the paper defines \(q_0\), \(u\), \(\Gamma_G\), and \(H\) in different gauges, the proof must be repaired by one of:

1. redefining all objects in the same canonical \(q_0\)-gauge;
2. proving the gauge residuals \(r_{\rm curv},r_{\rm aniso},r_H\) are perturbative;
3. switching to \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil/saturated rows;
4. abandoning wall escape and finding a source-robust row.

---

# 10. Final gauge-locking theorem

## Gauge-Locking Theorem

Assume the paper’s scalar \(q_0\) satisfies, in the same normalized derivative convention,

\[
q_0''=u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{D4-controlled residual}.
\]

Then the \(q_0\)-wall escaped by D3a is the same wall appearing in the D4 row factor. Therefore wall escape is admissible.

If these identities hold only with residuals, require:

\[
|q_0''-u|\le\tau/8,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G-(u-6q_0+2q_0^3)|\le c\tau,
\]

and

\[
H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
\]

to satisfy the D4 valuation/absolute-residual audit.

---

# 11. Verdict

Gauge-locking is not a broad conceptual blocker. It is a finite identity audit.

The exact test is:

\[
\boxed{
q_0''=u,\quad
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,\quad
H=-q_0u^3/288+\cdots
}
\]

all using the same \(q_0\).

If yes, D3a remains closed modulo D4.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:11:29)

_Thought for 8s_

## Continuing attack — gauge-locking can be tested by a “commuting triangle”

The gauge-locking condition now has three vertices:

\[
q_0''=u,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

The next step is to make this into a **commuting diagram test**. If the diagram commutes, wall escape is valid. If it does not, the exact residual tells us which part fails. This is the finite audit needed for D3a. 

---

# 1. The commuting triangle

Define three maps from the scalar \(q_0\):

\[
\mathcal C(q_0):=q_0'',
\]

\[
\mathcal G(q_0):=q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\mathcal H(q_0):=-\frac{q_0(q_0'')^3}{288}.
\]

The paper’s objects are:

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G,
\]

\[
H.
\]

Gauge-locking is the assertion that:

\[
\boxed{
u=\mathcal C(q_0),
\qquad
\Gamma_G=\mathcal G(q_0),
\qquad
H=\mathcal H(q_0)+\text{D4-controlled residual}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the following residuals vanish or are controlled:

\[
r_C:=u-q_0'',
\]

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3),
\]

\[
r_H:=H+\frac{q_0(q_0'')^3}{288}.
\]

If \(r_C,r_G,r_H\) are all zero, the triangle commutes exactly.

If not, each residual has a specific role.

---

# 2. Residual propagation into wall escape

Wall escape uses curvature. If

\[
r_C\ne0,
\]

then

\[
q_0''=u-r_C.
\]

At a live wall point,

\[
|u|\ge \tau.
\]

The projected convexity argument still works if

\[
|r_C|\le \frac18\tau
\]

and \(u\) is stable over the escape interval.

So the curvature residual condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|r_C|\le \frac18\tau.
}
\]

If this fails, wall escape using \(u\)-mass may not move the actual row-wall coordinate \(q_0\).

---

# 3. Residual propagation into signal survival

At the first-exit point,

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge c\tau.
\]

We want

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c'\tau.
\]

But if

\[
\Gamma_G=q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3+r_G,
\]

and

\[
q_0''=u-r_C,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q_0+2q_0^3+(r_G-r_C).
\]

Thus

\[
|\Gamma_G|
\ge
|u|-6|q_0|-2|q_0|^3-|r_G-r_C|.
\]

So signal survival requires:

\[
\boxed{
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau.
}
\]

A slightly stronger but simpler sufficient condition is:

\[
\boxed{
|r_G|+|r_C|\le c\tau.
}
\]

This is the true compatibility condition for \(\Gamma_G\). It is not enough to control \(r_C\) alone.

---

# 4. Residual propagation into D4

D4 uses

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{controlled}.
\]

But the natural map from \(q_0\) gives

\[
\mathcal H(q_0)=-\frac{q_0(q_0'')^3}{288}.
\]

Since

\[
q_0''=u-r_C,
\]

we have

\[
-\frac{q_0(q_0'')^3}{288}
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
+
\frac{q_0}{288}\left(u^3-(u-r_C)^3\right).
\]

Expand:

\[
u^3-(u-r_C)^3
=
3u^2r_C-3ur_C^2+r_C^3.
\]

Thus the curvature mismatch contributes

\[
\Delta_H^{(C)}
=
\frac{q_0}{288}
\left(
3u^2r_C-3ur_C^2+r_C^3
\right).
\]

If

\[
|r_C|\le \eta_C |u|,
\]

then

\[
|\Delta_H^{(C)}|
\le
C\eta_C |q_0||u|^3.
\]

So this is valuation-relative and can be absorbed into the D4 residual if

\[
\eta_C\ll \sigma_2(L).
\]

The full \(H\)-residual relative to \(q_0u^3\) is

\[
r_H^\ast
:=
H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

It decomposes as:

\[
r_H^\ast
=
r_H
+
\Delta_H^{(C)}.
\]

D4 requires:

\[
\boxed{
r_H^\ast
\text{ is absorbed into }L_{\rm eff}
\text{ or is half-leading.}
}
\]

For the scalar \(H\)-factor, the clean sufficient bound is:

\[
\boxed{
|r_H^\ast|\le c\,|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L).
}
\]

---

# 5. Strong gauge-locking package

The cleanest gauge-locking theorem should not separately state vague gauge compatibility. It should state exactly:

## Strong Gauge-Locking Package

On the wall-escape packet,

\[
r_C:=u-q_0'',
\]

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3),
\]

\[
r_H^\ast:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Assume:

\[
|r_C|\le c_1\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c_2\tau,
\]

and

\[
|r_H^\ast|
\le
c_3 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L).
\]

Then:

1. wall escape has curvature;
2. \(\Gamma_G\) survives at first exit;
3. D4 uses the same wall factor.

Therefore the gauge-locked D3a proof goes through.

This is better than simply saying “\(q_0''\approx u\)” because it includes the \(\Gamma_G\) residual and the D4 \(H\)-factor residual.

---

# 6. Exact-gauge package

If the definitions are exact:

\[
u=q_0'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0(q_0'')^3}{288}+\text{D4 residual},
\]

then:

\[
r_C=0,
\]

\[
r_G=0,
\]

and

\[
r_H^\ast
=
H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
\]

is precisely the ordinary D4 residual already being audited.

So exact gauge-locking reduces to the D4 residual audit.

---

# 7. If gauge-locking fails by affine drift

Suppose

\[
q_{\rm aniso}=q_0+\ell,
\qquad
\ell=am+b.
\]

Then

\[
r_C=0
\]

if both have the same second derivative, but

\[
r_G
=
-6\ell+6q_0^2\ell+6q_0\ell^2+2\ell^3.
\]

Near the wall \(q_0\approx0\),

\[
r_G\approx -6\ell+2\ell^3.
\]

For \(|r_G|\ll\tau\), \(\ell\) must be near one of:

\[
0,\quad \pm\sqrt3.
\]

But if \(\ell\approx\pm\sqrt3\), then the \(q_{\rm aniso}\)-wall is not the \(q_0\)-wall. Also the D4 row factor involving \(q_0\) will not align with the \(\Gamma_G\)-wall.

Therefore the only acceptable affine drift for D3a is:

\[
\boxed{
|\ell|\le Q^{-C}
}
\]

on the packet, i.e.

\[
\boxed{
|a||I|+|b|\le Q^{-C}.
}
\]

This is an explicit affine-gauge audit.

---

# 8. If \(H\) uses a different scalar

Suppose

\[
q_{\rm row}=q_0+\ell_{\rm row}.
\]

Then

\[
H=-\frac{q_{\rm row}u^3}{288}+\cdots
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
-\frac{\ell_{\rm row}u^3}{288}
+\cdots.
\]

At wall escape,

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon.
\]

The row residual from gauge drift is

\[
\frac{|\ell_{\rm row}||u|^3}{288}.
\]

Relative to the leading row factor

\[
|q_0||u|^3
\]

this is

\[
\frac{|\ell_{\rm row}|}{|q_0|}
=
\frac{|\ell_{\rm row}|}{\varepsilon}.
\]

Thus D4 requires:

\[
\boxed{
|\ell_{\rm row}|\le c\varepsilon\sigma_2(L).
}
\]

This is stronger than merely \(|\ell_{\rm row}|\le Q^{-C}\). It must be small relative to the wall threshold.

So if row gauge differs, the drift must satisfy:

\[
\boxed{
|q_{\rm row}-q_0|\le Q^{-C}\varepsilon.
}
\]

Otherwise the \(H\)-factor wall is not the escaped wall.

---

# 9. Final gauge-locking audit table

The paper should be audited with this table:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{object} & \text{identity needed} & \text{acceptable residual}\\
\hline
\text{curvature} & u=q_0'' & |u-q_0''|\le c\tau\\
\Gamma_G & \Gamma_G=q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3 & |\Gamma_G-(q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3)-(u-q_0'')|\le c\tau\\
H & H=-q_0u^3/288+\cdots & |H+q_0u^3/288|\le c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L)\\
row wall scalar & q_{\rm row}=q_0 & |q_{\rm row}-q_0|\le c\varepsilon\sigma_2(L)\\
affine primitive & q_{\rm curv}=q_0+am+b & |a||I|+|b|\le c\varepsilon
\end{array}
\]

This table is the precise gauge-locking test.

---

# 10. Conclusion

One step further shows that gauge-locking is not one identity but a commuting triangle with residual tolerances:

\[
u \leftrightarrow q_0'' ,
\qquad
\Gamma_G \leftrightarrow q_0,
\qquad
H \leftrightarrow q_0.
\]

D3a is valid if:

\[
\boxed{
r_C,\ r_G-r_C,\ r_H^\ast
}
\]

are controlled at the tolerances above.

If the paper’s definitions make these exact, the audit closes.

If not, the residuals are explicit and tell us exactly whether wall escape is still admissible.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:16:56)

_Thought for 10s_

## Continuing attack — collapse gauge-locking into a finite residual theorem

The previous step refined gauge-locking into a commuting triangle:

\[
u\leftrightarrow q_0'',\qquad
\Gamma_G\leftrightarrow q_0,\qquad
H\leftrightarrow q_0.
\]

Now I’ll push one level further: rather than require exact gauge-locking, we can define a **residual-tolerant D3a theorem**. This tells us exactly how much mismatch the proof can absorb before wall escape fails. This is important because the active downstream route uses wall escape as a row-energy lemma, while D4 remains the finite row-conversion blocker. 

---

# 1. Three residuals

Define

\[
r_C:=u-q_0'',
\]

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3),
\]

and

\[
r_H^\ast:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Then the exact identities are:

\[
r_C=0,
\qquad
r_G=0,
\qquad
r_H^\ast=\text{ordinary D4 residual}.
\]

The robust theorem should allow these residuals, provided they satisfy scale-compatible inequalities.

---

# 2. Wall escape with curvature residual

At a wall-live point,

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau.
\]

Since

\[
q_0''=u-r_C,
\]

the actual wall curvature is \(q_0''\), not \(u\).

For complex \(q_0\), set

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(m_0)}}{|u(m_0)|},
\qquad
Q(m)=\Re(e q_0(m)).
\]

Then

\[
Q''(m)=\Re(eu(m))-\Re(e r_C(m)).
\]

If

\[
|r_C|\le \frac{1}{8}\tau
\]

and

\[
|u(m)-u(m_0)|\le \frac18\tau
\]

on the escape interval, then

\[
Q''(m)\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus wall escape still gives a first-exit point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

So the curvature residual tolerance is:

\[
\boxed{
|r_C|\le c\tau.
}
\]

---

# 3. Signal survival with anisotropy residual

At the first-exit point,

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

But now

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3+r_G
=
u-6q_0+2q_0^3+(r_G-r_C).
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Gamma_G|
\ge
|u|-6|q_0|-2|q_0|^3-|r_G-r_C|.
\]

Hence signal survival requires

\[
\boxed{
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau.
}
\]

A simpler sufficient condition is

\[
|r_G|+|r_C|\le c\tau.
\]

This gives

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

and therefore

\[
G(m_1)=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2(m_1)\ge c\tau^4.
\]

---

# 4. D4 leading factor with \(H\)-residual

D4 wants a row factor of the form

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

The exact residual is

\[
r_H^\ast=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

If the row is schematically

\[
A_7\sim H\Gamma_G,
\]

then the \(H\)-residual contributes

\[
r_H^\ast\Gamma_G.
\]

This is harmless if it is half-leading relative to

\[
|q_0||u|^3|\Gamma|.
\]

Thus require

\[
\boxed{
|r_H^\ast|
\le
c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})
}
\]

or, after multiplying by \(|\Gamma|\),

\[
|r_H^\ast||\Gamma|
\le
c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})|\Gamma|.
\]

At a wall-escape point,

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge \tau.
\]

So an absolute \(H\)-residual floor must satisfy

\[
|r_H^\ast|
\le
Q^{-(C_\varepsilon+3C_\tau+C_L+O(1))}.
\]

But if \(r_H^\ast\) has valuation

\[
r_H^\ast=q_0u^3\cdot \rho_H,
\]

then it is valuation-relative and only requires

\[
|\rho_H|\le c\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff}).
\]

So again: absolute residuals create a corridor; valuation-relative residuals do not.

---

# 5. Unified residual-tolerant theorem

## Gauge-Residual Wall-Escape Lemma

Assume Gate 2 mass on \(I\):

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local bounds:

\[
G\le Q^{C_G},
\qquad
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\qquad
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Assume the gauge residuals satisfy on wall-escape neighborhoods:

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

and

\[
|r_H^\ast|\le c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})
\]

or the equivalent D4 projected-residual estimate.

Then the D3a wall-escape proof remains valid and produces a non-wall D4 sample \(m_1\) satisfying

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

and hence

\[
G(m_1)\ge c\tau^4.
\]

D4 and row mobility then give

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]

---

# 6. Affine gauge drift: quantitative exclusion

Suppose the curvature primitive and anisotropy scalar differ by

\[
q_{\rm aniso}=q_{\rm curv}+\ell,
\qquad
\ell=am+b.
\]

Then

\[
r_G=-6\ell+6q_{\rm curv}^2\ell+6q_{\rm curv}\ell^2+2\ell^3.
\]

On the wall,

\[
|q_{\rm curv}|\le \varepsilon,
\]

so

\[
r_G=-6\ell+2\ell^3+O(\varepsilon|\ell|+\varepsilon|\ell|^2).
\]

The residual tolerance is

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau.
\]

If \(r_C=0\), this forces

\[
|-6\ell+2\ell^3|\le c\tau+O(\varepsilon|\ell|+\varepsilon|\ell|^2).
\]

Thus \(\ell\) must be near one of

\[
0,\quad \sqrt3,\quad -\sqrt3.
\]

Only \(\ell\approx0\) is compatible with the same \(q_0\)-wall. If \(\ell\approx\pm\sqrt3\), then the wall \(|q_{\rm curv}|\ll1\) is not the wall \(|q_{\rm aniso}|\ll1\).

Therefore the acceptable affine drift is

\[
\boxed{
|a||I|+|b|\le c\varepsilon
}
\]

if the D4 row factor uses \(q_{\rm curv}\), or at least

\[
|a||I|+|b|\le c\tau
\]

for signal survival alone.

For D4 compatibility, the stronger condition is usually needed:

\[
\boxed{
|a||I|+|b|\le c\varepsilon\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff}).
}
\]

---

# 7. Gauge-locking decision tree

The paper should be audited using this decision tree.

## Case 1 — exact identities

If

\[
q_0''=u,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q_0''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{D4 residual},
\]

then gauge-locking is closed. D3a proceeds.

## Case 2 — small residuals

If the residuals satisfy

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\qquad
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

and

\[
r_H^\ast
\]

is D4-controlled, then gauge-locking is robustly closed.

## Case 3 — affine mismatch

If the mismatch is affine, require

\[
|a||I|+|b|\le c\varepsilon\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff})
\]

for D4 wall compatibility. Otherwise wall escape is moving the wrong scalar.

## Case 4 — non-perturbative mismatch

If any residual exceeds tolerance, D3a fails and one must use:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil / source-robust wall row}
\]

or rewrite the proof in the correct gauge.

---

# 8. Extra issue: derivative convention

Gauge-locking must be checked in the same derivative convention.

If the paper uses normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

then

\[
q_0''=u
\]

may mean

\[
\mathcal D^2q_0=u
\]

rather than

\[
\partial_m^2q_0=u.
\]

The wall-escape radius and \(u'\)-bound are sensitive to this scaling.

Thus the exact audit item is:

\[
\boxed{
u=\mathcal D^2 q_0
}
\]

if \(\mathcal D\) is the proof’s derivative, and all identities

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-q_0u^3/288+\cdots
\]

must use that same normalized \(u\).

A mismatch by powers of \(\lambda\) is not harmless; it changes the wall-escape scale.

---

# 9. Final strengthened gauge-locking theorem

## Gauge-Locked D3a Theorem

Let \(\mathcal D\) be the derivative convention used in \(u,\Gamma_G,H\). Assume

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q_0+r_C,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=(\mathcal D^2q_0)-6q_0+2q_0^3+r_G,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+r_H^\ast.
\]

If, on wall-escape neighborhoods,

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

and

\[
r_H^\ast
\]

is D4-controlled relative to

\[
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma,
\]

then wall escape and D4 are gauge-compatible.

If \(r_C=r_G=0\) and \(r_H^\ast\) is the standard D4 residual, gauge-locking is exact.

---

# 10. Verdict

One step further shows that gauge-locking consists of:

1. same scalar \(q_0\);
2. same derivative convention;
3. controlled curvature residual;
4. controlled \(\Gamma_G\) residual;
5. controlled \(H\)-factor residual.

All are finite identity/residual audits.

No new conceptual obstruction appears, but a derivative-convention mismatch or affine primitive drift would invalidate wall escape unless explicitly controlled.

Continue your attack

## Assistant (2026-04-27 14:19:40)

## Continuing attack — derivative-convention normalization and wall-escape scale

The last step identified a hidden derivative-convention issue. If the paper uses a normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

then the identity needed for wall escape is not necessarily

\[
\partial_m^2 q_0=u,
\]

but rather

\[
\mathcal D^2q_0=u.
\]

This matters because wall escape uses curvature in the physical variable \(m\), while Gate 2 and D4 may be written in normalized variables. I’ll now normalize this completely.

---

# 1. Two coordinate systems

Let

\[
t=\frac{m-m_I}{\lambda}
\]

or, equivalently, let

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m=\partial_t.
\]

Suppose the canonical identities are written in \(\mathcal D\)-coordinates:

\[
u=\mathcal D^2 q_0,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

Then in physical \(m\)-coordinates,

\[
\partial_m^2q_0
=
\lambda^{-2}\mathcal D^2q_0
=
\lambda^{-2}u.
\]

So the physical curvature is

\[
q_0''(m)=\lambda^{-2}u.
\]

Wall escape in \(m\)-coordinate should therefore use curvature scale

\[
\lambda^{-2}|u|.
\]

But if we perform wall escape in normalized \(t\)-coordinate, then

\[
\frac{d^2q_0}{dt^2}=u,
\]

and all previous formulas are unchanged.

Thus the clean rule is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Run wall escape in the same normalized coordinate in which }u=\mathcal D^2q_0.
}
\]

---

# 2. Normalized wall escape

Work in \(t\)-coordinate and denote derivatives by dots or \(\mathcal D\). Assume

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q_0.
\]

At a wall-live point,

\[
|q_0(t_0)|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(t_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

Assume

\[
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

For complex \(q_0\), set

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(t_0)}}{|u(t_0)|},
\qquad
Q(t)=\Re(e q_0(t)).
\]

Then

\[
Q''(t)=\Re(e\mathcal D^2q_0(t))
=\Re(eu(t)).
\]

If

\[
|\mathcal D u|\rho\le c\tau,
\]

then

\[
Q''(t)\ge c\tau
\]

for

\[
|t-t_0|\le \rho.
\]

Choose

\[
\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Then first exit occurs at normalized distance

\[
|t_1-t_0|\le C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

In physical coordinate,

\[
|m_1-m_0|\le \lambda C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

So all previous wall-escape estimates are correct if interpreted in normalized coordinate.

---

# 3. Correct normalized derivative bounds

The D3a local complexity should be stated as:

\[
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

Not

\[
|\partial_m u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}|I|^{-1}
\]

unless

\[
|I|\asymp \lambda.
\]

Since ordinary scale has

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

one must be careful with interval conventions. The safe statement is:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
}
\]

Then all threshold formulas use normalized distance.

The physical row mobility bound should similarly be written as:

\[
|\mathcal D\mathbf A_N|\le Q^{C_D}.
\]

Then the row-energy thickening interval in normalized coordinates has length

\[
Q^{-C_A-C_D},
\]

and in physical coordinates length

\[
\lambda Q^{-C_A-C_D}.
\]

---

# 4. Normalized threshold conditions

The wall-escape radius is

\[
\rho=Q^{-(C_\varepsilon-C_\tau)/2}.
\]

Curvature stability requires:

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le Q^{-C_\tau}.
\]

Thus:

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge 3C_\tau+2C_{u'}+O(1).
\]

This is unchanged.

Boundary-layer control should be measured in normalized length fraction inside \(I\). If \(I\) has normalized length \(\asymp1\), then:

\[
|I_{\rm bd}|\sim \rho |I|.
\]

So the previous condition

\[
C_\varepsilon\ge C_\tau+2A+2C_G+O(1)
\]

is unchanged.

If \(I\) has normalized length \(L_I\neq1\), then replace \(\rho\) by \(\rho/L_I\) in boundary fractions. Equivalently, require

\[
\rho\le Q^{-A-C_G}L_I.
\]

Thus the clean theorem should assume packets are normalized to unit size or include \(L_I\).

---

# 5. Normalized gauge residuals

Use the same derivative convention in residuals:

\[
r_C:=u-\mathcal D^2q_0.
\]

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3).
\]

\[
r_H^\ast:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

The tolerance conditions are:

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_H^\ast|\le c|q_0||u|^{b_\ast}\sigma(L)|\Gamma|
\]

or the relevant D4 residual condition.

No powers of \(\lambda\) appear if all objects are in the \(\mathcal D\)-normalization.

If a formula is written in \(\partial_m\)-normalization, convert first:

\[
\mathcal D^k=\lambda^k\partial_m^k.
\]

---

# 6. Consequence for Gate 2 identities

The Gate 2 identities must also be in the same normalization:

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q,
\]

\[
g=\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(\mathcal D q)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2g.
\]

If the paper writes primes, the audit must determine whether

\[
'
\]

means \(\partial_m\) or \(\mathcal D\). The real-rigidity proof must use the same derivative.

This is a hard guardrail:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not mix physical and normalized derivatives in }g,h,\text{ wall escape, or D4.}
}
\]

---

# 7. If there is a scaling mismatch

Suppose the paper defines

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q,
\]

but Gate 2 rigidity is written as if

\[
u=\partial_m^2q.
\]

Then the identity becomes

\[
\partial_m^2q=\lambda^{-2}u.
\]

The ODE

\[
u=q''=6q-2q^3+g
\]

would be mis-scaled by \(\lambda^{-2}\), destroying the integral rigidity theorem.

Therefore the Gate 2 real-variable theorem must be applied after rescaling to the normalized coordinate where:

\[
u=q_{tt}.
\]

The proof on \(J=(-2,2)\) is automatically normalized. So the canonical transfer into that theorem must include the rescaling.

---

# 8. Final derivative-convention audit table

The finite audit should include:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{object} & \text{required normalized identity} & \text{failure mode}\\
\hline
u & u=\mathcal D^2q_0 & wall escape and Gate 2 scale fail\\
g & g=u-6q_0+2q_0^3 & signal survival / rigidity fail\\
h & h=2q_0(\mathcal D q_0)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2g & G2-B fails\\
H & H=-q_0u^3/288+\cdots & D4 wall factor mismatch\\
u' & \mathcal D u & curvature stability scale wrong\\
\mathbf A' & \mathcal D\mathbf A & row mobility scale wrong
\end{array}
\]

All primes in the paper must be resolved against this table.

---

# 9. Final strengthened D3a statement

## Normalized Gauge-Locked Wall-Escape Theorem

Let \(\mathcal D\) be the derivative used in the canonical Gate 2 and D4 formulas. Assume:

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q_0+r_C,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3+r_G,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+r_H^\ast.
\]

Assume:

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

and \(r_H^\ast\) is D4-controlled.

Assume:

\[
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

Then the wall escape from

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\ge\tau
\]

produces a point with

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u|\ge c\tau,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c\tau,
\]

inside normalized distance

\[
O(\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}).
\]

Thus D4 applies at the escaped point, and row mobility follows using

\[
|\mathcal D\mathbf A_N|\le Q^{C_D}.
\]

---

# 10. Final extra finding

The additional hidden issue is derivative normalization. Once all derivatives are expressed in the same \(\mathcal D\)-coordinate, no new obstruction appears.

But if the paper mixes \(\partial_m\) and \(\mathcal D\), both Gate 2 rigidity and wall escape can be mis-scaled.

So the next audit must explicitly verify the prime convention in:

\[
q'',\quad g'',\quad h,\quad H,\quad A_N',
\]

and align all of them to \(\mathcal D\).

## Agent 4 / D — Final D3a gauge-locking and derivative-normalization theorem

We fix the derivative convention once and for all:

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

All D3a identities below are in \(\mathcal D\)-normalization. No physical \(\partial_m\)-derivatives are used unless explicitly converted by powers of \(\lambda\). This is necessary because wall escape, Gate 2, and D4 must use the same curvature coordinate. 

---

# 1. Normalized identities

The D3a wall variable is the scalar \(q_0\). The canonical source is

\[
u=\mathcal D^2 q_0.
\]

The first anisotropy channel is

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

The D4 row wall factor is

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

Equivalently, the exact gauge-locked system is

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q_0,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{D4-controlled residual}.
\]

---

# 2. Residuals

Define the three gauge residuals:

\[
r_C:=u-\mathcal D^2q_0,
\]

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-\left(\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3\right),
\]

\[
r_H^\ast:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

The exact gauge-locked case is

\[
r_C=0,\qquad r_G=0,
\]

and \(r_H^\ast\) is part of the usual D4 residual package.

The residual-tolerant assumptions are

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

and

\[
r_H^\ast\ \text{is D4-controlled}.
\]

Here “D4-controlled” means that \(r_H^\ast\) is either absorbed into the effective D4 leading matrix or satisfies the half-leading residual estimate required by D4.

---

# 3. Wall escape in normalized coordinates

Assume a wall-live point \(m_0\) satisfies

\[
|q_0(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_0)|\ge\tau.
\]

For complex \(q_0\), define

\[
e=\frac{\overline{u(m_0)}}{|u(m_0)|},
\qquad
Q(m)=\Re(e q_0(m)).
\]

Then, in \(\mathcal D\)-coordinates,

\[
\mathcal D^2 Q
=
\Re(e\,\mathcal D^2q_0)
=
\Re(e(u-r_C)).
\]

If

\[
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}
\]

and we restrict to normalized distance \(\rho\), then

\[
|u(m)-u(m_0)|\le Q^{C_{u'}}\rho.
\]

Choose

\[
\rho\asymp \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}
\]

and require

\[
Q^{C_{u'}}\rho\le c\tau.
\]

Together with

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

this gives

\[
\mathcal D^2 Q\ge c\tau
\]

on the normalized interval

\[
|m-m_0|_{\mathcal D}\le \rho.
\]

Equivalently, in the normalized coordinate \(t\) with \(\mathcal D=\partial_t\),

\[
|t-t_0|\le \rho.
\]

Thus \(Q\) is real-convex on that local interval. Since

\[
|Q(m_0)|\le |q_0(m_0)|<\varepsilon,
\]

convexity forces exit from the wall strip within normalized distance

\[
\rho\asymp \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.
\]

Hence there exists \(m_1\) such that

\[
|m_1-m_0|_{\mathcal D}\le C\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau},
\]

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

and

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

So the normalized wall escape radius is exactly

\[
\boxed{\rho\asymp\sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau}.}
\]

---

# 4. Signal survival

At the first-exit point \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Using the residual definition,

\[
\Gamma_G
=
\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3+r_G.
\]

Since

\[
\mathcal D^2q_0=u-r_C,
\]

we get

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q_0+2q_0^3+(r_G-r_C).
\]

Therefore

\[
|\Gamma_G|
\ge
|u|-6|q_0|-2|q_0|^3-|r_G-r_C|.
\]

At \(m_1\), if

\[
\varepsilon\ll\tau
\]

and

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

then

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2
\ge
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma_G(m_1)|^2
\ge
c\tau^4.
\]

So \(m_1\) is a valid non-wall D4 sample.

---

# 5. D4 compatibility through \(H\)

The D4 row factor uses

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+r_H^\ast.
\]

The escaped point has

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\qquad
|\Gamma(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

D4 compatibility requires \(r_H^\ast\) to be included in the D4 residual audit. In valuation form, the requirement is:

\[
r_H^\ast\Gamma
\]

is either absorbed into the D4 effective leading row map, or satisfies the half-leading condition

\[
|r_H^\ast|\,|\Gamma|
\le
\frac12 |q_0|\,|u|^{b_\ast}\sigma_2(L_\ast)|\Gamma|
\]

for the relevant D4 leading valuation \(q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma\). In the original \(H\)-factor case \(b_\ast=3\), this is

\[
|r_H^\ast|
\le
c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_\ast).
\]

If \(r_H^\ast\) is an absolute residual floor, it must satisfy the corresponding threshold-corridor exponent. If it is valuation-relative, no separate corridor is needed.

---

# 6. Final residual-tolerant D3a theorem

## Theorem

Fix the derivative convention

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

Assume Gate 2 mass on \(I\):

\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume local upper bounds:

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\le Q^{C_G},
\]

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

\[
|\mathcal D u|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

Assume gauge residuals

\[
r_C:=u-\mathcal D^2q_0,
\]

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-(\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3),
\]

\[
r_H^\ast:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
\]

satisfy, on wall-escape neighborhoods,

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau,
\]

and \(r_H^\ast\) is D4-controlled.

Then, after splitting

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q_0|\ge\varepsilon\},
\qquad
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\},
\]

either the non-wall branch directly supplies a D4 sample, or the wall branch supplies by normalized first-exit a point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau,
\]

and therefore

\[
|u(m_1)|^2|\Gamma(m_1)|^2\ge c\tau^4.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

If D4 row conversion holds at non-wall samples and row mobility holds, then

\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
}
\]

---

# 7. Exact remaining mismatch

D3a is closed under the theorem above unless one of these precise mismatches occurs:

1. **Derivative convention mismatch**

   The identities are not all written with the same \(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\).

2. **Curvature mismatch**

   \[
   |u-\mathcal D^2q_0|>c\tau
   \]

   on the wall-escape neighborhood.

3. **Anisotropy mismatch**

   \[
   |\Gamma_G-(\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3)-(u-\mathcal D^2q_0)|>c\tau.
   \]

   Equivalently,

   \[
   |r_G-r_C|>c\tau.
   \]

4. **D4 \(H\)-factor mismatch**

   \[
   r_H^\ast=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}
   \]

   is not absorbable and not half-leading in the D4 residual audit.

If none of these occur, the gauge-locking and derivative-normalization guardrail is closed.

## Agent 4 / D — Audit of potential D3a gauge/normalization mismatches

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a is logically closed as a theorem, but not yet certified against the paper definitions.}
}
\]

The remaining risk is not the wall-escape argument itself. It is whether the paper’s \(q_0,u,\Gamma_G,H\) actually satisfy the same normalized-gauge identities required by the theorem. The current shared material identifies these as required guardrails, but does not provide enough exact paper formulas to certify all of them. 

---

# 1. Derivative-convention mismatch

Required convention:

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

Every D3a identity must be written in \(\mathcal D\)-normalization:

\[
u=\mathcal D^2q_0,
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\cdots.
\]

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Not certified from the current material.}
}
\]

The handoff correctly states the required convention, but the actual paper formulas must be checked to confirm that every prime/double-prime in \(q'',\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},H\) means \(\mathcal D\), not \(\partial_m\).

## Failure mode

If the paper uses \(\partial_m\) in one place and \(\mathcal D\) in another, then

\[
\partial_m^2q_0=\lambda^{-2}\mathcal D^2q_0,
\]

so the ODE scale in wall escape and the \(L^2\)-rigidity identities are mis-scaled.

## Required close

Verify the paper uses:

\[
q_0''=\mathcal D^2q_0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G''=\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G,
\]

and

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q_0(\mathcal Dq_0)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]

If any formula is in \(\partial_m\), rewrite it in \(\mathcal D\)-coordinates before applying D3a.

---

# 2. Curvature mismatch

Define

\[
r_C:=u-\mathcal D^2q_0.
\]

D3a wall escape needs either

\[
r_C=0,
\]

or robustly

\[
|r_C|\le c\tau
\]

on the wall-escape neighborhood.

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Not certified from current material.}
}
\]

The downstream theorem assumes curvature compatibility, but the supplied handoff does not prove that the \(q_0\) used in the wall variable is the same scalar whose normalized second derivative is \(u=q''_{\can}\).

## Failure mode

If

\[
|u-\mathcal D^2q_0| \gtrsim \tau,
\]

then a live-source point

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\]

does not imply the \(q_0\)-wall coordinate has curvature. Wall escape may move the wrong object.

## Required close

Show in the paper definitions:

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q_0.
}
\]

If only approximate, prove

\[
\boxed{
|u-\mathcal D^2q_0|\le c\tau.
}
\]

---

# 3. \(\Gamma_G\)-identity mismatch

Define

\[
r_G:=\Gamma_G-\left(\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3\right).
\]

Since

\[
\mathcal D^2q_0=u-r_C,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G
=
u-6q_0+2q_0^3+(r_G-r_C).
\]

At the first-exit point, D3a needs

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c\tau.
\]

That follows if

\[
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau.
\]

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Not certified from current material, but the required test is exact.}
}
\]

The shared background repeatedly uses

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

but the paper’s precise definition of \(\Gamma_G\) must be checked in the same normalized derivative convention.

## Failure mode

If

\[
|r_G-r_C|\gtrsim \tau,
\]

then even after wall escape gives

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\ge c\tau,
\]

one cannot conclude

\[
|\Gamma_G|\ge c\tau.
\]

Then the escaped point may not be a D4 sample.

## Required close

Verify:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=\mathcal D^2q_0-6q_0+2q_0^3.
}
\]

Equivalently, using \(u=\mathcal D^2q_0\),

\[

}

If residual, prove

\boxed{
|r_G-r_C|\le c\tau.
}

# 4. \(H\)-factor / D4 wall-scalar mismatch

Define

\[
r_H^\ast:=H+\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

D4 needs

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{D4-controlled residual}.
\]

## Audit result

\[

The handoff says the expected structure is

H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288},

and that raw symbols should give

R_7\sim -\frac1{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\qquad
R_9\sim -\frac1{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

But it also says those row symbols and D4 data must be derived from the paper’s finite row algebra, not from zeta or downstream logic alone. 

## Failure mode

If \(H\) uses a different scalar \(q_{\rm row}\),

\[
H=-\frac{q_{\rm row}u^3}{288}+\cdots,
\]

while wall escape uses \(q_0\), then

\[

At the escaped point,

|q_0|=\varepsilon.
\]

The drift must satisfy

\[
|q_{\rm row}-q_0|\le c\varepsilon\sigma_2(L)
\]

or it is too large relative to the escaped leading term.

\[
\boxed{
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\text{valuation-relative D4 residual};
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
r_H^\ast
\text{ is absorbed into }L_{\rm eff};
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
|r_H^\ast|
\le c|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_{\rm eff}).
}
\]

If \(r_H^\ast\) is an absolute residual floor, it must satisfy the wall-threshold corridor:

\[
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1).
\]

---

# 5. Affine primitive mismatch

Even if

\[
\mathcal D^2q_{\rm curv}=u,
\]

there is affine freedom:

\[
q_{\rm curv}\mapsto q_{\rm curv}+am+b.
\]

But neither

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3
\]

nor

\[
H=-\frac{qu^3}{288}
\]

is affine-invariant.

## Audit result

\[
\boxed{
\text{Must be ruled out explicitly unless \(q_0\) is definitionally fixed.}
}
\]

If

\[
q_{\rm aniso}=q_{\rm curv}+\ell,
\qquad
\ell=am+b,
\]

then near \(q_{\rm curv}=0\),

\[
r_G\approx -6\ell+2\ell^3.
\]

The only affine drift compatible with the same wall is

\[
\ell\approx0.
\]

For D4 compatibility at wall threshold \(\varepsilon\), require

\[
\boxed{
|a||I|+|b|\le c\varepsilon\sigma_2(L).
}
\]

A weaker \(O(\tau)\) bound may preserve \(\Gamma_G\), but it is not enough for the D4 row wall factor.

## Continuing attack — actual-paper gauge-locking audit

I looked for the definitions needed to close the D3a gauge-locking guardrail against the draft, not just against our abstract theorem.

Current verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gauge-locking is mostly supported by the draft’s local notation, but not fully certified in }\mathcal D\text{-normalization.}
}

The paper appears internally consistent in the **local spectral variable \(t\)**: \(q(t)=\Phi'(t)\), the jet Gram matrices use \(q,q',q''\), and the centered reduced-patch definitions of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) use the same \(q_0,q'',q^{(4)}\). But the final D3a theorem was deliberately stated in normalized derivative convention

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

The draft sections I found mostly use ordinary local \(t\)-derivatives, not explicitly \(\mathcal D\). So the remaining mismatch is now precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Either D3a must be run in the paper’s local }t\text{-coordinate, or the paper must explicitly convert those formulas to }\mathcal D.
}

# 1. \(q\) and derivative convention in the draft

The draft defines the local phase derivative as

\[
q(t):=\Phi'(t).
\]

The jet-limit Gram block uses

\[
J(T)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q(T) & \frac12 q'(T)\\
\frac12 q'(T) & \frac1{12}(q''(T)+2q(T)^3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

This fixes the local prime convention in the early analytic sections: primes mean derivatives in the local spectral variable \(t\). The finite-\(s\) same-point blocks use the same convention at \(t_\pm=m\pm s/2\). 

So, at least in the local jet/Gram notation,

\[
q_0=q(m),\qquad q''=q''(m)
\]

are in the same \(t\)-derivative convention.

---

# 2. \(\Gamma_G\) identity

The draft’s centered reduced-patch section defines

\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right),
\]

and then defines

\[
\Gamma_G:=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

It also records

\[
g-h=-\frac{\Gamma_G}{6\pi},
\]

so the Gram-isotropy wall \(g=h\) is equivalent to \(\Gamma_G=0\). 

Thus, in the draft’s **local \(t\)-derivative notation**, the anisotropy identity is exact:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3.
}
\]

If we identify

\[
u=q'',
\]

then this is exactly the D3a signal-survival identity

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3.
\]

So the \(\Gamma_G\)-identity audit is closed **in the local \(t\)-coordinate**.

---

# 3. \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) identity

The same section defines

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}:=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

It derives this from the second centered Gram variation: at \(g=h\),

\[
(X_2)_D
=
-\frac{1}{32\pi}g^{-3/2}\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

The displayed derivation uses the centered Gram model and \(G''(m)\), again in the same prime convention. 

This matches the identity

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

under centered parity \(q'(m)=q'''(m)=0\). Indeed, differentiating

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3
\]

twice gives

\[
\Gamma_G''
=
q^{(4)}-6q''+12q(q')^2+6q^2q''.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
q'=0,
\]

so

\[
-\frac16\Gamma_G''
=
-\frac16q^{(4)}+q''-q^2q''
=
(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

Thus the draft’s \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) definition is consistent with the general D3a/Gate-2 identity in the centered regime.

So this audit is also closed **for centered parity**:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\quad\text{reduces to the draft’s formula when }q'=q'''=0.
}
\]

---

# 4. Curvature identity \(u=q_0''\)

Here we must be careful with notation.

The draft uses \(q_0\) as the centered value

\[
q_0=q(m),
\]

not as a separate primitive function named \(q_0(t)\). The actual local scalar is \(q(t)\), and

\[
q''=q''(m)
\]

is its second derivative. In our D3a notation, the wall variable \(q_0\) should be interpreted as the function

\[
m\mapsto q(m),
\]

with centered value \(q_0=q(m)\).

Therefore, in the draft’s local derivative convention,

\[
\boxed{
u=q''_{\can}=q''(m)
}
\]

is consistent **if** the paper’s \(q''\) in the Gram-anisotropy section is the full actual-zeta canonical curvature. The draft’s own later proposed canonical clarification says this should be read as

\[
q''=q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m),
\]

not as a complement-source curvature or proxy. 

But the current proof text must be checked for whether this canonical clarification is actually present. The existing PDF section I found defines \(q(t)=\Phi'(t)\) and uses \(q''\), but it does not by itself prove that this \(q''\) equals the fully canonical

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

rather than a local model/proxy. 

So the curvature audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{closed if }q\text{ is the full actual-zeta phase derivative }q_\zeta.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{not closed if }q\text{ is a local model, core-only, complement-source, or AFE proxy.}
}
\]

The draft explicitly warns in proposed edits that complement-source curvature

\[
q''_{\source,R}=(G^{\new})''(m)
\]

is not the same as the full canonical actual-zeta curvature

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m).
\]

That warning is exactly the necessary guardrail.

# 5. \(H\)-factor identity

The paper-side material gives the centered leading source calculation:

\[

\qquad
q''=2A_2.
\]

Therefore

\[
H_{\lead}=y_{\lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\cdot 2A_2
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]

Since

\[
A_2=\frac{q''}{2},
\]

we obtain

\[
H_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

This is exactly the D3a/D4 wall-factor identity with \(u=q''\):

\[
\boxed{
H_{\lead}=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
}
\]

The draft material also states the source factor as

\[
H:=yq'',
\qquad
H\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

turn70file2

So the \(H\)-factor audit is:

}
\]

But the **full** identity is not closed until the D4 correction package proves that the remaining terms are valuation-relative, quotiented, or half-leading:

The paper currently treats order-nine correction incidence as open, and the broader D4 correction package remains the main blocker.

## Not yet closed

Two items remain.

### A. Normalized derivative convention

The paper sections found use local \(t\)-derivatives. D3a was stated with

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

So either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{run D3a in the paper’s local }t\text{-coordinate;}
}
\]

or explicitly define

\[
\mathcal D=\partial_t
\]

on these packets and rewrite all formulas accordingly.

If later sections use

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

then the paper must state that the local \(t\)-coordinate is the normalized coordinate. Otherwise powers of \(\lambda\) enter \(q'',\Gamma_{G,2}\), and wall escape is mis-scaled.

### B. Full canonical curvature

The identity

\[
u=q''
\]

is closed only if \(q\) is the full actual-zeta phase derivative. It is not closed if \(q\) is any of:

\[
q_{\core},
\quad
G^{\new},
\quad
q_{\source,R},
\quad
\text{one-sided AFE proxy}.
\]

The paper needs the explicit convention:

\[
\boxed{
q=q_\zeta,\qquad q''=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

The proposed replacement definition in the handoff does exactly that, but the current PDF text should be checked/updated to make it explicit.

## 1. Add a normalized-prime convention after the Gate 2 anisotropy lemma

**Where to insert:** immediately after the proof of

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Differentiated form of the second Gate--2 anisotropy]
...
\end{proof}
```

i.e. after the block proving

```latex
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
```

### Insert

```latex
\begin{remark}[Derivative convention and gauge-locking for downstream use]
\label{rem:derivative-convention-gauge-locking-downstream}
All downstream Gate--2, wall-escape, and D4 row-conversion identities use the
same normalized derivative convention
\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]
Thus, whenever ordinary prime notation is used in a local packet coordinate in
the downstream sections, it is shorthand for \(\mathcal D\)-differentiation in
that normalized local coordinate.  In particular,
\[
q''=q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q_\zeta,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q_\zeta(\mathcal Dq_\zeta)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]

The scalar \(q_\zeta\) used here is also the scalar that appears in the
\(q_0\)-wall and in the D4 source factor.  Thus the wall coordinate is not an
arbitrary affine primitive of \(q''_{\can}\).  The affine freedom in solving
\(\mathcal D^2q=q''_{\can}\) is fixed by the canonical real phase convention
above.  This gauge-locking is necessary because neither
\[
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q+2q^3
\]
nor the source factor
\[
H_{\lead}=-\frac{q(q''_{\can})^3}{288}
\]
is invariant under affine changes \(q\mapsto q+am+b\).
\end{remark}
```

Rationale: the draft already defines the canonical real phase and anisotropy identities, but this insertion makes the \(\mathcal D\)-normalization and gauge-locking guardrail explicit at the point where the identities are introduced.

```latex
Choose source and wall thresholds

\qquad
```

## 4. Add a residual-corridor clause to D4 in the wall theorem

The wall theorem says \(r_H^\ast\) is D4-controlled. To capture the extended audit, add a precise residual classification after the D4 black-box statement in the wall-escape section.

**Where to insert:** after the proof of `Theorem [Gauge-locked wall escape in normalized coordinates]` and before

```latex
\begin{remark}[D3 is replaced by wall escape plus D4]
```

### Insert

```latex
\begin{remark}[D4 residuals in the wall-escape theorem]
\label{rem:d4-residuals-in-wall-escape}
In Theorem~\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}, the phrase
``\(r_H^\ast\) is controlled by the D4 residual estimate'' is to be interpreted
valuation-wise.  After extracting the effective D4 leading row map, write the
row residual as
\[
\mathbf R
=
\mathbf R_{\rm same}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm val}
+
\mathbf R_{\rm abs}.
\]
Here \(\mathbf R_{\rm same}\) denotes all same-valuation anisotropy-linear
terms; these are absorbed into the effective D4 row matrix.  The term
\(\mathbf R_{\rm val}\) denotes residuals carrying explicit additional
\(q_0\), \(u\), or anisotropy valuation, and these are controlled relative to
the leading row scale term-by-term.  Only \(\mathbf R_{\rm abs}\), consisting
of absolute canonical, tail, projection, or normalization error floors with no
useful \(q_0,u,\Gamma\)-valuation, is subject to a threshold-corridor condition.

Concretely, if the D4 leading valuation is
\[
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma
\]
and the wall-escape sample has
\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\gg \tau,\qquad |\Gamma|\gg \tau,
\]
then an absolute residual bound
\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}}
\]
must satisfy
\[
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1),
\]
where \(Q^{-C_L}\) is the D4 row-rank lower bound.  If D4 uses a filtered
leading block through \(u\)-valuation \(B\), replace \(b_\ast\) by \(B\).
This corridor condition does not apply to same-valuation terms absorbed into
\(L_\ast\) or to valuation-relative residuals.
\end{remark}
```

This captures the most important “final extra audit” from the extended conversation.

## 5. Add the filtered D4 formulation after the carrier quotient theorem

The current D4 theorem says the carrier quotient rows are schematically

\[
[\mathcal A_7]\sim H\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7],\qquad
[\mathcal A_9]\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}].
\]

That is useful, but the extended audit clarified that D4 should allow lower or delayed \(u\)-valuation layers. Insert a remark after the proof of `Theorem [D4 carrier-quotient row conversion through order nine]`, before the scalar incidence remark.

### Insert

```latex
\begin{remark}[Filtered D4 row observability]
\label{rem:filtered-d4-row-observability}
The schematic display in Theorem~\ref{thm:d4-carrier-quotient-through-order-nine}
is the expected minimal case of a more general filtered row-observability
statement.  In general, the anisotropy-linear part of a finite row vector may
be written as
\[
\mathbf A_N^{\rm lin}
=
q_0\sum_{b=b_0}^{B}u^bL_b\Gamma,
\qquad
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T.
\]
The correct D4 rank condition is that the cumulative filtered matrix
\[
\mathcal L_{[b_0,B]}(u)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
L_{b_0}\\
uL_{b_0+1}\\
\vdots\\
u^{B-b_0}L_B
\end{pmatrix}
\]
has
\[
\sigma_2\!\left(\mathcal L_{[b_0,B]}(u)\right)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]
The special case used in the clean carrier-quotient route is \(b_0=B=3\), with
\[
L_3\sim -\frac1{288}I_2
\]
in the carrier coordinates
\([\mathsf C_7],[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\).  If a lower \(u\)-valuation
anisotropy-linear layer appears, it should be promoted into the leading
filtered matrix rather than treated as an error.  If a minimal layer is
rank-one, the next \(u\)-valuation layers must be checked on its kernel until
both anisotropy directions are observed.
\end{remark}
```

This prevents future D4 audits from incorrectly treating lower-\(u\) terms as residuals.

```latex
If one nevertheless imposes scalar \(I\)-coordinate row energy as the downstream
```

## 7. Add row-mobility theorem as a standalone lemma

The current wall theorem ends with row mobility but does not isolate it. Add a lemma after the D3 wall-escape theorem remarks and before the “Current proof state” section.

**Where to insert:** after

```latex
\end{remark}
```

for `D3 is replaced by wall escape plus D4`, before

```latex
\section{Current proof state after the local package audits}
```

### Insert

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Row mobility: pointwise row lower bound implies row energy]
\label{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}
Let \(\mathbf A_N:I\to \mathcal H\) be a finite-dimensional row vector or
quotient-row representative on a packet \(I\).  Suppose
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]
for some \(m_\ast\in I\), and
\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}
\qquad (m\in I).
\]
Then there is an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with
\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]
such that
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12 Q^{-C_A}
\qquad (m\in J_\ast).
\]
Consequently,
\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

The same conclusion holds for a quotient-row norm, provided the chosen
quotient frame has polynomially bounded condition number and polynomially
bounded packet derivative on \(I\).  If a weighted packet norm is used, the
sample \(m_\ast\) is chosen in the polynomially thick core of the packet; the
standard boundary-layer exclusion used in the wall-escape argument supplies
this core condition.
\end{lemma}
```

This packages the existential-to-energy upgrade as a reusable result.

## 8. Add a short “downstream theorem” after row mobility

After the row mobility lemma, insert a combined theorem. This will make the section read as a closure package, not a list of remarks.

### Insert

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Local downstream closure from Gate 2 and D4]
\label{thm:local-downstream-closure-from-gate2-d4}
Assume the ordinary real-canonical local complexity bounds needed for
Theorem~\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}.  Assume Gate~2 on \(I\):
\[
\int_I |u|^2|\Gamma|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]
Assume the gauge-locking residuals in
Theorem~\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy} satisfy their stated
bounds, and assume D4 row conversion at non-wall samples in either carrier
quotient or filtered row form.  Finally assume row mobility as in
Lemma~\ref{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}.  Then
\[
\boxed{
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C}|I|
}
\]
for some polynomial exponent \(C\).

In particular, under row-energy architecture, the \(q_0\)-wall does not require
a separate source-robust wall row.  If the downstream architecture is
exact-point locked, this theorem is not sufficient and the \(q_0\)-adic
row-pencil or source-robust wall-row fallback must be used.
\end{theorem}
```

This captures the key structural conclusion of the extended wall-escape work.

# Structural status after these edits

These insertions capture the extended conversation as follows:

- Gate 2 is now based on \(u'\)-source thickening plus \(L^2\)-input rigidity, not old Remez/Cartan or pointwise target-smallness. The draft already includes this.
- D3a/wall escape is included, but needs syntax repair and a threshold/residual clarification.
- Gauge-locking is mostly captured by definitions, but should be explicitly tied to \(\mathcal D\)-normalization and affine primitive exclusion.
- D4 carrier-quotient row conversion is included and is the right direction.
- The scalar \(I\)-coordinate cross-channel wall remains a fallback blocker only if scalar-collapse energy is required.
- The row-mobility lemma should be stated explicitly because it is the bridge from existential sampling to row energy.

No further broad strategy insertions are needed. The next real mathematical bottleneck is finite D4 carrier/projection residual control, not the \(q_0\)-wall or Gate 2 local mechanism.

## 1. Add an explicit normalized-prime convention after the anisotropy identity

The draft defines \(q_\zeta=\mathcal D\Phi_\zeta\) and later says ordinary prime notation is local. Still, the D3a/Gate-2/D4 system depends heavily on the statement that all primes in the downstream package mean the same \(\mathcal D\). Add this as a formal remark.

**Where to insert:** immediately after the proof of

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Differentiated form of the second Gate--2 anisotropy]
...
\end{proof}
```

### Insert

```latex
\begin{remark}[Normalized derivative convention for the downstream package]
\label{rem:normalized-derivative-convention-downstream}
Throughout the downstream Gate--2, wall-escape, and D4 row-conversion package,
all derivatives are taken in the same normalized packet coordinate.  Equivalently,
ordinary prime notation in the local packet coordinate means
\[
'=\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]
Thus
\[
q''=\mathcal D^2q,\qquad
\Gamma_G''=\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(\mathcal Dq)^2-\frac16\mathcal D^2\Gamma_G.
\]
No downstream identity in this section should mix physical \(\partial_m\)
derivatives with normalized \(\mathcal D\)-derivatives.  If a formula is
transported from physical \(m\)-coordinates, it must first be rewritten using
\(\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\).
\end{remark}
```

## 3. Add a formal gauge-locking corollary after the compatibility lemma

The paper now has enough pieces to state gauge-locking formally: \(q\), \(u\), \(\Gamma_G\), and \(H\) must all use the same \(q\) and derivative convention. You already have `Real-canonical Gate--2 compatibility`; add a corollary right after its proof and before the residual version remark.

**Where to insert:** after

```latex
\end{proof}
```

of

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Real-canonical Gate--2 compatibility]
```

### Insert

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Gauge-locking for the \(q_0\)-wall]
\label{cor:gauge-locking-q0-wall}
In the real-canonical convention above, the \(q_0\)-wall used in wall escape is
the same scalar wall that appears in the Gate--2 anisotropy and in the D4
source factor.  Namely, for \(q_0=q_\zeta(m)\),
\[
u=\mathcal D^2q_0,
\]
\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]
and the D4 source factor has leading form
\[
H_{\lead}=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]
Thus \(q_0\) is not an arbitrary affine primitive of \(u\).  Any affine drift
\(q_0\mapsto q_0+am+b\) changes both
\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]
and
\[
H_{\lead}=-q_0u^3/288.
\]
Consequently, the wall-escape argument is applied only in the canonical gauge
fixed by \(q_\zeta\).
\end{corollary}
```

This makes the gauge-locking conclusion discoverable in the draft.

## 5. Add the missing row-mobility lemma

The wall theorem says “row mobility holds,” but the draft still lacks a standalone row-mobility lemma. Add it before `section{Current proof state after the local package audits}`.

**Where to insert:** immediately after the remark:

```latex
\begin{remark}[D3 is replaced by wall escape plus D4]
...
\end{remark}
```

and before:

```latex
\section{Current proof state after the local package audits}
```

### Insert

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Row mobility: pointwise lower bound to row energy]
\label{lem:row-mobility-pointwise-to-energy}
Let \(\mathbf A_N:I\to \mathcal H\) be a finite-dimensional row vector, or a
quotient-row representative in a fixed polynomially conditioned quotient frame.
Assume
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]
for some \(m_\ast\in I\), and
\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}
\qquad (m\in I).
\]
Then there exists an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with
\[
|J_\ast|\ge Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|
\]
such that
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12 Q^{-C_A}
\qquad (m\in J_\ast).
\]
Consequently,
\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-3C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

If the row norm is weighted by a packet cutoff, the same conclusion holds
provided \(m_\ast\) lies in the polynomially thick core where the cutoff is
bounded below by \(Q^{-C}\).  The buffered packet reduction in the wall-escape
argument supplies this core condition.
\end{lemma}
```

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Local row-energy closure from Gate--2 and D4]
\label{thm:local-row-energy-closure-from-gate2-d4}
Assume Gate--2 on \(I\):

\[
\boxed{

}

for some polynomial exponent \(C\).

Thus, under row-energy architecture, the \(q_0\)-wall does not require a
separate source-robust wall row.  If the final contradiction is exact-point
locked, this theorem is insufficient and the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil or
```

## 8. Add a residual-corridor clause to the wall theorem section

The draft has a D4 residual valuation ledger later in the D4 subsection. But the wall theorem uses `r_H^\ast is controlled by D4 residual estimate` without specifying the absolute-residual corridor. Add a short remark immediately after the wall theorem proof and before `D3 is replaced by wall escape plus D4`.

### Insert

```latex
\begin{remark}[Absolute residual corridor in wall escape]
\label{rem:absolute-residual-corridor-wall-escape}
In Theorem~\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}, D4 residual control
is interpreted valuation-wise.  Same-valuation anisotropy-linear terms are
absorbed into the effective D4 row matrix, and valuation-relative residuals are
estimated relative to the leading row scale.  Only absolute residual floors
require a wall-threshold corridor.

Concretely, if the D4 leading valuation is
\[
q_0u^{b_\ast}L_\ast\Gamma
\]
and the wall-escape sample satisfies
\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\gg\tau,\qquad |\Gamma|\gg\tau,
\]
then an absolute residual bound
\[
|\mathbf R_{\rm abs}|\le Q^{-C_R^{\rm abs}}
\]
must satisfy
\[
C_R^{\rm abs}
\ge
C_\varepsilon+(b_\ast+1)C_\tau+C_L+O(1),
\]
where \(Q^{-C_L}\) is the D4 row-rank lower bound.  If D4 uses a filtered
leading block through \(u\)-valuation \(B\), replace \(b_\ast\) by \(B\).
This condition does not apply to residuals carrying useful \(q_0,u,\Gamma\)
valuation.
\end{remark}
```

This connects the wall theorem to the residual ledger.

## 12. Add exact missing identity for \(H_{\lead}\)

The draft mentions \(H_{\lead}\) in the gauge-locking corollary, but the derivation

\[
H_{\lead}=y_{\lead}q''=-q_0(q'')^3/288
\]

should appear near the D4 carrier theorem or before it.

**Where to insert:** immediately before `\begin{theorem}[D4 carrier-quotient row conversion through order nine]`.

### Insert

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Leading source factor]
\label{lem:leading-source-factor-H}
In the centered reduced-patch normalization,
\[
H:=yq'',
\]
and the leading source term satisfies
\[
H_{\lead}=-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]
Equivalently, with \(u=q''_{\can}=q''\),
\[
H_{\lead}=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The centered source calculation gives
\[
y_{\lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\qquad
q''=2A_2.
\]
Hence
\[
H_{\lead}=y_{\lead}q''
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\cdot 2A_2
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^3}{36}.
\]
Since \(A_2=q''/2\),
\[
H_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]
\end{proof}
```

If this identity already appears elsewhere, still include it here as a local D4 reference; it is short and prevents readers from hunting.

# Summary of what these edits fix

After these edits:

- The derivative convention is explicit.
- \(q_0\) gauge-locking is formalized.
- The \(H_{\lead}\) identity is locally derived.
- Wall escape is stated with threshold conditions.
- Absolute residual floors are distinguished from valuation-relative residuals.
- Row mobility is a formal lemma.
- The D4 theorem is clearly carrier-quotient, not scalar \(I\)-coordinate.
- The scalar order-nine incidence wall is recorded as a fallback-only blocker.
- The residual valuation ledger no longer hard-codes \(u^3\) inconsistently.

I do not see a new definitional obstruction beyond these. The remaining mathematical blocker is still finite D4 row/projection residual control, especially if the final architecture requires scalar-collapsed \(I\)-coordinate row energy rather than carrier-quotient row energy.
